# Igros Kodesh

## Volume 23

## 8781

8781

B”H, 12 Tishrei, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

[Mr. Shalom Levin]

Greetings and Blessings,

I am writing to acknowledge with thanks the receipt of your letter from the 5th of Tishrei. Although the time, being the eve of the Yom Tov, does not permit me to write at length, I do not wish to delay my response until after the holiday. This is especially true since, regarding the matter itself, any elaboration for someone such as yourself is surely unnecessary.

I will only emphasize once more the point we touched upon in our conversation: that if each one of us, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael, were to approach the issues of the day based on a limited calculation—weighing only what is possible, what is within our capacity, and so on—it is quite possible that Eretz Yisrael would still be under the Mandate, or something similar, and both the writer and the recipient of this letter would be in some forgotten corner of Europe, or worse, G-d forbid.

However, as you describe your activities in the Teachers’ Union in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, you do not restrict yourself **at all** to remaining within the framework of the secretariat. Rather, you consider what is necessary, not merely what is possible according to a mathematical calculation.

Regarding your writing about the limited role of the chairman of the World Union: I will surely not be saying anything new if I express my opinion that if you were to issue an appeal—specifically in your capacity as chairman of the World Union—to all educational activists, and to the teachers first and foremost, stating that the time has come to acknowledge the bitter reality regarding the disappointments in education, etc. (which you write about in your letter), and together with this, the necessity to proclaim belief in the Living G-d who watches over our world and commands morality, justice, and integrity, etc.—and to do so with courage and in a full voice, in the style of the Shulchan Aruch at its beginning, not to be ashamed before those who mock—this would not only make an impression akin to an atomic bomb in the widest circles, but it would surely also have far-reaching positive results. To use the phrasing of the text: "And who knows if it is for a time like this that you have attained royalty."

It is ingrained in the desire of every person to do something exceptional, and like any matter in nature, one must certainly utilize this power in a positive and constructive manner. Although I am not well-versed in the activities and conduct of the chairmen of the World Union who preceded you, an appeal such as the one mentioned is a matter for its time. There has never been a more fitting opportunity or a more capable hour than our current generation—a generation full of disappointments, yet at the same time, full of a thirst for truth, even if large parts of our generation do not know where to seek that truth and are standing on the brink of despair regarding it.

Based on my impressions from meetings with representatives of various and diverse circles, my estimation is close to certainty that there would be a very great and pleasant surprise from the resonance that such an appeal would find, provided it is expressed with certainty and in a "loud voice, and he did not cease." I hope that you will utilize this unique and special opportunity.

With respect and blessings for a Chag Sameach.

Regarding your writing about the teachers of Chabad schools and their joining the Teachers’ Union: the only instruction they have received from me regarding their activities is solely and exclusively to be careful to avoid any partisan matter, and not to join organizations that have a partisan character.

I am not so familiar with the character of the union about which you write, but if the aforementioned concern does not apply to it, then the aforementioned instruction does not apply to it either. On the other hand, if it does have a partisan character, it is my hope that you, too—despite being a party to the matter—do not wish to divert the conduct of the people of Chabad, as people of Chabad, from the path they have followed for two hundred years, which is one of the most important factors in the success of their activities in many, many areas, and especially in the field of education.

#### ***8781***

Most of the letters are from the secretariat's copy, and some are from a photocopy of the letter. They are not marked with notes unless the source is different, or it has already been printed in other collections (in Likkutei Sichos, etc.).

**Mr. Shalom Levin:** Additional letters to him—above, Vol. 22, 8764, and what is indicated in the notes there.

Below, 8842, 8867.

**Touched upon in our conversation:** See also above, ibid.

**Teachers... partisan:** See also above, Vol. 17, letter 6353. Below, letter 8800, and elsewhere.

## 8282

B”H, 13 Tishrei, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Day of the Histalkus-Hillula of Admur Maharash

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, a bochur from the people and elevated from the people, one who seeks the good of his people, a man of noble character, a scion of a noble lineage,
R' Schneur Zalman shlita,

Greetings and blessings!

The telegram of blessing for Rosh Hashanah was surely received in due time. Based on the explanation in Chassidus regarding the verse, "Blow the shofar at the new moon, at the covered time (bakeseh) for our festival day"—that which is "covered" at the time of the shofar blowing is revealed on "our festival day"—I reiterate my wishes that all the blessings in which each and every one has been blessed will come to fruition in a revealed manner, and in the traditional phrasing: in a good that is seen and revealed.

This is especially so as this day evokes the memory of the day you were here, and subsequently, as recorded in my memory, your participation in the Hillula farbrengen in the shul of my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

In continuation of what was written in my previous letters, it is my hope that despite your increased and multiplied preoccupations, this day was also marked in your daily schedule in a fitting and special manner.

Moving from one topic to a related one, it was pleasant for me to learn that at a public gathering held here in N.Y. in honor of your visit the day after Yom Kippur, the speakers emphasized your connection to Chabad Chassidus and how you are integrated within it, to the extent that this is expressed even in your current exalted position.

By the way, as I was told, Mrs. G. Meir tichyeh related how you receive new faces: that you first inquire about the details of the lives—the spiritual and inner lives—of your visitors.

May it be G-d’s will that this, too, serves as a conduit for influence upon your visitors, to instill in them "of the spirit that is upon you"—this is the Torah of Chassidus, which contains that which is relevant not only to Bnei Yisrael but also to the nations of the world. For even the seven Noahide mitzvos are explained and illuminated in the Torah of Chassidus with a new light, hidden and bright, casting sparks in every direction.

In continuation of the above, enclosed is a copy of my general letter.

With appreciation, honor, and blessings for a joyous festival day, and with even greater intensity for Shemini Atzeres and Simchas Torah.

The above also serves as an answer to the question posed by Prof. Bergman shlita some time ago regarding the attitude of our Torah, the Torah of Life, toward the nations of the world.

## 8783

B"H, 19 Tishrei, 5724
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and diligent worker for communal needs, R' Azriel Zelig, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I have been alerted regarding the estate of Rabbi S. A. Elkin, a"h, who, according to reports, was a student of my father-in-law, the Rebbe (the Rebbe Rashab), n"e, and possessed letters in his holy handwriting. Since he passed away in Eretz Yisroel, may it be rebuilt and established, it is of the utmost importance to ascertain what has become of these holy manuscripts. Even though I am told he passed away some years ago, I still hope that something can be done regarding this.

In a similar vein, regarding the estate of Rabbi Neimark, a"h, of Tel Aviv—who, if I recall correctly, left no children—it is highly probable that he possessed items inherited from his grandfather, who was among the Chassidim of the Rebbe Maharash and the Rebbe Rashab, n"e.

Although time does not permit me to write and send letters, any preliminary investigation and inquiry is worthwhile, and I look forward to hearing good news regarding the above.

Due to the holiness of the festival, the Rebbe shlita has not signed this personally, and I am signing on his behalf,

The Secretary

#### ***8783***

**R' Azriel Zelig:** Slonim, may it be rebuilt and established. Additional letters to him appear in Vol. 18, 6768, and in the references noted in the footnotes there.

**Rabbi Neimark:** Avraham Yaakov.

**His grandfather:** R' Chaim Meshulam Zalman Neimark.

## 8784

B"H, 19 Tishrei, 5724
Brooklyn

Mr. Nachumi Hartzion, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 13 Tishrei, in which you write the main points of your acquaintance with the Chabad Chassidim and their movement, and that you were recently chosen to fulfill the role of a *garin* (core group) guide, etc.

Although you correctly wrote regarding the responsibility inherent in this matter, at the same time we have been promised: "He who comes to purify himself—and it is known how the Alter Rebbe, author of the *Tanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*—in this year, the 150th anniversary of his *histalkus* and *hilula*, emphasized: 'to purify others as well'—is assisted." Indeed, the awareness of the responsibility of the role is one of the primary conditions required of a *shaliach* and one chosen to fulfill such a task.

However, and this is the essential point for one who guides the children of Yisrael—each of whom is a child of the King, the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He—he must resolve to be, in the style of our Sages, "moist so as to moisten others." That is to say, a living example of a Jew who is hopeful, living according to the instructions of our Torah, the *Toras Chaim*, and through the fulfillment of its *mitzvos*, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them." And this must be done specifically with joy and a glad heart, and with *hislahavus*. This is the channel and the vessel for receiving the blessing of our Father in Heaven for success in fulfilling the role, and for overcoming obstacles and concealments, even if they should arise. After all, "Love your fellow as yourself" is a great principle in the Torah, and a fundamental one. If the result of fulfilling this *mitzvah* is to strive for the physical well-being of your fellow, how much more so regarding the well-being of the soul, which is also the well-being of the body, as is understood and seen tangibly.

Based on what you wrote regarding your acquaintance with the Chabad Chassidim, you have surely seen several examples of overcoming obstacles and difficulties, even those that on the face of it initially appeared to be extremely great and powerful.

We have just entered a new year—a renewal of the strengths of the Jewish man and woman, a renewal of the strengths of good and holiness.

With blessings for good tidings in all that is mentioned,

Due to the holiness of the festival, the Rebbe shlita did not sign this personally, and I sign on his behalf,

The Secretary

## 8785

B"H, 25 Tishrei, 5724
Brooklyn

Mr. A. L. Zuckerman, may he live

Peace and blessing!

In response to your question in your letter of 7/10 regarding the matter of *gilgul neshamos* (reincarnation of souls) as brought in various seforim—and specifically and at length in the writings of the Arizal—and the perspective of Chassidus on this.

The concept of *gilgulim* is found in several of our holy seforim from even before the time of the Arizal, as noted in the footnote*, although the authority of the Arizal is more than sufficient. It is understood that this matter is accepted both in the teachings of Chassidus and by the Gra of Vilna and his students, even though they opposed the teachings of Chassidus, etc. As mentioned, the matter is accepted, notwithstanding that some Jewish scholars—including those in the Middle Ages—did not accept the idea for various reasons, which is not the place to detail here.

On this occasion, allow me to enclose a copy of my general letter for this year, which I hope will be of interest to you.

With respect and blessing for good tidings through activities in the dissemination of Yiddishkeit,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

***

*) Zohar, Mishpatim (99b) and in several other places. Ramban (Introduction to Iyov). Rabbeinu Bachya (Bechukosai 26:11), and others.

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 33, p. 251, and completed according to the secretariat’s copy.

**My general letter:** See above, Vol. 22, letter 8779.

8286

**M. Schneerson**

Regarding the event you write about, see Shu”t Tzemach Tzedek, Shaar HaMiluim, Vol. 2. Be more precise in your Chitas studies and in giving tzedakah before davening on weekday mornings. And may Hashem grant you success.

## 8787

B"H, 29 Tishrei, 5724
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the 5th of Tishrei, which was received in due course, in which you write regarding the state of your health and that you have not yet conceived, etc.

Generally, in such matters, one should act according to the opinion of a specialist doctor, for it is incumbent upon a person to do what is within their power through the natural path, and there are several doctors in this field in Paris.

However—and this is also essential—sometimes pregnancy is delayed due to a lack of knowledge regarding all that is required in observing the laws and regulations of Taharas HaMishpacha. Therefore, you should clarify all the details regarding this with a Rav who is a *moreh hora'ah*. Even though, based on the education you received in our institutions, you surely know everything necessary, it is still worthwhile to clarify as mentioned, for "there is no righteous person on earth who does [only] good and never sins."

I trust that you observe the good custom of virtuous Jewish women to set aside money for tzedakah before lighting the candles every Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

#### ***8787***

**Sometimes... the family:** See also below, Igros 8800, 8895, and in many other places.

## 8288

B"H, 3 Marcheshvan, 5724
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter.

May it be Hashem’s will that you bring good tidings regarding both general and personal matters.

We have just emerged from the general month, the seventh month, which is *hamishuva* (the satiated one) and *mashbi’a* (which satiates) the entire year with goodness—goodness that is visible and revealed. This is especially true—

Through the *regalim* (festivals) that occur within it, *Zman Simchaseinu* (the time of our rejoicing), whose purpose is to draw the joy of Torah and mitzvos into the entire year.

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***8288***

General/personal. Published (dated 13 Marcheshvan) in *Likutei Sichos*, Vol. 18, p. 191, and completed based on a photocopy of the letter.

**Month... and satiates:** See *Hayom Yom*, 25 Elul. *Igros Kodesh* of the Rebbe Rayatz, Vol. 3, letter 794.

**Whose purpose is:** See also above, Vol. 22, letter 8224, and the references noted in the footnotes there.

**From the general month:** See *Likutei Torah*, Devarim (53d). *Maamar* entitled *Tzohar Ta’aseh*, 5702.

**The seventh month:** And all sevenths are beloved (*Vayikra Rabbah*, ch. 27:11).

**The satiated one and which satiates:** See *Vayikra Rabbah*, ch. 27:8. Explained in the *maamar* entitled *Yom Tov She’rosh Hashanah*, 5718.

**Through the regalim... Zman Simchaseinu:** For Shemini Atzeres (and Simchas Torah) is a festival in its own right (*Sukkah* 48a; and see Ramban and Ritba there). And on it, "they would **increase** in joy" (Rashi, s.v. *Bayom*; *Chullin* 83a).

**The joy of Torah and mitzvos:** See *Zohar*, Vol. 3, 256b. *Tikkunei Zohar*, 21 (96, bottom of page). Rambam, end of *Hilchos Lulav*.

## 8289

8289

B"H, 3 Menachem Av, 5724
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, who engages in communal needs, of noble lineage, etc., etc.,
R' S. Shlita

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter.

The story you write regarding my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi of our generation, is a precious matter. The blessings of Tzaddikim endure forever and continue to effect their purpose, especially according to the statement of our Sages that a Tzaddik who has departed is found even more than during his lifetime. This is as explained in Iggeres HaKodesh by our Alter Rebbe—this year being the one hundred and fiftieth anniversary of his histalkus and hillula—in Epistle 27 and its explanation.

At an auspicious time, please mention at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, those whom you write about, each according to their specific needs as appropriate to the content of your letter. May it be the will of Hashem that just as you have brought the request, you will also bring good tidings regarding this, and surely the merit of his ancestors, a lineage of noble stature, will assist him.

I have a strong hope that you are exerting yourself in spreading the wellsprings of the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov, his students, and his students' students, wherever your hand can reach, even to the truly "outside" places.

May it be the will of Hashem that we soon merit the fulfillment of the prophecy brought in the well-known Iggeres HaKodesh of the Baal Shem Tov, that when your wellsprings spread outward, the Master, King Moshiach, will come.

With respect and blessing for good tidings.

#### ***8289***

**R' S.:** Langer, Toronto.

**"A precious matter":** Shabbos 10b.

**"The story you write":** Upon the arrival of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, to New York, one of my acquaintances named Chaim Silver [see Igros Kodesh of the Rebbe, Vol. 7, letters 1868, 1859 — to him] suddenly fell ill with... and the doctors despaired of his life. He asked me, since my father, of blessed memory, was a Chossid of Lubavitch and his Rebbe had come to New York, to write to him and ask for a blessing for a complete recovery, and that he would also give tzedakah in whatever amount the Rebbe would mandate. A letter came back from the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that he should give one thousand dollars to Tomchei Temimim in Montreal, for "an angel of one hundred is not comparable to an angel of one thousand." He lived and stood on his feet, and immediately sent his son to Montreal and paid the money... And in the month that the Rebbe, of blessed memory, passed away, immediately in the second month, Mr. Silver, of blessed memory, passed away.

**"Statement of our Sages":** Zohar Vol. 3, 280a.

**"The well-known Iggeres HaKodesh":** Printed at the beginning of Kesser Shem Tov.

## 8790

B"H, 6 Mar-Cheshvan, 5724
Brooklyn

To the families of the immigrants from Morocco in Kfar Chabad, 
founded by and under the leadership of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisrael, 
may Hashem grant them long life.

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Bereishis,

...And continuing from the conclusion of your letter, where you note that you are writing at the time of your study of the holy Zohar, surely from the weekly portion, Parshas Bereishis:

The words of the Zohar (11b) are well-known: "Bereishis bara Elokim—this is the first of all commandments, and this commandment is called the fear of Hashem... fear is the foundation for a person to fear his Master, because He is Great and Ruler, the foundation and root of all worlds, and all before Him are considered as naught... it is called the beginning of **Da’as**... and this is the foundation and basis for all the other commandments of the Torah," etc.—see there at length.

Based on what is stated there, it is understood and also simple that there must be knowledge—in the language of the Zohar, "the fear of Hashem is the beginning of Da’as"—of how He is Great and Ruler, the foundation, etc. This is knowledge in the measure that the Torah calls "knowledge," which comes only through study in a manner of *kevi'us itim* (fixed times) for study, just like the study of any other part of our Torah, the Torah of life.

And this is the essence of the teachings of Chassidus Chabad, as is explained in many places, including the *Kuntres Limud HaChassidus* by my father-in-law, the Rebbe—see there at length.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that you bring good tidings regarding all of the above, and as the conclusion and seal of this letter of mine:

Indeed, *kevi'us itim* for the study of the inner dimension of the Torah, the words of the Living G-d, adds to the blessing of Hashem, the Source of Life, in whatever is needed for each and every one, of whom it is said: "And you who cleave to Hashem your G-d are all alive today."

## 8491

B"H, Thursday, Parshas Lech Lecha, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the congregation of Yeshurun, lovers and cherishers of Torah and mitzvos, may Hashem grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

As in previous years, this year as well—and specifically this evening—a gathering of the yeshiva’s activists took place as a beginning and introduction to the upcoming annual event for Merkaz HaYeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch, on the 22nd of Kislev, may it come upon us for good. On this occasion, I focused on the Parshas HaShavua, in accordance with the teaching of the Alter Rebbe, Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch—this year marking 150 years since his passing—that "a Yid must live with the times," meaning, according to the directives of the Parshas HaShavua. I would like to highlight here one of the points that was touched upon, and that is:

When the Ribono shel Olam said to Avraham Avinu, **"Your reward is very great"** (*scharcha harbeh me'od*), Avraham Avinu replied, how could he receive this reward if he was childless and his heir was Eliezer? In doing so, Avraham Avinu praised Eliezer highly as the one who managed his household, who led his battles, and who spread his (Avraham’s) Torah, as our Sages of blessed memory note regarding the words, "the son of the steward of my house" (*ben meshek beiti*).

Seemingly, it is difficult to understand why Avraham Avinu, while expressing his dissatisfaction with the fact that his servant Eliezer would be his heir, nevertheless praised him so highly. This is explained, however, by the fact that although Eliezer indeed possessed very great virtues, Avraham Avinu wanted his heir to be specifically his own son; otherwise, the **hemshech**—the continuation and eternalization of everything that Avraham represented—could not be secured.

This highlights that a person’s true reward is when all his achievements and accomplishments in his life are passed on and continued by his children and grandchildren; only then do all those achievements become perfected and possess true and lasting value.

It is the holy duty of every Yid and every Jewish woman to ensure that the great spiritual inheritance of Avraham Avinu is passed on and continued by the Jewish children. Every day, in the morning at the beginning of the day and at night at the conclusion of the day, we say in Krias Shema: **"And you shall teach them to your children"** (*v'shinantam l'vanecha*). This means that as a person begins the day, a Yid must remember the Divine command to provide for the chinuch *al taharas hakodesh* of the **children** and **students** (*Sifri, Va'eschanan*), and after finishing the day, one must first give an accounting of how one has fulfilled this duty.

Only a few weeks remain until the annual dinner of Merkaz HaYeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch. It has already been, B"H, many, many years that the Lubavitcher yeshivos and Lubavitcher students have been fulfilling the *v'shinantam l'vanecha* with great mesiras nefesh in all parts of the world. It is to be hoped that the yeshiva activists and lovers of Torah and mitzvos in general will also demonstrate mesiras nefesh—which in this case means simply *mesiras haratzon*, the good will to utilize these few weeks and strengthen their efforts for the upcoming annual event, which is one of the main pillars of the central Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch.

In the merit of this, every one of the workers and supporters will be privileged to have the Divine promise fulfilled: **"Your reward is very great,"** and in its most essential point—to have true Yiddishe nachas from one's own children and grandchildren *shichyu*, for long days and good years, in both material and spiritual matters together.

With respect and blessings for success and good tidings,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 8,292

8,292

B"H, 9 Menachem Av, 5724
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., Moreinu HaRav Shimon Moshe 
May he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Motzaei Shabbos regarding your acceptance of the position of Maggid Shiur at the Yeshiva Achat in Rishon LeTzion.

May it be the will of Hashem that you merit to succeed in raising students whom all who see them will recognize as the "seed blessed by Hashem."

The hint in this is: *Berech* (blessed) is related to *berichah* (a pool/reservoir) and *hemshech* (drawing down); *Hashem*—He who was, is, and will be as one; *seed*—that they should draw down into every place they are the "above nature" that exists within nature, to reveal the Elokus that is in the world, until it is as in this week’s Parsha: *E-l Olam* (G-d of the world), and not *E-l HaOlam* (G-d of the world [as a separate entity]), for the world is not an independent reality, and *kal v'chomer*.

And we have been promised that "he who comes to purify," and the precision of the Alter Rebbe—this year being the 150th year since his histalkus and hillula—is well known: that he is assisted in purifying others as well.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

***

 **Moreinu HaRav Shimon Moshe:** Diskin, Bnei Brak. Additional letters to him: see Vol. 18, 6,775.

 **Berech... and hemshech:** See Torah Or, Miketz 37c, and elsewhere. **Hashem... as one:** Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah, ch. 7 (82a). See Sefer HaMaamarim Melukat, Vol. 4, p. 3, and the references in note 8. **E-l... Olam:** See Likutei Torah, Tavo 42d, 43c; Hemshech Tzaach-Resh-Yud-Beis, Vol. 1, ch. 133, and elsewhere.

 **And we have been promised... precision:** Yoma 38b; Likutei Torah, Drushim for Shemini Atzeres 88b.

## 8,393

B"H, 10 Marcheshvan, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

The esteemed and elevated man of merit, Mr. Yitzchak David Bezalel, may he live and be well,

Shalom u’Bracha!

The chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned Rabbi Shmuel Pesach Bogomilsky, may he live, conveyed your regards to me upon his return from visiting your community. He also told me of the assistance and the gracious reception you extended to him during his visit. Many thanks to you.

It is my strong hope that the impressions and the hisorerus from Rabbi Bogomilsky’s visit will bear fruit in strengthening Yiddishkeit and the observance of Torah and mitzvos in your community. Surely, you are utilizing every opportunity to act and accomplish in this direction; for if this has always been the duty and privilege of every individual, it is all the more so in these days of ours, and in a place where there are not many who are engaged in the dissemination of Torah and Yiddishkeit.

May it be the will of Hashem that, since we have just come from the seventh month—which is saturated with all good, both physical and spiritual, the general month whose influence extends to all the months and days of the year, and whose Yomim Tovim conclude with Simchas Torah—that it should be so for you and for all the members of your community, may they live.

With blessings for good tidings.

#### ***8,393***

**Your community:** Kabul, Afghanistan.

**May it be the will:** See also above, Letter 8,381, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 8294

8294

B"H, 10 Marcheshvan, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants of the National Convention of Agudas Yisrael in the United States and Canada, may Hashem grant them life.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your notification and invitation to the national convention scheduled to open, with the help of Hashem, on Thursday of this week, I wish to express my wishes for the success of the convention. The essence of success is that it should bring forth fruit and the fruit of fruit in tangible actions and achievements, for "the deed is the essential thing." 

It is well known how our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch—this year being the 150th anniversary of his passing—emphasized that one must search—and if one searches, one finds—for guidance in the weekly Torah portion for the events of the week. In this week’s parsha, which corresponds to the day the convention opens, we are told of the birth of Yitzchak Avinu, which was above the natural order, and immediately thereafter, of the natural means that were necessary to employ in order to protect Yitzchak from negative influence. And in the Torah, the juxtaposition of matters is itself a teaching.

Indeed, there is no closer connection than that of the soul and the body, which are embraced and bound together, to the extent that the existence of the soul and the body in a Jewish person is one.

Regrettably, in every generation, there are those who rise up against us—some against the body and some against the soul. Both are equally evil, though there is a fundamental difference between them: as long as the body exists, there is the possibility of teshuvah. Conversely, the danger from our enemies of the soul is greater than the danger from our enemies of the body, since it is not always so visible to the naked eye, as is understood and is also simple. Furthermore, those who rise up against the existence of the body come from the outside, whereas those who rise up against the existence of the soul and the values of the soul come from both within and without—and the danger from within is more severe. We find this in the principle that "the deeds of the fathers are a sign for the children," as told in the parsha and in the Midrash regarding the trials of Avraham Avinu due to the schemes of Nimrod, Og, Avimelech, etc. Greater than these was the trial of sending away Yishmael and Hagar, for here the danger came from those who were in Avraham’s own household.

For this reason, even though Yitzchak’s birth was above the natural order, regarding his guidance and upbringing, Avraham could not rely on a miracle. He was forced to employ natural means—harsh measures, contrary to the nature of Avraham Avinu, which is the attribute of Chesed. Even though this attribute was the essence of his greatness and being, the Ribono shel Olam told him, "Do not be distressed, etc.," because (specifically through this) "through Yitzchak will your seed be called."

From here we derive the lesson that one must not be deterred by those who argue that for the sake of peace, or external unity, etc., one should remain silent and refrain from taking action, and certainly not engage in a defensive war—let alone an offensive war—against those who destroy and dismantle. This is not the case; on the contrary. It is a "time to act" to defend and to fight the "war of Torah," the Torah of truth—and truth means that there are no compromises. It is not enough to merely defend; one must, in the end, also rescue the wandering souls and place them on the path of truth, the path of Torah and mitzvos in daily life. And the primary point is to strengthen and expand the education of Jewish boys and girls on the basis of absolute purity—a true, traditional education without compromises.

May it be the will of Hashem that He grant them success in gathering strength for the war of Torah and its mitzvos, both a defensive war and an offensive war as mentioned above, even though it is through the ways of Torah, "whose ways are ways of pleasantness," in order to save the souls of Jewish boys and girls wherever they may be, for every single soul is an entire world. 

With respect and blessings for success.

## 8295

8295

B”H, 17 Cheshvan, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the G-d-fearing, distinguished, and learned Rabbi Shlomo שי' Lorincz,

Peace and blessing!

With much delay, I received your letter and the enclosure regarding the words of the Member of Knesset and your own speech. Thank you for your thoughtfulness in sending them to me.

Unfortunately, the latest troubles cause the earlier ones to be forgotten—at least in the public memory. I am referring primarily to the phenomena in Jerusalem, the Holy City, may it be rebuilt and established. Although surely everyone has already realized that the source of all these phenomena is one and the same, the astonishment is all the greater at the lack of an appropriate response. And if one were to say that it is not just lacking a little to reach one hundred percent, but rather much, much more than that.

It is simple that before my eyes is the teaching of the Mishnah, “Do not judge your fellow until you reach his place,” and I strive, based on the commandment, to “judge every person favorably,” and to repeat this again and again. But after all this, the difficulty still stands in its full force.

May it be the will of Hashem that, finally, Bnei Yisrael will come to correspond with one another solely regarding the elevation in holiness, from good to better, and so on. In the language of our Rabbeinu HaZakein, the Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch—this year being the 150th year since his passing—regarding the end of days, that “then the occupation of Torah and mitzvos will not be to refine refinements, but rather to unify higher unifications.” And indeed, even in the *ikvesa d’meshicha*, the end of the exile, even though we are still before the *aschalta d’geulah*, there must be something akin to this, just as it is the accepted custom of Yisrael that on Erev Shabbos one already tastes of the foods of Shabbos Kodesh.

With respect and blessing,

Enclosed is a copy of the General Letter for Rosh Hashanah, the content of which is relevant for the entire year, and I hope it will be of interest to you.

#### ***8295***

**General Letter:** See above, Vol. 22, Letter 8279.

## 8797

B"H, 24 Cheshvan, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Dr. Yosef Schechter, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge with many thanks receipt of the booklet "Jewish Studies in Secondary Education," as well as your article. It is my hope that in the future you will continue to send me your publications that you think might interest me.

Although I have not had the time to study the booklet as thoroughly as it deserves, I did see the space allocated to the chapter "Teaching Chassidus in Our Time." It is entirely insufficient relative to the importance of the subject, as the chapter itself begins by stating that much time and energy should be devoted to those chapters in our literature that **relate to the person in a personal way** (the author's emphasis). Yet these chapters, in a systematic and concentrated form, are found primarily in the literature of Chassidus.

There is another point that highlights the limitation of the aforementioned chapter even further: the subject is new to many teachers and has not seen much light in educational literature, whereas the content of several other chapters in the booklet has already been discussed in many books and at greater length. It is understood that my intention is, Heaven forbid, not to find faults; these words are said only with the hope that at the appropriate opportunity, the matter will be rectified, and the merit of the many depends upon it.

With respect and blessing,

I have requested my secretariat to send you some of our publications.

## 8,700

B"H, 26 Menachem Av, 5724
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write regarding a medical examination—apparently from some time ago—upon which the doctor based his statement that your wife, may she live, is supposedly unable to have children.

You do not write all the details regarding this. Since many new medical treatments have been discovered recently, and especially in the very last few years, it is appropriate that you consult once again with a specialist in this field and ask him whether any of the aforementioned innovations are applicable to your situation.

Since one is always in need of the blessing of Hashem Yisbarach—who is the Giver of the Torah and the One who commands the mitzvos—it is understood that one’s daily conduct must be in accordance with the instructions of our Torah, the Torah of life, and in the fulfillment of its mitzvos, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them." This is especially true regarding precision in observing the laws and statutes of *taharas hamishpachah* (niddah, *hefsek taharah*, immersion in a *mikveh* that is *kosher*, etc.). You should also clarify whether there is any lack of knowledge in this area that leads to a deficiency in their fulfillment (which should be clarified with a *moreh hora'ah*), as this is the path to receiving Hashem’s blessing, especially in the situation mentioned.

When you write the exact names of yourself and your wife, along with the mother’s name of each of you, in *Lashon HaKodesh*—as is the custom to mention in prayer—they will be mentioned in prayer regarding the aforementioned.

Regarding your question about my opinion concerning adoption: In most cases, the conduct with the adopted child is without revealing to him that he is not their biological offspring. In any event, the conduct toward him is as if he were their biological offspring, which leads to prohibitions regarding hugging and kissing (which are permitted only between children and their **biological** parents, and not those who take a child for upbringing). As for what is brought in the *sefarim* regarding raising an orphan in one’s home, it is understood that this is only possible if one is careful in the necessary manner regarding all of the above. This is one of the most difficult matters, and only when one is certain that they can be careful as required is there room to consider the question of adoption.

With blessings for good news in all the above.

P.S. In my secretariat, they do not write in French, and therefore the response is in *Lashon HaKodesh*. However, you may continue to write in French in the future, as I read that language.

## 8752

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Kislev, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, a man of the people who seeks the good of his people, a man of noble character, a scion of a noble lineage,
R' Schneur Zalman,
Shlita,

Greetings and blessings!

In connection with your birthday, I hereby join all those who bless you with long, good, and fruitful years. May it be the will of Hashem that you utilize all your potential for the strengthening of traditional Judaism and the dissemination of the wellsprings of Chabad, for by utilizing one’s talents and potential, they continue to increase and multiply. For the neshamah is in the image and likeness of the "Higher Man," and the body is a microcosm and reflection of the neshamah. We see in the body that the more one uses and exercises a limb, the more its strength develops and grows; the same applies to the powers of the soul. This is also true regarding the utilization of one’s potential—that one who utilizes them to their fullest is provided from Above with even more. And if you would say that this is the concept of "he who has one hundred, wants two hundred"—in spirituality, this does not mean a punishment that a person will never have spiritual satisfaction. On the contrary, since he has acquired "one hundred," he is granted a strong desire to acquire "two hundred," and there is nothing that can stand before such desire.

I have not yet replied to you regarding several points in your previous letter, including the matter of planting a forest in memory of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, etc. However, as I recall, this question arose during one of our conversations when you were here. At that time, I expressed my astonishment: when our religion and Torah embrace the entire world—the world in its literal sense, and the "small world" which is man, with all his affairs, details, and the details of those details, including both joyful events and those that are the opposite, chas v'shalom—why must we knock on the doors of others to find some foreign branch to plant in the vineyard of the House of Israel? Seemingly, I have not found for the time being any matter of planting a forest in someone's name, neither in the laws of Israel nor in the customs of Israel (and the custom of Israel is Torah), although there is the concept of erecting a building, such as the Hand of Avshalom and the like.

It is understood that what is recounted in the words of our Sages (Gittin 57a) regarding the planting of a cedar tree at the birth of a Jewish son or daughter, etc., is not of the same category as the aforementioned. Similarly, (Taanis 14b) and Shmuel B 18:18. Note also Peah, end of chapter 2. In any case, until I find a basis for the aforementioned, I refrain from expressing an opinion on this.

However, I know full well that there are many methods for fundraising, and many of them have no basis in the customs of Israel; in some of them, only a refined soul suffers, and the matter of planting a forest is no worse than those. On the contrary, there is benefit in this in the field of agriculture, etc. Nevertheless, considering the nature of the people of our generation, who, when they see something done and repeated several times, sanctify it—and not only that, but attribute to it an extra holiness—this, in my opinion, at the very least enters the category of "the dust of 'do not add'" (especially since in most cases, the results of transgressing "do not add" lead to transgressing "do not diminish").

Of course, I do not publicize my aforementioned position regarding the planting of trees in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, in someone's name, for it is not my concern at all to cause damage to a fundraiser, etc. This was one of the reasons I hesitated until today to write all of the above to you as well, but since you touched upon this matter in detail, I have put it in writing as mentioned.

— Although I did find in the Shas the concept of planting, and in abundance (Bava Basra 14a), and seemingly there is a connection to the aforementioned according to some commentators there—that through this one fulfills the mitzvah of settling Eretz Yisrael (although there it speaks of fruit-bearing trees, vineyards, unlike barren trees (Tamid 29b). Note also the Mishnah at the end of Arachin). And furthermore, our Sages of blessed memory spoke at length about such things in Midrash Rabbah, Parshas Kedoshim (25:3), but even this is not akin to the matter at hand: planting for the sake of a memorial for a specific person or a specific event.

2) It is understood that, in general, I was enthusiastic about the matter of a Chabad settlement in the vicinity of Tzfas-Meron, but for the time being, I lack all the details regarding this, and primarily regarding the type of people suitable to settle there who would be appropriate for the immigrants from Russia. Furthermore, Mr. Shlomo, may he live, Danchik, is utilizing his stay here for the sake of the current Kfar Chabad, "and one does not mix one joy with another." My hope is that in the not-too-distant future, I will again correspond with you on this point.

3) It is understood and also simple that I am interested in all the details regarding your home, your office, etc. It is surprising that you write that you are not sure if in Elul I would want to read about this in detail, for in such matters, on the contrary—a month that is the seal and summary of the passing year and a preparation for the month of Tishrei and the coming year is precisely the time suited for such matters. My hope is that I will read this in your future letters, and I will permit myself to add that in this, too, all the abundance and detail is to the good.

As we stand at the beginning of the month of Geulah, I will express my wishes for the redemption of the individual, the redemption of the collective, and the redemption of the "public, the population that is in Eretz Yisrael" (Berachos 58a). May it be the will that it happens in our time.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8757

B"H, Friday, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Beis Elokim V'zeh Sha'ar Hashamayim, 5724

Above all, this includes the halachos and dinim that pertain to daily life, in accordance with the fundamental principle of our Sages, of blessed memory, that the essential thing is the performance of mitzvos in practice.

It is surely known to all that the Alter Rebbe, Baal HaTanya v'Shulchan Aruch and founder of Chabad — for whom this year marks 150 years since his histalkus, and whose Yom HaGeulah, 19 Kislev, is near the time of your shul’s celebration — invested great effort to ensure that the shul — beis knesses and beis medrash combined — should stand at the necessary level in all respects: regarding the holiness of the shul, the nusach of tefillah, public shiurei-limud, and so on. In all generations, and especially in our time, the shul established on the purity of holiness is the foundation of all foundations for the fulfillment of Torah and mitzvos for the collective and for the individual.

May Hashem Yisbarach grant that it be fulfilled that the new shul should be, as mentioned above, "the house of Elokim and the gate of heaven" in all respects.

I send my greetings and blessing to all the members and mispallelim of the Beis HaKnesses D'Chassidim, and to all those gathered and participating in this great simcha shel mitzvah. May the Ribono shel Olam bless everyone, them and their households, with everything they need in both gashmius and ruchnius alike.

May we all merit the complete and true Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, very soon.

With respect and blessing.

## 8758

8758

B"H, 8 Kislev, 5724
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from 3 Parshas Vayeitzei,

Thank you for the good news regarding the doctor’s opinion concerning the health of your son, *sheyichyeh*.

Regarding why I did not answer concerning the Bar Mitzvah *seudah*: there is still plenty of time to decide on this. Furthermore, and most importantly, in such matters the decision depends on the local conditions and the individuals in your surroundings, etc. Therefore, you should consult with friends in your area as the time approaches.

However, the main point is that since Chazal have extolled the greatness of the day one reaches the age of *mitzvos*, and explained regarding it (Zohar Vol. III 101a) the verse "I have this day begotten you" (see also Zohar Chadash, Parshas Bereishis 10c, 15 bottom of side d), it is most appropriate that—regardless of what your decision may be—on this day that he becomes thirteen years old, the Bar Mitzvah boy should speak words of Torah and *hisorerus* at a gathering of at least ten adults. Following this, there should be a *legimah* (refreshments), for Chazal have said, "Great is a *legimah*, for it brings [people] closer," etc., and they should bless him with whatever he needs in both *gashmius* and *ruchnius*.

May it be Hashem’s will that you and your wife, the *rabbanit* *tichyeh*, derive much true *nachas* from him.

With respect and blessings for good news.

P.S. Regarding my previous letter concerning caution with cortisone: the same applies to other antibiotics. Although, naturally, the side effects are not the same for all of them, in any case, doctors have recently been expressing reservations about this and are seeking alternatives. One of the suggestions is to change the medication from time to time.

***

**Regarding the Bar Mitzvah seudah:** See also above, Vol. 22, Letter 8390, and the references in the notes there.

**Chazal have said:** Sanhedrin 103b.

**Regarding my previous letter:** Above, 8726.

## 8758

B"H, 9 Kislev, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned individual, engaged in communal work, etc.,
Rabbi Yitzchak Meir, may he live,

Shalom and blessings!

I received a letter from the Philipp Feldheim publishing house, accompanied by several pages from his book—a commentary on Pirkei Avos that is soon to be published—with a request that I write an evaluation of it. Enclosed is a copy of my response, the content of which is sufficiently explained therein.

I take this opportunity to express my wishes that you utilize the talents with which you have been gifted—as an energetic activist and an eloquent speaker whose words are matched by his heart and deeds, meaning in thought, speech, and action, as explained in the language of the Tanya Kadisha by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe (this year being the 150th anniversary of his passing)—to disseminate traditional Judaism in its purity, without compromise. Especially in our generation, a generation perplexed by the alarming blurring of boundaries, one must guard with even greater intensity the fences and boundaries established by our predecessors. I also wish you success in going from strength to strength in your activities for the sake of education in purity and holiness. May it be the will of Hashem that you do all this with joy and a good heart.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

For the sake of the matter, and in accordance with the words of our Sages, "Whoever wishes to be a Chassid should fulfill the words of Avos," I will note at least one or two comments regarding the pages sent to me.

Regarding the Mishnah: "Everything is foreseen, yet permission is given":

It is surprising that there is no reference to the Rambam, the definitive authority, namely the Yad HaChazakah, Hilchos Teshuvah. An entire chapter—chapter 5—is dedicated to this there.

Regarding the actual problem of knowledge and free will:

Seemingly, the crux of the solution is this: The contradiction to **free will** is **necessity**, not **knowledge**.

In other words, and by way of example: (If we were to imagine) a person who knows the future—his knowledge does not contradict the free choice of the person about whom he predicts that tomorrow he will perform a certain act, since the action does not come about because of the knowledge, but rather through his own choice. A second example: An expert psychologist knows how a person he knows well will behave in a few moments. This does not contradict the free choice of the person he knows. The difference between a moment and thousands of years is one of quantity, not quality.

The Ohr Sameach on the Rambam there collects several opinions in explaining this problem.

- A general note: I have always wondered why there is no caution exercised in writing and printing "G-d" rather than the full word (according to the Shach, Yoreh Deah, siman 179, se'if katan 11—this is the preferred way, and according to many Acharonim, even after the fact).

***

**Rabbi Yitzchak Meir:** Bunin. Another letter to him—above, Vol. 12, 3812.

**In the Tanya Kadisha:** Chapter 17. See also Kitzurim VeHe'aros LeTanya, p. 93.

**From our Sages:** Bava Kamma 30a.

**The problem of knowledge and free will:** See also above, Vol. 17, letter 5883; Vol. 3, letters 439, 442. Likutei Sichos, Vol. 7, p. 368.

**That there is no caution:** See also above, Vol. 9, letter 2775; Vol. 7, letter 1894.

With blessings for good tidings, and a happy 19 Kislev and Chanukah.

## 8,716

It is somewhat surprising that since your last letter, you have not written detailed letters, or letters in general.

With blessings for good tidings and with the blessing of the Chag HaGeulah,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
S.M. Simpson

## 5724

B"H, Erev 19 Kislev, the day of our redemption and the liberation of our souls, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the annual celebration of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Tmimim Lubavitch, may Hashem grant them life,

Peace and Blessing!

The annual celebration takes place this year shortly after 19 Kislev—the day of liberation of the Alter Rebbe, the Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch, the founder of Chabad, for whom this year marks 150 years since his passing.

It is therefore to be expected that all participants will come to this annual event filled with enthusiasm, which will be expressed in concrete actions to fulfill the financial needs of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Tmimim Lubavitch to the fullest extent.

In a well-known letter, the Alter Rebbe explains that the news of his liberation reached him at the moment he was reciting the verse in Tehillim (55:19): *Padah b’shalom nafshi*—"He has redeemed my soul in peace"—etc.

This instance of *Hashgacha Pratis* should certainly serve as a lesson for each and every one of us. For everyone requires a personal redemption from all the difficulties and obstacles in daily life that hinder one from achieving what must be achieved each day, both in *gashmius* and in *ruchnius*.

Our Sages, of blessed memory, explain the aforementioned verse in Tehillim with the following profound words: "The Holy One, blessed be He, says: Whoever occupies himself with Torah, with *gemilus chasadim*, and prays with the *tzibbur*, I account it to him as if he had redeemed Me and My children from among the nations of the world" (Berachos 8a).

With this, our Sages, of blessed memory, emphasize that the personal redemption of every Jew, and of the Jewish people together with the Holy One, blessed be He (kiviyachol), is directly connected to Torah, *gemilus chasadim* (*mitzvos* between man and his fellow), and *tefillah* (*mitzvos* between man and the Makom).

The annual event to support the Yeshivos Tomchei Tmimim Lubavitch provides an opportunity to have a share in all three of these things, which are unified within the Lubavitcher yeshivos: Torah—both *nigleh* and *pnimius haTorah*—which leads to *ahavas Hashem* and *yiras Hashem* (as the Rambam emphasizes at the beginning of Chapter 2 of *Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah*), and teaches the deeper meaning of "*tefillah b'tzibbur*"—gathering all thoughts and *kochot hanefesh* and uniting them with the Holy One, blessed be He, and with all Jews. Through *tzedakah* and *gemilus chasadim* for the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Tmimim Lubavitch, especially on the occasion of this annual celebration, each and every person becomes a partner in all three things that bring *geulah* and *pedus*, liberation and redemption, for the individual and for the collective. May the Holy One, blessed be He, help that each and every one should merit this to the fullest extent.

With respect and blessing for great success in all the aforementioned,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 8763

8763

B"H, 25 Kislev, 5724
Brooklyn

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, a man of character and many accomplishments,
Rabbi Chaim Yaakov, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 19 Kislev, a day of good tidings and a day of redemption, along with its enclosure.

Many thanks for the satisfaction you caused by sharing the good news regarding the developments at the teachers' seminary, etc. Surely, for someone like yourself, it is unnecessary to point out what is explained in many Chassidic texts: that every success of this kind widens the channel for even greater success, in accordance with the directive of Chazal to "ascend in matters of holiness". Furthermore, the directives of our holy Torah also provide the strength to do so, and this is well understood.

This is also the lesson of these days of Chanukah: that one must increase in light from day to day, without taking into account that the sun has set outside. On the contrary, precisely when the sun sets, the directive is renewed to increase in light—"a mitzvah is a candle, and the Torah is light," and the "light of the Torah" refers to the inner dimension of Torah.

There is another point here, based on the narrative of Chazal that the fighters in Israel did not destroy the oils, but rather defiled the oils in the Heichal. That is to say, the great danger is the illumination of light from "defiled oil," which is greater than the issue of a total lack of light. The moral lesson is surely understood.

With blessings for success in education on the foundation of purity and holiness, for a happy Chanukah, and for good tidings in all that was mentioned, with respect.

## 8,724

B"H, 27 Kislev, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants of the farbrengen of the Chag HaGeulah, 19 Kislev, in the city of Netanya, in our Holy Land—may it be built and established speedily in our days through Moshiach Tzidkeinu—may Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter conveying the good news of the aforementioned farbrengen on this day of tidings and day of redemption—the redemption of Rabbeinu HaZaken, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, which is also our own redemption and the deliverance of our souls.

As is well known, the saying of our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, is that the Torah of Chassidus and its matters are the inheritance of the entire Jewish people, of every single man and woman.

May it be the will of Hashem that, in accordance with the well-known words of Rabbeinu HaZaken, "The note that descended from the heavens, in the dew of lights, by the decree of the holy angels, in the secret of the holy fellowship, the students of our holy Rebbe: that which a Chassidishe farbrengen can accomplish, the angel Michael cannot accomplish," the blessing of Hashem will be drawn down in all that is needed for each and every one of you and your households, shlit"a, within the collective of our people, the Children of Israel.

Included in this, of course, is the continuation of the inspiration of the aforementioned day, which our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, described as a Rosh Hashanah for the entire year—a year blessed in both physicality and spirituality alike.

And may we proceed from the aforementioned redemption to the complete and true redemption, very soon, through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With respect and with the blessing of Chanukah,

**M. Schneerson**

***

**8,724**
Printed in Likutei Sichos, Vol. 15, p. 513.

**Saying:** See also above, Vol. 22, letter 8,737, and the references in the footnotes there. Below, 8,779.

**The well-known Iggeres HaKodesh:** Igros Kodesh, Vol. 1, letter 110.

**In the letter:** Igros Kodesh, Vol. 3, letter 784.

**Described it:** See the aforementioned Igros Kodesh.

**Day of tidings:** She'eilot U'Teshuvot Min HaShamayim, 60.

**Our redemption:** This refers also to the body, and not only the deliverance of our **souls** (similar to how the body of Admur HaZaken was also redeemed from imprisonment). This is understood based on the well-known Iggeres HaKodesh of Admur (Rashab) n"e, that the effects of this day relate also to "all our actions," including "matters of the world that are necessary for the sustenance of the body." And this is not the place to elaborate.

**According to the... well-known words:** Transcribed in a letter of my father-in-law, the Rebbe (in the collection "Amirat Tehillim").

**Within the collective:** See Zohar Chadash, Vol. 3, 33b: "A person should not separate himself from the collective" (and it must be said that regarding the matter of prayer—which is essential and more pertinent during a time of judgment—this is why there is no contradiction from Berachos 30a and Zohar Chadash 44b).

## 8725

8725

By the Grace of G-d, 27 Kislev, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

After a long interval, it was a pleasure to receive your letter along with the memorandum dated 19 Kislev attached to it.

It is my strong hope—even though you do not mention it—that you are aware of the significance of this day of good tidings, the liberation of the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, which is also our own liberation and redemption. Perhaps you even participated in the farbrengens held annually on that day, several of which take place in Jerusalem, the Holy City, may it be rebuilt speedily.

May it be the will of Hashem that this day influences all the days of your year, in the dissemination of traditional Judaism, our holy Torah—the Torah of truth—and the light of the teachings of Chassidus and its matters in particular.

It is understood that I read the aforementioned memorandum with interest. It appears that the issue of the calendar has once again been placed on the agenda of the international arena. May it be the will of Hashem that, at long last, our brethren, the Children of Israel, will not lend a hand to those who destroy matters of Judaism. This is especially true in light of what is known from Jewish history and hinted at in many places in the Midrashic teachings of Chazal: that were it not for the aforementioned cooperation, no outside hand would have power even over the material matters of the Jewish people, and certainly not over their spiritual matters. In the well-known phrasing: were it not for those who "emerged from you," there would be no room for destruction.

Indeed, these days of Chanukah teach this very lesson. Consider the Hellenists who championed the name of the prevailing "culture," arguing that the Jewish people should be like all the nations and imitate the deeds of the idolaters. If they were forced to maintain certain Jewish aspects—that is, Torah and mitzvos—they would study Torah (but only for the sake of wisdom and understanding). Their [sacrifice] was the introduction of a pig into the Temple, even up to the Altar. Regarding the *ner mitzvah*, they defiled the oils (though they did **not** destroy the oil), for on the contrary, their goal was that the Menorah be lit, but with impure oil, and so on.

To our great sorrow and regret, in our own era, which is full of trials, this matter still hovers among us—Hellenists of all types and shades, etc. It is difficult to elaborate on such a distressing matter, and I will leave it at that.

Incidentally (and surely you are aware of this as well), the imprisonment of 19 Kislev also came about solely because members of the Jewish people lent a hand, etc., as is well known. Together with this, the master of the redemption, our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, warns in his well-known Iggeres HaKodesh regarding the liberation and redemption—in his own words—about the abundance of kindness that Hashem has shown us, etc. Despite all this, one must not "let their heart become haughty above their brethren," etc. Perhaps, through this, Hashem will place it in the hearts of their brethren, "as water reflects the face," etc.

This has been the Chabad approach from the beginning: to draw them near to Torah and mitzvos (and not, Heaven forbid, by lowering the status of Torah and mitzvos), founded upon the love of a fellow Jew, which is one and the same with the love of Hashem and His Torah.

With respect and with blessings for a happy Chanukah.

## 8726

B"H, 29 Kislev, 5724
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 25 Kislev, the first night of Chanukah.

At an auspicious time, I will mention you at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for the fulfillment of your heart’s desires for the good.

It is my hope that you have established fixed times for the study of both the revealed Torah and Chassidus every day, with an increase on Shabbos, which is holy to Hashem. For this is also the path to receiving the blessing of Hashem in all that you require, and for your efforts in the natural realm to succeed, in accordance with the verse, "And Hashem your G-d will bless you in all that you do."

It is appropriate that you have your tefillin checked if this has not been done in the last twelve months, and I trust you are keeping up with the three well-known daily study portions of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S. It is surprising that you apparently do not recognize or see the contradiction within your own letter. Even a slight contemplation reveals how great is the power of the *sitra achra* (the enticement of the "old and foolish king"). I am referring to the beginning of your letter, where you mention that you were privileged to succeed in studying at the holy Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim, but that you "had to" leave the Yeshiva (and as mentioned, you do not recognize or question the fact that you "had to") in order to return to your parents. Yet, later in your letter, you inform me of the sequel: that upon leaving the Yeshiva after working for some time, you entered the army (which it is understood and simple to see was of no help to your parents, and served only to fulfill the departure from the Yeshiva). Following that, Heaven forbid, there was a car accident, etc., and from then until now you have been occupied with doctors and their treatments (which it is understood and simple to see that this, too, is of no help to your parents, but rather the opposite). After writing all of this **yourself**, you do not see the immediate conclusion: that not only should you not have left the Yeshiva, but you were obligated to study our holy Torah with persistence and diligence, to be meticulous in the performance of mitzvos, and to be a living example of this to your entire environment, especially to the young men among our Sephardic brethren. Not only would those unfortunate matters not have occurred, but this is the only way and channel for receiving the blessing of the Giver of the Torah, who is also the One who sustains and provides for all in His goodness, with grace, kindness, and mercy for the entire world.

And although one does not cry over the past, may it be His will that you now merit to succeed in publicizing among the youth of our Sephardic brethren (who, for various reasons, are not so accustomed to studying Torah in a yeshiva, except for a short time) that whatever the reasons were in the past, they have no place now. They should study in the great yeshivos for many years. Consequently, your words will emerge from the heart, from your inner self, and will enter the heart of the listener and achieve their effect. After all, these are the days of Chanukah, whose essence is to increase in the "candle of mitzvah and the light of Torah" from day to day, etc., and a word to the wise is sufficient.

## 8729

[Kislev 5724]

This is the opposite of the opinion of the Gra (Commentary to Mishlei 5:18, 7:12, 4:22, and especially 20:9; Commentary to Heichalos Pekudei 17, Tikkunei Zohar 107b, and elsewhere, **in many places**). It is the opposite of the opinion of R. Chaim Vital (in his introduction to Shaar HaHakdamos), the opposite of the opinion of Rabbeinu HaZaken, **and others.**

According to Torah law—in matters of monetary law, one must ask a Rav who is expert in monetary law and deals with them; in matters of forbidden and permitted, a Rav who deals with these laws (which is why the halacha follows Rav in matters of prohibition and Shmuel in monetary matters)—from which it is understood that regarding the inner dimension of Torah, the halacha follows those who are knowledgeable in this, etc.

## 8730

B"H, Chanukah, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the activists and friends of the Beis Rivkah schools in general, and to the participants in the twentieth annual banquet in particular,
May Hashem protect them and grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

This year’s annual banquet, which takes place only a few days after Chanukah, provides a brilliant opportunity to transform the inspiration of this luminous Yom Tov into practical action.

The lesson of lighting the Chanukah candles contains three fundamental points, which have a direct connection to the problems of our time and provide practical guidance:

(a) The Chanukah candles (which symbolize "the mitzvah is a candle and the Torah is light") must be lit when it is **dark.** This teaches us that one must not be discouraged by the "darkness" and spiritual poverty, because even a little bit of light from Torah and mitzvos dispels a great deal of darkness.

(b) The Chanukah candles must be lit in such a way that their light shines **outward.** This teaches us that one must not be satisfied with the fact that it is bright and warm at home with the light of mitzvos and Torah; one must also strive to bring light into the street and into the entire surrounding environment.

(c) The Chanukah candles are lit in a manner of **mosif v'holech** — with one additional candle each night of Chanukah. This teaches us that the work of strengthening and spreading Torah-Yiddishkeit must be in an **increasing** measure, and that this work itself contains the assurance of increasing success.

Our Sages, of blessed memory, emphasize that women—just like men—are obligated in the mitzvah of the Chanukah candle, because the women also had a share in the miracle of Chanukah. In this regard, the mesiras nefesh of the Jewish women of that time to protect the sanctity of the Jewish home and to keep the honor of Jewish daughters pure and unblemished is especially highlighted.

Today, more than ever, the demand of the hour is to educate Jewish daughters in the spirit of their historical role—as those upon whom the continuity of the Jewish way of life, and the very existence of our people, depends to a very great extent. And this was the purpose of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in founding the Beis Rivkah schools twenty years ago.

I wish to hope that each and every one will recognize it as a personal responsibility and privilege to support the Beis Rivkah schools, **mosif v'holech,** in an increasing measure.

Especially since this work and support are a channel to receive the blessings of the Ribono shel Olam, in an increasing measure, in everything one needs, materially and spiritually.

With blessings for outstanding success.

## 8731

B"H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Teves, 5724
Brooklyn

Rabbi, Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc., R' Sh. Z.
Shlita

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the second day of Chanukah. Regarding the points raised:

Enclosed is a copy of my letter to the *yishuvim* shluchim in accordance with your suggestion. I am certain that when you receive good news regarding this, you will inform me as well.

2) Regarding the forest, etc. — It seems they did not show him my actual letter. If a copy is found, please attach it to this letter of mine. In any case, the difficulties—that in a forest there is no issue of anything contrary to Torah and mitzvos—he himself also raised, noting that this is not the case, especially in a *shmittah* year. If the committee were to stand guard, the bitter reality in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) and abroad in such matters has shown that it is not the committee that decides, but rather the director, the official, etc. *V'dai l'meivin* (a word to the wise is sufficient).

3) Regarding the question concerning the settlement of Eretz Yisrael—since there is an agricultural benefit, etc.—I also noted this benefit in my letter. However, I pointed to *Maseches Tamid 29b*, which states that there is no mitzvah of settling Eretz Yisrael regarding non-fruit-bearing trees. As for your writing that we find there [a reference] to the memory of a certain person—I also addressed this in my letter, noting that this is indeed found, but only regarding **buildings** and the like.

This can be clarified according to what is explained in *Chassidus*, that building and a name, etc. (in the *Sefiros*), both relate to the *Sefirah* of *Malchus*, whereas vegetation and forests relate to *Ze'er Anpin*.

Many thanks for the brief report you provided regarding the *farbrengen* in Kfar Chabad.

Regarding the conclusion of that same paragraph concerning the title, etc.—the situation now is no longer in my hands (following the well-known letter on the aforementioned matter, which was written to the one who is already in the World of Truth, and thus the matter is closed). Furthermore, the main point is that he (our friend, shlita) should live long days in his position, and even more importantly, that he should utilize all his potential to the fullest for the desired purpose and intent. This is similar to what is explained in many places, and as is evident even in physical life, that through the use of a bodily limb, its strength and capacity increase—and how much more so through the use of spiritual powers. My intent is that through full utilization for the good, one’s ability and potential will grow, and we "ascend in matters of holiness."

It is clear that I am in complete agreement with you for having absolutely rejected the offer of the Chief Rabbinate. If, several years ago, the matter was not at all suitable for you, then certainly it is not so now, after the situation has deteriorated as mentioned, etc. There is no need to dwell on this painful matter, especially since it has reached not only (the sending of *mashgichim*—**representatives** of the Chief Rabbinate for Israeli ships (including those traveling for pleasure) on Erev Shabbos after midday) to *chillul Shabbos* (a silence that is publicized, and **publicity** acts as an admission—**and there is no one protesting**), and the drafting of women (at the very least an *avizarayhu*—an accessory—to *gilui arayot*), but also to the realm of *avodah zarah* (and would that it were only an *avizarayhu*), especially in these days in connection with their holidays, and the embracing, etc., etc., which are increasing in a strange and unusual manner in connection with the visit, etc. May Hashem protect us.

At a time of favor, I will again mention your brother, shlita. May it be Hashem’s will that his health condition be like the instruction of these days of Chanukah—an increase, until he returns to his full strength.

It is understood that the delay in the publication of Volume 11 (and 12, etc.) of the *Talmudic Encyclopedia* is regrettable.

With blessings for a bright and joyous Chanukah and for good tidings in all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8732

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Teves, 5724
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

A rumor has reached me—though it seems strange—that peace does not currently dwell among the staff of shochtim in your camp, and what is even stranger and more distressing is that it is specifically "among the shochtim of Anash."

If this rumor is true, chas v'shalom, then without entering into the reasons for the lack of peace or the potential claims each side may have against the other, it is understood and simple that first and foremost, a drawing together of hearts is necessary—and even more than just drawing together. For this is the great principle in the Torah of Ahavas Yisrael. See the wonderful (and, in its negation chas v'shalom, alarming) words on this subject in the maamar "Hechalzu" by the Alter Rebbe—this year being the 150th year since his histalkus and hillula—in Likutei Torah, Parshas Matos; in the mitzvah of Ahavas Yisrael by the Tzemach Tzedek in his Sefer HaMitzvos; and in the Kuntres Hechalzu by the Rebbe (Rashab), along with the addition there from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, ztzel, nbgm, zy"a. There is no need to elaborate on a matter that is both understood and simple.

Regarding the conflict itself, both sides can present their claims in writing and send them to the Rabbonim of Eretz Yisrael, tichyeh, from where the entire team of shochtim originated, or to a Beis Din there, with a request to express and instruct the Daas Torah on all that has been said.

May it be the will of Hashem that these written words, though few in quantity, will immediately take effect, and that peace will dwell in your camp. Furthermore, as is the prayer and hope of Bnei Yisrael, may the talmidei chachamim **increase** peace.

Through this, the blessing of Hashem will also increase, for the vessel that holds this blessing is peace, as our Sages stated in their Mishnah.

We are currently at the conclusion of the month that contains the Yom HaGeulah of the Alter Rebbe, which is also our redemption and the liberation of our souls. The Baal HaGeulah emphasized this, as he was comforted by the verse, "He has redeemed my soul in peace."

Awaiting good tidings.

***
