## 8734

8734

B”H, Zos Chanukah, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

A report has reached me that there are those who have a custom in their holy congregation at public gatherings (men and women), and especially before and after the chuppah at the wedding feast, where a woman also sings—whether she recites the established blessings or just a general blessing, but in any case, it is done with a singing voice.

The astonishment and wonder that this information has aroused in me is understandable, for the words of our Sages of blessed memory on this matter are well-known in many places (including the beginning of the Shas in Maseches Berachos 24a, and in the poskim), which negate the aforementioned practice absolutely and decisively.

The astonishment is even greater knowing the fondness for the holy Zohar among our Sephardic brethren, for even in the holy Zohar, Parshas Naso, in its Holy of Holies—the Idra Rabba Kadisha (page 142, side a)—they spoke at length in negation of the aforementioned matter.

And if this is the case in every place and situation, how much more so in public, and regarding a matter pertaining to the marriage of a son and daughter of Israel. In this regard, our Sages of blessed memory specifically emphasized that if a man and woman are worthy, the Shechinah dwells between them. [1] And all the more so at the very beginning and foundation of the matter—at the time of the erusin, kiddushin, and nisuin—when the foundation is laid for an eternal building, and the beginning of the wedding blessings is "He who created all for His glory," [2] and they conclude with many blessings for the chassan and kallah, and so on, until we say "where there is joy in His dwelling place"—in the dwelling place of Hashem, may He be blessed and exalted. Surely, there must be extra purity and extra holiness, to the point that it should be appropriate to the example (in the phrasing established by the Anshei Knesses HaGedolah in the aforementioned blessings) of "making Your creation rejoice as in the Garden of Eden of old" (before the first sin, etc.).

Furthermore, since the time is one exclusively for mercy, blessing, and kindness, then in addition to the negation of the matter absolutely in its own right, there is the added factor that the matter—in the language of the Idra Rabba Kadisha—is *dinin* (judgments) that spread through 248 paths. Moreover, their beginning is "the beginning of strife"—the voice of a woman. As our Sages of blessed memory state there: "It is taught... and the five *dinin* spread through 248 paths, and so it is taught: a voice [of a woman]... hair [of a woman]..." See there.

As we come from the days of Chanukah, which, in the words of the great teacher, our Rabbi the Rambam, at the beginning of Hilchos Chanukah, were a time when "they issued decrees... and laid their hands upon their daughters"—and the Jewish people sacrificed their lives for this, and they prevailed, and days of joy and Hallel were established from then until the end of all generations, for even when the [other] festivals are nullified, the days of Chanukah remain—my hope is strong that in this way, too, the matter will be rectified completely. And they, too (the women of his holy congregation), will be part of that rectification (see Rashi, Shabbos 23a, side a, s.v. *hayu*: "and through a woman the miracle was performed"), so that the aforementioned mitzvah gatherings will be fully in accordance with the statement of our Sages of blessed memory that wherever ten are gathered, the Shechinah rests—how much more so in the midst of many, many times ten. And it will be fulfilled that "there is joy in His dwelling place," and in the joy of the King of the world—He will bless and bestow upon each and every one an abundance of blessings from His full, open, holy, and wide hand.

With respect and regards to the administration of the holy congregation and the Rabbis—shlita—at their head, and with a blessing for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

***

[1] Our Sages emphasized: Sotah 17a.
[2] Regarding the statement of our Sages: Sanhedrin 39a.
[3] "He who created all for His glory": See Rashi, Kesubos (8a), s.v. *sameiach*: This gathering is for the honor of the Makom.
[4] "The joy in His dwelling place": See Bach and Beis Shmuel (Even HaEzer 62:11) that one does not say [the blessing] (and there is no joy) when the yetzer hara rules. And see Sdei Chemed—by the Chida—Asifat Dinim, Ma'areches Chosson v'Kallah (end of section 12).
[5] "The beginning of strife": The judgment of man (Kiddushin 40b).
[6] "The days of Chanukah remain": From the words of our Sages, brought in Sefer HaChaim, Part 3, beginning of section 27. And in many places. And see Ramban, beginning of Parshas Beha'aloscha, that the words of our Sages "The candles will never [be extinguished]" allude to the candles of Chanukah.

## 8735

B"H, Zos Chanukah, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the N'shei U’Bnos Chabad
May Hashem grant them life

Blessings and Peace!

As we take leave—until next year, G-d willing—of the luminous Yom Tov of Chanukah, I send this message and reminder to the N'shei U’Bnos Chabad, and through them to all Jewish women and girls, may they live: Although Chanukah is celebrated for no more than eight days a year, the content of Chanukah and the lesson of the *ner Chanukah* are valid for the **entire year.**

The moral of lighting the Chanukah candles contains three fundamental points, which have a direct connection to the problems of our time and provide practical guidance:

(a) The Chanukah candles (which symbolize *ner mitzvah v’Torah ohr*) must be lit *mishtishka ha’chama*, after sunset, when it is **dark.** This teaches us that one must not be overwhelmed by the "darkness" and spiritual poverty, because even a little bit of light from Torah and mitzvos dispels a great deal of darkness; and all the more so, a great deal of light.

(b) The Chanukah candles must be lit *al pesach beiso mibachutz*—so that their light shines **outward.** This teaches us that one must not be satisfied with the fact that it is bright and warm at home with *ner mitzvah v’Torah ohr*; one must also strive to bring light into the street and into the entire environment.

(c) The Chanukah candles are lit *mosif v’holech*—with one additional candle each night of Chanukah. This teaches us that the work to strengthen and spread Torah-Yiddishkeit must be in an **increasing** measure, and that this work contains within itself the guarantee of **increasing success.**

Our Sages, of blessed memory, emphasize that women—just like men—are obligated in the mitzvah of *ner Chanukah*, because *af hen hayu b’oto ha’nes*—the women also had a share in the miracle of Chanukah. In this context, special emphasis is placed on the *mesiras nefesh* of the Jewish women and girls of that time to protect the holiness of the Jewish home and to keep the honor of Jewish daughters pure and unblemished.

Today, even more than ever, Jewish women and girls must remember the special responsibility—and eternal privilege—that Divine Providence has placed upon them and gifted them: to continue and uphold the Jewish way of life upon the foundations and traditions of Torah and mitzvos in daily life.

As the *akeres habayis*, the Jewish woman is the **foundation** of the Jewish home.

Upon her, to a very great extent, depend the very foundations of Jewish existence: *taharas hamishpachah*, *kashrus*, the holiness of Shabbos and Yom Tov, the *chinuch* of sons and daughters—the entire structure of the home and of all members of the family, which is connected to the general continuity of the Jewish way of life in general, and the very existence of the Jewish people.

May the Chanukah candles, with their content of *ner mitzvah v’Torah ohr*, **always—every day, at every time, and at every hour**—shine within you personally and within your families, may they live, and as living and luminous examples for others as well.

May the light of Torah and mitzvos, permeated with Chassidic warmth and vitality, penetrate into all corners of your home, and spill over into the street as well.

Strengthen and expand your dedicated activity, according to the content-rich program of N'shei U’Bnos Chabad, to the fullest extent.

And may the Ribono shel Olam help that all of the above be carried out *mosif v’holech*, in an increasing measure, and that this should bring into your homes, and into the midst of all Klal Yisrael, Hashem’s blessings also in an increasing measure, in everything one needs, *b’bnei, chayei, u’meizona revicha*: true Jewish *nachas* from children, may they live, good health, and abundant *parnassah*, both in material and spiritual matters alike.

With blessings for great success and for good tidings regarding all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8,736

8,736

B"H, 9 Teves, 5724
Brooklyn.

Mrs. Zlata, may she live:

Blessings and peace!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from 3 Teves, as well as the previous one, to which you have surely already received a response.

Regarding what you wrote about the house, etc., and what more you can do—it is understood that the first priority (perhaps even more important than sending seforim) is that the house should be conducted with hachnosas orchim, especially hachnosas orchim that is connected with hachnosas kallah or hafatzas hamaayanos, etc. Since a Jewish woman is the *akeres habayis*, it is understood that Hashem Yisborach grants the strength to carry this out in a good way (notwithstanding the fact that you are correct that it is not the same as before). For in spreading goodness, one receives special assistance from Above. It is surely unnecessary to elaborate that this is one of the ways—and one of the highest ways—to provide nachas ruach for the neshamah and to act for the *ilui haneshamah*.

May Hashem Yisborach help you to act in this with more energy and in good health, and ultimately Hashem Yisborach will bless you so that it will be with a good heart, and also with nachas and joy from your descendants, may they live...

8737

B"H, 9 Teves, 5724
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos, 8 Kislev.

I believe I wrote in my previous letter as well that I am not familiar with the details of the incident itself that you wrote to me about, and which you also mention in your letter. There is no point in intervening in such matters from a distance, especially in Jerusalem, the Holy City, where there are many rabbis present. The entire point of the letter was that there is absolutely no place for bringing complaints to anyone before inviting the person in question to a Rav (or a Beis Din) in Eretz Yisrael—may it be rebuilt and established—and preferably in Jerusalem, the Holy City, itself. You should present all your claims there, and they will instruct you in the Da'as Torah regarding this. If the other party refuses to appear before a Rav, etc., then (as is the custom in Yisrael) you will receive a *kesav siruv* (a letter of refusal) against that person from the Rav, as well as instructions on whether you are permitted to bring your claims elsewhere. For regarding every Jew, and especially for Anash who are educated in the ways of Chassidus according to the paths of our Rebbes, our holy Torah is a *Toras Chaim*—a guide for daily life and for all the details of a person’s life, both in matters between man and Hashem and between man and his fellow. No person should take the law into their own hands; on the contrary, when one is convinced in his own eyes that he is in the right, there is all the more reason for extra caution in this, and this is well understood. Our **holy** Torah is also a Torah of **life**—true life.

In writing your letter during the days of Chanukah, when the war of the Greeks was not against the **wisdom** of the Torah, but rather "to make them forget Your Torah" (which is the holy Torah of the Ribono shel Olam), and similarly regarding the mitzvos, to force them to abandon the mitzvos which are called "the statutes of Your will"—and Bnei Yisrael sacrificed their lives for these points, without considering calculations based on intellect, etc., and they succeeded in this conduct until the matter was established for all generations—this is a lesson for every single person within all of Yisrael: that (in the language of the verse) "If you walk in **My statutes**" (and Chazal explain that you should be **toiling** in Torah), etc.—and specifically through this, "I will give your rains in their time," etc., the blessing of Hashem in everything a person needs, from His full, open, holy, and generous hand.

Due to the importance of the matter of peace, etc., this letter is sent as urgent.

At a time of favor, may you be remembered for the fulfillment of your heart's desires for the good in all the matters you write about, and first and foremost—for a good shidduch very soon, in all its details.

With blessings for good tidings in all that was mentioned.

**M. Schneerson**

## 8,738

8,738

B”H, 10 Teves, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

May it soon be transformed into joy and gladness.

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter from some time ago—the reply to which was delayed until now for various reasons—in which you write about your feelings regarding a potential shidduch with a certain avreich, may he live, and the reasons for and against it.

What is not sufficiently clear in your letter is whether the feelings you describe are stable, or if it is possible that this is merely a passing mood. One of the ways to test this is to see how you are affected by a break from seeing and meeting with the avreich; during such a time, you would be able to evaluate the matter and your feelings more objectively.

If, during the time you were physically apart, you nevertheless corresponded frequently, you should at least now take an appropriate break from all contact, including writing, and observe the result.

If the relationship is stable on both sides—yours and the avreich’s—then you can explain to him what he needs to do to address the negative factors, such as the matter of learning Torah with diligence and persistence **now**. Surely, over the course of a few weeks, he will be able to discern for himself whether he can maintain this lifestyle, etc.

2) Regarding the opposition of [family/others], etc.—if the examination and the results, based on what is explained above, are definitively positive, the aforementioned opposition will surely diminish on its own. You can also ask friends to speak with them to explain the situation, etc.

May it be the will of Hashem, who oversees every individual with Divine Providence, that He guide you toward what is good regarding the most essential matter mentioned above, and in all your affairs.

With blessings for good tidings.

#### ***8,738***

**One of the ways to test this:** See also above, Vol. 14, Letter 5,085; Vol. 12, Letter 3,941.

## 8,739

B"H, 11 Teves, 5724
Brooklyn

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter—which arrived after a long delay—in which you write the main points of the history of your life and that of your family, may they live.

When you provide the names precisely in Lashon HaKodesh, along with the mother’s name for each (as is the custom when mentioning them in prayer), they will be mentioned at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for the fulfillment of their heart’s desires for the good in all the matters you write about.

Regarding what you write about the lack of complete joy: it is surprising, for it is surely known to you and your husband, may he live, that trust in Hashem Yisbarach—the Creator of the world who leads it even now—is one of the foundations of our Torah, the Torah of life, and that Hashem is the essence of good, and it is the nature of the Good to bestow good.

However, one’s conduct in daily life must be in accordance with the instructions of our Torah, the Torah of life, and the fulfillment of its mitzvos, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them," for we have been commanded in this by the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He.

As for your writing that you desire more children, but there is a financial question: this, too, apparently stems from the fact that your level of bitachon is not complete. Even though you surely say from time to time what has been accepted and passed down from generation to generation—that Hashem Yisbarach sustains the entire world with His goodness, with grace, with kindness, and with mercy—nevertheless, in your specific case, according to the first mitzvah in the Torah (and even the order of the Torah is itself Torah), you are obligated to be fruitful, etc. Regarding the mitzvah of Hashem and the request of Hashem, it is as the Sages said: "I do not ask [of them] except according to their ability."

It is my hope that these few lines will suffice to clarify the situation as it is, and that with a little contemplation, you will arrive at the decision to conduct yourselves in the direction mentioned above, and with joy and a glad heart.

It is appropriate that you have your husband’s tefillin checked, and that every weekday, before putting them on, he should set aside a few coins for tzedakah. You should observe the good custom of kosher daughters of Israel to set aside tzedakah before lighting the candles every Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 8,440

B"H, 11 Teves, 5724
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the 10th of Teves—may it soon be transformed into gladness and joy—in which you write the main points of your life story and conclude regarding a shidduch, etc.

Generally, in matters of shidduchim, one must be precise about the essential point: that she be suited to what is written, "A woman who fears Hashem, she shall be praised." We have no business with signs, omens, etc., such as those you write about.

Rather, the primary conduit and vessel for receiving Hashem’s blessing is conduct in daily life that conforms to the instructions of our Torah, the Torah of life, and the fulfillment of its mitzvos, regarding which it is said, "And he shall live by them." Increasing in this adds to Hashem’s blessing; for in matters of goodness and holiness, regardless of how good the situation may be, there is always room to add, since we are connected to the Holy One, Blessed be He, who is infinite.

It is appropriate that you have your tefillin checked—if this has not been done in the last twelve months—and that each weekday, before putting them on, you set aside a few coins for tzedakah. Likewise, you should keep the takkanah of reciting the monthly Tehillim—as the Tehillim is divided for the days of the month—every day after morning davening.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 8741

B"H, 13 Teves, 5724
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing man, a man of many accomplishments, possessing fine character traits, etc.,
R' Nissan, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter, which brings the good news regarding the publication of the third edition of your book, *Taharas Mayim*.

May it be the will of Hashem that the printing be completed in a good and auspicious hour, and may the will of Hashem succeed in his hand to disseminate the observance of the purity of the daughters of Israel—*taharas mayim*—for "water" refers only to Torah, in accordance with the instruction of our Torah, the Torah of life.

And as per the instruction of the days of Chanukah, from which we continue to draw, may this spread and be accepted throughout all the dispersions of the Children of Israel, to conduct oneself as *mehadrin min hamehadrin* (the most meticulous), in accordance with what is brought in the *poskim* to be meticulous regarding the *mikveh* as much as possible, in order to fulfill the opinions of our Sages.

And if this instruction applies in all places and at all times, how much more so in this generation, the footsteps of Moshiach, the end of the exile. Immediately upon the conclusion of this period comes the instruction that purity leads to, etc., Eliyahu the Prophet, remembered for good, the herald of the Geulah, and the fulfillment of the prophecy, "And I will sprinkle upon you pure water, and you shall be purified." For the attribute of the Holy One, Blessed be He, is measure for measure: that through the *mikveh* which purifies, etc., the Holy One, Blessed be He, also purifies Israel, in the true and complete Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With respect and with blessings for success in the aforementioned, for long days and good years.

***

**His book *Taharas Mayim*:** See also below, ibid.

**Spread and be accepted:** *Rema*, *Orach Chaim* 671:2.

**Comes the instruction:** *Sotah*, at the end.

**His attribute:** *Pesikta Zutarta*, *Shemos* 3:6.

**The *mikveh* purifies:** *Yoma* 85b, in the *Mishnah*.

## 8442

8442

B”H, 15 Teves, 5724
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 12/25, in which you write about your son, may he live, regarding what you heard from him concerning his outlooks, etc., and the impression this has made on you and your wife, may she live.

We see that often, more can be accomplished through friends than through parents. This is provided that the friends speak words that come from the heart, which enter the heart of the listener and perform their effect. Naturally, this comes in addition to your own words and those of your wife, may she live.

Regarding this matter, there is another approach: since, as you write, he is still single, it is appropriate to endeavor to find (in a suitable manner, so that he does not suspect us of forcing him) a shidduch with a daughter of Israel who is observant of Torah and mitzvos and fears Hashem, and who is firm in her mind and outlook in this regard. For then, there is room to say that in addition to her influence, the shidduch itself may influence him to forget the negative matters and negative thoughts, etc.

Since, according to what is brought in the holy sefarim, the laying of tefillin has a special influence on the mind and the heart—that is, on the intellect and the emotions—it is appropriate to make the utmost effort that your son should lay tefillin every weekday, at least for a short time on his head and arm. However, the tefillin must be checked and kosher. And it is good that before laying them, as mentioned, he should set aside a few coins for tzedakah.

And since such thoughts often come to one who was born at a time when the parents were not precise in the exact observance of taharas hamishpachah (niddah, hefsek taharah, immersion in a kosher mikveh, etc.) [due to a lack of knowledge of all the details, which leads to a deficiency in fulfillment, a matter which should be clarified with a rav who is a moreh hora'ah], if this was indeed the case, G-d forbid, there must be teshuvah for the above: regret for the past and a good resolution for the future to be precise in this as much as is required. One should also endeavor that their friends and relatives be careful in this mitzvah, especially within the context of general conduct in daily life, so that it is consistent with the instructions of our Torah, Toras Chaim, and the fulfillment of its mitzvos, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them."

At an auspicious time, mention your son, may he live, at the holy tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all that has been mentioned.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S. It is appropriate that you have his (the writer's) tefillin checked, as well as the mezuzos in your home, to ensure they are all kosher according to law. And your wife, may she live, should maintain the good custom of kosher daughters of Israel to set aside tzedakah before lighting the candles every Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov.

In my secretariat, we do not write in French, which is why the response is in Lashon Kodesh. However, he may write in French, as I am able to read that language.

#### ***8442***

**What is brought in the sefarim:** See Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim, Laws of Tefillin, 25:6; Shulchan Aruch of the Alter Rebbe, ibid., 11; Tanya, Chapter 40 (56b).

## 8,443

8,443

B”H, 15 Teves, 5724
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write about a proposal for a shidduch that is pleasing to both parties, etc., and that the only issue is financial, primarily on the part of the parents of the young man, may he live.

In such a situation, the direct path is to find friends of theirs who can influence them. Especially since, even according to simple, sound logic, there is no room at all for a matter of a few thousand liras to take precedence over a fundamental matter, etc., which is called a *binyan adei ad* (an everlasting edifice).

You do not mention in your letter where they wish to establish their home. The differences in the price of apartments in various locations in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, are very significant. Perhaps establishing the home in a different location than the one discussed would solve the aforementioned problem, or at the very least, diminish it. Naturally, I am referring to a place where those who observe Torah and mitzvos reside, for that is something that cannot be compromised.

Your dedication and commitment to the work of Heaven—the education of the children of Yisrael, and specifically in the Chabad school named after my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisrael—at whose holy gravesite you should mention this, will stand you in good stead for all of the above.

With blessings.

## 8745

B"H, 17 Teves, 5724
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings,

In response to your letter of 12/30 with the enclosure, in which you write regarding your son, *sheyichyeh*, and the thought he shared with you.

It is understandable that this is the greatest misfortune, *R"L*, that could possibly occur: for a Jew to be thinking, as you write, about a *shiksa*. One must do everything possible to prevent this misfortune. The primary obligation lies with the parents, especially since this is an eternal misfortune—not only in *Olam HaZeh* but also in *Olam HaBa*. If parents do everything to protect their children from harm in this world alone, how much greater must the effort be to prevent a misfortune—the greatest one—in both worlds.

I do not wish to elaborate on such a deeply painful matter, where such actions effectively assist Hitler—*yimach shemo*—whose goal was for there to be as few Jews as possible; this is the path that leads to that. One must hope that by acting with the proper effort, together with deep *tefillah* to Hashem Yisbarach from everyone who is interested in the true good of your son, *sheyichyeh*—and first and foremost, naturally, the parents and those closest to him—it will lead to safeguarding and preventing this greatest misfortune that he himself wishes to bring upon himself, *chas v'shalom*.

May Hashem Yisbarach help you to report good news, just as you have brought the news regarding this deep pain.

You should have your *tefillin* checked, as well as your son’s, *sheyichyeh*, and the *mezuzos* in your home, to ensure they are all *kosher* according to the *din*.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,
Secretary

***

**With such actions:** See also *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 26, p. 376.

## 8746

B"H, Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Shemos, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students of the holy Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim in Eretz Yisrael, may Hashem protect them,
May they live,

Greetings and blessings!

Following up on my previous message, I am referring to the transmission of the content (at the very least) of the *maamarim* and *sichos* that were delivered here during the days of the seventh month—which is "satiated with all good" and provides satisfaction for the entire year—which I requested the guests from Eretz Yisrael to convey to you specifically.

It is my hope that they were transmitted as they should be—that is, in words that come from the heart.

I am writing this now as well (at least in brief)—and surely this was not necessary except for the sake of preference, extra alacrity, and being even more careful—to urge you regarding the point of the *maamarim* and *sichos* as it pertains to your actual *avodah* and the "therefore" (*uvchein*), which is:

An increase in persistence and diligence in the study of the revealed Torah and Chassidus;

An increase in *yiras Hashem* and *ahavas Hashem*;

—This requires an increase in *hisbonenus* in the matters of the teachings of Chassidus, in accordance with the ruling of the Rambam (*Yesodei HaTorah*, end of chapter 2): "This honored and awesome G-d, one is commanded to love and fear Him, etc. And what is the path to His love and fear? At the time that a person **contemplates** His deeds, etc., and sees from them His **wisdom**, etc., and develops a great desire **to know** the great Name, etc., immediately he..."

And in order for this love and fear to come into actuality, and even to the point of practical deed, this is the *avodah* of *tefillah*, as is explained at length (and the methods for this for each individual) in *Kuntres HaTefillah*, *Kuntres HaAvodah*, and in many other places.

Furthermore—and this is also essential—to do everything within your ability and possibility to increase the number of students in the yeshivos, first and foremost by being a living example, so that everyone will want to be like you.

And also by speaking words that come from the heart, to influence your friends and acquaintances to enter the "four cubits of Torah" and the "four cubits of *tefillah*" together, in the manner of our Sages' teaching: "Hashem loves the gates of Zion"—the gates that are distinguished in *halacha*, the study of Torah, and (the study of the *avodah* of *tefillah*, which leads to) the *avodah* of *tefillah*.

Words that come from the heart enter the heart, and ultimately, they accomplish their effect.

And all of this—the influence upon others—is among the essentials of *avodah*, for "there is no *avodah* like the *avodah* of love," as our Sages taught: "And you shall love Hashem your G-d"—make Him beloved upon all creatures, etc., "with all your soul"—love Him until the exhaustion of the soul.

See the *Iggeres HaKodesh* of our Alter Rebbe (at the beginning), where he brings this opinion as a practical *halachic* ruling.

This activity also adds to one's success in the study of the revealed Torah and Chassidus and in the *avodah* of *tefillah*, as our Sages say regarding the verse, "Hashem will illuminate the eyes of both of them"—the light of the King’s countenance is life.

And if in all *mitzvos* the great virtue of alacrity is known, as it is stated and repeated in the words of our Sages, how much more so regarding the aforementioned—the study of Torah, the *avodah* of *tefillah*, and *tzedakah* (spiritual *tzedakah* with one's fellow, to bring him into the "four cubits" of *tefillah* and Torah)—the fruits of which a person consumes in this world, while the principal remains for the World to Come.

With blessings for success in this holy *avodah*, the study of our holy Torah, the *avodah* of *tefillah* (which is in place of a *korban*), and the *avodah* of *tzedakah* (which is equal to all the *korbanos*)—and especially when all this is done in Eretz Yisrael, the Holy Land.

—Awaiting good tidings from the actions of each one of you in all that has been stated, and of your success in this.

Especially in accordance with the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe: "Every individual is a *rabim* (a multitude)."

—And we are standing before the 24th of Teves, the *yom hilula* of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, the *Baal HaTanya*—the *posek* in the hidden aspects of Torah—and the *Shulchan Aruch*—the *posek* in the revealed aspects of Torah—our *Nasi*, and "the body follows the head"—

I conclude with a blessing to go from strength to strength and to ascend in holiness.

**M. Schneerson**

## 8798

8798

B"H, 24 Teves, 5724
- The Yahrtzeit of Rabbeinu HaZaken - Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and upright individual, engaged in the needs of the community, etc., R' Menachem Ben-Tzion, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from the 10th of Teves—may it soon be transformed into joy and gladness—and those preceding it.

Enclosed is a copy of my letter to the students [T'—Talmidim] in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily, which I am certain they will utilize as appropriate. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding this as well.

Wishing a complete and speedy recovery to your wife, may she live and be well, and to your children, may they live and be well, and looking forward to good news regarding communal matters as well,

**M. Schneerson**

Regarding your question about the colors in the illustration of the Aleph-Beis, etc.—do whatever is most effective in terms of engaging the students, may they live and be well.

For in the Middle Ages, several books were printed—among them *Rosh Chodesh*—where every page was a different color (for aesthetic purposes).

And as for one who desires only black, so that it might evoke *STaM* [Sifrei Torah, Tefillin, and Mezuzos] and the like (and see *Shir HaShirim Rabbah* on the verse "black as a raven"; see also the *Gilyon Maharsha* to *Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah*, beginning of section 271)—well, on the contrary, we find **distinct** colors in the stones of the *Choshen* and the *Ephod*. And see *Yoma* 37a.

#### ***8798***

Published in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 11, p. 320, and completed based on a photocopy of the letter.

**R' Menachem Ben-Tzion:** Wilhelm, Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt speedily. Additional letters to him appear above, Vol. 21, 8118, and in the references noted in the footnotes there.

**My letter to the students:** Above, 8796.

## 8,450

8,450

B"H, 27 Teves, 5724
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned individual, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Yitzchok, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 14 Teves, along with the enclosed minutes from the meeting of the directors, etc.

It is surprising that in all the back-and-forth discussion, no one noted the reason for the lack of success in previous years regarding the 10 Shevat gathering. After all, success in the future depends on eliminating the cause, and as was written in previous years, the cause was twofold:

a) And this is the main point: the lack of communication between the school directors for various and strange reasons.

b) And this is secondary, and apparently comes as a result of the first cause: a lack of funds for expenses.

Another point that is not understood in the minutes is that there is no mention at all of the esteemed Rav and Chossid, R' D. Ch., may he live—even though regarding several efforts, lobbying in offices, and financial matters, they turn to him once or twice, etc., and demand from him, claiming that the entire network rests on his shoulders and is his responsibility.

It is understood that the purpose of 10 Shevat is not for trips for the sake of a trip or the like, especially since this also involves bitul Torah; there must be some spiritual reward, not just mere pleasure (taanug), which is related to the word *helem* (concealment) and *hester* (hiddenness).

Another point—and this too is surprising—is that it was not mentioned at all that this year 10 Shevat falls on Erev Shabbos, and there must be sufficient time for *ratzo v'shov* well in advance after the gathering. Perhaps the intention was to hold it on the eve of 10 Shevat.

Since it appears from the above that the minutes were written or the discussion was held in haste, I will await the continuation or clarification of the above before I respond to the essence of your question.

As per your request, the letter is being sent via express mail.

With blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

***

**8,450**

**R' Yitzchok, may he live:** Ginsburg, Kfar Chabad. Additional letters to him—above, Vol. 22, 8,391, and in the references noted there. Below, 9,016.

**R' D. Ch.:** Rabbi Dovid, may he live, Chanin.

## 8752

8752

B"H, 11th of the month, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter.

We stand but a few days before the yahrtzeit of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, which is a day of ascent from level to level, as hinted at in many places and explained in the writings of the Arizal.

Since, according to the words of the Alter Rebbe (in his Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 27, and its explanation), through hiskashrus to the tzaddik—and "a tzaddik who has departed is found in all worlds even more than during his lifetime"—a spirit awakens a spirit and draws down a spirit: spiritual life, thoughts of teshuvah, and good deeds, as well as matters of this world.

It is understood from this that the ascent of the tzaddik brings about an ascent for all those whose spirit he draws down, an ascent in spiritual matters and in worldly matters.

And whoever is closest—through strengthening oneself and increasing one’s efforts in walking the straight path he taught us, and walking in his ways—is first in line for the blessing.

This is especially true regarding a tzaddik who is a Nasi of Klal Yisrael, who, while living on the face of the earth, conducted himself with the love of a father for his children toward every single Jew, concerned for their affairs of this world and their affairs of the world to come, in a relationship and hiskashrus of Rebbe and Chossid, to the point of the manner of "the luminary and the light"—an internal and essential hiskashrus.

With blessings for a good month and good tidings from a meaningful yahrtzeit-farbrengen, both at its appointed time and throughout the coming year.

**Menachem Schneerson**

***

And since **because of this** I have received unfavorable reports regarding the arrangements there, etc., it is my duty to urge and reiterate this, and you, sir, were the intermediary, etc.

## 8758

8758

B"H, Erev the Yom Hilula of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished, G-d-fearing, and learned bochur, one who seeks the good of his people, a man of noble character, a scion of a noble lineage,
R' Schneur Zalman
Shlita

Shalom u’Bracha!

As we approach the Yom Hilula, an *eis ratzon* (time of favor), it is my desire, as is my custom, to renew and strengthen the connection between us, at the very least in writing.

The day of a Tzaddik’s passing is a day of *segulah*, as explained by our Alter Rebbe in Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 27, and its commentary. After the passing, once the limitations imposed by the body have been removed, the connection with the *Tzaddika d’atpatar* (the departed Tzaddik) is on a much higher level, both in spiritual matters and in worldly matters—and "whoever is closest is first to receive the blessing."

You, shlita, have merited to know my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, both as an Admur and in both worldly and spiritual matters, ever since the visit of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. As I recall, you told me that, on the contrary, the beginning was when you heard a *maamar* of Chassidus from him for the first time then. And even though, according to your words, the matter was at that time in the category of *makif* (encompassing light), the Nesi’im of Chabad have explained that a *maamar* of Chassidus reaches the soul in all five of its levels—*nefesh, ruach, neshamah, chayah, yechidah*—and the *yechidah* within the soul is the true essence of the *makif*.

And based on what the *baal hahilula* writes in his holy *sicha* of 19 Kislev (5693, section 17), these five levels of the soul correspond to the four worlds of *Atzilus, Beriah, Yetzirah, Asiyah* and the worlds of *Ein Sof* that are above *Atzilus*, for a Jewish person is a complete world, encompassing all five of these worlds.

And the *yechidah* within the soul is a *makif* that penetrates to the ultimate inwardness, down to the "heel" of the soul and the "heel" of the body.

May it be the will of Hashem that the merit of the *baal hahilula* (including the Chassidic interpretation of this—the refinement he effected) stand for each and every one in whatever they require.

With respect and blessing.

On this occasion, I wish to express my thanks for the *pidyon nefesh* sent through Rabbi Helevitz and Rabbi Gorodetzky, shluchim, including the inner *nachas ruach* from the point of the *pidyon nefesh* that you sent me, which—as it was conveyed to me—"stood the test in connection with the well-known visit." And may we conclude with good.

***

8758

## 8760

8760

B”H, 15 Shevat, 5724
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, involved in communal needs,
R’ Ephraim Eliezer, may he live, HaKohen

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 13 Shevat, as well as the previous one from 5 Shevat with its enclosure.

Many thanks for sending them to me; they are returned herewith, after I copied the excellent words of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, whose yahrtzeit we observed on 10 Shevat and from whom we draw our guidance.

I was particularly impressed by what I found at the conclusion of the matter, that within the four amos closest to the summit of the mountain, one feels, etc.

Based on what was discussed at the farbrengen, this is founded upon the halacha regarding how four amos acquire [property/space]. This is even more significant than standing behind a wall, for a wall acts as a partition—even when it has gaps, it partitions in many respects—whereas this is not the case with four amos. And the rest is understood.

Regarding your mention of the version of the name Rava with an aleph: I believe I explicitly mentioned at the farbrengen that this is indeed the case in Yalkut Shimoni (42, 3) and Pesachim (117a), and one should examine the Dikdukei Sofrim for further references.

With blessings regarding the significance of this day, the Rosh Hashanah for trees, for man is the tree of the field, and especially a Torah scholar (Taanis 7a).

#### ***8760***

**R’ Ephraim Eliezer:** Yalles, Philadelphia. Additional letters to him: above, Vol. 22, 8288, and the references in the notes there.

**At the farbrengen:** Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Beshalach, 11 Shevat.

**Within the four amos... one feels, etc.:** See also below, letter 8972.

**Halacha... acquire:** Bava Metzia 10a.

**The version of Rava:** In Tanya, Chapter 7 (11b): "Just as Rava did for his students, when he would first say a humorous remark before them, and the Sages would be gladdened." See also Likut Perushim l’Tanya there.

## 8762

B"H, 15 Shevat, 5724
Brooklyn

The Administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, Jerusalem branch
The Holy City in our Holy Land, may it be built and established speedily in our days through Moshiach Tzidkeinu
May Hashem grant them life

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letter from Erev the Yom Hilula of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisrael, in which you write that you have been elected to the aforementioned administration, and of your desire and generous heart to expand the activities of *hafatzas hamaayanos*, etc.

May it be the will of Hashem that the promise of Chazal be fulfilled in you in its entirety: "He who comes to purify is assisted," and the well-known *dikduk* of the Alter Rebbe is that [the assistance is] to purify others.

However, since an increase in the success of any matter requires a corresponding increase in *is'arusa d'lesata* (arousal from below), you will surely do everything that depends on you to translate this resolution from the heart to all the limbs, for "the heart divides [its influence] to all the limbs."

This leads to actual deed, in day-to-day activities, for "the deed is the essential thing," and furthermore, "deed is higher."

This is, of course, understood from the *parshiyos* of these weeks, in which we discuss the precedence of *naaseh* (we will do) to *nishma* (we will hear), and the greatness of the concept of *naaseh* preceding *nishma*.

As we stand on 15 Shevat, the New Year for Trees—and "man is the tree of the field," especially a *talmid chacham*—may it be His will that all activities that grow from (study—which leads to action—study of) the Tree of Life, our Torah, the Torah of life, be renewed, and may they yield good fruits—the *mitzvos*.

And from the *hisorerus* and strengths of this day, the New Year, may it be drawn down into all the days of the coming year.

And it is also a day when the moon is in its fullness.

With blessings for success in your holy work mentioned above, and in the manner of "which you shall set before them," and with blessings for good tidings, detailed in all that has been said.

***

**The heart divides:** See Zohar Vol. III, 221b.
**The deed is the essential thing:** Avos 1:17.
**Deed is higher:** See Zohar Vol. I, 115a; Zohar Vol. III, 108b.
**Study:** See Kiddushin 40b.
**To purify... Alter Rebbe... him:** This version is cited and explained in *Likutei Torah* (Devarim 89d).
**Day to day:** See *Likutei Torah* Bamidbar (19c-d).
**Especially a talmid chacham:** Taanis 7a.
**Fruits - mitzvos:** Sotah 46a.
**Which you shall set before them:** See *Hilchos Talmud Torah* by the Alter Rebbe (the conclusion and seal of the laws). *Torah Or*, beginning of *Parshas Mishpatim*.

## 8763

B"H, 16 Shevat, 5724
Brooklyn

## 8764

B"H, Thursday, the day of "all that Hashem has spoken we will do," 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the avreich Yosef, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter regarding the arrangements for your Bar Mitzvah, and, of course, first and foremost, the recitation of words of Torah, a maamar Chassidus, and giving to tzedakah.

And since the continuation will be on the upcoming Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Yisro—the core of which is the giving of our Torah, the Torah of life—and the continuation thereafter with the beginning of Parshas Mishpatim:

It is well known what our Rabbeinu HaZaken, the Baal HaTanya (the authority on the nistar of Torah) and the Shulchan Aruch (the authority on the nigleh of Torah), taught: that Bnei Yisrael must learn from the weekly parsha lessons for the matters of the week.

May it be Hashem’s will that one of the fundamental lessons from these aforementioned parshiyos will always be before your eyes, and that is:

**"For the Bnei Yisrael are My servants"**—says the Ribono shel Olam—"and not servants to servants." Therefore, it is forbidden for a Yid to say, "I love my master," which alludes to all the matters of this world; one must not be among those who, because of their desires for the matters of the world, become servants and enslaved to the yetzer and its affairs.

Rather, one must always remember: "I am **Hashem your G-d** who brought you out of the land of Egypt, **from the house of bondage.**"

To be a true free man, and as our Sages of blessed memory taught, there is no free man except for one who occupies himself with Talmud Torah, for study leads to action—the fulfillment of the mitzvos.

And the merit of tzedakah will stand by you in all of the above, with greater strength and intensity, and in a manner of *ma'alin bakodesh* (ascending in holiness).

With the blessing that your parents, may they live, should derive from you much true nachas—Yiddishe, Chassidishe nachas—and for good tidings in all that was mentioned.

## 8765

8765

B"H, 20 Shevat, 5724
Brooklyn

Greetings and Blessings,

I read your letter from Tuesday with great astonishment. It seems to me that—whether consciously or unconsciously—you have been given incorrect information. In any case, the content of your letter has been forwarded to the administration of the yeshiva, to whom this entire matter belongs.

I must express my great astonishment regarding Jews who have witnessed the kindnesses of Hashem Yisbarach and the miracles that saved them from the hands of the nations, and who have been gifted with a good son, a *baal kishron*. It appears that the only thing troubling them is how they can force and arrange for their son to take a portion of his young years away from learning our holy Torah, *Toras Chaim*, and dedicate it instead to, etc. All the "calculations" with which one attempts to justify such an attitude are certainly not for those who have seen and lived through those times—may we be spared from such things today—and they should not allow themselves to be deceived by the *yetzer hara*.

I do not wish to dwell at length on this entire matter, which, as stated, belongs to the yeshiva administration and the parents. However, since you have touched upon the question and wish to connect it to the Ten Commandments, to "honor your father and your mother," I cannot allow myself to pass over it in silence, and I have expressed my aforementioned astonishment.

May Hashem Yisbarach help that, in the end, every Jew—man and woman—should perceive the true truth, which is our holy Torah, *Toras Emes*, and fulfill its *mitzvos*, regarding which it is written, "and he shall live by them." May they strive to spread them to the maximum extent possible within their entire environment, and first and foremost regarding their children, for whom one bears **a deep, soulful responsibility.**

With blessings for good tidings regarding all that has been said above.

## 8766

B"H, 21 Shevat, 5724
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, Chassid, and Tzaddik, a man of many accomplishments, etc., etc.,
Rabbi N.M. shlita,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 25 Teves—which reached me in due time—in which you write regarding the adoption of a child by...

With appreciation, honor, and blessing.

Regarding the general matter of adopting children, it is surprising that I have not yet found anyone who has paid attention to the following point. Although several responsa have already been published detailing various laws that arise from the matter of adoption, no one has raised the issue regarding the essence of the matter itself, etc.

The concerns that have arisen for me are that adoption in our current days is not like in previous generations, where the fulfillment of the mitzvah of raising an orphan in one's home, etc., was such that the entire environment, including the child being raised, knew that these were not his parents. Now, it is **the opposite**—they do everything possible to conceal this detail. Furthermore, under pressure from doctors, who claim to be experts in matters of the psyche, they decide that it is forbidden to reveal this to the child (as it might disturb his peace of mind, etc.). The result of this is that their conduct with the adopted child is as if he were their own biological child, which consequently leads to all the issues of *yichud*, hugging, and kissing, etc., etc., on a daily basis. And surely, it is impossible to be careful about this, even if the adoptive parents are truly G-d-fearing.

And even if they reveal to the adopted child when he grows up that these are not his parents, it is highly questionable whether it is possible to change the behavior that has been ongoing for many years prior. Based on what has been said, there is certainly a Rabbinic prohibition, and according to the Rambam, there is also a Torah prohibition. And indeed, even regarding a Rabbinic prohibition—it is different when it is a matter that is repeated again and again, etc. (In addition to what is brought and explained in the books of *nigleh* regarding this—see also *Iggeres HaTeshuvah* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, Chapter 7). Seemingly, based on the above, the entire matter of adoption is highly questionable. And the reason for leniency in such a case—that "it is better that they be unwitting [sinners than willful ones]"—is seemingly not clear, as many would refrain from adoption if they knew the above. See also *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim* siman 608 and *Shulchan Aruch* of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe there regarding the various parameters of "it is better that they be..."—based on which the leniency of "it is better..." is not clear in the present case. And certainly, for one such as yourself, further elaboration is unnecessary.

## 8757

B"H, Tuesday, Parshas Im Kesef Talveh, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Shomrei Shabbos Gemilas Chasadim Society
May they live,

Peace and Blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter and its enclosure, in which you inform me of the annual meeting on Motzaei Shabbos Mevarchim Chodesh Adar.

According to the instruction of our Sages in their Mishnah, on the first of Adar, announcements are made regarding the *shekalim* and regarding *kilayim*. Seemingly, the connection between these two matters is not understood, to the point that they are announced and proclaimed on the same day.

It is possible to explain this—based on the words of the commentators on the reasons for the *mitzvos* regarding the prohibition of *kilayim*—that by doing so, one alters the laws of nature and its ways, which the Creator of the world and its Guide established, that grass, herbs, and trees should produce fruit only according to their kind.

In accordance with this, an announcement is made regarding the *shekalim*, that the communal offerings must come specifically from the new *terumah*, for one should not mix one year with another.

On the contrary—the Mishnah (and even the introduction itself is Torah) prioritizes the announcement regarding the *shekalim* over the announcement regarding *kilayim*.

This is so even though, on the face of it, the announcement regarding *kilayim* should take precedence, as the urgency in this matter is imperative (so that one does not sow *kilayim* in the interim), and furthermore, the prohibition is constant throughout the entire year, and every person is warned against it—which is not the case with *shekalim*, especially since it is possible to weigh them even at a later time, given that they collect *terumah* even for the future.

It is understood from the above that in order for there to be the desired conduct in the world, the beginning is dependent upon the conduct of the Jewish people in their own affairs in this manner, and from the spiritual, it cascades down into the physical.

Therefore, **after** the Beis Din actually implements the law of Torah and sends word to all the cities of Israel, proclaiming that they should bring their *shekalim*—because one must not mix one year with another regarding offerings and spiritual matters in the world—this cascades down also to the seed (the vegetative) in the earth (the inanimate), that it should be specifically according to its kind.

The same applies to the *mitzvah* of *gemilas chasadim*, which is the greatest level of *tzedakah*, equivalent to all the offerings. Through the fact that the Jewish people perform this with a cheerful countenance, the performance of the *mitzvah* cascades downward into what a person needs for all his requirements—in children, life, and sustenance (bread—vegetative), and even to the fulfillment of the promise, "Tithe so that you will become wealthy," in its literal sense—in silver and gold (inanimate).

And measure for measure—in the cheerful countenance of the King of the world—all of the above is increased.

With blessings for success in your work in all the aforementioned, and with joy and goodness of heart,

**M. Schneerson**

Enclosed is a check—my participation, *bli neder*, in the aforementioned.

8768

By the Grace of G-d
23 Shevat, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Chevra Shas of the congregation Shearis Yisrael
in the city of Baltimore
May Hashem protect them and grant them life

Peace and Blessing!

It was with pleasure that I learned through your Rabbi, the distinguished Torah scholar, G-d-fearing, and learned man, Rabbi Menachem Mendel HaKohen, may he live, that you are preparing for a *siyum* celebration of Maseches Nedarim during the week of the seventh of Adar, the day on which Moshe Rabbeinu, the redeemer of Israel, was born.

He who received the Torah from Sinai and transmitted it, and so on, to the many students throughout all the generations.

For even though at the standing at Mount Sinai, those who were present and those who were not present were all in attendance, as explained in the words of our Sages, nevertheless, Moshe, the faithful shepherd, is the one who stands between Hashem and us; he stands, connects, relates, and explains the word of Hashem to the Children of Israel.

Every single one of them is **sworn** from Mount Sinai to fulfill the Torah and its *mitzvos*. This oath is also a bestowal of strength from Above to fulfill the *mitzvos*. As is explained at the beginning of Maseches Nedarim, even regarding that which one swears to himself to fulfill a *mitzvah*, through this he spurs himself on—how much more so is this true for one who is sworn by the Giver of the Torah and the Creator of man.

And although, on the face of it, a difficulty arises: if the fact that one is already sworn from Mount Sinai is not enough to enable him to withstand the war of the *yetzer* and overcome it, what will his own oath to fulfill the *mitzvah* add?

The explanation is understood from our Sages at the conclusion of the Maseches: "If it is true that he committed a transgression" (because he did not withstand the war of the *yetzer* and transgressed the will of his Creator, yet despite this), "he is bound" so that his disgrace will not be **seen**. For sometimes the fear of flesh and blood and the shame before them acts more powerfully than the fear of Heaven, and so on.

Something similar to this is the one who swears to fulfill a *mitzvah*—the oath of the soul within a body of flesh and blood, especially when he reveals and also articulates the oath with his physical mouth, tongue, and lips.

And the aforementioned incident (from the conclusion of the Maseches) regarding the woman and her husband who commits adultery is particularly relevant to our subject and serves as a fitting allusion. For the standing at Mount Sinai is the wedding of the Holy One, Blessed be He, with His people Israel, where they were commanded: "And you shall perform them" (the *mitzvos* of the Torah), "and you shall not wander after... which you **stray** after them"—a warning against every sin, iniquity, and transgression. The root and beginning of these is the first sin of the primordial serpent; the serpent came upon Chavah and cast impurity into her, as is alluded to and explained in many places, and at Mount Sinai, their impurity ceased.

May it be the will of Hashem that every individual within the entirety of Israel will strengthen himself and increase his study of Torah in a manner that leads to action—the fulfillment of *mitzvos*. "This is the Torah"—to distinguish between the impure and the pure, and (within the category of the pure) between the holy and the profane—the will and needs of the soul versus the will and needs of the body.

For it was precisely in the partnership of both together that the Torah was given to them.

And in a manner where the partners **(with the definite article)** both desire to create a partition—"with all your heart," with both your inclinations.

However, the thickness of the partition—this corresponds to the custom (and nature) of the individual: there is one whose *yetzer* does not stand against him, such as one who is naturally diligent and lacks the feeling of pleasure by nature—and therefore it is sufficient for him not to become sunken in the needs of his body (which he loves more by nature) through the command from Mount Sinai. Below him is one whose *yetzer* is burning, and so on—who is in need of the soul’s stimulation by swearing to himself, and so on.

But even regarding this, we have been promised that "none shall be cast away"—that he will certainly eventually do *teshuvah*, as the final ruling and conclusion of the Maseches states: "The woman is permitted."

With respect and blessing.

## 8759

8759

B"H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh Mevarchim Adar,
Brooklyn, N.Y.
Parshas Mishpatim and Parshas Shekalim, 5724

To the annual banquet of the Ladies Auxiliary of Brownsville and East New York for the Lubavitcher Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim,

Shalom u’Bracha!

In connection with the annual banquet, this coming 10 Adar, I send my wishes and blessing to all the supporters and participants. May the Ribono shel Olam help that the event should be a great success in every respect.

The sedra of this Shabbos—Parshas Mishpatim—is a continuation of Matan Torah, as our Sages, of blessed memory, say regarding the words **"And these** are the ordinances" (V'eileh ha'mishpatim): that the "vav" signifies an addition and a continuation.

Likewise, the sedra **Tisa**, from which we read the **Parshas Shekalim** this Shabbos, reminds us of Matan Torah, when the Ribono shel Olam gave us the second Luchos.

At Matan Torah, Yidden became truly **free** by taking upon themselves to be **avdei Hashem**—to serve the Ribono shel Olam alone. Therefore, the first matter that the sedra Mishpatim addresses, right from the beginning, is the concept of an **eved ivri** (a Hebrew servant), and how a Yid should not want to be enslaved to another, and should not want to say, **"I love my master... I will not go out free"**—meaning, "I love my master (with all worldly comforts)... I do not want to go out to freedom"—but rather, he should specifically desire to be free to serve the Ribono shel Olam alone. And therefore, the Torah says that a Yid who wants to remain a servant to another servant must have his ear pierced—the Jewish ear that heard the Divine command at Mount Sinai: **"For the Bnei Yisrael are My servants"**—"Yidden are My—Hashem’s—servants."

A living example of an **eved Hashem** is Mordechai HaYehudi, as the Megillah of Purim tells us: **"But Mordechai would not bow down or prostrate himself"**—Mordechai would not kneel or bow to Haman or to his avodah zarah.

To raise a "nation of Mordechai" (am Mordechai) can only be done through a Torah-true chinuch, a chinuch al taharas hakodesh, which is the purpose and task of the Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch, which is being led, B"H, with great success.

And great is the merit of every individual who has a part in this.

May Hashem Yisbarach grant you success so that you may continue your good work in an increased measure, and in this merit, you will also be blessed in an increased measure, in everything that you and your families, shichyu, are in need of, both in gashmius and in ruchnius alike.

With blessings for success and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

***

8759

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 11, p. 291, and completed according to a photocopy of the letter.

Our Sages: Shemos Rabbah 30:3; see Rashi on the verse.

## 8750

B"H, 26 Shevat, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the congregants—with the Gabbaim at their head—of the Poalei Agudas Yisrael Synagogue in Kiryat Shalom, near Tel Aviv, in our Holy Land, may it be built and established speedily in our days by Moshiach Tzidkeinu,
May Hashem preserve them and grant them life,

Peace and Blessing!

At the time, the *pidyon nefesh* was delivered to me by the esteemed Chossid, a man of fine character, Rabbi Ch. N. Kovalsky, as was the notification regarding the schedule for reciting Tehillim, etc.

The immense importance of reciting Tehillim and studying Torah in the synagogue surely requires no elaboration, as it is explained in many places in our holy books, and elucidated at length in the holy letters and *sichos* of our Rebbes, the leaders of Israel.

I write only to encourage and to urge, in accordance with the teaching of our Sages: "One only encourages those who are already diligent." I encourage you to exert effort to increase the number of participants in Torah study sessions—both in the revealed aspects of Torah and in the inner dimensions of Torah, which in our generation have been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus—and likewise, to include all the congregants of the synagogue in the recitation of Tehillim.

The recitation of Tehillim should take place every day after the morning *davening*—following the division of Tehillim for the days of the month—and on *Shabbos Kodesh Mevarchim Hachodesh*, in the morning before *davening*, the entire five books of Tehillim should be completed, as they correspond to the Five Books of the Torah.

One should also connect the above to the *parsha* of this week, *Parshas Terumah*—an offering to Hashem—regarding the building of the *Mikdash* and the *Mikdash* that is called a *Mishkan*.

Their essence—as our Sages state—is a place of *tefillah*, and a place toward which **all** prayers are directed, toward the Holy of Holies: the place of the *Aron*—which represents the study of Torah.

And the book of Tehillim is, indeed, the *tefillah* within the Torah.

With respect and blessings for good tidings regarding all the above.

## 8751

B"H, 26 Shevat, 5724
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rav, G-d-fearing, learned, and accomplished, R' Dov Yehuda, shlita,

Shalom u’Bracha!

Following a hiatus, I received your letter of 23 Shevat, in which you write regarding the matter of the shul.

Although, in general, it is not my practice to involve myself in such matters—unless my opinion is explicitly requested, etc.—since, as I surmise, the background is **not** straightforward, and furthermore—and this is the main point—the primary consideration must be to increase the number of shuls that are established on the foundation of holiness, especially in our current era and in our camp, etc., I have therefore expressed my opinion accordingly: While it may be correct for the time being, for several reasons, for you to be in the shul you write about, regarding a permanent arrangement—based on the above—it is better to establish a shul of your own. Even if its beginning is small, its end will surely be great; may it be His will that it be very great.

It is understood that a judge has only what his eyes see, and it is not my intention at all to insist upon my opinion as stated. However, on the other hand, I am not at liberty to conceal what appears to me to be for the benefit of all those interested and involved—that it should be in the manner described above. Even if it is not possible for the shul to be in your home specifically, you should strive for a shul that can be more independent than the current one.

Since we are approaching the month of Adar, whose focal point and center are the days of Purim—the days of "sending portions to one another"—and one of the reasons for this is to bring the hearts of all Jews closer together, leading to true unity, may it be His will that this activity begin immediately from the Shabbos when we bless the month of Adar, increasing and adding until the moon reaches its fullness in the middle of the month.

With respect and blessing for good tidings regarding all the above, and for true nachas from your son, shlita, about whom you write—in the midst of all your children, shlita—together with your wife, the Rabbanit, tichye.

***

## 8742

8742

B"H, 28 Shevat, 5724
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 16 Shevat, regarding the question of adopting a child, etc.

Since the approach to adopting a child in our time involves exerting every effort to make the child comfortable—including ensuring that the child feels that these are their true, natural parents—I do not see, even after safeguarding against other matters, how one can avoid issues of *yichud*, physical affection, etc. [This is true even if the child were to know that these are adoptive parents; all the more so as is the current practice, as mentioned, of concealing this from the child]. It can be said that this is impossible, and these are certainly prohibitions *miderabanan*, and in part—according to other *poskim*—prohibitions *min haTorah* as well.

And as mentioned above, this is all even after ensuring the other matters, such as the child’s lineage and their *kashrus*, etc.

Therefore, as stated above, I do not see any possibility of assisting anyone in such a matter; on the contrary, one must actively discourage it. Certainly, further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

Although you do not mention it, I assume you have consulted with a medical specialist in this field regarding having children, especially since new treatment methods have been discovered in this area in recent years. May it be the will of Hashem that you be able to share good news regarding all that was mentioned above.

At a time of favor, you will be mentioned at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zi"e*, for the fulfillment of your heart's desire for the good.

It is appropriate to have your *tefillin* checked, as well as the *mezuzos* in your home, to ensure they are all *kosher* according to the law. Your wife, *tichyeh*, should observe the good custom of Jewish women to give *tzedakah* each time before lighting candles on *Erev Shabbos* and *Erev Yom Tov*.

With blessings for good tidings in all that was mentioned,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,
Secretary

8743

B”H, end of Shevat, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Ben-Zion, may he live, known as Prof. Dinur,

Greetings and blessings,

I have just received the offprint from the collection *HaIshiyut VeDorah* (The Personality and Its Generation), and I thank you for your thoughtfulness in sending it to me.

On this occasion, I must apologize that for several reasons—primarily due to the multitude of my preoccupations—I have not yet expressed my heartfelt thanks for the offprints and books you sent me previously. It is my hope that you will judge me favorably, as our Sages of blessed memory have instructed.

As I am still under the impression of the *yom hilula* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and based on the words of the Arizal that holiness never departs from its place, and especially in light of the adage common among Chassidim, “Once a Chassid, always a Chassid,” I will take the liberty of pointing out the merit you attained in having the privilege of spending several months in the tent of the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva. Based on the aforementioned principle, I am certain that not only did it not depart from its place, but it moved to a higher state, finding expression from time to time in good deeds of which an "opponent" would not be capable, for they require the light and warmth whose source is Chassidus and its matters.

Moving from one subject to another within the same vein, this serves as an acknowledgment with thanks (and in continuation of a previous acknowledgment) of your book, *Olam SheShaka* (A World That Sank). It is understood from what was written above that one can say this only regarding a physical and material world, and even regarding the Beis HaMikdash—**if** it is made of wood and stone. For while parchment may be burned, the letters remain; moreover, they return below and are written anew, even to the point of being engraved upon the hearts of thousands and myriads of Jewish men and women, and even engraved in letters of fire. This is like the two versions regarding this: white fire (and also) black fire. For there must be two lines—the right hand that draws near and the left hand that pushes away—and in general terms, "turn from evil and do good." In the *avodah* of the soul, this is the matter of *ahavah* and *yirah*, the path to which is among the primary subjects of the holy Tanya.

It is understood that I read with special interest the other pages in your aforementioned book where you speak of your time spent, as mentioned above, within the four cubits of the holiness of Tomchei Temimim. Although several expressions are "seemingly" the opposite of the essence and would have been better replaced by their opposites, at the same time, these expressions also reinforced in me the feeling that you are still under the influence of that period and its matters—to such an extent that you find it necessary to defend yourself against the influence of that time, and to justify steps and actions, and so on and so forth. In other words, it seems to me that even in your private world, this world has not "sunk." May it be the will of Hashem that not only will you not resist this influence, but on the contrary, you will utilize it to the full extent of your possibilities, even to the point of the well-known slogan—the dissemination of the *maayanos* (the wellsprings). And if a verdict is issued against me that (from time to time) I am a dreamer, etc., may it be the will of Hashem that what is written above—even if, seemingly and at first glance, it might be called a product of the imagination—will be drawn down into the world of action. For in our era, which is full of wonders and unusual phenomena, the imagination is met and realized in action—which is the main thing.

This is also the place for me to acknowledge with many thanks the receipt of Volume 1 of your work, *Yisrael BaGolah* (Israel in the Diaspora).

Following the custom of the Jewish people, I will take the liberty of offering a comment here as well, based on the difference found in the books of the great figures of Israel—the Rishonim and those of the Middle Ages. It is that regarding matters of Torah, or matters connected to Torah, they discuss them as if they were part of the daily life and time of the one discussing them. An example is the *shakla v'tarya* (the give-and-take) regarding the laws of *Kodshim* and *Taharos* hundreds of years after the destruction of the Beis HaMikdash, and the like. This applies not only to the commentators on the Mishnah, etc., but even to the *Sheilos U’Teshuvos* (Responsa) literature, in which one finds many matters discussing things that happened to the Jewish people in the desert, etc. From this, it is understood that when one cites books written in a certain period that discuss a certain matter or event, it is no proof at all that in the time of the author of the book, this matter was current in daily life; it requires special investigation with collateral evidence to confirm that this is indeed the case.

These words are directed in particular toward the question of the reading of the Torah that you touch upon in your book. This matter happened to come to my attention when your book was received; I searched through it and found that it implies that in the time of Rashi, the order of the Torah reading was once every three years, and the proof for this is that Rashi discusses it in such-and-such a book, etc. Based on what was said above, this is no proof at all. Although I am not currently involved in this subject, it seems to me clear that long before the time of Rashi, and especially in the countries where Rashi lived and those adjacent to them, the reading for the completion of the Torah was once a year.

Incidentally, but in the same vein, it is surely known to you that there is a version of three years and a half-year, and the references for this are in the book by Mordechai Margaliot regarding the differences between the people of the East and the people of Eretz Yisrael, difference 48.

I would be interested to know if you have historical material regarding the reign of Jewish tribes in North Africa (the Sahara) during the Middle Ages. As I recall, there was a *Kohen* or someone similar there, and eventually, she also fell in battle and her reign ceased.

As is customary among Jews to conclude in a manner similar to the opening, I take the liberty of enclosing an offprint pamphlet that appeared in connection with the *hilula* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

With respect and blessing,

## 8744

Brooklyn

## 8,709

1 Adar, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Administration of the Gemilas Chesed Fund of the Chabad Synagogue in Bnei Brak, in our Holy Land—may it be built and established speedily in our days by Moshiach Tzidkeinu—may they live,

Shalom u’vracha!

I have read with pleasure the report and the summary of the Fund’s activities over the past period, as well as the letter from the Fund’s chairman, the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs and many accomplishments, etc., R’ Menachem Yisrael, may he live—dated Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Im Kesef Talveh.

This is also relevant to the day—1 Adar—in accordance with the instruction of our Sages in their Mishnah: "On the first of Adar, they make an announcement regarding the shekalim and regarding kilayim."

Seemingly, the connection between these two matters is not understood, to the point that they are announced and proclaimed on the same day.

One may explain, as a possibility, based on the words of the commentators on the reasons for the mitzvos regarding the prohibition of kilayim: that by doing so, one alters the laws of nature and the ways which the Creator and Guide of the world instilled, that "grass, herbs, and trees bearing fruit" should be specifically "after its kind."

In accordance with this, they announce the shekalim, so that the communal offerings will come specifically from the new terumah, for one must not mix the offerings and matters of one year with those of another.

Furthermore, the Mishnah places the announcement regarding the shekalim before the announcement regarding kilayim (and even this order is Torah).

This is so, even though, on the face of it, the announcement regarding kilayim should take precedence, as the priority here is necessary (so that one may uproot the kilayim as soon as possible, and even more so, so that one does not plant kilayim in the interim). Moreover, this prohibition is constant throughout the year, and every individual is warned about it—which is not the case with shekalim, especially since it is possible to weigh them even at a later time. Furthermore, when one contributes to the lishkah, one intends to contribute also for the future **collection**.

It is understood from the above that in order for there to be the desired conduct in the world, the beginning and the dependence lie in the conduct of Bnei Yisrael in their own affairs in this manner; from the spiritual, it cascades down into the physical.

Therefore, **after** the Beis Din sends word to all the cities of Israel and announces that they should bring their shekalim—because one must not mix one year with another regarding offerings and spiritual matters—this cascades down into the seeds (the vegetative) in the land (the inanimate), so that everything should be specifically "after its kind."

The same applies to the mitzvah of Gemilas Chesed, which is the highest level of tzedakah, equivalent to all the offerings. By Bnei Yisrael performing this with a cheerful countenance, the performance of the mitzvah cascades downward into what a person needs for all their requirements: in children, life, and sustenance (bread—vegetative), and even to the fulfillment of the promise, "Tithe so that you may become rich," in its literal sense—in silver and gold (inanimate).

And measure for measure—in the cheerful countenance of the King of the world—all of the above is increased.

With blessings for success in your work in all that is mentioned, and with joy and a glad heart.

Enclosed is a check—my participation, bli neder, in the above.
