## 8757

B"H, 3 Adar, 5724
Brooklyn

To the Avreich Ezra Binyamin, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

...Your previous letters were received. It gave me pleasure to see that you are studying and scrutinizing your learning of Tanya, etc. Although, in general, precision in every word for people of our level is only possible after becoming proficient in many seforim and maamarim of Chassidus. Regarding your many questions on Iggeres HaKodesh—you should discuss this with the mashpi'im of Chassidus with whom you meet.

As for your question regarding what is explained in the Likkutim on Parshas Yisro concerning the superiority of mitzvos after Matan Torah compared to before Matan Torah—seemingly, this does not apply to mitzvos that they were **commanded** to perform before Matan Torah (based on what is explained in the Likkut on Parshas Lech Lecha). After all, even regarding Bris Milah, etc., the Rambam writes in his commentary on the Mishnah (Chullin, end of chapter 7) about the superiority of Matan Torah.

The distinction (in brief, at least) is this: What they fulfilled on their own before Matan Torah was merely "scents" and spirituality. Therefore, in the staff of Yaakov and the like, no holiness remained afterward. What they **were commanded** to fulfill (**specifically in the physical**) left a holiness in the physical even afterward (and this is why Avraham was compelled to administer an oath in the manner of "place your hand under my thigh"). However, this was only a holiness that the created being (the staff) could attain (the root of the created beings), because there was a decree that the lower realms could not ascend to the higher realms. After Matan Torah, the essence of which is the nullification of that decree, He sanctified us **with His mitzvos**, which is incomparable to the root of the created beings (which are merely "scents" relative to the holiness of the Creator).

In any case, see the aforementioned Likkutim for the basis of this distinction.

Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 23, p. 326, and completed based on a photocopy of the letter.

**In the Likkut on Parshas Yisro:** Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 3, p. 887 and onwards.

**In the Likkut on Parshas Lech Lecha:** Printed there, p. 757 and onwards.

## 8798

B"H, 4 Adar, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants in the study of Shas at the Shaarei Emunah Synagogue in the city of Toronto,
May they live,

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to learn from the G-d-fearing, esteemed, and energetic Rabbi A. Parshan, may he live, that you are completing the Shas. Surely, following the custom of Israel, you are also "attaching the beginning to the completion"—the beginning of the Shas—on the eve of the fourth day, the parsha of "And they shall take to you pure olive oil... to cause a lamp to burn continually."

May it be the will [of Hashem] that the study of Torah, both the revealed and the inner dimensions (the *maor* of the Torah), both of which are alluded to in the aforementioned verse: "to cause a lamp to burn," and "and they shall take olive oil"—

And as our Sages, of blessed memory, said: "One who sees olive oil in a dream should anticipate the light of Torah, as it is written, 'olive oil,' etc."

My Torahs, which are **pure**—the revealed Torah and the inner dimension of the Torah—for words of Torah cannot contract *tumah*. We are obligated in the study of Torah constantly, by day and by night in the literal sense, and by day and by night in the spiritual sense; at the time when the Beis Hamikdash exists, and at the time of the *galus*, regarding which it is said, "He who dwells with them in the midst of their *tumah*."

And as is alluded to in the verse and explained by our Sages, of blessed memory: "continually," even in *tumah*.

May it bring forth light for all the Children of Israel in all their dwelling places.

And as is alluded to in the verse and explained by our Sages, of blessed memory: Why is a lamp needed? In order to illuminate for us, "to cause a lamp to burn continually, that there may be light before Me continually."

Before the Children of Israel specifically, as is alluded to in the verse and explained by our Sages, of blessed memory: "And you shall command the Children of Israel"—specifically Israel—"because they crowned Me over them at the sea."

And from then until now, twice every day, when we recite the Shema, in the evening and in the morning, as our Sages, of blessed memory, said: "He shall accept upon himself the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven," crowning Him above and below and to the four corners of the heavens.

And the prerequisite for all of the above is as stated in the verse, "beaten for the light," and according to the interpretation of our Rebbe, the author of the Tanya and the Shulchan Aruch: Through being "beaten" (*v'nafshi ke'afar lakol tihyeh*—my soul shall be as dust to all), one becomes [a vessel] for the "light" (*p'sach libi b'sorasecha*—open my heart in Your Torah, and ultimately to the *maor* of the Torah).

With respect and with best wishes to all the participants in this most exalted celebration mentioned above,

[Signature]

8759

B”H, 5 Adar, 5724
Brooklyn

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, R’ Tzvi, may he live, known as Dr. Harkavy,

Shalom u’Bracha!

Your letter was received after some delay, in which you write regarding the sending of printed materials in large quantities, etc., to there, etc., etc.

Since there are various opinions on this matter, I am refraining from expressing an opinion or participating, etc., and I ask for your forgiveness.

It is surprising that for a long time I have not received any of the printed materials that you have published, even though surely, as has been your custom for some time, you have had several of them, and you will surely send, through those who do His will, everything that has appeared. Thank you in advance.

I will take the liberty—based on the style of Chazal, “up to a hundred times”—to arouse you regarding what we have discussed many times: the great importance of studying the *pnimiyus haTorah* that was revealed in our generation through the teachings of Chassidus. This is especially true in our generation, which is full of confusion and the undermining of foundations, etc., and particularly in the Holy Land, of which it is said, “The eyes of Hashem your G-d are always upon it, from the beginning of the year to the end of the year.” For many years now, this study has become increasingly widespread and is growing, in accordance with the words of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, the founder of Chabad philosophy, that the teachings of Chassidus are the inheritance of the entire Jewish people, in the literal sense—not as something that one treasures as more precious than anything else and therefore hides from the sight of all, and even from one’s own sight, in the well-known style of “a secret of secrets.” For in these generations of ours, “it is a **mitzvah** to reveal this wisdom”—a revelation that extends even into the daily life of the weekdays, until it is evident that “in all your ways, know Him.” This matter depends only on one’s will, for the ability has been granted from of old, and the command is explained in several of our holy books, and with special emphasis in the books of the Gra, no less than in the books of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe.

With blessings for good tidings in all that was mentioned, and with a blessing for a happy Purim.

**M. Schneerson**

## 8780

B”H, 7 Adar, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the honorable congregants—and the Gabbaim at their head—of the Shomrei Shabbos synagogue, who participate in the fixed times for Torah study, may Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to learn through the esteemed Chossid, the G-d-fearing man, etc., R’ Y.L. Raskin, of the fixed times for studying our holy Torah in public at the aforementioned synagogue.

The great importance of conducting Torah study sessions in a synagogue certainly requires no elaboration, as it is explained in many places in our holy books, and explained well in the letters and holy sichos of our Rebbes, the Nesi’im, may their merit protect us.

I write only to encourage and to prioritize—in accordance with the dictum of our Sages, “One only encourages those who are already diligent”—to exert effort to increase the number of participants in these Torah study sessions, both in the revealed aspects of Torah and in the inner dimensions of Torah, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus. Furthermore, one should strive to include all the congregants of the synagogue in this.

There is a hint to this in the beginning of this week’s parsha: “And you shall command... that they bring you pure olive oil... to kindle a lamp continually.”

Torah study—both the revealed and the inner dimensions (the “light” of the Torah)—are both hinted at in this verse: “to kindle a lamp” and “that they bring you pure olive oil.”

As our Sages have said, “He who sees olive oil in a dream should anticipate the light of Torah, as it is said, ‘pure olive oil...’”

We are obligated in Torah study continually, by day and by night, in the literal sense, and by day and by night in a spiritual sense; at the time when the Beis Hamikdash exists and at the time of exile—of which it is said, “He who dwells with them in the midst of their impurities.”

As is hinted in the verse and explained by our Sages, “continually”—even in a state of impurity.

Through this, light will be drawn down to all Bnei Yisrael in all their dwelling places.

As is hinted in the verse and explained by our Sages, “Why is a lamp needed? In order to illuminate for us, ‘to kindle a lamp continually,’ so that there should be light before Me continually.”

Specifically before Bnei Yisrael, as is hinted in the verse and explained by our Sages, “And you shall command Bnei Yisrael”—because they crowned Me over them at the sea.

From then until now, twice every day, when we recite Shema, in the evening and in the morning—as our Sages have said, “He must accept upon himself the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven,” crowning Him above and below and to the four corners of the heavens.

The prerequisite for all of the above is as stated in the verse, “beaten for the light,” and according to the interpretation of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya (who rules in the hidden aspects of Torah), and the Shulchan Aruch (which rules in the revealed aspects of Torah): Through being “beaten” (“and let my soul be as dust to all”—this is accomplished) one becomes “for the light” (“open my heart in Your Torah”—and even to the light of the Torah).

With respect and blessing for good tidings in all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8781

B"H, 7 Adar, 5724
Brooklyn.

Mr. Gershon, may he live,

As for what to influence them with, this is explained at the end of Megillas Koheles: "Fear Hashem and keep His mitzvos, for this is the whole man." In the phrasing of Chazal, "the deed is the essential thing"—daily life conducted in accordance with the instructions of our Torah, the Torah of life.

These days, the days preceding Purim, remind us of and instruct us in all of the above, as it is written, "And many of the people of the land became Jews," etc. This surely also alludes to the "people of the land" that exist within each and every one of us—the nefesh habehamis, the "spirit of the beast that goes down to the earth."

With blessings for good news and a happy Purim.

8782

***

8782

General details. Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 6, p. 375, and completed based on a photocopy of the letter.

**S.D.H. ... 5629:** Sefer HaMaamarim 5629, p. 86.

**Chazal in their Mishnah:** Beginning of Maseches Megillah.

**On the eleventh ... until the fifteenth:** The eleventh corresponds to the numerical value of the letters *Vav-Hei* of the Name, and the fifteenth corresponds to the numerical value of *Yud-Hei* of the Name, which Amalek separated (Shelah, Parshas Tetzaveh, 269a), and Haman was a descendant of his (Targum Sheni to Megillas Esther; Maseches Sofrim, Ch. 13). See S.D.H. "Megillah Nikreis," 5629.

**Time ... day of Purim:** Two opinions in the Gemara there.

**Even the day:** This is more precise than "time" (see Magen Avraham, Orach Chaim 270, in the commentary: "The time of the giving of our Torah").

**According to the interpretation of Chazal:** Megillah 16b, bottom of the page.

## 8784

[13 Adar, 5724]

(1) Not sending the letter—**certainly** this will add nothing to the correction and improvement. And sending it—at the very least, it will not escape doubt (and regarding the **general** matter, but) regarding individuals—**certainly** many will be deterred by this.

## 8784*

#### ***8784\****

8585

B"H, Days of Purim, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, a man of the people who seeks the good of his people, a man of noble character, scion of a noble lineage, R' Shneur Zalman, shlita,

Shalom u’vracha!

In accordance with my custom, founded upon the mitzvos and customs of the House of Israel, I wish to fulfill the mitzvah of *mishloach manos ish l’re’ehu*, and as the text states, through a messenger.

For this reason, and for other reasons that will become clear below, I am sending this (along with a letter) to you via a special emissary, as according to my information, this is a time-sensitive matter, and also so that it does not pass through many hands. And although the Torah is protective of the property of Yisrael, certainly in a case such as this, we are not concerned.

1. It has just come to my attention that there is a matter which, if it comes to fruition, is liable to lead to new controversy, the inflaming of passions, and so on, between those who have recently begun to be labeled "religious" and their counterparts.

(I am using the term "labeled" intentionally, for any label is not the true essence of the name that denotes the true essence of the thing being named; for all Bnei Yisrael are believers, the children of believers, with no exception. Rather, for various reasons, there are those who, in the language of the Rambam, their *yetzer* has coerced them, and it seems to them that the concept of "believers, children of believers" does not befit them. But the truth eventually triumphs, and this is also the promise of the text, "that no one cast away be banished from Him.")

The matter is, as I have been informed, that the Hebrew University in Jerusalem is preparing to publish a new edition of the *Torah Shebichtav*, taking into account the most recent discoveries and various manuscripts, and first and foremost the manuscript known as the [...] Aleppo Codex (*Keser Torah*!). And furthermore—and this is why I have written—it has occurred to those preparing the aforementioned for print that the main text should not be the accepted and sanctified version upon which many generations of sons and daughters of Yisrael have been raised, including those in our generation who are in the category of "their *yetzer* has coerced them," but rather the version of the aforementioned Codex. And since a significant portion of it is missing—it seems to me about a third—they will complete the missing parts from other manuscripts which, in the opinion of the publishers, can be relied upon. And in the notes section, whether in the margins or at the end of each volume, they will also note the accepted version and the versions of other manuscripts, and so on and so forth.

One can understand the storm that is liable to erupt if a partition is erected between different circles among Bnei Yisrael regarding the *Torah Shebichtav* as well. We have enough troubles caused by partitions made by biased men—in various and strange matters—but at least for now, regarding the *Torah Shebichtav*, there is one version for everyone, and in this, Bnei Yisrael are distinguished from those who follow the Septuagint, the Samaritan translation, and so on. Even those among Bnei Yisrael who fought against the *Torah Shebichtav*, starting from the matter of the Exodus from Egypt and the Giving of the Torah, at any rate, regarding the version itself, they did not enter into battle.

And now, G-d forbid, they are preparing to erect a partition in this as well.

What increases the danger is another matter: apparently, they are arming themselves with the argument and reasoning that this is a "demand of pure science," since our accepted version is supposedly based solely on the version of Yaakov ben Chaim, etc., whereas when we have merited to have more manuscripts, it is as if it has been clarified that even the Rambam had other versions, and first and foremost the aforementioned Codex. And if so, and since Bnei Yisrael are people of *mesiras nefesh*, they will go out in a *milchemes mitzvah*, so to speak, for the purity of the *Torah Shebichtav*, provided that the main text is printed specifically with the changes, as mentioned above.

And although the changes, as I have been informed, are not so prominent and are mainly regarding *chaser* and *yaseir*, vowels, and cantillation marks, and the like, nevertheless, as mentioned above, the question here is not the quantity of the changes, but the very matter of erecting a partition and causing a rift in hearts.

It is not my intention in this letter to reject the entire matter of comparing manuscripts, etc.—on the contrary—but rather not to touch the main text, which should remain in the accepted version specifically, and only in the notes and introduction, etc., should the variant versions appear. And on the contrary, whoever elaborates and details them is to be praised (provided he does not present his own opinion as a definitive conclusion of the many or as a simple fact, but rather to say everything in the name of its author).

In such a way, the honor of science is also maintained, but it would also be in ways of pleasantness and ways of peace, and the well-known league will be forced to look for another matter to justify a war against believers, children of believers.

In the manner of "men of science" in our time, it is impossible to approach any discussion on such a matter without them bringing proofs that Professor So-and-so also thinks so. And although this is not my profession, it seems clear that even the German Kittel, in his first editions of the Tanach, did not dare to change the main text, and all his notes appeared in the margins and the like. Only after the Second World War and the destructions, etc., did they print a new (third) edition of his, and the main text is based on the Leningrad Codex, under the influence of his co-editor P. Kahle. And although since then many non-Jews have followed in his footsteps, this does not necessitate that specifically in Jerusalem, the Holy City, they should also do such a thing.

According to the information I have, the one at the head of the entire matter is Prof. Goshen-Gottstein. I do not know his attitude toward religion, toward the love of Yisrael, toward peace among Bnei Yisrael, and his zeal for science. In any case, it is certainly better to preempt the evil in a secretive manner and as soon as possible. Therefore, as mentioned, this letter is sent by a special emissary, and I rely on your understanding—if you will manage the matters and how. May it be His will that you succeed in this, and I await good news.

And with greater emphasis: all of the above stands even if the aforementioned Codex were complete; all the more so when a third of it is missing and they will need to complete it from other manuscripts, etc.

2. And from one matter to another, regarding the days of Purim, when the nullification of the decree was through Mordechai the Jew gathering thousands of school children and teaching them the Torah of Hashem, until they said, "We are with you for life, etc."—I am touching here once again on the painful problem of the mission, and in continuation of our telephone conversation, since I received information that there was a decision to impose upon them as well the Compulsory Education Law and official registration, through which their activity would be limited, etc., and that they handed the matter to a special committee that will investigate the situation and submit a report, etc.

It is understood and simple that my position on the aforementioned is that I cannot but specify it clearly, and it is: that there is no other advice for this plague, *avodah zarah* and its derivatives, other than—eradication. And whatever the temporary tactics may be, one must follow the path of the only remedy for the aforementioned plague, and be careful not to mislead the public into thinking that the aforementioned decision (that they come under the Compulsory Education Law) is a remedy for the problem itself, and thereby distract the public and lull them to sleep. For the aforementioned decision is a simple matter from the outset: that a sinner who entices and leads astray should not be rewarded. And in the phrasing of our conversation, that a law, as long as it is in force, must be kept by everyone, and specifically the enticers and those who lead astray were exempted from it. Consequently, this is not a new decision, but the activation of an old law, and they have not yet begun regarding the plague of the mission.

As for the well-known argument of whether it is possible to eradicate the plague of the mission in our time, the era of democracy, etc., and what the nations of the world will say—in many countries there has been such a law for many years, such as in Austria, Norway, and several other countries, without anyone raising a voice or chirping that there is any slight hint of coercion or denial of freedom of conscience, and the like.

According to my information, the main difficulty originates in France, which apparently has the largest mission in Eretz Yisrael. And furthermore, and primarily, since there are special relations with France, they demand special rights with extra assertiveness, to the point that, according to rumor, the first to begin crying out like a "robbed Cossack" was the French ambassador, who apparently relies on those same relations. I also heard that the French ambassador is an extreme zealot, and he exploits these relations in this matter which is close to his heart. Some believe there is also a secret agreement regarding special rights for France, and therefore they also allowed them the raising of pigs, and although the official reason is that it is only for their own needs, etc., the internal reason, according to what was said, is not to infringe upon the rights of the French.

But from any point of view, the argument and demand are just: what do the rights of France in Eretz Yisrael have to do with converting the sons and daughters of Yisrael from their religion? And is it at all possible that such "rights" should exist? And also, why are they so alarmed, for the spreading of Christianity is not a political matter of France but of the Vatican! And certainly there are other diplomatic explanations to influence the French, etc.

With appreciation, honor, and blessing,

M. Schneerson

## 8787

B"H, 17 Adar, 5724
Brooklyn

Mr. Moshe Isser Hakohen
Shalom u’Bracha,

It was a pleasure to receive your letter from the eve of Wednesday, in which you write regarding your state of mind and your perspective concerning Chassidus, its teachings, and its matters, etc.

It is my firm hope that by becoming acquainted with this Torah more deeply and internally, you will draw closer to it and to its conclusions. Especially since, ultimately, the inner dimension of Torah revealed in the teachings of Chassidus is the soul and the interiority of our holy Torah—the revealed Torah—or, in the phrasing of the holy Zohar, the *neshamah d’Oraisa*.

Regarding your mention in your letter that in previous generations there were those who opposed this teaching, etc., they explained their reasoning and justification at length: they feared that by following this teaching, one might, G-d forbid, distance oneself from the fulfillment of practical mitzvos and the like. If, in that era, there were differences of opinion as to whether there was any basis for such a concern, then after the passage of some two hundred years since the teachings of Chassidus were revealed, everyone admits and answers the question "What is the sign of a Chassid?" by noting that he prays longer than one who is not a Chassid, he wears two pairs of tefillin rather than one, his beard is grown, etc. That is to say, reality has come and proven that not only is there no foundation for the aforementioned concern, but on the contrary: when one encounters a person in the marketplace whose beard is grown, who has peyos, whose clothing is long, who eats *shmurah* on the festival of Pesach, and who also wears *tefillin d'Rabbenu Tam*, it is highly probable that he was raised on the knees of the teachings of Chassidus.

It is simple that there is no intention in the above, G-d forbid, to disparage any of the righteous souls who were concerned about the aforementioned in that era, for at that time it was in close proximity to the well-known sects that breached the fence, etc., and in a time of emergency, one is concerned even about a very remote doubt. This is not the case after such a long trial period, and primarily after the reality that we see even with physical eyes.

And regarding your mention in your letter about the customs of one's ancestors, etc., all the early Chassidim were children of ancestors who were not Chassidim, and this is well understood.

May it be the will of Hashem that, in accordance with the instructions of the days of Purim from which we draw, that "the Jews had light, and gladness, and joy, and honor," etc., and "sending portions," etc., so too shall it be for us—namely, the drawing together of hearts, the essence of which is *ahavas Yisrael* directed by *ahavas haTorah* and *ahavas Hashem*, all of which are among the foundations of the teachings of Chassidus and its matters.

With respect and blessing,

## 8787*

B"H, 18 Adar, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students of... Yeshivas Lubavitch, Toronto

Shalom u’Bracha!

I was pleased to receive your letter, in which you write about the various *siyumim* you are making.

It is surely unnecessary to emphasize to you that among Jews, a *siyum* is nothing more than a transition to a higher level, such that a *siyum* is truly a beginning to reach further and higher.

May Hashem Yisbarach grant you success so that you may learn with *hasmadah* and *shekidah*—learning that leads to *maaseh*—the fulfillment of *mitzvos* with *hiddur*. May you be a source of true Yiddishe and Chassidishe *nachas* for your parents and teachers. This is actually in your own hands, as our Sages, of blessed memory, have said: **"You labored and you found"**—one only needs to want it.

I hope you had a good and happy Purim and fulfilled all the *inyanim* of Purim. Especially since Jewish children had a very great part in the miracle of Purim, as our Sages, of blessed memory, relate: when Mordechai gathered thousands of Jewish children and studied Torah with them to the point of *mesiras nefesh*, then the decree was nullified, and "the Jews had light, and gladness, and joy, and honor."

May the Ribono shel Olam help that for you, within the rest of *Klal Yisrael*, the promise "so may it be for us" will be fulfilled.

With blessings for success and for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe Shlita,

Nissan Mindel
Secretary

## 8788

B"H, 22 Adar, 5724
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., R' Nosson Menachem, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your book, *Rambam al HaTorah*, and I thank you for your thoughtfulness in sending it to me.

May it be the will of Hashem that you utilize the possibilities at your disposal to disseminate traditional Judaism as explained and in accordance with the instructions of our Torah—*Toras Chaim* (the Torah of life). There are two primary aspects to this: *hora'ah* (Torah, from the word *hora'ah*—instruction) as a guide in life, and Torah (which is the source that gives) life and serves as a roadmap for how life should be lived in accordance with its name.

The essential point in all of the above is the actual deed. In the words of Chazal, "The deed is the essential thing"—the fulfillment of practical *mitzvos*, including their minutiae, down to the slightest detail of the words of the Sages and the customs of Israel, preceded by the negation of everything forbidden, or even that which is undesirable, etc.

Through all of this, a person (*"You are called 'Adam'"*) fulfills the purpose of his creation, as it is written, "Let us make man (*Adam*) in our image, after our likeness." *Adam* is named for *adameh l'elyon* (I will resemble the Most High), as is especially emphasized as a prerequisite for the giving of the Torah: "And you shall be to Me a kingdom of priests." The *avodah* of the *Kohanim* also follows this order: washing (and distancing oneself from everything undesirable) in the *kiyor*, and only after that, the *avodah* in the holy place.

With respect and blessings,

P.S. Regarding the subject of *Rambam al HaTorah* itself, it is understood that most of the Rambam's perspectives and commentaries on the Torah are to be found not in his books that are *piskei halachos* (legal rulings), but rather in his books and treatises whose content is the foundations of the faith, interpretations, and explanations, etc. From this, the conclusion is that while for several reasons it is necessary to bring what is found in the *piskei dinim* of *Yad HaChazakah*—since the explanations in the Torah there are also definitive and absolute *halachah*—the primary place to cite is from his book *Moreh Nevuchim*, his letters, and his commentary on the *Mishnah*. And this is simple.

## 8789

8789

B"H, 22 Adar, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Administration of Pirchei Agudas Yisrael in New York
May Hashem grant them life

Greetings and Blessings,

It was a pleasure to receive your letter, in which you inform me of the upcoming completion of the Six Orders of the Mishnah, to be held this coming Motzaei Shabbos, Shabbos Parshas Vayakhel-Pekudei.

In accordance with the well-known instruction of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe (author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch) that every Jew must study the weekly parsha each day and derive practical guidance for the week’s life from it, there is much to be learned from the aforementioned matter as well. The parshiyos mentioned (Vayakhel-Pekudei) and the parsha of the week that begins this Motzaei Shabbos (Vayikra) speak of the construction of the Mishkan **in actuality.** Its purpose is, as the verse states, "And I will dwell among them," which Chazal interpret with precision: it does not say "in it," but "among them"—within each and every Jew.

This involves making peace and connecting the physical with the spiritual across all levels and categories:

To draw the Shechinah of the Ribono shel Olam into the world, even into this physical world, by means of His dwelling in the Mishkan—which was fashioned from gold, silver, copper, and so on—the materials of the physical world. This is achieved by offering sacrifices from animals, through which the Jewish people sanctify the animal, raising it upon the altar as a pleasing fragrance to Hashem.

Even prior to this, it is achieved through the contribution of the Jewish people to the building of the Mishkan, as they "raised" (which also connotes elevation) gold, silver, etc.

All of this comes about through the inspiration and empowerment of the neshamah over the body, and the nefesh Elokis over the nefesh habehamis.

The path to achieving this peace is, as Chazal instruct, through engagement in Torah. For one who engages in Torah lishmah brings peace to the Heavenly entourage and the earthly entourage.

This is relevant to the completion of the Six Orders of the Mishnah, for peace is the vessel that holds blessing for the Jewish people, as it is said, "Hashem will bless His people with peace." The preface and preparation for this is explicitly stated at the beginning of that very verse (which is why this opening was brought into this Mishnah here): "Hashem will give strength to His people." Strength refers to Torah. Through the giving of the Torah and engagement in it, it follows (as the conclusion of the Six Orders of the Gemara states) that Torah scholars increase peace in the world.

The Torah, which is strength, was given to the Jewish people—who are the "boldest" among the nations—so that they might utilize the strength inherent in their nature for the matters of Torah and mitzvos (the line of "doing good"). The strength of Torah then subdues the brazenness found in the affairs of the world (the line of "turning from evil").

Based on the above, the great necessity of Torah study and the magnitude of its impact become clear—especially during the period of strength in a person's life, when one is young and a bochur.

May it be the will of Hashem that this study be, as Chazal instruct, a study that leads to action—a conduct appropriate to daily life, even in mundane matters and on weekdays.

As is brought in the books of mussar and Chassidus, there is a hint in the opening of the Six Orders of the Mishnah: "From when do we recite the Shema in the evenings?" The beginning of the Torah and the instruction of our Sages in their Mishnah is that in the "evenings"—when there is darkness in the world—it is a mitzvah for everyone to recite the Shema, to proclaim that "Hashem our G-d, Hashem is **One**." The **Aleph** hints at the "Alufo shel Olam" (the Master of the world). By calling out and drawing the **Aleph** into the **Chet** (the seven heavens and the earth) and the **Dalet** (the four directions of the world), we make peace between the Ribono shel Olam and the world.

With respect and blessing.

## 8790

By the Grace of Hashem, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Vayakhel-Pekudei, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Convention of Nshei U’Bnos Chabad
Montreal
May Hashem grant you life!

Blessings and Peace!

In accordance with the well-known Torah teaching of the Alter Rebbe, the Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch, the founder of Chabad, that "a Yid must live with the times"—with the parsha of the week, for the Torah reflects all current events and provides the necessary guidance for daily life—

The parshiyos of **Vayakhel-Pekudei** of this Shabbos, and the parsha of **Vayikra** of the coming Shabbos, contain very appropriate and pertinent guidance for the convention.

I will touch upon a few of them here:

In Vayakhel-Pekudei, the Torah recounts how the Mishkan and all its holy vessels were **actually** made, repeating all the details that had already been conveyed at length in Terumah and Tetzaveh. This entire lengthiness, which the Torah could have technically spared, underscores the importance of **asiyah** (action), as our Sages, of blessed memory, express it: **"The deed is the essential thing."** If previously the discussion was how Hashem conveyed the entire plan of the Mishkan to Moshe Rabbeinu on Mount Sinai, now it is told how the matter was actually **carried out** through the **personal** participation of every man and every woman (**"all the men and women"**); at the same time, it is emphasized that the women provided a living example for the men (**"and the men came with the women"**), with their heartfelt self-sacrifice to fulfill the Divine will.

The inner intent of the Mishkan was **"And I will dwell among them" — within each and every one**: that every Jewish heart and every Jewish home should be a dwelling place for the Divine Shechinah; just as the inner intent of the korbanos was that every Jewish heart should draw closer to Hashem (**"a korban from you"**), as the Torah emphasizes right from the beginning of **Vayikra.**

Through this, the **netzachiyus haTorah** — the eternity of the Torah — finds expression.

For although the Mishkan of gold and silver, etc., was temporarily destroyed, and the korbanos of cattle and sheep were temporarily halted, the Mishkan **"among them"** and the **avodah shebalev** (service of the heart) were never touched; on the contrary, they were even strengthened.

Reflecting on these mentioned parshiyos of the Torah at this time, every man and woman must awaken in themselves new strengths to do everything possible to bring to expression the eternity of the Torah through living deeds in daily life, so that upon every Jewish heart and every Jewish home, Hashem may say: "This is My Mishkan, and their tefillos are My korbanos!"

To help realize the above, not only within oneself but also in others, in the entire surrounding environment — this is the task of Nshei U’Bnos Chabad. For this reason, Hashem has gifted them with a very great measure of heartfelt and deep feelings of **ahavas Hashem, ahavas haTorah,** and **ahavas Yisrael,** and has granted them the merit to be the **akeres habayis** (the foundation/mainstay) of every Jewish home.

May Hashem Yisbarach grant you success in your annual undertaking and in your activities throughout the entire year, to fulfill your far-reaching task to the fullest extent.

With blessings for success and good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8791

27 Adar, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the annual gathering of the "Netzivei HaYeshiva" supporters of Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch in Montreal, may Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

The annual gathering takes place this year shortly after the yahrtzeit of the Rebbe Rashab, the founder of the first Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva in Lubavitch, together with his son, my father-in-law the Rebbe, the co-founder and active director of the Yeshiva in Lubavitch and the founder of the Lubavitcher Yeshiva in Montreal.

One of the directives of the Baal HaHillula, which is especially important for our time, is:

In the present time, one cannot, and one must not, make calculations as to what can be accomplished and what cannot; rather, that which requires improvement—one must immediately set out to address with strenuous effort, and then the Ribono shel Olam helps.

(Kuntres U'Ma'ayan, p. 22)

This instruction is particularly relevant to the field of chinuch. If, years ago, one could still think in certain responsible circles about what could and could not be demanded of the new generation, and how to "attract" them, and so on—it is now entirely clear that the only approach to chinuch is to establish it upon the firm foundations of Torah and mitzvos, without compromises and without dilution, but with the definitive resolve that one must and is obligated to act in this regard with strenuous effort. Then one is assured that one will succeed, with Hashem's help, to the fullest extent.

Especially since our generation is not afraid of a challenge and is always more prepared to accept the full truth than a half-truth, or a quarter-truth.

And this is the approach of "Tomchei Temimim," where the name itself already points to **Toras Hashem Temimah**—the Divine Torah, both the revealed Torah and the inner dimension of Torah, Toras HaChassidus—is **one and whole**; and the students, the **Temimim**, are **whole**—whole in their outlook and whole in their conduct.

The success, with Hashem's help, of the Lubavitcher Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim in Montreal has confirmed how correct this approach is. It is to be hoped that the esteemed balebatim, who have enabled the constant growth, in quantity and in quality, of the Yeshiva throughout all these years, will continue to exert all their efforts to maintain and further expand all the activities of the Yeshiva.

The merit of supporting Torah and spreading Torah and mitzvos will surely stand by everyone, each and every one, in everything they need, both in material and in spiritual matters.

With blessings for success and for good tidings.

In continuation of our conversation when you were here, I cannot hold back from adding that, certainly, the true flowers are meant not only to delight the eye, but primarily to produce fruit and the fruits of fruit—good for food and essential for the sustenance of the species. In the spiritual sense among Jews, and in the language common to our Sages of blessed memory, "fruits" refers to nothing other than mitzvos and good deeds, which are beautiful and magnificent, and which provide continuity and eternal existence for generations and generations of generations.

## 8,793

28 Adar, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

It was with great astonishment, and even greater pain, that I read your letter from yesterday. In it, you write the reasons—ostensibly—to justify your opposition to a religious education program by certain circles, even in the current situation where no other group has the possibility of penetrating the environment and the locations in question. This means that the youth there will be left vulnerable to a contrary education—and not merely a neutral one, as experience in the recent past has shown.

As for the beginning of your letter, where you state that you wish to add further explanation, I did not manage to understand it. For there is nothing new in this explanation; it has already been written two, three, and many more times in the party press. Furthermore, we touched upon this very point in our conversation. Moreover, were it not for this explanation, there would have been no room from the outset for even a mistaken doubt regarding this question. It is understood and simple that all the doubts you write of, and the doubts added in the aforementioned press with various "spices and seasonings" and so on, are not at all comparable to the damage that is liable to befall thousands of children of the Children of Israel—and I fear to say, tens of thousands.

The damage, as I said in our conversation, is not only regarding the youth—through an education that is diametrically opposed—but also the loss of the possibility to introduce a religious atmosphere into places that, were it not for this, might not even know of the very existence of tefillin, kashrus, and so on. As is known to you and your colleagues regarding several such cases, and in particular—for when religious schools are established, even with a minimal program, one is compelled to bring in couples who live a religious life, a shochet, a mohel, a mikveh, and so on.

It often happens that due to the excessive back-and-forth on the matter, one forgets the essence of the question in its simplest form. First and foremost, this entire matter is a practical question that concerns the registration that will take place in a few weeks, and in the weeks following that—regarding the new immigrants who arrive every single month.

The question does not brook delay, since the results—if, G-d forbid, the possibility of opening religious schools by the aforementioned circles is denied—are immediate and will be felt at once in the new immigrant housing. Immediate, quite literally, on that very day; it is possible that there will be no religious element there at all—no kashrus, no Shabbos observance, no family purity, and so on. And after a few days, when the youth visits schools that are supposedly neutral, but in reality—where they will not see or find any religious element—the results are clear.

And after asking your forgiveness, in such a situation and at such a time, one considers what the inner intention of a certain circle is, and that it surely contains the calculation of what the influence will be at the time of the elections, and so on.

Even if you were to say that the concerns you write about are well-founded, and to such an extent that they go beyond the category of a "perhaps" (shema)—such that they have the power to negate a "certainty" (bari) for the sake of immediate benefit—even then, there would be room to say: "the loss is outweighed by the gain." And it is self-deception to say that these concerns are in the category of a "certainty." In my opinion, in most cases they are not even a "doubt," but on the contrary, it is near-certain that they will not materialize. And even if in some place they were to materialize in practice, even there, the gain is greater than the loss you fear.

As I see the situation, and as is tangibly evident in several places in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established), the problem, when viewed without embellishment, is this: on one hand, it is possible that in the coming months, boys and girls will learn about the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He, and will be told about His Torah—and not in a theoretical manner, but (necessarily?) also regarding the practical aspect of it—and in dozens of neighborhoods they will see an example of life according to the Torah and mitzvos. On the other hand, there is an alliance with people from the extreme left, and also within the circle you write about, in order—Heaven forbid—to fight against introducing Hashem, His Torah, and His mitzvos to thousands of families of the Children of Israel. As I said to you in our conversation, for a hungry person, it makes no difference why they are preventing him from getting bread to satisfy his hunger; whatever the intentions may be, he is starving to death, G-d forbid.

Seemingly, there is room for a difficulty: if the situation is so simple as stated above, how is it possible that there is any doubt as to what the approach of a religious person should be? But this, too, is understood from the precision of the *order* of the verse, that "a bribe blinds the eyes of the wise and perverts the words of the righteous." A verse does not lose its simple meaning; even *after* the blindness and perversion have arrived, he is still called "wise and righteous," it is just that he is blind, G-d forbid. Like the parable brought in the books of mussar, that a small piece of paper, if held very close to the eye, covers and hides the entire world in its fullness. And surely for someone like you, further elaboration is superfluous.

It is simple that I have a *limud zechus* (a favorable interpretation) regarding the content of your letter. By way of a preface to what you write at the beginning of your letter—that you "pondered" my words—my hope is strong that it was not my words that you pondered, and for two reasons: First, because they were extremely simple and there is no room for further pondering regarding them. Second, because they are not "my" words, but rather the simple approach of a simple person, which every single individual is obligated to reach and will reach the aforementioned conclusion (aside from the fact that he imagines he has the aforementioned piece of paper). The *limud zechus* is that it is certain and near-certain that these are not your own ponderings, but rather the reaction of someone from the party or the like, who told you about the content of our conversation, and that person cast doubt or even raised a clamor: "How is it possible to touch the interests of a party?"—even if the touching is only in the realm of a doubt or a double-doubt, and especially since a decision had already been made. And since a decision had been made, as the well-known slogan goes, there is no room here for doubt or question; rather, one must find justification for the decision that was reached. Once it is reached, it becomes in the category of "I have decreed a statute, I have issued a decree, and you have no permission to ponder after it."

Before I conclude, I will repeat my request for forgiveness for the aforementioned expressions. It is not, Heaven forbid, that I regret them, for in relation to the gravity of the problem, they are not at all appropriate—they are too weak. The request for forgiveness is for my having used unusual expressions in letters that you receive, since, seemingly, when two people meet once, there is not yet permission to use such expressions, etc.

May it be the will that the aforementioned words will, at the very least over time, emerge from the category of "idle words"—that is, words that have no results. And may the merit of thousands of families of the Children of Israel—who demand with all their might from each and every one: "Do not stand idly by the blood of your neighbor" (in the wake of the denial of the possibility of appropriate education, at the very least minimally appropriate, for their sons and daughters; a demand with a loud voice, and those who do not demand—on the contrary, in truth, their obligation is even more in force)—stand for them.

I will remind you of what you said and repeated a few times in our conversation in connection with the aforementioned problem: "If only they had forsaken Me (meaning—the party) and kept My Torah." I am confident that if you convey the aforementioned words to the party in this phrasing, surely many will agree with it, and even those who do not agree, it will have a weakening effect upon them. And his reward is with him—the reward of every speaker of truth, especially when he is for the time being in the minority.

With respect and with blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

It is understood and simple that I would be pleased to receive your response to all that has been said, even if for the time being you do not agree with all of the above.

It is also understood that you have permission to convey the content of my letter to whoever you think will be helped by this regarding the aforementioned thousands of families of the Children of Israel. In any case, I would be pleased to hear of the results regarding all of the above.

I cannot refrain from adding one more remark: it is ironic that all the arguments you write—the conclusion of which is to deny a certain circle the involvement in religious matters—are the very same arguments that the circle standing to the right of your party uses against your party, with the very same conclusions.

And one more remark that is seemingly superfluous, but for the sake of completeness I must put this into writing as well: it is simple that my outlook is that even when the aforementioned circle in question fulfills all the promises they give regarding the management of the religious school, it is surely and certainly not the maximum, and not even the middle path. And to add also, that this is the same regarding the totality of the state-religious schools in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established), whose level regarding "religious" is in the category of a minimum—of course, this includes the Chabad schools that are in the state-religious education stream. And even the "Independent" religious schools are also at such a level—due to reasons that perhaps in part are not dependent on the management of the aforementioned schools, but in part are certainly dependent on them. There is no room here to elaborate on such a painful and distressing matter.

May we merit that for the upcoming Pesach, all four sons in all the homes of the Children of Israel—in all circles and in all places—will be of the type of the "wise son." And through this, they will hasten the exodus from servitude to redemption, the exodus from the bitter, double-and-redoubled darkness of exile in which the Children of Israel in the United States, in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established), and in all their settlements find themselves, through the true and complete Redemption—until the conclusion of the Seder Pesach as it should be: "Next year in Jerusalem."

With blessings for a good Shabbos, a good month, and a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 8795

*[Adar 5724]*

"You do not calculate hours for months, and they would offer the Rosh Chodesh sacrifice in the Beis Hamikdash, etc." — this is even though the molad then was the true molad (unlike in our times, where it is based on calculation—only an average—as is brought in the Rambam). And the **location** of the molad (where the moon is actually covered) is in Eretz Yisrael and its vicinity (unlike in the United States—where it is already **many** hours **after** it has been covered, etc.).

## 8797

8797

B"H, 11 Nissan, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Moshe Aram,

Shalom u’Bracha,

I was recently informed of your appointment to your new position at the Agency, etc. Since every matter occurs through Hashgacha Pratis, and every appointment provides new opportunities—and consequently, additional responsibility—I wish to express my hope and blessing that you will fully utilize these new opportunities, in addition to those you already possessed. As we discussed during our meeting, may you use them to disseminate the eternal values of our people, the Children of Israel, from the day we became a nation at the standing at Har Sinai.

This is especially pertinent as we see tangibly that these very values are the secret to the eternal existence of our people, the sons and daughters of Israel, despite the fact that we are the fewest among the nations, and "the kindness of the nations is a sin." Our generation has witnessed this as a brand plucked from the fire of the Holocaust and persecutions the likes of which have never been seen, G-d forbid, while all the nations—both enlightened and unenlightened—stood by, etc. We have no one to rely upon but our Father in Heaven, the living G-d, who gives us a Torah of life and its mitzvos, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them."

Since you were chosen unanimously, this further increases your capacity for influence and your potential. May it be His will that you succeed in bringing these matters from potential into actual reality.

As we approach the festival of Matzos, the time of our freedom, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good, I hereby express my blessing for a kosher and happy holiday, and for true freedom—freedom from material worries and freedom from spiritual worries—and to carry this freedom and joy throughout all the days of the year.

With holiday blessings,

It is a pleasant duty for me to express once again my gratitude to you for your interest in the affairs of Kfar Chabad. I am certain that you will continue to extend your assistance to them should they require it. Furthermore—and this is the main point—I hope you will take an interest in what is happening there, not only by hearing about it, but also through personal observation, visits, etc.

#### ***8797***

**Mr. Moshe Aram:** Additional letters to him—see above, Vol. 22, 8685, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 8,798

[11 Nissan 5724]

Thank you for the good news from the 27th of Adar regarding the putting on of Rabbeinu Tam tefillin. Regarding what you wrote about the "trembling" associated with this, etc.: in general, everyone is commanded, "Serve Hashem with joy, and rejoice with trembling." However, regarding your connecting this trembling specifically with the putting on of Rabbeinu Tam tefillin, see the importance—and even **more** than importance—of putting on Rabbeinu Tam tefillin in *Shaar HaKollel*, Chapter 11 (by Rabbi Lavut on the Siddur), and in many other books (specifically in the book *Me'asef LeChol HaMachanot*).

## 8,799

B"H, 11 Nissan, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chassid, G-d-fearing, and meticulous in his mitzvah observance,
R' Shlomo Yosef, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha,

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 6 Nissan, as well as your previous one.

In anticipation of the Festival of Matzos, the season of our freedom, which is approaching for us and for all of Israel for the good, I hereby extend my blessing for a kosher and joyous holiday and for true freedom—freedom from material worries and from spiritual worries—from everything that hinders the avodah of Hashem with joy and a glad heart.

And may this freedom and joy be drawn down into all the days of the year.

Especially since the avodah of Hashem, as we are commanded in our Torah, the Torah of life, encompasses all of a person’s affairs throughout the entire day and night, as it is said: "In all your ways, know Him."

With holiday blessings and for the fulfillment of your requests for the good,

**M. Schneerson**

Regarding what you wrote concerning the shochet...—even at the outset, I did not express an opinion on the substance of the claims or who is correct, etc.—only that there are alarming claims, and consequently, a clarification is necessary. And that is all.

Upon receiving the news regarding your election to the Rabbinate—it is understood that I was pleased that the electors recognized your stature, etc., etc. On the other hand, I was hesitant regarding "the elected"—whether this is a matter for writing a "Mazal Tov," etc., or otherwise—since this is an entry into a position full of trials, and complex ones at that. May it be the will of Hashem that you emerge from all the trials in peace and completeness, and even more—and this will prove that from its inception, it was a matter of a Mazal Tov blessing and success.

## 8800

11 Nissan, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem keep them and grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

Every Yom Tov has its own unique content and specific directives, which must find expression not only on the days when the Yom Tov is celebrated, but throughout all the days of the year.

The lesson of every Yom Tov is twofold: in the direction of *aseh tov* (doing good) — what one must do; and in the direction of *sur meira* (turning away from evil) — what one must avoid. Often, the second part is even more important, for if one is not guarded against the undesirable, it can happen that the good and positive is also utilized in a negative direction.

The above is especially important in connection with the first of the Yomim Tovim — Pesach, the Yom Tov of *Yetzias Mitzrayim*, which occupies such a central place in Jewish life that the Torah has commanded every Jew to remember and mention *Yetzias Mitzrayim* **every day**, and each day itself — both by day and by night.

* * *

The redemption from Mitzrayim, the content of **Yom Tov Pesach**, is connected with the **Korban Pesach**.

The redemption from Mitzrayim was not merely a redemption of many individuals—of six hundred thousand adults and their families—but the redemption began from "I have surely seen the affliction of **My people**" (*ami*), for which reason it was demanded of Pharaoh, "Send out **My people**," and Moshe fulfilled his mission, "And take out My people, the children of Israel, from Mitzrayim."

Accordingly, one might have expected that the *Korban Pesach* would also emphasize the point (motive) of the **people** (*am*) of Israel, the entire community. In fact, however, the approach and the instruction are the exact opposite. It is true that the instruction was given to the *entire congregation of Israel*, to all Jews together as one congregation, but the instruction was: every house must have its own *Korban Pesach*; everyone had to be previously assigned and counted for the *Korban Pesach*; everyone had to be in his designated house or *chaburah* (group) for the entire time of eating the *korban*.

Through this, the Torah teaches us that the way to accomplish things—even when it concerns accomplishing for the *klal* (community) and even when it concerns the redemption of the *klal*—is that while the orientation must be toward the *klal*, the content must be that each person must first and foremost concentrate on himself, his household, and his very immediate circle. And even there, one must concentrate not on general considerations and communal resolutions, but rather focus his main attention and energy on carrying out, in daily life, the individual "small" decisions; for it is precisely this that, in the end, brings about the redemption of the individual and the redemption of the *klal*.

This instruction is especially important for leaders and heads of groups and movements, and particularly for those who are meant to be spiritual leaders in their communities. Too often, one is preoccupied with "world problems" and "great matters," and it is only from time to time, or very rarely, that one hears a leader concerning himself with the "ordinary small" problems of daily life that directly affect his community members.

The more prominent a leader is, the more he "feels" he must speak to all of humanity; and if he is gifted with a good imagination, he fancies that he is also speaking to future generations. If he is endowed with oratorical abilities, he considers it his duty to shake the "world conscience" with fiery words that find an echo in the press, so that he becomes a leader of leaders and a spokesman whom others envy for "his press," seeking to imitate him and surpass him.

Not infrequently, the "led" listener is dragged along, and together with the leader, they decide what the various governments must do, how humanity in general must conduct itself, and how to make all future generations happy. And "naturally," after such "world decisions," there is no room to "lower oneself" and make a great outcry about the high percentage of children whom the "led" are raising in such a way that they cannot, under any circumstances, be categorized as the *ben chacham* (wise son) of the Haggadah—not to mention the children who receive a more "advanced education" and are a fifth son who is not at the Seder at all.

And are these leaders truly certain that every one of the "led" parents is at the Seder?

* * *

As it is in the *klal*, so it is in the *prat* (individual): every person consists of a "leader"—(the head and heart, *sechel* and *middos*)—and "the led"—(the limbs). And here, too, the same thing often happens as mentioned above: one makes general, communal resolutions regarding the entire *olam katan* (the person): one will be good and pious toward Hashem and toward people. Immediately upon waking, he acknowledges that Hashem places the *neshamah* into him that gives him life; already at the first *brachah*, he knows that Hashem is *Melech HaOlam*—the full master of the entire world; quite early, before *davening*, he takes upon himself the *mitzvah aseh* of "Love your neighbor as yourself."

However, when it comes to details and "small matters"—such as not "swallowing" the words in *davening* in general and in *Krias Shema* in particular, reflecting on Hashem's greatness and, *lehavdil*, on the smallness of man (not excluding oneself) before every *Shemoneh Esrei* each day—he lacks the time and patience. Regarding guarding oneself from *hasagas gevul* (encroaching on another’s livelihood) by taking a customer from another—he fears that **through this**, there will be a lack in the *parnassah* that... Hashem gives him. And when Pesach arrives and he needs to help a simple poor person with *maos chitim*—he imagines the splendor of *Yetzias Mitzrayim* and decides that just as it was then, he and his household must have *kelei kesef u’kelei zahav u’semalos* (silver vessels, gold vessels, and garments), so what is left for *maos chitim*?

* * *

May it be the will of Hashem—that He bless and grant success—that every one of you learns from these, and all other, urgent instructions of the Yom Tov of *Zeman Cheiruseinu* (the time of our liberation). And just as at the time of *Yetzias Mitzrayim*, the redemption of the *klal* came as a result of the redemption of the *prat*, may it be so today:

That every Jewish individual and every Jewish family, their daily conduct—down to the smallest detail—should be conduct according to Torah, without any compromises and without dilution. This will bring the *Geulah HaAmitis VeHaShleimah* through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, and it will be fulfilled: "As in the days of your exodus from the land of Mitzrayim, I will show you wonders."

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 8802

[26-27 Nissan, 5724]

This is, of course, provided that it does not involve an issue of *hasagas gevul* (encroachment).

Between the place of the *krias haTorah* and the *Aron HaKodesh* — there should be at least one row of seating as a partition.

The *mechitzah* must be higher than a person’s height.

**Regarding one that is not transparent** for those looking from the women’s section: Why force oneself to rely on a *heter* (which is, in any case, a great stretch) — without feeling that here the women’s section is higher **(and even more so)** in elevation than the men’s section? See *Sukkah* 51b, bottom: "And they would come... and they would still come... (until) they instituted... from above." And in *Chiddushei Aggados* it states that the change of them sitting above is called **in itself** a **great** *tikkun* compared to before!

And in an offhand manner, he nullified with his words the equivalence of all this!

***

## 8803

B"H, 27 Nissan, 5724
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 25 Nissan, in which you write regarding various matters, etc., and opinions concerning the upcoming term of study.

However, the main point is entirely missing. I am referring to your diligence and perseverance in the study of Torah, both Nigleh and Chassidus. Furthermore, I have heard nothing from the sidelines regarding this, especially following my letter from the middle of the winter, which surely reached you as well, since it was intended for you too. Beyond what was stated there—which is the essential point—it is incumbent upon each and every student of the holy Yeshiva Toras Emes to strive and do everything within his power to increase the number of students. Yet, regarding your activities in this area, nothing has been heard either. Surely, in your return letter, you will inform me in detail, as mentioned above, regarding the progress of each one of you in the study of Nigleh and the study of Chassidus (and it goes without saying that the manner of study must be as Chazal instructed: that it leads to action, meaning progress in the performance of mitzvos with hidur). Likewise, [inform me] how many students have joined the walls of the Yeshiva through the efforts of each one of you.

Regarding this, it is said: "If one says, 'I have labored and found,' believe him; 'I have not labored and found,' do not believe him." This means that if they have not found [success], it is certain that they did not exert the necessary effort.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above, and likewise regarding each of your fellow students, may they live and be well.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S. It is understood that the *kaluginker* (the adversary) will not lack excuses and justifications (if, G-d forbid, the above is lacking), and will cast the blame on someone else, claiming that you are in the right. Chazal have already informed us that whoever listens to and accepts such excuses is listening to the will of the *kaluginker*.

Based on the above, it is understood and simple that you must be within the four cubits of Yeshiva Toras Emes, and the study must be *aliba denafshei* (for one's own self), as mentioned above, without paying heed to the enticements of the *kaluginker*. And this is clear.

## 8804

8804

B"H, 27 Nissan, 5724
Brooklyn.

Blessings and peace!

I received your letter in due time, but for several reasons, the response has been delayed until now. It is my hope that by the time you receive this letter, your state of mind has already improved.

I am directing this response toward the conclusion and seal of the month of Nissan, the month of freedom and redemption—which, of course, includes personal redemption from all thoughts and matters that cause confusion—and as a preparation for the month of Iyar, the month of radiance (*ziv*), for as our Sages of blessed memory explain, the radiance and light in this world of ours are intensified during this time.

It is understood that my intention in what I have said concerns you: that now is an opportune time to increase Hashem’s blessing for your success in all your affairs, beginning with the strengthening of your health in the literal sense. Through an action in this regard (even a small one) on the part of the person, they grant and add many times over in blessings from Above. The primary action required of a person is to strengthen their trust in Hashem and to contemplate His providence—His *hashgacha pratis* over every detail of every human being and every detail of their lives. The immediate conclusion to be drawn from this is not to pay heed to thoughts that arouse any worry or sadness, Heaven forbid. This is especially true according to what is explained in the teachings of our Rebbes, the *Torah* of Chassidus: that the matter of sadness is absolutely negated. This negation should not be achieved through debate with oneself or by bringing proofs and the like, but rather through *hesech hadaas*—diverting one’s attention and not paying heed to these thoughts. If it is not easy to rid oneself of them, one of the advised methods is to occupy the mind with matters that have no connection whatsoever to the previous thought—not even to negate that thought, but simply with something entirely different.

Furthermore, since everything must have some foothold in the ways of nature, it is appropriate that you consult a doctor and follow their instructions. As to which doctor to turn to, consult your family physician. Do all of the above with strong trust, in the style of King David, the sweet singer of Israel, on behalf of every Jewish man and woman: "Hashem is my shepherd, I shall not lack; Hashem is for me, I will not fear," and with health and a good heart.

With blessings for a good state of mind and for good tidings in all the above, and with regards to your parents, may they live and be well.

P.S. I would like this letter to be received while it is still the month of Nissan, or at the very least by the beginning of the month of Iyar—the letter is being sent via express mail.

#### ***8804***

**As our Sages explain:** See Rosh Hashanah 11a.

## 8778

B"H, 27 Nissan, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants of the 11th annual luncheon of Agudas N'shei U’Bnos Chabad in Cleveland, Ohio
May Hashem grant you life.

Blessings and peace!

It is with pleasure that I received the news regarding your upcoming luncheon on Sunday, the first day of Rosh Chodesh Iyar (30 Nissan), may it come upon us for good.

May Hashem Yisborach help that this annual endeavor be crowned with great success in all respects.

Since this event is taking place at the conclusion of the month of Nissan, it is to be hoped that on this occasion, the significance of this month of redemption and the Yom-Tov of Pesach will be emphasized for all Jewish women, and especially for Chabad women, particularly regarding *chinuch* *al taharas hakodesh*. For the entire foundation of (the *Seder* and of) the *Haggadah* with which the Yom-Tov of Pesach **begins** is the *mitzvah* in the Torah, "**And you shall tell your son**"—to recount and explain to the **children** the significance of *Yitziyas Mitzrayim*, also as a preparation for *Kabbalas HaTorah*, in order to reach the level of "**They recognized Him first**" ("the children were the first to recognize the Almighty"), as was the case at the splitting of the Red Sea, with which the Yom-Tov of *Yitziyas Mitzrayim* **concludes**.

The *Seder* and the *Haggadah Shel Pesach* teach us that one must not give up hope even on a *ben rasha*, and one must bring him to the *Seder* table as well. At the same time, one must not rely on the *ben chacham* to grow into a good and pious Jew on his own. One must occupy oneself with **all** Jewish children, without exception.

This is, in fact, one of the tasks of Chabad women everywhere: to support the institutions and activities that aim to elevate all Jewish children to the level of a *ben chacham*. This is in addition to the primary task of *N'shei U’Bnos Chabad* to bring as much light and *kedushah* of *ner mitzvah v’Torah ohr* into their homes and into their surroundings.

With blessings for success and for good tidings.

#### ***8778***

**They recognized Him first:** Sotah 11b.

## 8488

B"H, 28 Nissan, 5724
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the accomplished Chossid, who acts with distinction in Torah and mitzvos, etc., who sits in judgment and directs his community with integrity,

Rabbi S.
Shlita

Greetings and blessings!

Through the esteemed Chossid, the accomplished, noble, and distinguished Rabbi Y.L. Raskin, may he live, I received the request for a blessing and a *pidyon nefesh* on behalf of his son, Maimon, may he live.

At an auspicious time, I will mention him at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of the request. May it be the will of Hashem that in the near future you will be able to share good news regarding this, news that is visibly and revealedly good.

We are currently in the month of Nissan, the month of redemption—which includes redemption from all matters that distract from the *avodah* of Hashem with joy and a glad heart.

During the days of *Sefirah*, the manner of counting is not merely ordinal (first, second), but rather "one, two"—meaning that one ascends from level to level, adding to and also including the levels of the past. It is an increase in the gates of holiness, as explained in the books of *chochmas ha'emes* regarding the concept of the days of *Sefirah*: to ascend through the forty-nine gates of holiness and reach the ultimate fiftieth gate, as it is written, "You shall count fifty days."

May there likewise be an ascent and improvement regarding the physical health of the aforementioned, within the entirety of *Klal Yisrael*. As is known, the great virtue of the Jewish body—in the words of our *Rabbeinu HaZaken*, "And You chose us from among all nations and tongues" refers to the material body (see *Tanya Kadisha*, Chapter 49).

May your holy activities on behalf of the holy institutions named after my father-in-law, the Rebbe, where the *pidyon nefesh* will be read at the holy *tziyun*, stand to his merit in the aforementioned matters.

With respect and with blessings for a good Shabbos and for good tidings.

#### ***8488***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 7, p. 284; completed based on the secretariat's copy.

**Rabbi S. Shlita:** Messas, Casablanca.

**The manner of counting:** See *Torah Or* 34b; *Sefer HaMitzvos* of the Tzemach Tzedek 28a.

**As explained:** See *Likkutei Torah*, Bamidbar 12a and onwards.

## 8807

B"H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Vayehi Biyom HaShemini,
Shabbos Mevarchim Chodesh Iyar,
5724. Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter.

Based on the statement of our Sages in the Sifra on the Parsha of this week: "And Moshe said" — Moshe said to Yisroel... **"Just as** He (Hashem) is unique in His world, so too shall your avodah be unique before Him... If you do so, the glory of Hashem will appear to you."

The interpretation of the Baal Shem Tov on this is well-known: This is a *klal gadol* (great principle) — that a person should always have only one thought in the avodah of the Creator, may He be blessed. He should think that everything that exists in the world is entirely filled with the Creator, may He be blessed. He should bind himself to His glory, may He be blessed, with complete love. His thought should always be attached [to Him]. This is the interpretation of the verse by way of *remez*: "And he shall not depart from the Sanctuary." When he must speak of the matters of this world, it should be... like a person who leaves his home to go outside, but his mind is set on returning immediately; while he is walking, he is thinking about when he will return to his home... his true home being the Creator, may He be blessed.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that each and every one fulfills all that is stated above with true joy, just as it was on the "eighth day" then.

"And all the people saw and sang" — the fulfillment of the aforementioned promise: "If you do so, the glory of Hashem will appear to you."

With blessings for success in your holy work and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***8807***

General details. Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 7, p. 297, and completed according to a photocopy of the letter.

**Sefer Tzavaas HaRivash:** Published by Kehot, section 84.

**In the Sifra:** Shemini 9:6.

**Interpretation of the Baal Shem Tov:** *Sefer Tzavaas HaRivash*.

**Klal gadol:** See *Shabbos* 68a.

**Everything is filled:** *Berachos* 10a. And see *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah*, end of chapter 2.

**Bind himself... with love:** See *Sifrei*, Va'eschanan 6:5.

**From the Sanctuary:** See *Sanhedrin* 19a.

**Thinking about when:** Note the words of the Baal Shem Tov: Wherever the *ratzon* (will) is, there the person is considered to be standing (Zos Chanukah, 5640, ch. 3 — and not merely a thought, as the simple reading of the language in *Tzavaas HaRivash* might suggest).

**And sang:** And they praised (Targum Yonasan). And in the Sifra there: They opened their mouths and recited a song.

## 8808

8808

B"H, 30 Nissan, Erev Rosh Chodesh Iyar, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter.

We stand on a day that unites Nissan, the month of Geulah—the Geulah of the body and the Geulah of the soul (from Mitzrayim, the nakedness of the land)—together with Iyar, which is the month of *ziv*, the "radiance of the blossoms" in the land, and named for the Patriarchs, who are the "radiance of the world."

May it be the will of Hashem that we merit, very soon, true peace and the unification of spirituality and physicality—beginning with the spirituality and physicality within the "small world," which is man, the body and the soul, and extending to spirituality and physicality in the world at large.

As our Sages say: One who engages in Torah *lishmah* brings peace to the heavenly retinue and the earthly retinue. This is explained at length by Rabbeinu HaZaken, the author of the Tanya (the *pnimiyus* of Torah, the *neshamta d’oraysa*), and the Shulchan Aruch (the *nigleh* of Torah, the *gufi Torah*).

This is also related to the parsha we have just concluded, according to the interpretation of our Sages at the beginning of the parsha:

Moshe said to Yisrael... **Just as** He (Hashem) is unique in the world, so too must your *avodah* be unique before Him; see there.

With blessings for success in your holy work,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8809

8809

B"H, 30 Nissan, Erev Rosh Chodesh Iyar, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, man of action, G-d-fearing, learned, etc., R' Shmuel, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

Following our conversation, I reiterate my blessing that your trip, together with your wife, the Rabbanit, may she live, to visit Eretz Yisrael—may it be rebuilt speedily by Moshiach Tzidkeinu—should be in a good and auspicious hour.

If it is said regarding one who passes by a perfume shop that its scent is absorbed, how much more so is this true of a visit that is not merely in passing, but in the Land of which it is said, "The eyes of Hashem your G-d are always upon it, from the beginning of the year to the end of the year." In that Land, the possibility is granted for the absorption of the scent, and internally as well—matters from which the neshamah derives pleasure, and the body derives pleasure as well. For the body of a Yid is also holy, and possesses the holiness of the body.

As is also stated in the words of Rabbeinu HaZaken, "And You have chosen us from among all peoples and tongues—this refers to the body," etc. (Tanya, Chapter 49, see there carefully).

And as we stand...

With respect and blessings.
