## 8114

[?] Nissan, 5724

To the esteemed and distinguished, etc., R' Naftali, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your question—a request for an explanation regarding the concept of *Shechinah*, which is mentioned many times in the words of our Sages, of blessed memory.

This matter is explained well, especially in the books of Chassidus and *maamarim* of Chassidus, and in many places—you will find them through the subject index printed at the end of *Tanya*, *Torah Or*, *Likutei Torah*, and others.

Nevertheless, I will touch upon the matter briefly here, although, naturally, not in an exhaustive manner at all, for the canvas is too short, etc.

Since Hashem is the ultimate perfection and is devoid of all limitations and boundaries, it is understood that, in the phrasing of our Alter Rebbe, the essence of *Elokus* is not that He is a Creator of worlds. Simultaneously, in the phrasing of the Rambam in his *Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah*, He is the One who brings all existence into being; all beings exist only from the truth of His existence, and all beings require Him. It is therefore also understood that just as it is impossible for a created being to grasp the concept of creation *yesh me'ayin* (something from nothing), so too—and this is the very point—it is impossible for a created being to grasp *Elokus*, even as *Elokus* is the Creator of the world and the One who brings all existence into being.

In the phrasing of the great Jewish philosophers: "If I knew Him, I would be Him."

Even though one discerns and understands that the thing does not create itself, and one is compelled to say that the created *yesh* has a source that brings it into being, this understanding is merely a logical necessity regarding the existence of the Creator, but not an understanding of *Elokus* itself, even from the perspective that He is a Creator.

The language of the Rambam mentioned above, that all beings require Him, includes that they do not only require Him for the essence of their creation and the point of their existence, but they also require Him for all the needs of their existence and their vitality, down to the most minute details (although, according to the teachings of Chassidus—and unlike the *Moreh Nevuchim*—the details are also subject to *Hashgacha*; even the smallest detail is under the *Hashgacha Pratis* of Hashem, who desired to oversee even the minute details of creation and the created beings). And it arose in the *Ratzon HaElyon* (the Supernal Will) that there should be *Hashgacha* and an extension of *Elokus* below—including matters that the human intellect can grasp.

In the phrasing of the Sweet Singer of Israel: "When I behold Your heavens, the work of Your fingers, etc.," to the point that this includes an instruction for man’s *avodah* to his Creator: "Lift your eyes on high and see who created these" (as explained at length in the *maamar* of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe on the aforementioned verse, which also serves as an introduction and foundation for *Sefer HaChakirah* by his grandson, the Tzemach Tzedek).

These matters of the extension of *Elokus* that are enclothed within the world below, to the point that it is revealed even to the created being, are the level called *Shechinah*, so named because it "dwells" (*shochenes*) and enclothes itself.

And there is a fundamental point here: one must not, Heaven forbid, divide the Above into separate parts (this is only from the perspective of the observer and the created being—that there is a matter he understands and a matter he does not understand). But in the truth of the matter, there are no "things" in the plural, but rather one existence that is in absolute simplicity.

And *kal v'chomer*: If regarding the human soul, one cannot divide it into 248 parts, or 365 parts, or 613 parts, and yet the eye of the observer distinguishes between the vitality in the foot and the vitality in the brain in the head—even though in both, it is one and the same thing: the soul that gives life to the body—how much more so, and to an infinite degree of distinction, is this the case regarding the Above. Therefore, regarding what is stated that the *Shechinah* dwells in the *Beis HaMikdash*, the meaning is not, Heaven forbid, that it is *only* the aspect of *Shechinah*, but rather to emphasize that the *Elokus* is there in a manner of "dwelling" and "enclothing," to the point that it was visible even to physical eyes—that the place of the *Aron* was not included in the measurements, the ten miracles that occurred in the *Beis HaMikdash*, etc., etc.

As stated above, the aforementioned is only one detail in explaining the concept of *Shechinah*, and there are many more. Even within this detail, many more explanations are found in various books of Chassidus and *maamarim* of Chassidus.

It is my hope that you have fixed times for the study of the teachings of Chassidus, in *ksav yad* (manuscripts), with an increase on the day of Shabbos, which is holy to Hashem.

With respect and blessing for a kosher and happy Pesach.

B"H, 3 Iyar, 5724
Brooklyn.

Nusach HaAri,
Manchester,

## 8412

B"H, 7 Iyar, 5724
Brooklyn

To the participants in the study of the holy Tanya
at the Shaarei Tefillah Synagogue, in Toronto
May they live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

It was with pleasure that I learned of the completion of the third part of the Tanya, *Iggeret HaTeshuvah*, on Sunday, Parshas Emor, "And you shall say," Pesach Sheni.

May it be the will of Hashem that, as with every matter of the completion of Torah—the conclusion of any subject in our Torah, especially when done in public—there will be an increase in the study of Torah. This includes an increase in the vitality and light within this study. Regarding the increase brought about by the students, we are promised—in this and similar matters, and as the conclusion and seal of the aforementioned *Iggeret HaTeshuvah*—that "a person who sanctifies himself a little from below, they sanctify him much from above."

Furthermore, it adds an explanation to this: as stated previously, etc., regarding the level of *sovev kol almin*, meaning that the sanctification from above is not only "much" in quantity, but also in quality. And more than that—it is an *ein eroch* (incomparable), an *ein eroch* of *sovev kol almin* relative to *memale kol almin*.

From the continuation immediately following this: "And so it is exactly regarding the matter of reward, etc.," it is understood that everything stated above applies also to the reward for the mitzvah mentioned—reward in the World to Come and in this world—for the study of Torah is among the things whose fruits one eats in this world, while the principal remains for the World to Come.

As is the custom from time immemorial to connect the matters of the week with the weekly Parsha: The teaching of Chazal regarding the verse "Emor v'amarta" (Speak and you shall say) is well known—"to warn the adults regarding the children." Just as there is a reality of greatness and smallness in the world at large, so too, in the "small world" that is man, every person possesses his own greatness and his own smallness. The greatness in man is the intellect in the brain and the feeling in the heart, and the smallness in man is (even to the point of) the aspect of action within him. Man is commanded that the "great" within him should warn the "small," in accordance with the warning of Chazal that study must be for the sake of action, and even more so, that "great is study" (the essence of the greatness in study is that) which leads to action.

In all of the above, there is also the lesson of Pesach Sheni. As explained by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisrael: "The meaning of Pesach Sheni is that there is no such thing as 'lost'; one can always rectify. Even one who was *tamei*, one who was on a distant journey, and even 'for you'—meaning it was by his own will—nevertheless, one can perform a *tikkun*," provided one truly desires it. Furthermore, there is no limitation of time in this, etc.—unlike the first Pesach, which is seven days, etc.—for the matter of *teshuvah* happens in a single hour and a single moment, and one does not move from there until he is forgiven, and until it is "for a favor" before Hashem, and he is pleasing and beloved before Him, may He be blessed, etc.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8,433

B”H, 8 Iyar, 5724
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of Monday, in which you write the main points of your life story.

It is surely unnecessary to emphasize the necessity of conducting one’s daily life in accordance with the instructions of our Torah, the Torah of life (instruction in life), for this is the only way to be happy—both in spirituality and in physicality, both in the life of the World to Come and in the life of this world. Based on this, the answer to your questions is also understood: you must strive to continue your studies in a school and an environment imbued with yiras shamayim. Taking into account the influence of the street, etc., one needs a firm yiras shamayim, without being impressed by the temptations and incitements that come from the "left." Regarding the schools you mention, the Bais Yaakov seminary certainly has priority over many of the other schools.

Regarding your second question: at your age, which you write is fifteen, the friendship you write about is of no benefit and is absolutely undesirable. It is not only undesirable according to the instructions of our Torah, the Torah of life, but even according to the simple common sense of the people of the world, it leads to completely undesirable results. Surely, the weakness in your health and the mental strain are, at least in part, a result of the aforementioned or from thinking about the aforementioned.

As to your question of how to refuse to continue the friendship in question—the answer is also based on what has been said: it is not that you are refusing any person, but rather that you are fulfilling the instruction of our Torah, the Torah of life. Furthermore, even the other party, if he is truly religious, ought to do the same, out of a full understanding of the Torah’s instruction.

May it be Hashem’s will that you bring good news regarding all of the above.

With blessings.

## 8815

10 Iyar, 5724
Brooklyn

To the distinguished Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent scholar,
Rabbi M. HaKohen, may he live

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your book, *Chelkas Meir*, and I offer my congratulations.

Along with this, I join the gathering of those who bless you, especially in honor of the conference arranged in your honor.

May it be the will of Hashem that for many years to come, you will utilize all the possibilities that exist, as well as the possibilities that can be created, to establish traditional Judaism—Judaism without compromises—in a manner of "do not fear anyone."

For if this is the only path of our Torah, the Torah of truth, in all times and in all places, then it is certainly so in this country and in this era, which is full of confusion and blurring of boundaries, to the point of changing values, and even further—to the point of calling evil good and good evil, putting darkness for light and light for darkness.

And we have been promised—"He who comes to purify"—and the precision of our Rabbeinu HaZaken (the author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch) is well known: "to purify others"—"is assisted."

With respect and blessing.

As is customary in such matters, I have transcribed here some of my notes (at least in haste) regarding the contents of the book:

**At the beginning.** The Rambam’s introduction. "**All the mitzvos, etc., were given with their interpretation, as it is said, 'And I will give you the tablets of stone, and the Torah, and the mitzvah'—'Torah' refers to the Written Torah, and 'the mitzvah' refers to its interpretation, etc.—the Oral Torah.**" Seemingly, this requires study, for we derive that the mitzvos were given with their interpretation from what is written regarding the *shemitah* year, "And Hashem spoke to Moshe at Mount Sinai," as is found in *Toras Kohanim* there. And it is even more difficult, as the Rambam himself brings this source for this matter in his introduction to the *Peirush HaMishnayos*.

Perhaps it can be explained based on what is known regarding the principles of the Rambam, that "it is his way to take the simplest exposition, etc., and sometimes he brings a verse that is not mentioned in the Gemara at all" (*Yad Malachi*, Principles of the Rambam, and references there). Based on this, the precision of the *Tzofnas Paneach* on the Rambam (by the Rogatchover) is also resolved, for in the *Shas* (*Berachos* 5a), it explains "the mitzvah" as referring to the Mishnah, etc., "to teach them," as referring to the Gemara. And this is well understood.

However, it is still difficult, for according to the Rambam, we only learn that the mitzvos and their interpretation were given to Moshe at Sinai. From where do we know that *divrei sofrim*, etc., and everything that a veteran student is destined to **innovate** were also given to Moshe at Sinai? Perhaps it can be said that he follows his own system, that all decrees, enactments, and customs, etc., are a *mitzvah* to obey (see *Hilchos Mamrim*, beginning), and if so, the definition of this *mitzvah* includes *divrei sofrim*, etc.

**By the way:** The Rambam’s introduction to the *Peirush HaMishnayos* on *Seder Zeraim*—even though it is printed as such in the *Shas*, etc.—it is evident from its content that it is not dedicated to *Seder Zeraim* at all, but rather to the entire *Shas*.

**There.** A discussion regarding the matter that a *ben noach* is not commanded in *kiddush hashem*. In the *Sefer HaMitzvos* of the Rambam (Positive Mitzvah 9), he writes explicitly that this is so in the Gemara in *Sanhedrin*. Furthermore: he writes in the *Sefer HaMitzvos* there afterward, and brings proof for this mitzvah from the verse "And I shall be sanctified among the children of Israel"—even though he already wrote this at the beginning of the mitzvah—it implies that here his intention is to point out that this mitzvah is an obligation (only) for Israel—as he wrote before this—and he explains that our Sages (who said that a *ben noach* is only commanded in seven mitzvos) derived this from what is written, "among the children of Israel."

**At the end.** Regarding the words of the *Marcheshes*, that since women are exempt from *Hallel*, then according to the one who says that the reading of the *Megillah* is equivalent to *Hallel*, they should also be exempt from the *Megillah*. And this is the reasoning of the *Bahag*.

If so, it must be that the *Bahag* disagrees with the *Tosafos* (s.v. *Mi*, *Sukkah* 38a). And according to him, women would not be obligated in *Hallel* on the nights of Pesach, contrary to the simple reading of the *Shulchan Aruch*, which does not bring a dissenting opinion on this—and see *Shulchan Aruch HaRav*, 472, paragraph 25. I do not have the *Sefer Marcheshes* at hand.

## 8816

8816

B"H, 1st of Iyar, Parshas Emor, Pesach Sheini, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter.

Regarding these days: Our Sages, of blessed memory, state, "Amor v'Amarta" (Speak and you shall say) — to warn the adults concerning the children. This concept of greatness and smallness exists in the world at large, and similarly, it exists in the "small world" that is man. In every person, there is the "great" and the "small." The great part of man is his head, his Chochma, and his intellect, while the small part of man is his limbs and the aspect of action within him. Man is commanded that the great part of him must warn the small part. Just as our Sages warn that learning must be for the sake of doing, there is an added dimension here: the greatness of learning lies in the fact that it leads to action.

In all of the above, there is also a lesson from Pesach Sheini. As my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisrael, explained: "The concept of Pesach Sheini is that nothing is ever lost. One can always rectify matters, even one who was tamei, one who was on a distant journey, and even regarding 'lachem'—even if it was done willfully—nevertheless, one can still achieve rectification" if one truly desires it. Furthermore, there is no limitation or measurement in time—unlike Pesach Rishon, which is limited to seven days, etc.—for the essence of Teshuvah can be achieved in a single hour and a single moment. There is no limitation in this matter—unlike Pesach Rishon, where chametz may not be found in one's possession—for through complete Teshuvah, even intentional sins ("lachem," as mentioned above) are transformed into merits. Through Teshuvah, one does not move from that state until he is forgiven, until he is "for a favor" before Hashem, and is pleasing and beloved before Him, may He be blessed, etc.

With blessings for good tidings in general and in particular,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8,419

18 Iyar, 5724
Brooklyn

Rabbi [Name],
Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos, and addressing each point in order:

1) The question of the Conservative rabbis:

In my opinion, the hesitation regarding this straightforward matter is puzzling. I mean that the arguments (or as they call them, the "compromises") you mention have no place at all. This is not a compromise, but a surrender of the entire issue. It is clear that from their side, they are demanding to be recognized just as others are recognized, and as is well known, this is the crux of the matter.

Consequently, a compromise in one area **must** inevitably lead to a similar compromise in other areas ([...] regarding the area of Gittin), and first and foremost regarding synagogues, rabbis, marriages, and so on. They demand this as a matter of course—in all corners of the globe, including, first and foremost, in Eretz Yisrael. They merely add that, naturally, one must be an expert in the specific field; therefore, one must be proficient in the laws of Gittin if dealing with a Get, and in the laws of Kiddushin if one wishes to perform a marriage, and similarly regarding synagogues.

The compromise that someone will decide that a specific individual **from their ranks** is reliable, and that is all—this will **certainly** be interpreted as **proof** that the Conservative movement itself is not disqualified, but rather that one must be knowledgeable, etc.—a requirement that is also demanded of the Orthodox. Furthermore, this is merely pouring oil on the fire. If they tell the Conservatives that the Orthodox will be the ones to decide who is "fit," this is not a compromise, but on the contrary, it only increases the division. Moreover, there is no salvation in this at all, because if someone validates a certain individual today as being "fit," then in principle they are recognizing their rabbis, and consequently, they can grant *semicha*, etc. The matter is simple, and any further elaboration is superfluous. I will only add two points, which are also fundamental:

a) Regardless of how things are interpreted at your conference or in your circles, the deciding factor will be how these things are interpreted in public opinion, in the press, etc., and primarily in their stronghold—New York—where they control all avenues of publicity. *D’le* (a word to the wise is sufficient).

b) You are surely aware of the battle in London against the Chief Rabbi, Rabbi Brodie, and similarly, the well-known telegram of "The Seven" (regarding religious coercion), and recently, the resolutions of the Conservative convention. It is highly doubtful that the timing of all these together is merely coincidental. It is highly probable that this is a calculated tactic. If, G-d forbid, one of the compromises you write about—or anything similar—is accepted, they will exploit it not only to cause destruction in this specific area, but to intensify their attack by all means and in all areas. As we have seen tangibly in the past, any issue is easier to overcome at its inception, when the controversy is still minor. This is not the case when one makes concessions, etc.; the appetite of the one to whom you conceded only grows, until eventually there is no room left for compromise, only for total submission to them. And a battle against total submission is linked to a much greater controversy, much greater division of hearts, etc.

To substantiate the "concern" mentioned above, there is room to add another detail: as the situation stands, even according to their own words, the question concerns a **small number** of Conservative rabbis. That is to say, this is not a matter of livelihood or the collapse of congregations, but **solely** a question of prestige. Even in the future, it is highly doubtful that the number of those among them who would want to deal with Gittin will increase, for several reasons. Consequently, this is not a concession toward a specific individual, but a concession regarding prestige—that is, toward their ideology.

The argument you write, that a significant portion of the fundraising comes through them, and the similar argument brought here, that they represent hundreds of thousands of organized people, etc.—it is simple that for this very reason, one would be forced to permit all of the above regarding the Reformers as well. According to statistics, the Reformers are wealthier in funds and also have a larger number of organized people.

Since you already mentioned the matter of the telegram... the rumor that has spread here (and as of now, it has not been denied, and consequently, the damage it causes is...) is that a telegram was sent before the coronation ceremony, the content of which was: "Do not cause an uproar, and after the coronation, we will compromise with you," and that this telegram was supposed to be confidential. In addition to the general weakening of the position here caused by the rumor about the telegram's content, many circles emphasize the "insurance" (*bauarenish*) that the telegram would be kept secret, adding that this itself is proof that the matter is politics and a form of "trading in religion," etc., etc. *Dai* (enough), etc.

As mentioned, I am not saying anything here regarding the actual existence of the telegram, the wording of the telegram, or the accuracy of the rumor. Rather, regarding public opinion and its reaction, as of now, there is only this rumor without any denial, neither in its entirety nor in its details.

Recently, they added a rumor to the aforementioned one, that in connection with the wedding of a grandchild, it will be here, and consequently, it will be easier to reach an understanding, since there will be no pressure (from the Neturei Karta?), etc. It is understood that I am not responsible for the truth of this rumor either, only for the damage caused by it.

I read with interest what you wrote in your letter regarding *oneg* and *simcha* on Shabbos and Yom Tov. It seems that at one of the *farbrengens*, we also spoke about this in one way or another (based on the note in the *Likkutim* for Parshas Devarim 5723—I believe it was sent to you at the time).

Regarding the shipment of *tashmishei kedusha* and the like to African countries, etc., if the addresses are sent here, I will endeavor to do what I can.

Many thanks for the good news regarding the activities of your wife, the Rabbanit, in the vineyard of Chabad. As I have said since long ago—and after asking for your forgiveness—the language of the verse is: "They made me a keeper of the vineyards; but my own vineyard I have not kept." That is to say, they are also vineyards **according to Torah**, yet there is a difference between "vineyards" and "my own vineyard," to the point that people are making noise and complaining about this, etc. If you ask, regarding yourself, in my opinion, your "vineyard" is the matter of the Encyclopedia, and together with that—the *hafatzas hamaayanos* in the appropriate manner. I fear to say—based on the beginning of your letter—that they are making you a keeper of vineyards of rabbinical matters, etc.—vineyards according to Torah, but not *your own* vineyard, a *mitzvah* that cannot be performed by others.

The *pidyon nefesh* in your letter will be read at an auspicious time at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulh"h, nbg"m, zy"a*, and may it be G-d's will that you hear good news regarding this.

These days, Rabbi Sh. Elberg visited me, and in our conversation, I reminded him of his promise to publish a *Pardes* booklet dedicated to our Rebbe HaZaken (in connection with the 150th year of his *histalkus* and *hillula* last year). He answered me that during his visit to Eretz Yisrael, he spoke with you about participating with an article in the aforementioned booklet, and until now, it has not materialized. However, he promises that when he receives it from you, as mentioned, he will be able to publish the booklet with additional articles within a short time. It must be an article from you that has not yet been published. Surely, any addition from me to what is written above is unnecessary, except on the basis of the Sages' teaching: "One only urges the diligent," and to add from my side a request and encouragement regarding this.

As we stand on the day of Lag B'Omer, the day of the *hillula* of Rashbi, and prefacing with the teaching of the Sages (beginning of *Bereishis Rabbah*) that the Torah is the blueprints and ledgers through which the world was created—it is understood that this is also the case regarding this "small world," the human being, and certainly regarding those whose Torah is their profession. The example in the Torah (*Shabbos* 11a) of those whose Torah is their profession is Rashbi and his colleagues.

The matter of Rashbi in Torah—from which we also understand his matter in the world—is to remove the partition between the *pnimiyus* (inner dimension) of Torah and the *nigleh* (revealed dimension) of Torah, and in a manner of drawing the *pnimiyus* into the *nigleh*. Therefore, his conduct in the world was also in this manner: the *pnimiyus* of the world—which is the Torah—he occupied himself with and drew into the revealed, physical world, as is told in the holy *Zohar*.

From this, there is a directive for the generation of the footsteps of Moshiach, which is in many respects similar to the generation of Rashbi, as explained by the Sages (*Zohar* Vol. III, 58a, based on *Zohar* Vol. I, 117a)—that his matter and main point must be the drawing of the *pnimiyus* of the Torah into the revealed, in the style of the well-known *hafatzas hamaayanos chutzah*. From this, there is also a directive for a person regarding his conduct in the world, in the style of the Rambam: that it should be **evident** in his actions (and he details—including—ten things: in his eating and drinking, etc., and in his business dealings) that this is according to Torah, the *nigleh* and *pnimiyus* united into one Torah.

And in the language of our Rebbes, "Because (*eikev*) he listened"—that even the heel (*eikev*) is Chassidic.

With respect and blessings for good news in all that is mentioned,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8820

8820

B”H, Lag BaOmer, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter.

As we stand on the day of Lag BaOmer, the yom hilula of Rashbi, and bearing in mind the teaching of Chazal that the Torah is the blueprints and ledgers through which the world was created, it is understood that this applies as well to the "small world" that is man. This is all the more true regarding those whose Torah is their occupation, for the example provided in the Torah for those whose Torah is their occupation is Rashbi and his colleagues.

The concept of Rashbi in Torah (from which we can also understand his purpose in the world) is to draw down the pnimiyus of Torah in such a way that the pnimiyus becomes revealed. This is why his conduct in the world was also in this manner: he engaged in the pnimiyus of the world—which is Torah—and drew it down into revealed, physical rain, as is recounted in the Zohar. His general mission was the clarification of the partition between the upper and lower realms.

From this, there is a directive for the generation of the footsteps of Moshiach, which is—in many respects—similar to the generation of Rashbi, as explained in the Zohar. Its primary point and focus must be the drawing down of the pnimiyus of Torah into the revealed realm, in the style of the well-known expression, "spreading the wellsprings outward." This also applies to a person’s conduct in the world, in the language of the Rambam, that it should be **evident** in his actions (and his actions include the ten matters): in his eating and drinking, etc., and in his business dealings—that they are according to Torah, with the nigleh and pnimiyus united as one Torah.

And according to the explanation of our Rebbes, the Nesi’im, regarding the precision of the terminology and the praise, "Eikev asher shama" (Because you listen), even the "heel" (eikev) itself "listens"—meaning that even the "heel" and its matters should be Chassidish.

With blessings for success in your holy work,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8821

B"H, Lag B'Omer, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants in the housewarming celebration of the
"Beis Rivkah" School and Seminary in Yerres, France
May Hashem protect them and grant them life

Peace and Blessing!

In anticipation of the housewarming celebration of the "Beis Rivkah" School and Seminary, I hereby express my blessing to all the participants in the joy of this great mitzvah, foremost among them the Rabbis shlita, the communal activists shlita, and everyone who assisted and exerted themselves in this great endeavor, whether with their person or their means. May the Ribono shel Olam reward them and send blessing and success in all the work of their hands.

It is well known how much our Sages of blessed memory extolled the honor of the women and daughters of Yisrael, and how much they emphasized their immense importance in the life of our people, to the extent that they said that when the Ribono shel Olam came to give the Torah to His people Yisrael—the Torah of life, the instruction for daily living—He turned to the women first, as our Sages of blessed memory expounded: "Thus shall you say to the House of Yaakov"—these are the women—"and tell the Children of Yisrael"—these are the men.

And if this was so in all times and eras, how much more so in our own time, when the environment and the "street" are not, as they were in the past, saturated with Yiddishkeit and Torah life, but on the contrary, are sometimes even opposed and hostile to it. Thus, the entire education of the sons and daughters of Yisrael in the spirit of Torah and mitzvos depends on the educational institutions that are purely holy, and on the home itself. And we see tangibly that due to various reasons (living conditions, the husband’s preoccupation with matters of livelihood, etc.), the education in the home depends primarily on the *akeres habayis*, the mother of the children.

From this, we understand the great value of the "Beis Rivkah" School and Seminary, whose primary tasks include not only training teachers and instructors, but also educating the daughters of Yisrael for their essential role—to be the *akeres habayis* and to build the House of Yisrael.

Furthermore, regarding education: any improvement in a child, even in a small detail, is liable to create a fundamental change in their adulthood, as is known from the parable of the seed planted to become a fruit-bearing tree.

This is especially true when those being educated and influenced today are the educators and *mashpi'im* of tomorrow.

The "Beis Rivkah" School and Seminary unites all these points.

Certainly, everyone whose heart is sensitive to Yiddishkeit and to the true good of the House of Yisrael will exert themselves as much as possible for the benefit of the institution and the building in all its details, so that the glory of this house may be great—in its construction, and also, and primarily, in the students who are educated and influenced within it—great in quality and also in quantity.

With respect and with a blessing for success in all the aforementioned.

#### ***8821***

**To the extent that they said:** Mechilta and Rashi on Yisro 19:3.

**Furthermore, regarding education:** See also below, Letter 8831.

## 8822

B"H, Lag B'Omer, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

The Administration of the Bais Rivkah School and Seminary
Yerres, France
May Hashem preserve them

Peace and Blessing!

It was with pleasure that I received the news regarding the preparation of a memorial book for the supporters of the aforementioned institutions, and I, too, participate in this with a willing heart.

It is my prayer that this memorial book will correspond to what is stated: "Then those who fear Hashem spoke to one another... and a book of remembrance was written before Him for those who fear Hashem and for those who contemplate His Name." This verse encompasses the three garments of the soul, which are the three modes of human action: thought, speech, and deed.

And deed is the essential thing, for every matter connected with actual deed has continuity and endurance. This is all the more true regarding matters of goodness, truth, and holiness, the entirety of which is that they are eternal.

This is especially true of a matter connected to education in purity and holiness, and above all, the educational institution "Bais Rivkah," whose goal is not only to educate the daughters of Yisroel so that they are worthy of their name—daughters of Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah who built the house of Yisroel—but it is also an institution that educates educators, educators in a manner of "growing fruit and the fruit of fruit," ever-increasing and ever-brightening.

May it be the will of Hashem that all those inscribed in this memorial book have their remembrance and their account rise before Hashem for good, for grace, for kindness, for mercy, and for a good life and peace, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With blessing.

This letter was printed in error previously in Vol. 9, letter 2662.

**And deed is the essential thing:** Avos, Chapter 1, Mishnah 17.

## 8823

B"H, 23 Iyar, 5724
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, man of action and possessor of fine character traits,
Rabbi N. (may he live and be well),

Shalom u’Bracha!

It was with pleasure that I received your book, *Taharas Mayim*, third edition.

May it be the will of Hashem that this edition, too, achieves the goal of establishing and disseminating the matter of the purity of the daughters of Yisrael—one of the foundations of the House of Yisrael in general, and of the private home of each and every individual.

And since a foundation, as its name implies, is that upon which the existence of the house built atop it rests, it is understood that any addition to the strength and stability of the foundation must be increased as much as possible in all such matters. We have been promised by Chazal: "One who comes to purify"—and the precision of our Alter Rebbe is well known, that this includes purifying others as well—"is assisted."

This is clearly visible in a tangible way, specifically in our current era, where the *baalei batim*, and the youth at their forefront, accept with a willing heart every instruction for *hiddur* (beautification) in this matter, and all the more so in details that have a basis in *din*.

And if you would say so, this very thing is emphasized in this matter itself: both regarding the *tumah*—which is [transferred] even by a *mashehu* (a minute amount) (and in the stringency of Rabbi Zeira, which is a settled *halacha* to be stringent)—and likewise in the manner of the *taharah*, where even a single hair can invalidate the entire process.

And as we stand in the days of *Sefirah*, which, as Chazal explain, this *sefirah*—"And you shall count for yourselves"—is in the spiritual sense of "and she shall count for herself seven days,"

May it be the will of Hashem that very soon the prophecy will be fulfilled, that the *sefirah* will lead to "and after she is purified," and "I will sprinkle upon you pure waters and you shall be purified," in the true and complete *Geulah* brought by Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With respect and blessing for long days and good years, and to see good fruit from his labor—the labor of Torah that leads to *halacha l’maaseh*—and in good health.

Based on the above at the conclusion of the letter, one should explain the connection of the request "May it be Your will... that the Beis Hamikdash be rebuilt" to the *Sefirah*, even according to those who hold that [the counting of *Sefirah*] is a Torah obligation even in our time.

## 8824

B"H, 23 Iyar, 5724
Brooklyn.

Mr. Zvi, known as Dr. Harkavi,
Shalom U’vracha!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter, in which you also write that you have not published anything recently. It is understandable that this surprise is even greater than the first, when I had remarked that you had published something but had not sent it here.

I read with interest about your relatives who are there, etc. Moving from one topic to a related one, I will take the liberty of transcribing here one of the points discussed regarding this matter. It is based on the ruling that all of Klal Yisrael constitutes one complete stature. Just as in a body, where strengthening the health of any one limb adds to the health of all the other limbs, so too is it regarding the individual limbs of the aforementioned complete stature. From this, the immediate conclusion is that an increase in Torah and mitzvos—specifically in action, which is the essential thing, the fulfillment of practical mitzvos day by day, which are vital, the existence and the foundation of all Bnei Yisrael [fitting for their name, "Torah of life," and the mitzvos, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them"]—certainly and absolutely adds to the "health" of each and every one of Bnei Yisrael. Distance does not hinder this in the slightest, and as mentioned above, this is a certain and tangible help and assistance from one's own self, and also for the success of efforts in other ways. Yet, it is precisely regarding this type of help that no one occupies themselves, and they do not even speak of it—v’d’l (and to the wise, a word is sufficient).

In this assistance, there is no need for meetings, votes, or asking for the opinion of the majority, since everyone has free choice in this matter and can increase it more and more, including influencing others to bring them even closer to Torah and mitzvos. Thereby, one can help all Bnei Yisrael wherever they may be, both in Eretz Yisrael (may it be built and established) and in the Diaspora, for they are all in need of help, even if not in the same area or to the same extent, and k’l (the matter is understood).

These days are days of segulah—the days of Sefirah, which connect the time of our freedom with the days of the receiving of the Torah, with the preface of "we will do" before "we will hear," an acceptance together with a promise—"engraved (charut) on the tablets."

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8827

25 Iyar, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

It is with great astonishment and even greater sorrow that I read your letter, which begins with praise to the Ribono shel Olam that you are—Heaven forbid—traveling to Eretz Yisrael on a ship whose owners are Jews, and the captain, sailors, and the entire crew and service staff are all Jews, or 99 percent of them are Jews; and you continue by writing that the merit of our holy forefathers should bring success to the journey!

I would have thought it unnecessary to explain the reason for my great sorrow, but the content of your letter compels me to write at least a few lines about it, even though no matter how much one were to write, it would be insufficient compared to the gravity of the matter. In short:

A journey on such a ship is—for every passenger, to say nothing of the crew employed on the ship—a) a desecration of Shabbos, b) in public (*b'farhesia*), c) participating in a *chillul Hashem* in public (even before all the non-Jews) who are aware of the aforementioned, d) this is done in the name of the entire Jewish people, whose contributions on various occasions have helped the operation and functioning of the ship on Shabbos.

It must also be added that this is a rare opportunity to desecrate the Shabbos in public **every single moment** of the twenty-four hours of Shabbos Kodesh, even when one is sleeping! For the ship travels even while one sleeps. [In contrast, when one is on land, whatever kind of life one leads, at the very least one is not transgressing *chillul Shabbos b'farhesia* while sleeping.]

The above applies with full force regardless of where the ship is traveling or when it departs, provided it is traveling during the twenty-four hours of Shabbos. In this case, there is the additional factor that you wish to travel to a land that even non-Jews call "**the Holy Land**"—not because the United Nations holds this to be so, but because it is written in our holy Torah, which has linked the existence of Eretz Yisrael specifically to the observance of Shabbos, as indicated in many *sedros*, among them—by *hashgacha pratis*—also in the *sedra* that we are going to read **this Shabbos Kodesh**.

The above is already a maximum misfortune, Heaven forbid, but the journey about which you write adds misfortune upon misfortune. In addition to the two or three Shabbosos that, as written above, are connected with *chillul Shabbos b'farhesia* Heaven forbid, there is **also** in this case the desecration of both days of Shavuos in public—the Yom Tov when the Aseres HaDibros were given, given with all the thunder and intensity as described in the *Midrashim*, where one of the Aseres HaDibros is "**Guard the day of Shabbos to sanctify it**." It is simply that we live in a time when people have become accustomed to all sorts of unbelievable things, so an event such as the one described above can also take place, with no one to protest or object.

Naturally, I know that there are those who have taken the responsibility upon themselves—**without** knowing how a ship is operated, while at the same time considering themselves great experts in the matter—and have permitted the *chillul Shabbos b'farhesia* that is conducted in the name of *Klal Yisrael*. And as it is told, one is to believe that on Shabbos, a Jew stands on the ship in a *tallis* and davens to the Ribono shel Olam to "**sanctify the Shabbos**," knowing that at that very moment, the machinery is being turned on and operated by Jews, telegrams are being written and communications made, cooking and washing are taking place, etc., all by Jews, specifically for Jews, and every one of the passengers makes use of it, as well as electricity, water, **and** all the services that are performed through *chillul Shabbos*.

But it is also self-evident that our holy Torah is not changed by this, for our holy Torah is an eternal Torah that the Ribono shel Olam gave to the Jewish people, and people cannot change it.

Just as our Sages, of blessed memory, have instructed that a Jew must never despair, I do not wish to give up hope even now that you, and together with you many, many other Jews, will not commit this *chillul Shabbos b'farhesia* and *chillul Yom Tov b'farhesia*, and you will cancel your aforementioned journey. Great is the merit of Shabbos to bring you long life and good years, and naturally, the most important thing—to have true Jewish Torah-nachas from your children and grandchildren, *shichyu*.

With blessings for good tidings regarding what was written above.

If, due to canceling the journey so shortly before departure, this is connected with a financial loss, it is **of course** understood that taking into account the great prohibition of *b'farhesia*, I will **gladly** return the full sum to you, with heartfelt thanks for the opportunity to save a Jewish soul from such a misfortune, Heaven forbid. In addition, it is possible that there will be others who will not have the excuse that "if Mrs. ... is traveling, it is a sure thing that it is permitted," and they too will refrain from it. It is well known that saving even one Jew is equivalent to saving an entire world.

You have attached a check for *tzedakah* to your letter in connection with the journey. This is the first time in my life—and I hope I will never have to do it again—that I must return such a check. But it is **self-evident** that I cannot have any connection to a matter that is linked with *chillul Shabbos b'farhesia*, and especially when one wants the *tzedakah* to assist in that *chillul Shabbos*, Heaven forbid. Therefore, the check is returned herewith. I would like to hope that you will accept my words, in accordance with today's *sedra*—"**You shall keep My Shabbosos**... I am Hashem."

Then it is a matter of *tzarich iyun* (requires further study) whether the interruption will be considered permanent. 2) Whether one can argue this point, even with difficulty, regarding the middle of the *beis medrash*, as opposed to when there is at least one row of people davening. For sometimes "the middle" is meant to exclude the ends—(as is known, the proof is from *Terumos 3:5*; see *Tziyon Yerushalayim* there).

## 8829

8829

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished, Torah-scholar, profound and sharp student, etc., Rabbi Yitzchak, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

For a long time now, I have observed and contemplated your diligence and perseverance in the study of Torah, dedicating your nights as your days and increasing [your efforts] from time to time.

Following this, I derived special satisfaction from the news that, as we discussed, you have prepared and arranged original Torah insights for print, and they will, G-d willing, soon appear and be published.

My hope is strong that the aforementioned will inspire you to increase even further in perseverance and diligence in both the revealed and the inner dimensions of Torah (which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus), and that the fear of Hashem will be his treasure, as the Sages commanded: "And even so, the fear of Hashem is his treasure" (see Shabbos 31a, bottom of page). And the command of our Torah is also a source of strength.

Together with this, [there should be] involvement in spreading the wellsprings outward, charity in spiritual matters, and also charity in the literal sense, for one who has nothing of his own, and to revive the spirit of the lowly, etc.

For "charity elevates," etc., to the point that one’s mind and heart become a thousand times purer, as our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe explains this well at the beginning of his book, *Torah Or*.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that all of this should be with abundance in both material and spiritual matters.

**Menachem Schneerson**

With blessing — in the accepted formula — for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness, and for success in all that is mentioned.

P.S. As a token of affection, I am including here a few notes on your aforementioned book.

**Introduction. At its beginning.** The Beis Hamikdash is the **foundation** of the world, for it is one of the seven things that preceded the world.

His intent is that from there the Shechinah will spread (which is called thus because of [the verse], "And I will dwell among them" — which is said regarding the construction of the Mishkan, which is called a *mikdash*) throughout the entire world.

One should establish this based on the Sages, that the *shetiyah* (foundation stone) is the Beis Hamikdash (Sanhedrin 26b). And even according to the one who disagrees there regarding the interpretation of the verse, he does not disagree on the substance of the matter, that the Beis Hamikdash is the foundation and base of the world, which are the words of the Sages (Yoma 54b, and as the Rambam [writes] in his commentary on the Mishnah there).

From the *Baraisa* of the seven things created before the world was created, etc., [including] the Beis Hamikdash — [this serves as] proof of its precedence, but not that it is the foundation of the world and the foundation in the literal sense as well. Torah and Teshuvah, etc., will prove [this].

**There.** The Beis Hamikdash, its matter is the offerings and the Ark, etc., the dispute between the Rambam and the Ramban, etc. See there.

There are several points to note regarding what you wrote in your book, and what I believe to be the explanation of the positions of the Rambam and the Ramban is understood from what follows: a) Regarding the purpose of the construction of the Beis Hamikdash; b) Regarding the matter of the Ark — (and I have elaborated on all this elsewhere):

a) The Rambam writes in *Sefer Hamitzvos* (Positive Mitzvah 20) that we were commanded to build the Beis Hamikdash for the service, that the offering should be there, etc., and to it should be the pilgrimage, etc., and this is what He, may He be blessed, said: "And they shall make Me a sanctuary." And similarly, it is in the Rambam at the beginning of *Hilchos Beis Habechirah* and in *Sefer Hamitzvos*, Root 12. This is not the opinion of the Ramban, who wrote: The primary object of the Mishkan is the place of the resting of the Shechinah, which is the Ark (beginning of Parshas Terumah. And see also Ramban, Eikev 10:5).

Seemingly, this poses a difficulty for the Rambam, for this very verse that he brings, "And they shall make Me a sanctuary," explains the intent of the construction: "And I will dwell among them," and this place of "And I will dwell" is also explicitly stated in many places in Scripture to be the Ark (see there in the Ramban). And a proof (or at least a reminder) for the matter is also from the words of the Rambam himself (*Moreh Nevuchim*, Part 3, Chapter 45), and these are his words: "And we were commanded to build a Temple to His Name, may He be blessed, and to place in it the Ark which contains, etc."

And it must be said that even according to the Rambam, the object of the sanctuary is the resting of the Shechinah, and primarily it is upon the Ark, and consequently it is understood that the perfection of the holiness of the Mishkan depends upon it.

— And therefore, the Mishkan, at a time when it did not contain the Ark, had the status of a *bamah gedolah* (great high place) (Tosefta, Zevachim, end of Chapter 13. And see also Meiri, Megillah 9b). And one should not raise a difficulty from the fact that the Beis Hamikdash retains its holiness even after the Ark was hidden (and even after it was removed) — for this is because "the Shechinah is not nullified" (Rambam, *Hilchos Beis Habechirah*, end of Chapter 6); unlike the Mishkan, which was from the outset only "for a time," a temporary dwelling and not a resting place and inheritance. —

Rather, the Rambam speaks regarding the matter of the mitzvos that the Children of Israel were commanded **to do** in the Beis Hamikdash, while the Ramban speaks regarding the **object** that is in the Mishkan **itself**, which is "And I will dwell among them," and this was primarily through the Ark.

b) The difficulty is well known as to why the Rambam did not count the making of the Ark in the enumeration of the mitzvos (and especially since he counted the mitzvah of carrying it on the shoulder. And this is discussed at length in the commentary of R. Y. Perla to the *Sefer Hamitzvos* of the Rasag, at the end, Parshah 52). Moreover, in *Sefer Hamitzvos* there, when he explains the reason he does not count the making of the "Menorah, the Table, the Altar, and others" because "they are all parts of the Sanctuary and everything is called a Sanctuary," he does not mention the Ark at all. — Seemingly, one can answer that the Ark’s matter is **only** a vessel to be "And I will dwell among them," and this is the general matter of **all** the Torah and mitzvos, "and it is not appropriate to count the commands that include the entire Torah" (*Sefer Hamitzvos*, Root 4. And see also there). And the command to make the Ark, even though it is a "special act," its matter includes the matters of "the entire Torah" and "all the mitzvos," and therefore it is considered a general command, similar to "And you shall not harden your necks," which he brings in *Sefer Hamitzvos* there. — And yet, the building of the Beis Hamikdash is counted even though its matter is "And I will dwell among them," because in the matter of the Beis Hamikdash there are other matters: the offerings, etc., **and they** are the ones that were counted in the 613 mitzvos — unlike the Ark. (The placing of the Tablets in the Ark — according to this interpretation — is only a detail of the matters of the (holiness of the) Ark, or that it is not for all generations). — And yet, the Rambam counts the positive mitzvah of carrying on the shoulder and the negative mitzvah of not removing [the poles], because — according to this view — the **holiness** of the Ark and its matter of "And I will dwell among them" does not depend on this, but rather it is a special command **to the Kohanim** that they should carry it on the shoulder, etc.

But this interpretation of the Rambam's position is forced, for after all, since there is a command for a "special act," the making of the Ark — why should it not enter into the count of the mitzvos? And what does it matter that its **matter** is inclusive, since there is an additional command for a "special act"? Moreover, it is a *kal v'chomer* from the positive mitzvah of the belief in Hashem, which the Rambam counts even though its matter is even more inclusive (and note the *Sefer Hamitzvos* of the Tzemach Tzedek, beginning of the mitzvah of the belief in G-dliness).

Therefore, the interpretation of the Rambam's position must be in a different way, and by way of introducing the **great** questions: a) Why did the Rambam omit all the laws of making the Ark? b) How is it that Yoshiyahu took the Ark from its place, which the Children of Israel were **commanded** to place there, and hid it? And in the Shas (Yoma 52b) it is proven that this was not according to the command and the like, but rather that he **worried** **lest** it be exiled to Babylon **after some time?**

And to answer all the above, one can say that the act of Yoshiyahu **proves** that the verses are **to be taken literally**, that the making of the Ark and bringing it into the Holy of Holies is solely so that there will be "And I will meet with you there." And after this has been done, and in a manner that "it is not nullified" forever — then **we find no mitzvah** in the making of the Ark. Rather, as long as it exists (and after it is revealed in the time to come) — they were commanded to carry it on the shoulder and not to remove the poles. — And therefore, the making of the Ark is not counted among the mitzvos (for generations) and its laws of construction were not brought, for what is done is done, and from the time of the building of the First Beis Hamikdash — there is no command regarding this. And with this, that which in the wars of the Philistines and the like they did not hide the Ark until the war passed (and similar to what Yoshiyahu did) is also answered — and based on the above it is understood, for in the Mishkan of Shiloh, etc. — the removal of the Ark from its place would nullify the "And I will meet with you there," for in its removal the Mishkan had only the holiness of a *bamah gedolah* as mentioned above (and the reason — because it was only a temporary dwelling).

— And only that in a place of *pikuach nefesh* (the death of the men of Beis Shemesh — I Samuel 6:19 — and the death of Uzza — II Samuel 6:7) it was permitted not to return the Ark to the Mishkan.

And based on the above, the act of Yoshiyahu is strong proof for the Rambam's position that there is no positive mitzvah at all (once the Beis Hamikdash is built) to make an Ark. — And in my opinion, all this is clear and also simple.

However, Yoshiyahu hid the Ark in the Beis Hamikdash specifically and not in another place, because even though "the Shechinah is not nullified," nevertheless there are **several** levels in the resting of the Shechinah in the Beis Hamikdash, as explained in Yoma 21b.

And they were commanded with an **eternal** positive mitzvah — that in the Beis Hamikdash there should be that level of resting [of the Shechinah] that comes through having brought the Ark there in a manner of a permanent dwelling. And at a time when Israel is meritorious, there is a higher level than this: when the Ark is present (at least hidden) in the Beis Hamikdash, and more than this — when it is in its place (in the Holy of Holies, etc.).

However, it still remains to be understood: according to the one who says (Yerushalmi, Yoma, Chapter 5, Halachah 4) that the sprinkling on the cover must touch [it] — how did Yoshiyahu hide the Ark, for (at least *l'chatchilah*) it must touch. — And it can be said: a) That the worry that it would be exiled to Babylon is sufficient power to hide the Ark **at a time when there is no obligation** (even *l'chatchilah*) that it be in the Holy of Holies, even **if afterwards** by way of **consequence** the touching on Yom Kippur cannot occur (and there are many examples of this, and even in clear obligations and prohibitions. And see in this *Sdei Chemed*, *Asifat Dinim*, system of Yom Kippur, section 1, subsection 10. **And references there** to Shas, Rishonim, etc.). b) The one who says it must touch may hold like the one who says Yoshiyahu did not hide it (but rather the Ark was taken to Babylon). [And not like the ruling of the Rambam — that it was hidden].

* * *

Based on the above, there was no service in the Ark (like in the other vessels of the Mishkan); and its matter is a vessel for the revelation from above.

And it is still difficult regarding the matter of the sprinkling between the poles, etc. And it can be said by way of introducing the question: how was this during all those years that the Mishkan was in Nov and Givon and the Ark was in Kiryat Ye'arim and the City of Zion? And it must be that the essence of this is the **place** (the poles) of the Ark that is in the Holy of Holies. But it is difficult according to the one who says that the sprinkling on the cover must touch the cover (Yerushalmi there). And it must be that even according to him, it is not a hindrance at all, and Nov and Givon will prove it. And it requires further study.

* * *

**At its beginning. Page 23.** The roofs of Jerusalem and its walls and their holiness, etc. See *Tzofnat Paneach* — by the Gaon Rogatchover — to Makkos (18a) and page 19, who compares the words of the Rambam, etc. — based on the assumption that there is a matter that requires the interior and there is a matter that is invalid on the exterior, and the aforementioned, etc., is not exterior and also not interior. — I later saw that he touched upon this in his book (page 26).

**There, page 51.** That the obligations of Shabbos are that one should not perform the action and not that the action should not be done, and for example in writing, etc. — One cannot say this regarding all the obligations of Shabbos, as is proven in many places and especially regarding writing — from the obligation of taking the roof of the *Chet* and making it into two *Zayins* (Shabbos 104, bottom of page). And even though Rashi explains there that the book needs it — the reason is not because it completes, etc. (for this is the explanation of Rava there), but rather that it is considered writing two letters (and even though seemingly there is proof to the contrary from the fact that writing with the left hand is exempt — one can say the reason is that it is impossible for there to be writing with the weak hand (and see Tzemach Tzedek to Shabbos, Chapter 12, Mitzvah 4 (50:3)) — like that which is with **his** right hand). And note also from the one who carries out half a dried fig and then another half a dried fig, that if he preceded and lifted the first one, he is exempt (Shabbos 80a).

And it is difficult regarding the fact that it must be in the manner that people carry out specifically (Shabbos 92a), and one can say that otherwise it is not called carrying out.

And note from *Tosafos* (Bava Basra 55, bottom of page). And this is not the place to elaborate.

## 8830

8830

By the Grace of Hashem, Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the annual dinner of Yeshivas "Achi Temimim" Lubavitch in Newark,
May Hashem preserve them and keep them alive.

Peace and Blessing!

Taking into account that the annual dinner is taking place in the month of Matan Torah, a few days after the Yom Tov of Kabbalas HaTorah, each and every one will surely express the spiritual elevation of the Yom Tov and the practical directives that must be implemented, especially in connection with the aforementioned annual undertaking.

It is worth noting that the Yom Tov of Shavuos does not have its own "date" (neither a specific month nor a specific day) in the Torah, unlike other Yomim Tovim. Rather, it is marked as the "50th day" of Sefirah, which we begin to count on the second day of Pesach, the day after Yetzias Mitzrayim.

Through this, the holy Torah emphasizes that Shavuos is the ultimate goal of the Yom Tov of Pesach; that **Zman Matan Toraseinu** is the perfection of **Zman Cheiruseinu** — that true and complete liberation, both for the individual and for the collective, both materially and spiritually, can be achieved only through **Kabbalas HaTorah.**

We live in a time, and in a country, where despite the outward "freedom," the world in general, and the younger generation in particular, is still quite strongly enslaved and does not know how to free itself from the chains of spiritual confusion. The only hope that Jewish children will not be dragged along with the current lies in a Torah-true yeshiva education, where the golden chain of Torah MiSinai is maintained; the holy Torah, **Toras Emes,** where the truth must always remain whole, without compromises and without dilution.

The Lubavitcher Yeshiva "Achi Temimim" in Newark is an important fortress of Torah that deserves the fullest support. It is a great obligation and a rare privilege for each and every one to support this yeshiva. I greet all the participants in the annual dinner and send each and every one of the supporters and friends of the yeshiva a heartfelt blessing, that Hashem Yisbarach should grant them success in the yeshiva's undertaking, and in their personal undertakings, and in everything they need, materially and spiritually.

With blessings for success and for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 8831

8831

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Yosef Dekel
Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter, as well as the book "Nuclear War and Nuclear Peace" by Yehoshafat Harkabi. Thank you for this, and for the future, as I am sure you will continue to do so.

As is the custom of the Children of Israel to find allusions in the Torah to every matter and detail, and as we stand just a few days before the time of the giving of our Torah, the essence of Torah is to refine matter and physicality until the powers hidden within them are revealed, reaching back to the First Source—the power of the Creator within the created, through Whose word the heavens were made, and by the breath of His mouth all their hosts. From this, it is understood how great are the eternal powers that exist in every thing and every matter; one must simply penetrate into the interior of the matter to reveal, as mentioned, that which is hidden within its very core and inwardness.

Science is now beginning to discover this in matter in the literal sense, which is one of the points of inquiry in the field of nuclear science. From stage to stage and level to level, this inquiry deepens regarding human beings and their affairs as well—for in the phrasing of our Sages, of blessed memory, each person is an entire world. This is especially true when one causes the internal to rule over the external, the form over the matter, and the true spirituality over the garments and *kelipos* that cover it, until every detail in creation—and all the more so the totality of creation—proclaims, "I am Hashem your G-d," and "Hashem is the G-d; there is nothing else besides Him."

With respect and with blessings for *mo'adim l'simcha* and for receiving the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 8832

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

We stand at the beginning of the third month, in which the Torah was given to the three-fold people through a third-born [Moshe] on the third day.

The essence of the matter of Matan Torah is the nullification of the decree and the separation between the upper realms and the lower realms. Moreover, it is "I (Hashem) who initiates"—meaning that this nullification begins from the side of the Upper One, where there is no limitation, to the point that a complete unification is possible.

May it be Hashem’s will that everyone does what is dependent upon them regarding this connection between the upper and the lower in all matters—both spiritual and physical, both particular and general.

This begins with these levels as they exist in Torah (the hidden and revealed aspects of Torah) and extends down to the physical and material "lower realm," than which there is no lower, and the soul and spiritual vitality within it, through which Hashem speaks.

This action and avodah bring about the fulfillment of the prophecy: "And the glory of Hashem shall be revealed, and all flesh together shall see that the mouth of Hashem has spoken."

With blessings—in the language of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe—for receiving the Torah with joy and inwardness,

**M. Schneerson**

***

8832. General/Particular. Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 13, p. 156 (dated 3 Sivan) and completed according to a photocopy of the letter.

**Rosh Chodesh Sivan:** See Shabbos 86b; Torah Or, beginning of Parshas Yisro.

**The third month... on the third day:** Like the Sages (Shabbos 88a), and so is the halacha (Shulchan Aruch HaRav, beginning of 494).

**Third-born:** See the commentary of Rav Nissim Gaon (Shabbos ibid.).

**Nullification of the decree... initiates:** Shemos Rabbah 12:3.

**Hidden and revealed aspects of Torah:** Which are level upon level (Zohar III, 73a).

**Physical... no lower:** See Tanya, Chapter 36.

**Soul... speaks:** Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah, Chapter 1.

**And the glory... spoken:** Revelation without any garment; they will see with sensory perception that the mouth of Hashem speaks and brings into being all created things (see Tanya and Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah, ibid.).

## 8833

8833

B”H, Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished, G-d-fearing, and learned, a bochur of the people and exalted among the people, one who seeks the good of his people, a man of noble character, a scion of a noble lineage,
R’ Schneur Zalman
Shlita

Greetings and blessings!

In anticipation of the festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah, which is approaching us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I wish to convey my blessing to you, in the style of my father-in-law, the Rebbe — that you may receive the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

It is already brought in several seforim that the Ten Commandments encompass the entire Seder Hishtalshelus, as well as that which is above Seder Hishtalshelus, down to the lowest depths — and in the style of our Alter Rebbe in the holy Tanya, that there is nothing lower than it. Therefore, the **beginning** of the Ten Commandments is: "I am Hashem your G-d who brought you out of the land of Egypt," in an order from above to below, for the land of Egypt is infinitely lower than "your G-d" — *lehavdil*, Elokus as it is clothed in nature (*Elokim* has the same gematria as *hateva* [nature]). Similarly, there is the infinite disparity between "your G-d" and "Hashem," the Name of Essence, and likewise the infinite disparity between Hashem and "Anochi" [I], as the Zohar states: *Anochi* — He who is *Anochi*, who is not hinted at by any letter, nor even by any stroke.

And the **end** of the Ten Commandments reaches the depths of Sheol, where there is a need for the warning "Do not murder," etc. — a warning to one endowed with free choice, who has been given the capacity of free will, and down to the lowest level, until — in the style of our Sages — even a mosquito preceded you (see Tanya, Chapter 24).

All of this was given at once, as our Sages emphasized the unity of the Ten Commandments, that they were all given in one utterance and at one time. And this is the Torah — an *hora'ah* [instruction] — that form and matter, spirituality and physicality, are separate only to the eyes of flesh, to the point that they can appear to oppose one another, and even to be at war with one another. The task of man — "you are called *adam*" — is to begin by elevating the form over the matter, the spirit over the physical, and so on, until reaching unification, oneness, and *yichud* to its ultimate purpose — that every detail of creation, and certainly the entirety of creation, will proclaim "I am Hashem your G-d... you shall have no other," just as it was at the time of the giving of the Torah, leading to the recognition that there is nothing else besides Him.

With appreciation and honor, and with the blessing of *moadim l'simcha* and to continue the joy and inwardness of receiving the Torah throughout all the days of the year.

## 8,835

B"H, 10 Sivan, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

[Greetings and Blessings!]

It was with sorrow that I learned of your loss. In addition to sharing in your grief, please convey my condolences to his daughter and the family—though I do not know them personally—may the Omnipresent comfort them among the other mourners of Tzion and Yerushalayim.

The traditional and accepted phrasing of this condolence is characteristic, and two points within it should be noted: 

a) Regarding the sorrow itself: it connects the sorrow of the individual with the sorrow of the collective. This means that just as the destruction of Tzion and Yerushalayim is a mourning for the entire nation, so too is the mourning of the individual, for all of Klal Yisrael is one single stature. Consequently, it becomes easier to bear the sorrow and grief. 

b) Regarding the consolation: just as the consolation of Tzion and Yerushalayim is certain—being one of the foundations of our faith, to the extent that our Sages said that anyone who mourns for Yerushalayim will merit to see her consolation and her joy—so too is the matter of mourning, whose goal and purpose is the matter of teshuvah (Rambam, Hilchos Avel, end of Chapter 13). Thus, the consolation will certainly come from the One who comforts Tzion and builds Yerushalayim.

With respect.

***

**The phrasing:** See also above, Vol. 22, Letter 8,775. Likutei Sichos, Vol. 18, p. 210.

**All... one:** See also above, Letter 8,824, and the references noted there.

**Anyone who mourns:** Taanis 30b, and the sources noted there.

## 8836

8836

By the Grace of Hashem, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Al Pi Hashem Yachanu, 5724, Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Annual Convention of Nshei U’Bnos Chabad, may Hashem grant them life,

Blessings and peace!

Among the highlights of this week’s parsha, Parshas Beha’aloscha, is the description of the order in which the Jewish people traveled through the desert. "At the command of Hashem they would encamp, and at the command of Hashem they would travel; they kept the charge of Hashem, at the command of Hashem by the hand of Moshe" (Beha’aloscha 9:23).

Throughout all their journeys, the Aron Bris Hashem would travel ahead of them to seek out a resting place for them (10:33).

The holy Torah—which is eternal, and whose instructions are eternal and valid everywhere and at all times—emphasizes that only by following the Aron Hakodesh, the holy Torah, could the Jewish people enjoy rest and be protected in that terrifying desert, filled with poisonous creatures. This has always been the case throughout the long history of our people’s galus, and in all the journeys that we, the Jewish people, have traversed and continue to traverse, until the arrival of true rest and the Geulah Shleimah through Mashiach Tzidkeinu.

And as in all significant moments of Jewish life, so too, and especially in a time of travel, the Jewish woman occupies a central place. This is indicated at the conclusion of the same parsha, where the Torah relates that the people waited for Miriam and did not move from their place without her. While the people are on the road, it is not enough for Moshe and Aharon to accompany them; Miriam must also accompany them. Without Miriam, one does not travel! Our Sages, of blessed memory, explain that Miriam merited the honor that the entire nation, along with the Aron Hakodesh and the Ananei Hakavod, etc., should wait for her, because she had waited for and saved Moshe Rabbeinu when he was in a basket on the river.

We find ourselves in a time when, without the active assistance and cooperation of the Jewish woman in strengthening and spreading Torah and mitzvos in daily life, our people cannot move forward toward the "rest and the inheritance" that the Almighty has promised us. In all areas of Jewish life, especially in the field of chinuch al taharas hakodesh, Jewish women and girls must fulfill the task that Hashgacha Elyona has placed upon them. This is the duty of **all** Jewish women and girls, especially the **Nshei U’Bnos Chabad**, who have merited to stand under the illumination and revival of Toras Chabad and the Nesi’ei Chabad.

And my prayer is that the convention should fulfill all expectations and succeed in actualizing, in deed, that which must be accomplished by the convention in general, and by every member of Nshei U’Bnos Chabad in particular.

With blessings for outstanding success in personal and communal matters,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8837

B"H, Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Behaaloscha, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings,

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter.

As we stand at the conclusion of Shabbos Parshas Behaaloscha es haneros ("when you kindle the lamps"), there is a lesson to be drawn from the allusions in this parsha: The Alter Rebbe explains that these lamps are the souls of all the Jewish people—"The lamp of Hashem is the soul of man," and "You are called 'man'." In every single individual, the kindling must be in the manner of "behaaloscha"—meaning that, ultimately, the flame rises of its own accord.

Since this requirement is directed at every single person, it is certainly within their power, for the Ribono shel Olam does not make unreasonable demands of His creations.

The purpose of this is "that the seven lamps shall give light toward the face of the Menorah"—that every individual, regardless of how they may have begun their observance of Torah and mitzvos in one of the levels of "not for its own sake" (shelo lishmah), will through that process arrive at "for its own sake" (lishmah).

And even one who is called "outcast" (nidach)—who is, as is understood, even lower than one who is called "distant"—has been promised that "no outcast shall be cast away from Him," as is the ruling in the inner dimensions of Torah, and even as a clear ruling in the revealed dimensions of Torah.

May it be the will of Hashem that every person acts according to all that has been said regarding all their affairs, so that they will shine "toward the face of the Menorah," even those who for the time being are in the category of "outcast." And may this be done with a desire of the heart (re'usa deliba), in the manner of Aharon’s avodah, and the aspect of Aharon that exists within everyone—for Aharon is one of the seven shepherds—to the point that "from its base to its flower it is hammered work":

That the "base"—the lowest level within them—and the "flower"—the highest level within them—shall be one single piece of pure gold.

With blessings for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

***

With blessings for good tidings, and regarding the matter of the encyclopedia, it is also [to be viewed as] **"gam"** (also)—not, G-d forbid, as something secondary, but rather, **on the contrary**, as something of greater importance and stature (for, with all due respect, it can be done with the greatest gravity). Based on this, the phrase "gam alah" (also went up) is resolved (and the homiletical interpretation that "gam" refers to the Babylonian exile—apparently the Alter Rebbe does not hold of this [Torah Or, beginning of Parshas Shemos], and see Rashi on Shabbos 89b), whereas **"es"** (the particle denoting the direct object) is something that is always secondary.

## 8838

B"H, 23 Sivan, 5724
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished Rabbi Yitzchak Tzvi, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter, and continuing our conversation with your parents, may they live, regarding your questions:

1) Among Anash and Chassidim who deal with Calabria esrogim is the esteemed Rabbi Y. Jacobson, may he live (who I believe has been in contact with you for some time), who has personally visited the esrog orchards in Italy and examined them.

2) He is also knowledgeable regarding the signs and the method of identifying that a tree is not grafted.

3) Regarding what you wrote about the manner of the growth of the stem and the protrusions—it must be clarified whether both protrusions and non-protrusions grow on the **same** tree, and likewise regarding the variations in the stem. It seems that in the seforim, one does not find details such as those you describe as signs if they are found on the **same** tree, and one must clarify this with someone who was on-site and saw it for himself.

4) I hope that by now you have received regards from here from your parents, may they live, as well as from the guests from Manchester who visited here during the time of the giving of our Torah, the weeks before and after, and from what was discussed during those auspicious times. May it be Hashem's will that these matters have their intended effect, in accordance with their content, for the deed is the essential thing.

With respect and blessing for good tidings, and regards from your parents, may they live.

P.S. It is already brought in the sefer *Bikkurei Yaakov* (end of siman 648) that one should not rely on the signs, nor should one be stringent based on them. And even though this is contrary to the opinion of many of the Acharonim, it can be said that even according to their view, when there is a tradition regarding the region, and on that same tree esrogim grow with these signs—the other esrogim on that tree are also kosher (for according to all opinions, **these** signs—aside from the thick rind mentioned by the Chasam Sofer—are not definitive, etc.).
