## 8840

B"H, 28 Sivan, 5724
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 26 Sivan, in which you ask regarding your nephew, may he live, who wishes to study for a few years in a yeshiva, and the question of whether he should thereafter join a religious kibbutz, etc.

In my opinion, since the matter concerns the time after he has studied for a period in yeshiva—the study of our holy Torah, the Torah of life, which, as our Alter Rebbe states in his holy Tanya, is called the bread and nourishment of the soul, and through proper study, it unites with the soul of the student and they become one, and it becomes nourishment for the soul and life within it from the Life of Life, the Ein Sof, blessed be He, etc. (Tanya, Chapter 5)—

Based on this, it is not worthwhile to decide now what he will do after the aforementioned study, for the hope, according to what has been said, is that he will be elevated through this study, and he will decide in accordance with his situation at that time.

There is a strong hope that you are aware of the significance of the days of 12 and 13 Tammuz, the redemption of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, the Nasi of our generation.

May it be His will that everyone will be inspired to increase in matters of Torah and mitzvos, and in the dissemination of Yiddishkeit and its affairs to those near and far, with joy and a glad heart.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 8841

8841

*[Late Sivan]*

Regarding a *she'elas chalom* (dream inquiry) and the like — this is relevant only for select individuals and in exceptional circumstances. He should study with *hasmadah* and *shekidah* and conduct himself as commanded in the *Shulchan Aruch*, and Hashem will grant him success.

- Regarding speaking with me *panim el panim* (face-to-face) — this is handled by the secretariat.

#### ***8841***

Written on the margin of the letter dated Friday, *Erev Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Shelach*.

## 8842

B"H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Tammuz, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

[Mr. Shalom Levin]

Greetings and Blessings!

Your letter dated the 4th of Sivan has just been received; it was likely delayed due to the strike. I was distressed to see from your letter that you did not receive my response, which was written several months ago.

As we stand on the eve of the month of the Geulah of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, I wish to emphasize a matter timely to the occasion, in connection with his imprisonment and liberation: his dedication to the field of education, to which he devoted fifty-five years of his life. He was eighteen years old when his father appointed him the active director of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch, but he had been involved in education even before that. In all the lands of his wanderings, immediately upon his arrival, he dedicated himself to the work of education, prioritizing it above all his other endeavors. This was also the case in the United States; here, too, his primary work was to establish a network of educational institutions, starting from activities for children who did not even know the Aleph-Beis, up to the stage of studying Torah in the depth of Halacha—both in the revealed Torah and in the hidden Torah, the Torah of Chassidus, the inner dimension of Torah. This was his life’s work, and he literally risked his life for it during the days of the Yevsektsiya. It is the merit of these activities that stood by him to emerge into freedom with a high hand.

Certainly, my intention is not to recount the story of the day of Geulah merely for the sake of telling it, but rather, as the master of the celebration himself explained the concept of the story of the day: the events of those days must serve as a lamp to the feet of each and every one of us, to illuminate our path in utilizing every possibility and every stage in the education of the sons and daughters of Yisrael in the spirit of Torah, tradition, and the eternal values of our people. If there are matters that hinder and obstruct, one must overcome them, even if it requires a measure of mesiras nefesh—especially since, with us, B"H, we do not require mesiras nefesh, but rather mesiras haratzon (dedication of the will), and in the end, the truth prevails.

As is the way of all the children of Yisrael, who are known for their extra measure of devotion as a "stiff-necked people," I return once again to the point we discussed when we met, which I reiterated in my letter, and now again. Please forgive me if I must express my reservation regarding your position that the protocol of your office defines the scope of your activity, and that everything else is not your concern, etc. This is not what we received from the house of our Rebbe, as written above regarding the lesson from the story of the Geulah of 12-13 Tammuz. Furthermore, your position does not befit the comprehensive concept of our Sages, of blessed memory, who, in their holy manner, expressed it in a concise style: "A person is obligated to say, 'For my sake the world was created.'" The foundation of this obligation lies in the role of every Jew to bring to fruition the unity that exists in the entire world and the common point within the most diverse areas of the world—meaning that all matters of the world have a connection to every Jew, and he can be a ruler and master there, like a person acting within his own domain.

And if this is so in all areas, then all the more so in the field of education, especially in our current era, where even in a place of doubt, or a double doubt, etc., a Jew is obligated to do everything possible for him, in every place his hand can reach, and Hashem will complete it for him.

It is my hope that you will mark the days of Geulah, 12-13 Tammuz, in an appropriate manner.

With blessings for a good month and good tidings.

It is surely unnecessary to repeat that it would please me to receive your response to all that has been said, provided it is with an open heart.

## 8843

B"H, 1 Tammuz, 5724
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 24 Sivan, in which you list some of the problems that are occupying your thoughts.

In accordance with your age and the saying of our Sages, of blessed memory, "If not now, when?", you must strive all the more to study our holy Torah—the Torah of life (a title that also includes the meaning of "instruction" for life in this world of ours)—with consistency and diligence. May this study lead to action, as commanded by our Sages, and we are promised, "You have labored and you have found".

Once you have acquired a certain measure of Torah knowledge, you will return to the problems you wrote about, reflect upon them, and find their solutions.

After all, the giving of the Torah to our entire people, the Children of Israel, was also specifically through the precedence of "we will do" to "we will hear."

It is my hope that you have acquaintances, and even more importantly, friends who are G-d-fearing and dedicated to His Torah, as for several reasons this is a good and necessary thing; there are many such people in Tel Aviv.

It is appropriate to have your tefillin checked—if this has not been done within the last twelve months—and each weekday, before putting on tefillin, to set aside a few coins for tzedakah.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

#### ***8843***

**Saying of our Sages:** Avos 1:14.

**As commanded by our Sages:** Kiddushin 40b.

**And we are promised:** Megillah 6b.

## 8844

B"H, 1 Tammuz, 5724
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings,

In response to your letter of Monday, in which you outline what you have been through and conclude with various ideas regarding your arrangements in the near future.

Given the situation you describe, and the fact that you are already in the United States, it is not advisable to leave here. Instead, you should utilize your familiarity, connections, and your work here in previous years in the field of *chinuch al taharas hakodesh* to find suitable employment for yourself.

May the *Ribono shel Olam*, who sustains and provides for the entire world in His goodness, with grace, kindness, and mercy, provide you with your livelihood in the appropriate place and in the appropriate manner.

Regarding what you wrote about adopting a child: You are surely aware of the difficulties and complications that follow adoption. First and foremost is the prohibition of *kiruv* (physical closeness), embracing, kissing, etc., which is almost impossible to avoid. Therefore, before you make a decision, you should clarify all of the above with a *rav moreh hora'ah* (as they are the ones directly involved in the matter).

It would be proper to have your *tefillin* checked, as well as the *mezuzos* in your home, to ensure they are all *kosher* according to *din*—if this has not been done within the last twelve months.

At a time of *ratzon*, I will mention you and your wife, *tichyeh*, at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, navgam, ze'er*.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*.

**Regarding the adoption of a child:** See also above, letter 8800, and the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 8846

8846

B”H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, 3 Tammuz, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter.

As we stand on the eve of Shabbos Kodesh, the parsha of "I am your portion and your inheritance," it is well known that the ruling of the Rambam states that these words do not apply only to the tribe of Levi, "but rather, every single person from among all the inhabitants of the world whose spirit moves him and whose intellect understands him to set himself apart to stand before Hashem, to serve Him and to worship Him, to know Hashem, and he walks upright as Hashem made him, and he casts off from his neck the yoke of the many calculations that human beings seek—such a person is sanctified as holy of holies, and Hashem shall be his portion and his inheritance forever and ever, and He will provide for him in this world that which is sufficient for him, just as He provided for the Kohanim and the Leviim. Behold, David, peace be upon him, says: 'Hashem is the portion of my inheritance and my cup; You support my lot.'"

May it be Hashem’s will that each and every one of you increases in diligence and perseverance in the study of Nigleh and Chassidus, and may this be with health of body and soul.

And this Shabbos is also the beginning of the redemption of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisrael, which is also our redemption and the liberation of our souls.

With blessings for good tidings in matters both personal and communal,

**M. Schneerson**

***

**8846**

General/Private. Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 8, p. 325, and completed according to a photograph of the letter. See also Letter 8857 below. 9 Teves. Sicha of 12 Tammuz 5724.

**Ruling of the Rambam:** Hilchos Shemitah V'Yovel, at the end.

**Every single person:** And not "every person" — for each one remains in his previous category even after his spirit moves him, etc. (See Magen Avraham 1:8 and the translation and Chazal there. Torah Or 37c on the verse in Tehillim 87:5). In the present case, it may be said that in general there are two categories: those whose Torah is their occupation, and the rest (see Berachos 35b; Torah Or, beginning of Parshas Terumah).

**From among all the inhabitants of the world:** Including the nations of the world — see Rosh Hashanah 1:2 (and from here is a proof for the Rambam’s version in the Mishnah there) — for the righteous among the nations of the world have a share in the World to Come (Rambam, Hilchos Melachim, end of Chapter 8).

**Whose spirit moves him:** Shemos 35:21. And "generosity" is a trait of the heart (see Ramban there).

**And whose intellect understands him:** The wisdom that is in the mind.

**To set himself apart... is sanctified as holy of holies:** Similar to Divrei Hayamim I 23:13, which is said regarding the Kohanim [and the Kohen Gadol, which fits the term "holy of holies," for only he enters that place. See Chiddushei Aggados, end of Horayos; Zohar Vol. 3, 176b; Bava Kamma 38a].

**To stand... to serve Him:** Devarim 10:8.

**To serve Him and to worship Him:** See Menachos 109b.

**Upright... seek:** See Koheles 7:29.

**Forever and ever:** The language of Sifrei, Devarim 23:7.

**For the Kohanim and the Leviim:** This is the text in the Rome edition of the Rambam.

**Behold, David:** Even though he was not from the tribe of Levi.

**Says:** Tehillim 16:5.

**You support my lot:** Only "support," for there must be some labor (Rambam, Hilchos Talmud Torah, Chapter 3, Law 10; and see Hilchos Talmud Torah of the Alter Rebbe, Chapter 3, Section 3) and according to the precision of the Radbaz here. But it is difficult, for if so, he is not "just as He provided for the Kohanim." Perhaps from here is a proof for the Kesef Mishneh (in Hilchos Talmud Torah there) that one may say the Rambam only excludes one who sets his heart [to rely on others while he does nothing].

Therefore, there are two modes: "Hashem is the portion of my inheritance," or "You support my lot." And this is not the place to elaborate.

## 8847

8847

B”H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, 3 Tammuz, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished Rabbi, the distinguished Chossid, G-d-fearing, occupied with communal needs, etc.,
Moreinu HaRav Shlomo Yosef, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

... Due to circumstances, the sending of this letter was delayed. In the interim, I was visited by the distinguished Rabbi, etc., etc., HaRav I.Y., may he live, and we spoke at length regarding several matters. I will transcribe here some of the points, as it is my hope that when the opportunity arises, you will be able to act upon this to bring these matters to fruition.

1) Regarding the ships: The aforementioned person told me explicitly that neither he nor the Chief Rabbinate ever issued a permit in this matter [though in his opinion, for those traveling on the ship (as opposed to the crew), it is merely a Rabbinic prohibition. I did not wish to dwell on this point, for even a Rabbinic prohibition—which lasts for twenty-four hours, a full day and night, and is done in public—is significant. I only hinted that according to many Poskim (the Ramban, the well-known Responsa of the Chasam Sofer, and others), it is even a Torah prohibition, and there is no need to elaborate here. However, I] took the opportunity to speak once again about the possibility of having the ships dock for the hours of Shabbos Kodesh. Judging by his reaction, it seems there is room for him to continue looking into this possibility, even though his response was that, to his knowledge, there is no prospect that they will agree to this. To this, I replied that for several technical reasons, the docking is mandatory anyway for several days at a time, and it depends on the good will to schedule the docking for the day of Shabbos Kodesh.

2) I emphasized, and repeated, that **it is imperative** to do something regarding the permit for marriage [among our brethren the Sephardim] at an early age, as permitted by the law of the Knesset, for several reasons: First of all, because even now there are **many** cases of betrothal and kiddushin, and even marriage, which are performed in secret due to the law, and the resulting harm is understood. Furthermore—

And this is also essential—in our generation, if only the Ashkenazim would also marry off their sons and daughters closer to the appropriate age, and not as the current situation is; and all the more so regarding the Sephardim, who have been accustomed to the aforementioned since time immemorial.

The magnitude of the rectification is beyond words. He promised that when the opportunity arises, he will look into the possibility of at least lowering the marriage age by a year or so.

3) Regarding the question of the "Marbak" (slaughterhouse) publicized in the newspapers: In my opinion, it is a great stumbling block that the shechitah should fall under a general organization—for according to the way of nature, in the end, it will be [...] the sole proprietor, or at the very least, the deciding factor in this.

And since, for the time being, in all general organizations the deciding voice belongs to the secularists, the breach that can emerge and grow from this, G-d forbid, is understood. Although the aforementioned reason and concern—it is difficult to say if it will convince the public opinion—one should utilize in such a case the opposition of the kosher meat merchants who fear for their livelihood, and the opposition that will certainly come from several towns for whom the matter of kosher meat is one of the sources of their income, and more.

In my opinion, the only way to cancel the aforementioned plan is solely through political pressure on the religious groups participating in the aforementioned—that they should withdraw from it. Then, even if the remaining partners continue, at least they will not have sole authority, and a word to the wise is sufficient.

Enclosed is a copy of the telegram regarding the departure of the aforementioned person from the United States.

I would add to the above that it seems from the words of the aforementioned person that he considers your opinion **greatly** and respects your views.

Rabbi R. S. Elberg, may he live, will now be visiting Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. I will repeat here what I wrote previously regarding the claim of R. S. (in response to my request to the aforementioned regarding the *Pardes* booklet dedicated to the Alter Rebbe)—that he is waiting for an article of weight from you regarding the Alter Rebbe, his books, and his teachings (or one of these three).

## 8848

8848

B"H, Motzaei Shabbos, Parshas "I am your portion and your inheritance among the Children of Israel," 5724. Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants of the Tanya study group at the Shoneh Halachos synagogue in the city of Netanya, in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established speedily by Mashiach Tzidkeinu,
May Hashem keep them and grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

It was with pleasure that I received the news that you have completed the first part of the holy Tanya.

And surely, following the well-known custom of "connecting the beginning to the completion," you have immediately begun the second part, which is Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah (and its introduction).

Regarding the content of the conclusion of the first part: "For Hashem your G-d is a consuming fire," as is discussed elsewhere—

—and perhaps one could say that the intention here refers to the maamar "For on this day He shall provide atonement" (Likutei Torah, beginning of Parshas Acharei)—

—the analogy of a "consuming fire" is that just as fire is not considered to be "light" or "fire" at all, nor does it illuminate below unless it catches onto a physical object—and it also "consumes" and destroys it—so too is it regarding Hashem (who becomes) "your G-d" (your strength and vitality), who illuminates and is revealed below specifically through the 613 mitzvos, as is explained briefly at the end of chapter 53, which is the conclusion of the first part.

Their fulfillment in truth is through love, which is the root and foundation for the fulfillment of all positive mitzvos (which also includes the mitzvah of fear, which is the root and foundation for the fulfillment of all negative mitzvos), the service of Aharon, who loves (and draws down love even to) the creatures, the creatures of the world.

May it be the will that this study be great, for it will lead to the action of fulfilling the mitzvos, so that, in the words of the author of the Tanya, our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, each and every one will walk in the straight path that he has taught us, and we will walk in his ways, may his merit protect us.

This is regarding the service of Hashem in heavenly matters; and in worldly matters, may you find even more of Hashem’s blessing, and "whoever is closest is prioritized for blessing."

With respect and blessing.

The laying of the cornerstone for the new synagogue and also a center for the youth, our brethren, the children of Israel, may Hashem keep them and grant them life—

With respect and with a blessing of *L’chaim, l’chaim v’livracha*,

**M. Schneerson**

B"H, Erev the days of redemption, 12-13 Tammuz, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch
For the Chag HaSiyum,
Montreal

Peace and Blessing!

The Chag HaSiyum—which takes place immediately following the days of redemption of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisrael, the founder of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch in Montreal—will surely be imbued with the impression of these significant days.

The mesiras nefesh of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for the institutions of Torah, for the students of the yeshivos, and for all matters of Torah and mitzvos, which led to his life-threatening arrest, also brought about his miraculous liberation. This must always serve as a reminder—which must be translated into practical action—that mesiras nefesh for Torah and mitzvos, not only for oneself but also for a fellow Jew, must triumph even against the strongest obstacles; and certainly when the obstacles are quite small, or are nothing more than imagined.

And although no one can compare, in strength and mesiras nefesh, to the Baal HaGeulah, one must also not forget that as a faithful shepherd and Nasi of our generation, the Baal HaGeulah ignited in each and every one of us a glowing spark of mesiras nefesh and additional strength to be able to follow the path that he paved for us.

I hope that each of the students completing their studies—for this "Siyum" is nothing more than a preparation for the beginning of a higher level—will continue the study of Torah, Nigleh and Chassidus, and the fulfillment of mitzvos, with an increased measure of mesiras nefesh—mesiras haratzon—and with growing hasmadah, shekidah, and hiddur, and will also utilize their fullest influence on others in the same direction.

And may Hashem Yisbarach grant you success in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With blessings for outstanding success and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8850

8850

B"H, 12 Tammuz, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter.

As we stand on this day of redemption—which, as explained by the Baal HaGeulah in his letter for the first celebration of 12 Tammuz, is a "festival day of the redemption of Israel, who are engaged in the dissemination of Torah"—the dissemination must be specifically among many students (as continues in his letter, "Torah of the many"). In the language of the Rambam: "to teach His upright ways and righteous judgments to the many."

This engagement in the dissemination of Torah is accomplished by those who themselves teach and study Torah in public, or by those who support with their wealth and their efforts the institutions and classes of Torah for the many, or by those who establish new ones, or by all of these methods combined.

May it be His will that each and every one does everything necessary in this regard, and may the blessing of the Baal HaGeulah (in the aforementioned letter) be fulfilled in its entirety: that Hashem will bestow upon them, within the entirety of our brethren the Jewish people, may they live, an abundance of life and manifold blessing, without limit.

With blessings for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8857

8857

B"H, 12-13 Tammuz, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter.

As we stand in the days of redemption, 12-13 Tammuz—the redemption of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi of Yisrael—which is also our own redemption and the liberation of our souls, may it be His will that everyone be redeemed from their many preoccupations and complex calculations, and that Hashem be their portion and inheritance.

As is well known, the ruling of the Rambam states that this does not apply only to the Kohanim and Leviim, but rather, "any person from among all the inhabitants of the world whose spirit moves him and whose intellect understands to set himself apart to stand before Hashem, to serve Him and to worship Him, to know Hashem, and he walks upright as Elokim created him, and he removes from his neck the yoke of the many calculations that human beings seek—such a person is sanctified as holy of holies, and Hashem shall be his portion and inheritance forever and for all eternity, and He will provide him with what is sufficient in this world, just as He provided for the Kohanim and the Leviim. As David, peace be upon him, says: 'Hashem is the portion of my inheritance and my cup; You support my lot.'"

May it be His will that you increase in diligence and perseverance in the study of Nigleh and Chassidus, and may this be with health of body and soul.

With blessings for good tidings, in general and in particular,

**M. Schneerson**

#### 8857

General and specific. See above, letter 8846, and the references in the footnotes there.

**"Any person":** Not just "every person"—for each individual remains in their previous category even after their spirit moves them, etc. (see Magen Avraham 1:8 and the translation and Chazal there; Torah Or 37c on the verse in Tehillim 87:5). In this context, it can be said that there are generally two types: those whose Torah is their primary occupation, and the rest (see Berachos 35b; Torah Or, beginning of Parshas Terumah).

**"From among all the inhabitants of the world":** Including the nations of the world—see Rosh Hashanah 1:2 (and this is proof for the Rambam’s version of the Mishnah there)—for the pious among the nations of the world have a share in the World to Come (Rambam, Hilchos Melachim, end of chapter 8).

**"Whose spirit moves him":** Shemos 35:21. Generosity is a trait of the heart (see Ramban there).

**"And whose intellect understands":** Wisdom in the mind.

**"To set himself apart... is sanctified as holy of holies":** Similar to Divrei Hayamim I 23:13, which is stated regarding the Kohanim [and the Kohen Gadol, which corresponds to "holy of holies," for only he enters that place. See Chiddushei Aggados, end of Horayos; Zohar III 176b; Bava Kamma 38a].

**"To stand... to serve Him":** Devarim 10:8.

**"To serve Him and to worship Him":** See Menachos 109b.

**"Upright... seek":** See Koheles 7:29.

**"Forever and for all eternity":** Language of Sifrei, Devarim 23:7.

**"For the Kohanim and the Leviim":** This is the text in the Rome edition of the Rambam.

**"As David":** Even though he was not from the tribe of Levi.

**"You support my lot":** Only "support," for there must be some labor (Rambam, Hilchos Talmud Torah 3:10; see Hilchos Talmud Torah by the Alter Rebbe 3:3), as the Radbaz notes here. But this is difficult, for if so, he is not "just as He provided for the Kohanim." Perhaps this is proof for the Kesef Mishneh (in Hilchos Talmud Torah, ibid.) that the Rambam is only excluding one who sets his heart [on relying on others, etc.].

Therefore, there are two modes: "Hashem is the portion of my inheritance," or "You support my lot." But this is not the place to elaborate.

## 8864

8864

B”H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Honorable Rabbi and Chossid, man of action, man of stature, descendant of holy lineage, etc., Rabbi Yitzchak Meir HaKohen, shlita.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your invitation to the "Fifth Great Assembly" scheduled to take place in the month of Menachem Av, may it come upon us for good, in Jerusalem, the Holy City, may it be rebuilt and established, by Mashiach Tzidkeinu, immediately.

I hereby express my blessing to you and to all the participants in the assembly, may Hashem grant them long life. May it be the will of Hashem that the prophecy, which is sought, hoped for, and promised, be fulfilled soon: "That all created beings will become one single group to perform Your will with a whole heart."

If you will say that in the style and phrasing mentioned above, there is included a complete program for every assembly for the sake of Heaven, at any time and in any place—and all the more so for an assembly of our brethren, the Children of Israel, who tremble at the word of Hashem and His Torah and mitzvos, in this era of ours, and in our Holy Land and the Holy City—may it be rebuilt and established:

(a) **"And they will become one single group"** — The creation of all Bnei Yisrael as one group in truth is possible only through the fulfillment of the mitzvah of "Love your fellow as yourself" for every soul of Israel, from the greatest to the smallest. For all the souls of the Children of Israel are compatible, and there is one Father for them all; it is only the bodies that are divided. And the soul is the essence, while the body is merely secondary (as all this is explained in Tanya, Chapter 32).

(b) **"To perform Your will"** — This means that the goal of this gathering and the unity of the Children of Israel is solely and exclusively to perform the will of our Father in Heaven.

(c) **"With a whole heart"** — This means that the manner of performance, the decisions, and the actions must be with all heart and soul, without hesitation, but rather clearly and decisively.

And there must be completeness in all three stages: thought, speech, and action. Start with deep contemplation that will reveal the knowledge of our eternal Torah and its clear instructions for all the problems of our confused generation; the raising of a voice with strength—the voice is the voice of Yaakov, "in the meditation of Torah" and its aforementioned knowledge; and finally, the end of action, and action is the essence—with practical results to permeate daily life with Torah and mitzvos in all branches of life, in all their details and the details of their details.

And if this is true in every era, it is all the more so in these days of ours, for it is the command of the hour and the need of the hour—both from the perspective of the situation, which demands extra effort, and from the perspective of the capacity of the hour, for the heart of the sons and daughters of Israel is awake, especially in this period of ours, which is full of events, upheavals, and disappointments, which have awakened in many circles, and especially in youth circles, an intense thirst for something true and stable.

And there is no truth except the Torah of truth and its mitzvos, which were given by Hashem, the G-d of truth—Torah and mitzvos without compromises and without concessions. For then, not only will "truth sprout from the earth" and be accepted, but from Heaven as well, a special Divine assistance will be reflected and drawn down for great success.

With respect, appreciation, and a blessing for success and good tidings.

You asked for my opinion on what the primary issues are that currently stand on the agenda and which have priority in the order of the day of the assembly—

The space is too short to contain it, so I will list only one or two things that appear to me:

**In the general and conceptual sphere:**

A clear declaration that in every place and at every time, **only** the Torah is our life—for the individual, for the community, and for the collective.

And because it is one Torah and a Torah of truth, given by the One Hashem, our G-d of truth, there is no place for combining the Torah with anything else—whatever it may be—and it rejects all compromises.

On the contrary, for those who deluded themselves and others that in the decline of the generations, the way to bring hearts closer to Judaism and its mitzvos is through compromises—the bitter reality has come and slapped them in the face, as they see that from a compromise in general, and by half, they have deteriorated to a third, etc., and on to the ideology that "all the nations are the House of Israel," and from there to bowing and nullification before every small nation, and from there to assimilation, G-d forbid, among the idolaters.

Our Sages of blessed memory have long warned that if one finds a "breach," the advised counsel is to "build a fence around it."

**In the Holy Land in particular:**

A practical—and constant—connection with the youth who are past the age of compulsory education by law, the majority of whom are currently not in a school framework and are left to themselves and the influence of the street—a connection, of course, for the purpose of instilling in them a spirit of fear of Heaven, love of Torah, and affection for the mitzvos, up to the point of fulfilling them in daily life.

**In the Diaspora, and especially where the time causes it:**

The Judaism of South America (and similar places), which is crying out for help in their spiritual situation. And of course, help not through sighs, but through sending emissaries there—each for an appropriate duration—of educators who are G-d-fearing, guides, and teachers of the way (of the King, the King of Kings), worthy of their name, etc., etc., who will sit with them and among them and encourage them and strengthen their spirit, the spirit of the Israel of old. And they will teach them—and the younger generation in particular—a way of life, in daily life, according to our Torah, the Torah of life, and the fulfillment of its mitzvos, of which it is said, "and he shall live by them."

P.S. **"In the meditation of Torah":** And prior to this (Pirkei D'Rabbi Eliezer, end of Chapter 2) it must be "the voice of Yaakov in the unification of the Name"—the service of prayer, until one unifies His Name—for then the "meditation of Torah" (Gittin 19a) is in order and as written in the Torah (see Rashi and Tosafos, Berachos 5b; Likkutei Torah of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, Parshas Bracha 96b).

**"He found a breach and built a fence around it":** This is the only advised counsel in **all** matters of Judaism, as instructed by Chazal regarding this in three categories, and in order: in Rabbinic laws that require strengthening (Eruvin 6a, Rosh Hashanah 19a). And even in Torah laws whose reasons have been revealed (Eruvin 100b, and see Sanhedrin 21b), and even in the statutes (chukim) and the innovation within the statutes (Chullin 110a, Hilchos Temurah of the Rambam, Chapter 6, and Rashi in Yoma 67b, Chullin 108a and in Tosafos, s.v. *mibasar* there).

## 8867

8867

By the Grace of G-d, 5 Menachem Av, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, and occupied with communal needs, R' Shneur Zalman Shragai, may he live and be well.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 27 Tammuz, as well as your previous one.

Many thanks for your thoughtfulness in informing me regarding the packages, etc. I assume you will continue to do so in the future, and I thank you in advance.

Regarding your observation about the special importance of the mitzvah of *ahavas Yisrael*—noting that even among the nations of the world, an Englishman loves his fellow Englishmen, etc.—the fundamental difference is understood from the wording of the verse, "And you shall love your neighbor **as yourself**." Just as a person’s love for himself is not dependent on his perceiving his own virtues—whether in intellect, character traits, or in thought, speech, and action; on the contrary, "love covers all transgressions"—so too is the commandment regarding the love of one's fellow: it must likewise be a self-love that is unconditional, not dependent on any specific thing or virtue, etc.

Based on this, we can understand the difficulty: how is it possible to reach the level of loving another "as yourself"? The Alter Rebbe provides the explanation in *Tanya*, Chapter 32. He begins by explaining the level of love for one's fellow that is easier to attain—"for who knows their greatness and virtue," etc.—but ultimately, this is still a love dependent on virtue. Therefore, he adds the explanation that "all are equal, and one Father has created us all," etc., "they are truly brothers."

See there.

A special emphasis on all of the above, according to the teachings of Chassidus, is explained in the *Sefer HaMitzvos* of the Tzemach Tzedek, Mitzvah of *Ahavas Yisrael*, Chapter 2. See there.

We bring this topic up in connection with the appropriate days, as we are currently in the *Bein HaMetzarim* (the Three Weeks) of the destruction of the Second Beis Hamikdash, which occurred because of *sinas chinam* (baseless hatred). It is simple to understand that we have been commanded to create a remembrance of the destruction, especially during these days, with the intention of bringing about a rectification. For the destruction, as the prayer states, is "because of our sins we were exiled from our land," etc., and it is impossible to nullify the effect without first nullifying the cause. Any deficiency or weakness in the cause brings about a deficiency and weakness in the effect, even if—as explained in the teachings of Chassidus—it is for the time being only in the higher worlds. Since the primary sin, as our Sages of blessed memory informed us, was *sinas chinam*, its rectification must be through *ahavas chinam*—that is, love that is unconditional. May it be His will that we soon merit the end of our exile and the true and complete Redemption through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, and may these days be transformed into joy and gladness.

With respect and blessings.

In my conversation with the esteemed Rabbi, the Gaon and Chassid, occupied with communal needs, R' I.Y. Unterman, the Chief Rabbi, the discussion also turned to the matter of the Israeli ships. In response to my question, he stated clearly that neither he nor the Chief Rabbinate had ever granted permission to travel on those ships.

#### ***8867***

Published in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 32, p. 245, and completed based on the secretariat's copy.

**R' Shneur Zalman Shragai:** Further letters to him—above, Vol. 21, 8429, and the references in the notes there.

**We bring this topic up:** See also letter 8869.

**As our Sages informed us:** *Yoma* 9b.

**In my conversation:** See above, letter 8847.

**Regarding the Israeli ships:** See also above, letter 8331, and the references in the notes there.

## 8868

8868

B"H, 5 Menachem Av, 5724

Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Shmuel Yitzchak HaKohen Avidgor, may he live

Greetings and blessings!

It is somewhat surprising that since your letter from several months ago, I have not received any correspondence from you, although my hope is strong that you are not being particular with me regarding the delay in my response, which is due to various preoccupations—and unfortunately, not all of these preoccupations are of a joyous nature.

Consistent with the style of your letter, I hope that you have participated in several Chassidic farbrengens in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established. Therefore, it was surprising to me that your name was not mentioned among those who participated in the celebration (in memory of) 12 Tammuz in Kfar Chabad. Surely, you participated in such a celebration elsewhere in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established.

It is unnecessary to emphasize to someone like you that the concept of "remembrance" is the awakening to actual deeds. In this specific case, it is in the spirit of the one whose celebration and redemption we mark on 12-13 Tammuz—who sacrificed his life for the strengthening and dissemination of Torah and mitzvos, without regard for obstacles or delays. During these days of the "Three Weeks," it is certainly fitting and proper to act and work in this direction. The memory of the destruction reminds us of and confronts us with the cause, as the text of the prayer states: "And because of our sins we were exiled from our land," etc. The purpose of the remembrance is for the sake of rectification, and the effect cannot be nullified except by nullifying the cause. May it be the will of Hashem that very soon we will merit the end of our exile and the true and complete redemption through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, and that these days will be transformed into joy and gladness.

With regards to your brother, may he live, and with honor, blessing, and thanks for conveying the regards.

## 8869

8869

B"H, 5 Menachem Av, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Schneur Zalman Maschari

Shalom u’Bracha!

It is with pleasure that I acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 26th of Tammuz, and I thank you for your attention.

...Seeing the feelings of your heart and your love for Kfar Chabad, within the context of Ahavas Yisrael in general, strengthening oneself in this is a matter of great timeliness, especially during these days of the Bein HaMetzarim, the period of the destruction of the Second Beis Hamikdash, which occurred due to sinas chinam, as our Sages of blessed memory have informed us. It is simple to understand that the command to create a remembrance of the destruction—especially during these days—is intended for the sake of rectification. For the destruction is, as the text of the prayer states, "because of our sins we were exiled from our land," and it is impossible to nullify the effect without nullifying the cause. Any deficiency or weakness in the cause brings about a deficiency or weakness in the effect, even if—as is explained in the teachings of Chassidus—it is for the time being only in the higher worlds. And since the primary sin was sinas chinam, its rectification is through ahavas chinam.

May it be the will of Hashem that very soon we merit the end of our exile and the true and complete Redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, and may these days be transformed into joy and gladness.

With respect and a blessing for health.

#### ***8869***

**Mr. Schneur Zalman Maschari:** Additional letters to him—see above, 8812, and the references in the notes there.

**As our Sages have informed us:** Yoma 9b.

8870

B”H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, 9 Av (deferred), 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished Chossid, G-d-fearing, man of action, etc.,
Rabbi R.M.P. HaKohen

Greetings and Blessings!

It gives me pleasure to learn that these days mark the conclusion—by the group of those who study Torah in public, and in a place of prayer, the Adas Yaakov synagogue, may Hashem grant them life—of Maseches Beitzah, and that they are continuing in holiness with the study of Maseches Sukkah.

And they are arranging matters so that the *siyum* will take place on the first *yahrtzeit* of his father-in-law—may he live a long and good life—the distinguished Chossid, G-d-fearing, man of action, a man of fine character who was occupied with mitzvos, and especially with the affairs of the synagogue, etc., Moreinu Harav Dovid HaLevi, may his soul be bound in the bond of life.

Indeed, all matters concerning the synagogue and the *beis medrash* have a special connection to this month, as per the prophecy of Yechezkel HaKohen: “Thus said the L-rd G-d: Although I have removed them far among the nations and although I have scattered them among the countries, yet I have been to them a *mikdash me’at* (a minor sanctuary—these are the synagogues and houses of study) in the countries where they have come.”

For as we stand in the days of remembrance for those days in this time—the destruction of our Holy Temple, the First and the Second—it is understood, based on the instruction of Chazal that “the deed is the essential thing,” and the explicit verse, “Fear G-d and keep His commandments, **for this is the whole** of man,” that the intent of this remembrance is that it should influence and lead to action in practice.

First and foremost, the content of this remembrance is the matter of the destruction and its cause, which are as explicitly stated in many places in Tanach and in the language of Chazal: “Because of our sins we were exiled from our land,” and “The hand that was sent against Your Sanctuary.”

From this comes the conclusion that the “war,” the weakness, and the deficiency in the cause (our sins) weaken and diminish the effect (our exile from our land, the hand that was sent against the Sanctuary) and hasten the Redemption—the true and complete Redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

As per the instruction of the *Moreh Nevuchim* (from his generation until our own) and his clear halachic ruling in *Yad HaChazakah*: The King Moshiach is the one who gathers the dispersed of Yisrael. Prior to this, and as a prerequisite and preparation for it, in addition to his being “one who contemplates Torah and occupies himself with mitzvos like Dovid his father,” he will “compel all of Yisrael to walk in it and strengthen its breaches.” Following this (and in this order), he will “fight the wars of Hashem” and be victorious over “all the nations surrounding him,” and he will “build the Temple in its place and gather the dispersed of Yisrael.”

May it be the will that each and every one will “fight against the cause—our sins”—through the fulfillment of Torah and mitzvos, to walk in it and strengthen its breaches.

And based on the promise that “one who comes to purify himself is assisted,” he will succeed.

Through this, he will hasten the end of our exile and bring closer the coming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu and our redemption.

And we will merit the fulfillment of the prophecy that these days will be turned into gladness and joy.

With blessings that very soon we will merit the true redemption of all the Children of Yisrael from the “wilderness of the nations,” which is the wilderness of exile. For regarding each and every one it is said, “And you are My sheep, the sheep of My pasture,” for the earth and all that fills it belongs to Hashem, and therefore all are “domesticated.” Even those who are found in *Ashtaros Karnayim*—a term for strength and wealth—who err by saying, “My power and the might of my hand have made me this wealth,” will ultimately not be cast away from Him. And the poverty of *Ashtaros Karnayim* is met by the shadow of the *Sukkah*, which teaches a person humility and lowliness, so that his heart will not be haughty to say, “Our hands have done this.” Rather, he remembers His wonders and His awe-inspiring deeds; he remembers the Exodus from Egypt, and “As in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt, I will show him wonders”—in our imminent redemption.

With regards to all the participants in the study, may they live and be well, with respect.

Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Great is the merit of this endeavor to stand by you in what you need and for the fulfillment of your heart’s desires for the good.

This is especially so in light of the well-known saying of the Baal Shem Tov, that Hashem’s love for every single Jew is incomparably greater than the love of elderly parents for an only child born to them in their old age.

It would be appropriate to have your tefillin checked, as well as the mezuzos in your home, to ensure they are all kosher according to the law. Your wife, tichyeh, should observe the good custom of kosher Jewish women to set aside money for tzedakah before lighting the candles every Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov.

With respect and blessings for good tidings in all the above.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

P.S. Regarding your writing about arranging a personal audience (pa”p), there is no necessity for this at all, as the response is written above. The Torah is protective of the money of Yisrael—the financial expenses of the trip—and in such a case, this also applies to the expenditure of energy, time, etc.

8875

## 8875*

[24 Menachem Av, 5724]

Based on the above, it is appropriate to speak with the baalei batim, the president, and so on, **from which** it becomes **clear** what the issue of the mechitza is. Those who oppose a proper mechitza have now **revealed** their true perspective, and from this it is understood that all those who believe in Torah min hashamayim (the opposite of the Conservatives) must fight for the sake of the mechitza, etc.

This does not prevent you **at all** from organizing the aforementioned petition, whether now or later. On the contrary, at that point he will not be able to oppose them as strongly as he does now, because by accepting the position, he acknowledges that they [the congregants] have the deciding vote even in spiritual matters. And even if they guarantee this in a contract, they are currently changing the contract.

This is not his business at all, and in general, it is a matter of great doubt whether it is permitted according to din.

#### 8875*

A response to R' Shmuel Pesach Bogomilsky, shlita, regarding his letter from 24 Menachem Av. Additional letters to him: above 8795, and those noted in the footnotes there.

**Based on the above:** In his letter: "This evening, Rabbi... called me, saying that the baalei batim of my shul visited him and showed him that they had prepared a 'petition' to make the shul Conservative."

**This does not:** In his letter: "In the constitution of the shul, and also in my contract, it is written that the Rabbi himself is responsible for matters of Yiddishkeit, and therefore I told them... that if they do not agree to the fixing of the mechitza, it means they are nullifying my contract."

**This is not his business:** In his letter: "I asked Rabbi Moshe Duber Rivkin, shlita, and he said that he cannot give permission for a 4-foot mechitza, nor to be the Rabbi on the condition that he will fix it over time... and especially to save them from [becoming] Conservative; such a spiritual question belongs to the Rebbe, shlita."

## 8777

8777

By the Grace of Hashem, 25 Menachem Av, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned individual, engaged in communal needs, R’ Chaim Yona
May he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

After a long interval, I was pleased to receive your letter of Monday, with the good news that you will soon be concluding the public study of *Ein Yaakov* which takes place in your home.

May Hashem Yisbarach help that it should be in a good and successful hour in all its details—both the completion of the *Ein Yaakov* and the immediate commencement of it anew, as is the custom among Jews, for *minhag Yisrael Torah hi*, that we attach the beginning to the completion.

And especially as it is explained in many places, the connection of **the** completion with **the** beginning, in various ways. One of them is:

Seemingly, one must understand how it is truly possible to fulfill the requirement of a true peace between people, whose opinions are not alike, etc.

A requirement with such intensity that it is said: "Hashem did not find a vessel that holds blessing for Yisrael **except** for peace."

The explanation for this is that it is made possible through the reading of *Krias Shema*, right at the beginning of the twenty-four-hour cycle, as in the beginning of the *Mishnah*: "From when do we recite *Shema* in the evening?" The content of *Krias Shema* is to crown Hashem as King, until one recognizes that "Hashem is One," in all seven heavens, upon the earth, and in the four corners of the world.

This acts to surrender and yield the will of each individual to the will of Hashem, the One. At that point, everything that can divide and differentiate disappears, and true peace is achieved. Hashem Yisbarach then bestows His fullest blessing, as we say at the **conclusion** of the *Shemoneh Esrei*: "Bless us, our Father, as one" (see *Tanya*, Chapter 32).

And as is explained at length in many places in our holy Torah, *Toras Chaim*, and more deeply in *Pnimiyus HaTorah*—for in the *Gemara*, this is the *Aggadah* found in the *Sefer Ein Yaakov*, in which most of the secrets of the Torah are hidden (see *Iggeres HaKodesh* of the Alter Rebbe, Epistle 23).

With blessings for success in all the above, and regards to all the participants, *shlita*, in the most exalted study mentioned above,

**M. Schneerson**

B"H, 25 Menachem Av, 5724

Judging by the tone of your letter, the hope is that you are doing everything within your power to spread Yiddishkeit in your location now, especially in light of what our Sages said in their Mishnah that a father merits through his children, etc., and we are assured that one who comes to purify himself is assisted.

This is especially true as we approach the auspicious days of the month of Elul, which is like a King who, before entering the city, is met by the townspeople who go out to greet Him in the field. At that time, anyone who wishes is permitted to go out to greet Him, and He receives them all with a friendly countenance, etc., as explained in *Likutei Torah*, Parshas Re'eh 32b, by our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, author of the *Tanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*.

With respect and blessing.

## 8879

B"H, 28 Menachem Av, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Rabbi Moshe Shapiro, may he live,
Rabbi of the great community of Atlantic City

Greetings and blessings!

It was with great interest and joy that I received the news that under your leadership, the members of the community have been inspired to build a new mikveh in your city, and that this coming Sunday the cornerstone laying ceremony will take place, at which you will deliver words of blessing on behalf of all the rabbis of the holy community of Atlantic City.

This time is particularly auspicious for such an endeavor, as we approach Rosh Chodesh Elul, which begins the forty days of teshuvah. It is well known how highly our Sages of blessed memory valued the importance of the mikveh, to the extent that they used it as a proof and analogy for the concept of teshuvah at the end of Perek Yom HaKippurim (the chapter of teshuvah): "Just as a mikveh purifies the impure, so too does Hashem purify Yisrael."

I conclude with heartfelt wishes that you will soon celebrate the completion of this project, and may this also hasten the fulfillment of the promise: "I will sprinkle pure water upon you, and you shall be purified" (taharah), "and I will give you a new heart..." (teshuvah), "and you shall dwell in the land..." (the true and complete Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu).

With respect and with blessings for a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah*.

Enclosed is a copy of my letter to the mikveh committee.

## 8880

B"H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Elul, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

R' Schneur Zalman

As we stand on Erev Rosh Chodesh Elul, it is timely to recall the words of the Alter Rebbe regarding the unique quality of the days of this month of mercy. It is like a king who, before entering his city, is met by the townspeople who go out to greet him in the field. At that time, anyone who wishes to go out to greet him is permitted to do so, and he receives them all with a friendly countenance, etc., as explained in Likutei Torah, Parshas Re'eh, 32b.

May it be the will that this matter also be fulfilled as in the language of our Rebbe—with a friendly countenance—Above, and consequently, it will be drawn down below with a friendly countenance as well.

Moving from one matter to another regarding the affairs of the King of the world, I express my hope that in the words of blessing you will deliver for the upcoming Rosh Hashanah, you will explicitly mention the Name of Heaven, for to Him all shall crown, and from Him come all blessings (including your forgiveness for this remark of mine).

With appreciation and respect, and with blessings for a *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year.

## 8884

B"H, 25 Elul, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 15 Elul. First and foremost, I must express the great satisfaction I felt upon seeing from your letter your attitude toward the affairs of Chabad and the Chabad schools, and furthermore—and this is the essence—your own words in your letter: "The spirit of Chabad and its Torah are also very close to me, and I strive to study it." Certainly, as our Sages of blessed memory have stated, study leads to action, especially when the person in question is an educator—and not only that, but a supervisor of educators. For every appointment comes from Heaven, from which it is understood that the strengths and possibilities are granted to fulfill that role and appointment with complete success. May it be His will that you exert influence in the aforementioned direction upon all those under your supervision as well. For we have been promised that one who comes to purify himself—and it is well known how our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, precisely interpreted this: not only to purify oneself, but also to purify others—is assisted from Above.

Regarding the actual question concerning the management of the school, you are correct in writing that the first and foremost priority in any school is the benefit of the students and their success in their studies and education. Therefore, it is essential that the administrator be the one most suited for that role. And since this conclusion is as stated, there is certainly the possibility of bringing it into reality. Moreover, as with all matters of our Torah, whose ways are ways of pleasantness, etc., here too there is the possibility of bringing it into reality in the aforementioned manner. As mentioned above, since you are the supervisor and the matter has been entrusted to your care, ultimately you will find the way to bring the conclusion into reality for the benefit of the students. May Hashem grant you success, and the promise that "one who comes to purify is assisted" certainly includes this area as well.

There is a strong hope that, in the end, even those who, for whatever reason, are not sufficiently considering the benefit of the students will see the truth and will even admit to you that at the time of the decision, you stood by your principles and did not heed their demands.

I look forward to hearing good news regarding all of the above.

As we approach the new year, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all that is yours: a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With respect and blessing,

By the Grace of G-d

***

I acknowledge receipt of your book, *Avnei Derech*, with a request for your forgiveness for the delay in this acknowledgment, which was due to several reasons. Thank you for your thoughtfulness in sending your book. A person’s creation—to a significant degree—reflects the author, and since this book also contains chapters from the history of your life, and given the distance between us, it also serves as a form of personal acquaintance with the author.

I am accustomed to thinking, when I receive a book from an author, that they did not send it to me "for nothing," and that the author’s intent is surely that I should examine the book. If I have any comments, the author would accept them, even if I do not identify with the author’s worldview. Therefore, regarding your book, I will permit myself to note a few comments, particularly on the internal point of the book: the portrayal of the *kvutzah* (collective) and the life of the *kvutzah*, a subject to which you specifically dedicate your book.

I hope you will agree that the matter of the *kvutzah* is not a goal in and of itself, and certainly not the ultimate goal; rather, its purpose is to achieve a desired and hoped-for order of life through collective cooperation.

In and of itself, the nature of the *kvutzah* is, on the face of it, to equate the small and the great, which is essentially the opposite of human nature; for just as human beings differ in their faces, so too do they differ in their opinions.

Therefore, the individual finds satisfaction and wholeness when they are able to bring into action everything they possess in potential, and to the fullest extent, not so much in the matters they share with their peers, but specifically in their individual sphere where they excel over their peers and environment, for that is their true self. On the other hand, man is not by nature a recluse—"it is not good for man to be alone"—and he seeks a social life within which, and through which, and with the help of which, he can reach his own wholeness.

Based on the aforementioned premise, on the one hand, the life of the *kvutzah* has great importance in that it provides a background for the pooling of the strengths of many people, thereby achieving greater results than the sum of all individual strengths. As is known, the activity of two people together is greater than double the activity of each one individually. Furthermore, among the positive aspects of the *kvutzah* is that it removes the undesirable jealousy and competition that often lead to the deterioration of relationships between one person and another, whereas collective action generally brings hearts closer together, and so on.

On the other hand, the purpose of the *kvutzah* is not to abolish all competition entirely, for one of the factors that stimulates extra effort, progress, and the utilization of all one’s strengths with alacrity, is precisely the fact that a person has a challenge and competition. Rather, the *kvutzah* should channel this natural competition into a higher sphere. In other words, instead of competition in an individualistic society beginning with the most basic, physical, and material needs—to the extent that, as our Sages said, "Were it not for the fear of the government (the necessity of society), one man would swallow his neighbor alive"—in a *kvutzah*, it is possible to transfer this energy to greater achievements, whether in a surplus beyond essential needs or in a more elevated sphere: the life of the spirit.

The conclusion from the above is that the matter of the *kvutzah* and the life of the *kvutzah* is not a goal and achievement in itself, but a stage, a preparation, and a path for the development of the individuality and uniqueness of each and every person, and their realization in the best and fullest manner.

This fundamental evaluation of the *kvutzah* applies not only after a full collective order of life has already been achieved and one must decide practically how to utilize the advantage of the strengths and how to highlight each person’s individual traits and talents in their full scope; it also applies right at the beginning of the *kvutzah*’s life. This is because often, and perhaps most of the time, the very order of the *kvutzah*’s life must, as mentioned, arouse internal resistance against the order and regime that attempts to subdue the individual as an individual and turn them into a part of the mass—the *kvutzah*. Conversely, if the individual knows that this is merely a stage in their development and a path that increases their potential to reach greater individual achievements—by freeing them from worries at a lower level (regarding their essential needs, which are obtained more easily and without waste of energy and time thanks to the collective action)—then this recognition will not only nullify their natural resistance, but will even add enthusiasm and dedication in fulfilling their roles in the *kvutzah*.

The above applies not only to the success of the *kvutzah* in general, but also to the content of life and the way of life in the *kvutzah*, which you also touch upon in your book, such as the relationships between parents and children and the like (and more so, as the damage in this area is liable to exceed the benefit), since these relationships are in the "spiritual" sphere of a person’s life, where the independence of the individual is important and essential.

There is another point, which in my opinion is important, and that is the change in feeling and attitude toward the *kvutzah* on the part of the founders of the *kvutzah* versus those born into the *kvutzah*. If the founders of the *kvutzah*, or those who came to the life of the *kvutzah* from a relatively close background, can find psychological satisfaction in recognizing that they arrived at this—as you write—from completely and utterly different lives, and from an environment permeated with an opposing worldview, and achieved the life of the *kvutzah* through toil, labor, sacrifices, and self-denial, all of which adds value and admiration to what has been achieved—then those who were born in the *kvutzah* or raised in it view this order of life as natural. For them, the limitations of the life of the *kvutzah* mentioned above are certainly more prominent than the positive sides, which must arouse in them psychological dissatisfaction or even rebellion, and at the very least, friction toward those who impose a collective regime upon them (and highlighting the *kvutzah* as a stage and preparation will be helpful here as well).

Hence the poignant problem, to which I did not find an answer in your book: what do we "give" to the generation born in the *kvutzah* as a goal or ideal that they would want to reach, even through toil, labor, and *mesiras nefesh* within the framework of the life of the society?

Lastly, it is understood that I read with interest the "Chapters of Life" at the end of your book. Here, too, I will permit myself to make a comment: it is a pity and a shame that you did not include in these autobiographical notes a record regarding the "source" that resulted in your wearing a *kippah* while reading verses of *Tanach* in the Knesset. Especially since you surely anticipated in advance that there would be a reaction from the left—a negative reaction—and yet you performed a significant act. The foundation for this is surely rooted and laid in the beginning of your life, in the home of your father or grandfather, and the like.

As is the way of the Children of Israel to integrate and connect the matters they discuss with the days of the year, and especially the days of *moadim* and holidays: even on Rosh Hashanah, our Sages emphasized the human being as an individual. And not only on the first Rosh Hashanah, the day G-d created the first man, but as a lesson and emphasis of our Sages: "Therefore man was created alone, to teach you (that in all generations and in all places) one soul is like a full world." They continued to explain that no two people are alike, therefore every single person is obligated to say, "The world was created for my sake." In other words, precisely in the fact that no person is like another, they are as important as a full world (*Sanhedrin*, end of Chapter 4). This matter also served as a central point for my letter for Rosh Hashanah, which is enclosed herewith, and which I hope will interest you.

## 8886

B.H., Days of Selichos, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem keep them and grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

Rosh Hashanah is determined by the Creator—not on the day when the world in general was created, but on the day when Adam HaRishon—the human being—was created.

The explanation for this:

With the creation of man, the entire creation of all six days of Bereishis was not only completed, but it was also supplemented and perfected.

Thereby, the perfection of creation was achieved—not only because man is the highest creature, but also because man is the creature that **can**, **must**, and **will**, eventually, bring **all** other parts of creation to **their** perfection.

This is achieved when man utilizes, to the **fullest** extent, all his own powers and all the powers of nature—whether in the world of **domem** (inanimate objects: earth, minerals, etc.), the world of **tzomei'ach** (plants), or the world of **chai** (living creatures)—for good and holiness.

***

The creation of man is distinguished, among other things, specifically by the fact that he was *nivra yechidi* (created as a **single individual**), unlike other creatures which were created in great numbers.

This shows us and emphasizes that **one single** human being has the potential to bring the entire creation to its purpose and perfection, just as the first man—Adam HaRishon—did. Immediately after his creation, on the first Rosh Hashanah, Adam HaRishon called upon and **accomplished** that all the creatures of the world should acknowledge the sovereignty of the Creator, proclaiming:

**"Come, let us bow down and prostrate ourselves, let us kneel before Hashem our Maker"**—

Through *hishtachaviyah* (prostration), through self-*bitul*, and only through this, can a created being unite and harmonize with the Creator, and thereby reach the highest perfection.

And our Sages, of blessed memory, teach us that from Adam HaRishon we learn and know regarding **every** person: "Therefore man was created as an individual, to teach you—one soul is as if a whole world."

This means: Every Jew, even in our time—in whatever place and condition he may find himself—has the fullest potential (and consequently, the obligation) to ascend and reach the highest level of perfection and to accomplish the same in the *olam malei*—in the entire creation.

Rosh Hashanah—the day of the creation of the first and individual man—reminds every Jew of this obligation.

Rosh Hashanah demonstrates the incorrectness of the excuses of those who do not fulfill their duty, claiming that it is impossible to change the world, or that their parents did not give them the necessary education and preparation, or that the world is vast and he is alone—how can he accomplish anything?

Rosh Hashanah provides the strength to fulfill this duty, for on this day the entire creation is renewed. A new year begins, with fresh powers, as on the day of the first Rosh Hashanah.

And as the content and order of the **tefillah** of Rosh Hashanah—the very act of petitioning proves that the request **can** be fulfilled, and that **the tefillah** can accomplish this—every **individual** prays in every tefillah of Rosh Hashanah:

**"Reign over the entire world... and let every created thing know that You have created it"**—that the Almighty's sovereignty should be acknowledged over **the entire world**, until **every** thing knows that Hashem is its Creator.

***

There were times when the aforementioned idea that one person can "change" the world evoked doubts, and it was necessary to bring proofs and evidence for it.

In our current era, unfortunately, one does not need to search for many proofs to be convinced that if not for the Almighty, who is the King of the world and *Hashem Melech*—*tichon tevel bal timot* (He reigns in such a way that the world is established and will not fall)—one person could, G-d forbid, destroy the entire world.

If this is so on the side of the opposite of good, then it is certainly true that on the side of good, one person can accomplish much, much more. For in truth, creation is good in its essence, and therefore more inclined toward good than toward the opposite.

***

May the Almighty help **each and every one** to accept firm resolutions on this day of Rosh Hashanah in the spirit of Rosh Hashanah, as mentioned above; and may they fulfill these resolutions in practice every day of the coming year.

The *hishtachaviyah* before the Almighty, which is expressed in all matters of daily life, by fulfilling the *mitzvos* of the Almighty, until—**"In all your ways know Him."**

And to accomplish the same in the world around oneself,

According to the content of Rosh Hashanah, which is not only the beginning of the year, but primarily—the "Rosh" (head) of the year,

Just as the head directs every limb of the entire body, so too must the *chayus* and the resolutions of Rosh Hashanah fill and direct the days of the year.

And then the entire body—(the year)—is healthy in all respects.

With blessings for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year.

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 8887

B"H, Days of Selichos, 5724
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants of the Siyum on Maseches Shabbos
in Kfar
Argentina (Nir Tzvi) — may they live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

Your *pidyon nefesh* has been received.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and upon all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all that is yours: a blessing of *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

With respect and blessing — that following the completion of Maseches Shabbos, you should occupy yourselves with *mitzvos* and the preparations for them from a place of (Shabbos) rest, and with expansion and greatness (like the conduct of the *Bei Reish Galusa*). This is in order to purify the "woman" — this is *Knesses Yisrael* — for her "husband" — this is the *Ribono shel Olam*. This is achieved by ensuring that all your actions are within the measure of a *mitzvah* (in matters of *mitzvah*), and even in your mundane affairs, you should transform them into *dinei Torah* (the Oral Torah). As our Sages explain (in the Oral Torah) regarding the conduct of "In all your ways, know Him," and with the blessing of *kesivah v’chasimah tovah*.

Published in *Heichal Menachem*, Vol. 1, p. 72, and completed based on a photocopy of the letter.

**Regarding your question:** A response to a question regarding what was explained in the *Kuntres Eitz Chaim* (in the Additions, p. 87) as to why Tanya is different from another book written with Ruach HaKodesh. The point is that since it was written with Ruach HaKodesh, it inherently includes every explanation and intellectual insight that is correct in its own right, even if the author did not consciously intend it.

## 8889

*[5724]*

...Regarding the notes in the Sifrei, Parshas Bracha: The fact that Hashem said to the children of Esav (in response to their question, "What is written in the Torah?") "You shall not murder," and similarly to the children of Ammon and Moav, "You shall not commit adultery," and to the children of Yishmael, "You shall not steal"—this is not the innovation of Matan Torah, for these are among the seven Mitzvos of Bnei Noach.

- Note the reference in Yevamos (47b) regarding the prohibition of idolatry, and see the commentaries there.

It can be said that He was compelled to tell them specifically about these Mitzvos because they are the very ones that are most severe for them, being the opposite of their nature (as is evident from the response of each of them, "All of his essence...").

And even though they were already commanded regarding these (via the seven Mitzvos of Bnei Noach), it can be explained simply: at the time of Matan Torah, Hashem asked them if they would accept the Torah **willingly**, and to this they answered, "All of his essence..." and therefore, "It is impossible for us to accept," etc.

Based on this, the Mechilta (Yisro 20:2) is easily understood, as it also contains the aforementioned account from the Sifrei and concludes: Rabbi Shimon ben Elazar says, "If they could not uphold the seven Mitzvos that the Bnei Noach were commanded and accepted upon themselves, how much more so [would they fail] with the Mitzvos of the Torah." Similarly, this is implied in the Sifrei, which concludes, "Could it be that they heard and accepted [the Torah]? The verse states, 'And them they shall not do,' and it says... rather, even the seven Mitzvos that the Bnei Noach accepted upon themselves, they could not uphold, until they abandoned them and gave them to Yisrael." And this is clear.

To interpret the Sifrei as meaning that the intent of the verse "You shall not murder," etc., refers to what is added in this commandment for Bnei Yisrael—beyond the prohibition of murder for Bnei Noach—is somewhat forced, for if so, the main point is missing from the text. However, there is some proof for this from the response of the children of Ammon and Moav regarding the rejection of "You shall not commit adultery," based on what is written, "And the two daughters of Lot became pregnant by their father." This implies that this prohibition was added in its severity at Matan Torah, but was permitted for Bnei Noach. Likewise, regarding the response of the children of Esav, based on what is written, "By your sword you shall live"—for it is obvious that the blessing of Yitzchak would not be to transgress the Mitzvos of Bnei Noach.

Regarding the statement of our Sages in Shemos Rabbah (30:9) that the nations of the world were given "raw" Mitzvos—note the commentary of the Ramban (Vayishlach 34:13): "And in my opinion, the laws they enumerated..." See also Chullin (92a, bottom of the page) regarding the thirty Mitzvos that the Bnei Noach accepted upon themselves, etc.

#### ***8889***

This letter is to Rabbi Yisrael Yitzchak Piekarski. Additional letters to him: above, Vol. 20, 7572; Vol. 18, 6742.

## 8890

B"H, Erev Sukkos, at the time of Mincha,
5725. Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the great Gaon, wise and understanding, a man of many talents, master of masters, etc., Rabbi Y.D. HaLevi — and his entire family — shlita.

I acknowledge receipt of your letter of blessing from the third day, Erev Yom Kippur, the day of the perfection of "Hashem will comfort," specifically with [His] will. Furthermore, its reward is great and its stature is lofty, etc., the day of the joy of His heart.

The words of the master have already been spoken, and "I will bless those who bless you," with the blessing of Hashem, which is greater than the primary matter.

May it be the will that soon, in our days, we will merit, together with the entirety of Klal Yisrael, to see the consolation of Tzion and Yerushalayim, and the fulfillment of the prophecy, "He will swallow up death forever, and Hashem will wipe away tears from all faces," and "Awake and sing, you who dwell in the dust," for Hashem will revive them with the dew of the great light from above.

With appreciation, respect, and the blessing of the Yom Tov, whose joy is threefold in Torah.

In continuation of what was discussed — I subsequently found in the Commentary on the Mishnah for Demai (Chapter 1, Mishnah 2) that "I have not eaten of it in my mourning" refers to the time before the burial (and so rules the Rosh at the end of Maaser Sheni*).

Regarding the conclusion of your letter about seeing a Kohen, etc. — and "to the Levi He said," I would point out what the Arizal wrote (in Likutei Torah and Shaar HaPesukim for Yechezkel) that in the time to come, the Leviim will be Kohanim. See also Tanya, Chapter 50, which adds to this that "the Leviim **of now will be** Kohanim in the future." One could say that this resolves the difficulty, for the Torah told us "for us and our children forever" [Rambam, Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah, beginning of Chapter 2]. He explains that those who are **now** (and not at that time) Leviim will be (because they will be born) Kohanim in the future.

I have just seen in the Commentary on the Mishnah published by Rabbi Kapach (may he live long, 5723) that the publisher notes that in the manuscript in his possession, the Rambam erased (?) the version that we have copied in our printed editions as mentioned above, and wrote in the margins a version that copies it as: "He is an Onen by Torah law only on the day of death" — just as he phrases it in the Yad HaChazakah. And we conclude with good.

At the beginning of Sefer HaMaamarim 5729 (Brooklyn, 5759) it is explained (and apparently based on a maamar of the Tzemach Tzedek) how the blessing of Hashem also contains the quality of prayer, "May it be the will," to draw down a **new** will to heal and to bless.
