## 8945

B"H, 23 Shevat, 5725
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos.

At an opportune time, I will mention all that you wrote about at the holy Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in accordance with the content of your letter.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the doctors' instructions for your wife, may she live, to avoid pregnancy, and that you asked a Rav about this, who permitted various methods for you, which you listed in your letter:

It is surprising that you do not mention a simple and effective matter, especially when combined with the methods you listed. This is the matter—**where a Rav has explicitly permitted it**—of delaying the Tevilah for a few days, as instructed by the doctor who knows your wife, may she live, and who also knows the day she is most likely to conceive. In most cases, a delay of two or three days is sufficient. You should discuss all of this with the Rav and the doctor, and they will instruct you.

Based on the tone of your letter, I trust it is unnecessary to emphasize the necessity of conducting your daily life in a manner consistent with the instructions of our Torah, the Torah of life, and in the fulfillment of its mitzvos, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them." Beyond the fundamental fact that this is Hashem’s command, it is also the path to receiving Hashem’s blessing in all that is needed, especially when one is in need of a special blessing. In your case, the emphasis is specifically on being careful as required in all the laws of Taharas HaMishpachah.

It is appropriate that you have your Tefillin checked, as well as the Mezuzos in your home, to ensure they are all kosher according to the law. Your wife, may she live, should maintain the good custom of kosher daughters of Israel to set aside tzedakah before lighting candles every Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov.

Regarding the tying of the fallopian tubes—in addition to the risks inherent in any surgery, particularly internal surgery, and especially when one’s health is fragile (and in several details, not entirely clear, as appears from your letter)—there are several negative aspects: a) This is an action to permanently prevent pregnancy, even for when she recovers, etc. b) Concerns from the perspective of the law, as your Rav will explain to you. c) There have been cases where, despite the tying, a pregnancy occurred afterward (the usual explanation for this is that the tie apparently came undone on its own, and since it is internal, there is no way to know about it).

With blessings for good tidings regarding all of the above.

On behalf of the Rebbe,
Secretary

## 8849

B"H, 8 Adar Rishon, 5725
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, Lod
To the Administration of Yeshivas Achei Temimim, Rishon LeTzion
May Hashem keep them alive

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Adar Rishon, in which you write regarding the proposal of the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and accomplished man of character, Rabbi Chaim Shaul, shlita, to merge Yeshivas Achei Temimim of Rishon LeTzion with Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim of Lod and Kfar Chabad.

For this is the very command, hope, and desire of our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, to expand the tents of the Temimim and their dwellings, in a manner of "increasing and continuing" in both the physical and spiritual realms alike—increasing and continuing and shining.

And all of this is as the instruction of this week’s parsha:

"And you" (*Ve'atah*—with the addition of the *vav*, a continuation from above, from the *Seder Hishtalshelus*) "shall command" (*tetzaveh*—from the language of *tzavta*, connection and *hiskashrus*) "the Children of Israel" (*Bnei Yisrael*—to me, the head, which is the level of *Chochma* (which in Torah is the matter of the inner dimension of Torah)) "that they bring you" (to the level of Moshe that is in every one) "pure olive oil" (which comes through its crushing, *iskafya*, etc.) "beaten" (the first of the oils, as it is written, "all the **fat** is for Hashem," and through *katit*—*bitul*—one arrives) "for the light" (of Torah, and through this one connects to the *Kudsha Brich Hu* in the level called *Maor*, and from this it is drawn to be that) "Aharon shall arrange it" (*simcha* of a *mitzvah*, and in a manner of) "an eternal statute" (a permanent and everlasting thing), as explained in *Chassidus*.

Looking forward to—and with a blessing for—good news in all the aforementioned,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8,951

B"H, 17 Adar Rishon, 5725
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I read with great astonishment your letter from Erev Shabbos Parshas Tetzaveh, in which you write regarding your distinguished grandson, the avreich, G-d-fearing and a talmid chacham... stating that you do not derive nachas from him (G-d forbid) regarding his physical health, etc.

I immediately inquired and investigated what is happening with your grandson, sheyichyeh, and I was informed once again of his success in the study of Torah—study that leads to action, as is obvious and simple. Regarding his health, the doctor found that everything is in order with him; it seems that his soul’s nature is such that he always demands much of himself regarding his spiritual standing, which consequently affects his health, etc. It is obvious and simple that traveling and moving from place to place will not change this in the slightest, and one can only hope it does not cause harm. After all, Chazal have taught us, "A person should always learn in a place that his heart desires," and who knows how he would adjust in a new place.

Regarding the continuation of your letter, that in a new place he should also learn some trade, for "Torah is good when combined with derech eretz"—in this very letter of yours, you preceded Torah to derech eretz. Certainly, the time has not yet arrived for your grandson, sheyichyeh, to steal hours that he currently dedicates to hasmadah and shekidah in the study of our Torah, the Torah of life—life, even in the literal sense, in this physical world—and to become confused by the many calculations, human thoughts, and schemes, which are the opposite of the fact that "G-d made man upright."

I know that the atmosphere of this country causes thoughts regarding one's future livelihood at a young age for sons and daughters. However, anyone who looks with open eyes at what is happening around him sees at every step that, in the vast majority of cases, people manage to earn a living in fields completely unrelated to the trade they learned in their youth.

I am sending a copy of my letter to your son, the Rav, sheyichyeh, as I do not know from whom the opinions written in your letter originated (even though, on the face of it, they are the opposite of the efforts of your son, the Rav, sheyichyeh, to go against the current of the United States—efforts made with energy and without regard for the opinion of the masses, etc., etc.).

May it be Hashem’s will that, in addition to the nachas you currently have from your grandson, sheyichyeh—and may you have even more true nachas from all your descendants, sheyichyeh—Hashem should add even more through the exceptional success of your grandson in the study of Torah, both in Nigleh and in Chassidus, without disturbances from outside matters. Certainly, when he is able to study in tranquility, the promise will be fulfilled in him: "Happy are you in this world, and it is good for you," etc.

With respect and blessing for good tidings.

P.S. Since everything is by Divine Providence, it is my duty (and privilege) to urge you regarding the necessity of setting fixed times for the study of the inner dimension of Torah, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus—a fixed time every day, with an increase on Shabbos, as explained in the writings of the Arizal.

## 8852

8852

B"H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Ki Sisa, 5725, Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter.

Regarding the subject of this week’s parsha:

**"And Hashem spoke to Moshe"** — for Moshe asked: Ribono shel Olam, how will the pride of Yisrael be exalted (especially since the incident of the Eigel had only just occurred)? The Holy One, blessed be He, said to him:

**"To say"** — for all generations (including even on the day of *pekidi*, when "I will visit their sin upon them" regarding the Eigel) —

**"When you take"** — you specifically — the head of Yisrael (and only Moshe, who had no **connection** whatsoever to the matter of the Eigel, for he was then on the mountain **with Hashem**).

**"Take the sum of the heads"** — you will be able to "lift their heads in exaltation," by means of which—

You take the sum, you count them, to reveal their affection before the Makom. And to atone for the sin that prevents the exaltation of their pride (and specifically, the sin of the Eigel)—

**"And they shall give, every man, a ransom for his soul"** — tzedakah, as it is written, "And break your sin through tzedakah."

* * *

And since every single soul of the House of Yisrael possesses a dimension of Moshe Rabbeinu, there is an instruction in our parsha: that through this dimension, every person must exalt his pride by revealing his affection before the Makom, by contemplating that "with an eternal love You have loved us, Hashem our G-d, etc., and You have chosen us" — this material body — "and brought us close, etc." Then, naturally, "as water reflects the face to the face," he too will be aroused to cleave to Him, to draw the Ohr Ein Sof B"H downward, and to elevate the entire world to Hashem. This is accomplished through the performance of Torah and mitzvos, and especially through tzedakah, which is the essence of the practical mitzvos and transcends them all, in fulfilling the command to make a dwelling place for Him, may He be blessed, in the lower realms.

With blessings for success in your holy work,

**M. Schneerson**

* * *

Regarding what you wrote about the *Kollel* boxes — the question is surprising after the urging **from each and every one** of our Rebbeim, the Nesi'im. Fortunate is the one who exerts himself in this, both in doing and in causing others to do.

In Rashi at the beginning of Parshas Va'era: "And I appeared to the Avos" (because they are the Avos) (and not because Avraham was a host to guests, etc.).

## 8853

B"H, 24 Adar, 5725
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from 19 Teves, which was received after a long delay, in which you write several questions regarding the laws and customs of Israel.

In general, it is not my practice to issue halachic rulings, nor is there any need for this, as there are many *morei hora'ah* (halachic authorities) in your city to whom you can turn. They will be able to explain the questions in all their details (which are often difficult to put into writing in a letter).

Nevertheless, since you have already written, I will answer the first question, in your own phrasing, regarding the matter of a woman covering her hair, and upon what the custom relies, etc.

This is a definitive law in our holy Torah, *Toras Chaim*, and not merely a custom (though the custom of Israel also carries great weight). Furthermore, even among the laws, there is a special importance to the fulfillment of this law—the covering of a woman’s hair (a married woman, of course)—as is understood from the magnitude of the reward for fulfilling this law. In the precise language [cited in the commentaries on *Shulchan Aruch*, *Orach Chayim*, section 75 (where this law of covering the hair is explained in detail)—the punishment is also mentioned there, but I choose to quote that which pertains to the reward]: the passage from the holy *Zohar* in *Parshas Naso* (cited in *Mishnah Berurah*, *Hilchos Krias Shema*, section 75): "Through this, they will be elevated in distinction above the rest of the world, and not only that, but her husband will be blessed with all the blessings from above and blessings from below, in wealth, in children, and in children’s children, etc."

To add to the above: it is a great wonder regarding anyone who has a spark of faith in their heart and desires that their life after marriage be truly happy—regarding the husband, the wife, and their children, whom Hashem will bless.

Is there truly any room for this discomfort (even **if we were to say** that there is discomfort) involved in covering the hair, when compared to the blessing from Hashem, the Creator of man, the Creator of the world, and its Guide?! This is a level of frivolity like no other, even if there were a doubt or a double doubt regarding the necessity of the matter, and all the more so regarding a matter that is explicitly stated.

It is understood that I am aware of the objection to the above, for there are many who do not observe this law. However, this objection has existed for thousands of years: "You are the fewest of all the peoples," and how is it that their laws are different from every other nation? To our great sorrow, even within *Bnei Yisrael*, one can find those who, for the time being, desecrate the Shabbos in public, and even intermarriage, *rachmana litzlan*. It is obvious that this does not detract, *chas v'shalom*, in the slightest from the vitality of our Torah, *Toras Chaim*, and its *mitzvos*, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them." Just as the making of the Golden Calf in its time (and in close proximity to the time of the Giving of the Torah) did not detract in the slightest from the vitality of the Ten Commandments, and subsequently the entire Torah and its *mitzvos*, down to our present generation.

And as we find ourselves a few days before the days of Purim, this—as mentioned above—was the argument of Haman, and his conclusion was not only the destruction of the spiritual life of the Jewish people, but to destroy **all** the Jews, from young to old, children and women.

For the existence of *Bnei Yisrael* **in every** place they may be is solely through the Torah and its *mitzvos*, which were given by the One Hashem to the one nation on earth.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 8853

[Adar 5725]

I have answered this many times (to the writer and to several others who asked similar questions) — yet I will write it once more:

1) It is a simple fact that it is possible, and within the power of Anash—may they live—who reside in the Holy Land, to accomplish **great and hidden things** there. This is **all the more so** when compared to all those movements and groups there that have recently opened various yeshivos, Talmud Torahs, shuls, etc., even though they do not have the leadership, the grace, or the assistance from various offices that exist for Chabad affairs, nor the connections that can be obtained (or that already exist), **and much, much more**—and most importantly: they do not have the special blessing of our Rebbeim, the Nesi’im, for Chabad affairs.

2) It is a simple fact that there is no place for sending "generals" from here.

3) It is a simple fact that there is no place for sending teachers and school administrators from here—and there is also no need for it—since, as mentioned above, these can be found on the spot.

4) It is a simple fact that the aforementioned requires organized work, and then there is **no limit** to the potential expansion (as evidenced by the activities of **actual** individuals: Rabbi Brook—may he live—in Rishon LeZion; Slonim—may he live—in Jerusalem; Zilberstrom—may he live—there; Wolf—may he live—in Lod; Chefer—may he live—in the village; Eidelkop—may he live—there, **and others**). And **as mentioned above**, they did not wait to be appointed time and again, nor for "injections" of encouragement, etc.

5) **It is a simple fact** that the absence of action—even when dressed in the guise of yiras shamayim and Chassidus, etc.—leads to results that are **tangibly** visible regarding the situation in general (the departure of hundreds of families of Chabad descent, and until a short time ago—various Chabad shuls, Rabbonim of Anash, etc.) and more.

6) There is no place for appointments from overseas, and it would be of no benefit either. For that which is required to be done regarding others (and not only regarding one's own livelihood) does not require an appointment. And one who does not want to do anything already has various excuses ready to continue in this approach, just as he has conducted himself until now, even though it is known to all and publicized that this approach is in **complete contradiction to the clear instructions** of our Rebbeim, the Nesi’im.

7) Advice and instructions of this type, about which he writes, are **clear** in every area according to its nature, based on how we see others have acted in parallel fields last year and two years ago—and in many matters: [look at] how each person acts on his own when the matter concerns **his own physical and private livelihood.**

8) It is a simple fact that if there were a drawing together of hearts and a unification of the people of Chabad, the success in the aforementioned would be many times greater. But even in the current situation, there is still a **vast** field for successful activities.

***

**Rabbi Brook:** Chaim Shaul.
**Slonim:** Azriel Zelig.
**Zilberstrom:** Aharon Mordechai.
**Wolf:** Efraim.
**Chefer:** Shmuel.
**Eidelkop:** Yona.

## 8955

8955

By the Grace of G-d, Rosh Chodesh Adar II, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Annual Banquet of the Ladies Auxiliary of Brownsville and East New York for the Lubavitcher Yeshivos Tomchei Tmimim

Greetings and Blessings!

This annual event takes place this year at a most auspicious time—in the period between the two Purims. This time is especially propitious for Jewish women, taking into account the significant role of Esther HaMalkah in the miracle of Purim, *bayamim hahem bizman hazeh* (in those days, at this time).

Esther HaMalkah could have felt quite secure in her personal situation; and Mordechai was certainly correct that **"relief and deliverance will arise for the Jews from another place"**—Hashem’s help could come through someone else. So why should she risk her life for others? But Esther did not make any personal calculations; she acted with *mesiras nefesh* to save Jews. And because of this, she merited that the Megillah is called by her name.

From this, there is a directive for Jewish women in all times: even though no woman can compare herself to Esther HaMalkah, it is certain that every single one can accomplish a great deal in her own way and in her own environment, if she fulfills the directives of the Torah and does so with her whole heart, just as Esther HaMalkah demonstrated a living example of what a Jewish woman is capable of doing.

And just as in the time of the first Purim, when Haman’s decree was nullified at the moment that Mordechai gathered the Jewish children and taught them Torah, with such enthusiasm and boundless love for Torah and mitzvos, to the point that they would not separate themselves from Mordechai HaTzaddik—in life, or G-d forbid, the opposite—

So too, in all times, is the foundation of the entire existence of our people: the Torah-education of Jewish children.

And this is the task and the work of the Ladies Auxiliary—to help the Lubavitcher Yeshivos Tomchei Tmimim provide a Torah-education *al taharas hakodesh* for their many students, *ken yirbu*.

The annual banquet is the highlight of this work, and I hope that everyone will do everything possible to ensure that the banquet is a great success in every respect.

May you all be blessed, together with your families *shichyu*, in everything you need, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for success, for good tidings, and a *Purim Sameach*.

#### ***8955***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 6, p. 376, and completed according to the secretariat’s copy.

**Gathered:** *Esther Rabbah* 9:3 (4).

## 8950

8950

*[7th of Adar adjacent to Nissan, 5725]*

...And this, too, is among the matters of these days of Purim, regarding which our Sages of blessed memory expounded, "For the Jews there was light (orah) — this refers to Torah." The Mitteler Rebbe explains (based on the teachings of the Alter Rebbe) the precision of the word "orah" with the additional "hey" at the end. For specifically, "Torah — ohr" (masculine) refers to the Written Torah, while "Torah — orah" (feminine) refers to the Oral Torah (and its root), which is attained through mesiras nefesh.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that, in accordance with the principle established by our Sages of blessed memory that "a verse does not depart from its literal meaning," there shall be for the Jews light, gladness, joy, and honor, also in the literal sense and in all matters.

#### ***8950***

Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 11, p. 343.

**Our Sages expounded:** Megillah 16b.

**The Mitteler Rebbe explains:** In Shaarei Orah, Shaar HaPurim, discourse beginning "V'kibel HaYehudim," Chapter 32 and onwards.

**The principle:** Shabbos 63a, and elsewhere.

## 8858

B"H, 11 Adar Sheni, 5725
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

...As we stand a few days before the days of Purim that are approaching, and specifically according to the words of the Sages in their Mishnah: "The Megillah is read" (also in the present tense) "on the eleventh," etc., "on the fifteenth."

May it be the will of Hashem that every man and woman, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael, will read and draw down the Megillah and its matters—all the matters of Purim. And this is in accordance with the precision of the name *Purim*, which is in the plural form, even though it is called "Purim because of the *pur* (lot)." The Tzemach Tzedek explained that this refers to two types of *pur*: the *pur* of Haman (from the *sitra achra*), and the *pur* which is the lot of holiness—"pleasant is our lot"—which is above *taam v'daas*, similar to the concept that "this is very good"—this refers to the *yetzer hara* when it is transformed into good.

And perhaps it is possible to add a point of precision here: that the name is specifically called by the term of Haman, *Purim*, and not *Goralos* (lots).

This is based on what is explained in *Chassidus* in many places: that the *avodah* of the *nefesh ha'elokis* within the *nefesh habahamit* and the body brings about an addition of strength even in the *avodah* of the *nefesh ha'elokis* itself, similar to the virtue of "bringing the righteous to *teshuvah*."

That is to say, the primary elevation of the time to come is that the *tzaddik* will be on the level of a *baal teshuvah* (and not that the *baal teshuvah* will be on the level of a *tzaddik*).

This is also necessitated by the fact that the soul, before its descent, was on the level of a *tzaddik*, who "sat with the King in His work," as the Sages said regarding the verse that He consulted with the souls of the *tzaddikim*. The descent is for the sake of an ascent (even while they are still in this world, clothed in a physical body)—in order to "transform darkness into light"—the elevation of *teshuvah*.

## 8859

8859

By the Grace of G-d, 11 Adar II, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the annual gathering of the "Netzivei HaYeshiva" supporters of Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch in Montreal,
May they live,

Peace and Blessing!

I send my greetings to all the participants in the annual gathering, together with the blessing that the undertaking should be met with great success in all respects.

This year, the annual gathering takes place in a leap year and in the month of Adar II. Our Jewish calendar, which determines all times and Yomim Tovim throughout the year, is connected to the movement of the moon and also to the *tekufos* (seasons), which are dependent on the movement of the sun. The lunar year remains "behind" by approximately 11 days per year relative to the solar year. Therefore, every two or three years, a leap year is introduced (with an additional full month) in order to **complete** the time (so that every Yom Tov should occur at the proper time: Pesach in the month of spring; Sukkos in the month of the autumn harvest, etc.).

One of the lessons of the leap year is that the Torah has given Jews the power to master time. Even though, in general, a person is not the master of **past** time, a Jew has the possibility to complete that which he has missed. Furthermore, it is even possible to acquire a "reserve" for the future, as is indicated by the leap year.

And in this very month—which is doubled in a leap year—the Yom Tov of Purim is celebrated. As our Sages, of blessed memory, relate, the decree of Haman the Wicked was annulled at the moment when Mordechai HaTzaddik gathered the Jewish children and awakened in them the spirit of *mesiras nefesh* for Torah-true Judaism. Through this, that which had previously been lacking in the realm of *chinuch al taharas hakodesh* (education in purity and holiness) was completed, and this brought about the miracle of ***v'nahafoch hu*** ("and it was turned about") and—**"For the Jews there was light and gladness, and joy and honor."**

When Purim occurs in a leap year, as it does this year, these two aforementioned points come together and are especially emphasized: the vital necessity of Torah-true education for the existence of our people, and the possibility granted to us not only to fulfill what we have missed, but also to create a "reserve" for the future.

I wish to hope that this year's annual gathering will give full expression to the above, and that the merit of *hafatzas haTorah v'hamitzvos* (disseminating Torah and mitzvos) will stand by each and every one of you, may you live, together with all of *Klal Yisrael*, to enjoy to the fullest measure "For the Jews there was light and gladness, and joy and honor"—with all its interpretations.

With respect and blessing for success and good tidings.

8,859*

/**Signature**/

## 8860

8860

B”H, 20 Adar II, 5725
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos, in which you write about the difficulties you encounter when studying the "content of the subjects" discussed in the Shabbos Kodesh sichos, noting that you understand the general concept but not always the details.

In general, the aforementioned sichos contain several parts, since those who come to this study also belong to different levels of Torah understanding. However, in each one of them, every type of person can find a point that is suited to their level of knowledge, in addition to understanding the general concept. This is certainly true for you as well; as you progress in your Torah study, you will surely understand one part, then another, and so on. There is no point in studying [other] books in order to understand these sichos, for that is not the way. Rather, one should progress in the study and understanding of Torah step by step. The main point is that it should align with the instruction of Rabbeinu HaZaken in Hilchos Talmud Torah, at the end of the first chapter, regarding the Torah study of women: that the primary effort should be that the study leads to action, permeated with yiras Hashem and ahavas Hashem (as is also understood from the aforementioned Hilchos Talmud Torah).

With blessings for success in everything and for good tidings in this.

## 8861

B"H, 21 Adar II, 5725
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished, etc., R' Chaim, may he live.

In response to your letter of 18 Adar II, in which you write various thoughts regarding the manner in which a *yad vashem* (memorial) should be established in merit of your mother, *a"h*. You wish to do this by investing money in an institution for the education of Jewish children on the basis of *taharas hakodesh* (purity of holiness), and you have two approaches regarding this.

According to the instruction of Chazal, "One does not delay the performance of a *mitzvah*," and "If a *mitzvah* comes to your hand, do not let it become sour [i.e., do not delay it]," it is correct to accept the suggestion [to establish it] in Jerusalem, the Holy City, may it be rebuilt and established soon. In that way, there will be immediate fruits from this investment—*tzon pri mitzvah* (the fruits of the *mitzvah*).

And if in all matters of goodness there must be alacrity, as mentioned above, so as not to delay, then how much more so in the area of *chinuch* (education), where if the student is not immediately absorbed into an appropriate framework, there is a danger posed by the undesirable winds blowing outside, etc., and a word to the wise is sufficient.

With the blessing that from here on you should know no more sorrow or distress, *ch"v*, and that in health and with a good heart you should act and accomplish in the dissemination of Torah and *mesorah* in a manner that is "increasing and illuminating."

And with blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 8864

8864

By the Grace of G-d, 6 Nissan, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Blessing and Peace!

In response to your letter of the 25th of Adar Sheni, in which you write about your birthday:

Surely you are increasing your involvement in matters of Yiddishkeit and mitzvos, as commanded by our holy Torah—Torah Chaim—to "ascend in holiness." Beyond the primary importance of fulfilling the commandment, this also serves as the channel and vessel to receive the blessings of the Ribono shel Olam in all that you require.

May it be the will of Hashem Yisbarach that the coming year be a good one for you, a year of success in both material and spiritual matters, and may you bring good tidings regarding all of the above.

With the blessing of a kosher and joyous Pesach.

P.S. Regarding what you wrote about the matter of loneliness: it is a great wonder, for surely you are familiar with the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, Nasi of Yisrael: "Chassidus has accomplished that one is never alone..." (i.e., Chassidus has removed the state of loneliness). If this is true regarding the connection between a Rebbe and a Chassid—as is explained there at length—then it is all the more true regarding the connection between one person and another in their surroundings. And it is certainly true of the connection between Hashem and the Bnei Yisrael. This is especially understood based on the foundation of our Torah, Torah Chaim, regarding the concept of Hashgacha Pratis: that it is literally true that Hashem Yisbarach oversees every single detail of life with individual providence, and His providence, His blessing, and the influence of His goodness, etc., are all one, for their source is the simple unity of the Ein Sof.

From the above, it follows and is understood regarding one’s actions, feelings, and outlook on life: every single person is in the world (a world of countless creatures of all types—speaking, living, growing, and inanimate) and has an influence upon them, just as the totality of things in the world influences them (even though it is understood and simple that these influences are not at all equal). Since this is the case, each one of them is full of content, at the very least in potential, and it depends on the person to activate this content and bring it from potential into action. This is true in principle for every Jew, whose task it is to be a partner in the work of Creation, in accordance with what has been said.

Regarding you, the wonder is even greater. For Divine Providence has granted you the merit of being placed in the field of educating the Bnei Yisrael—the children of the Makom, the children of Yisrael. Every good action you perform for them, and every influence you have upon them, creates an eternal bond between you—a bond that is spiritual, holy, good, and beneficial even below. In all these matters, space does not separate, and it is impossible for a rift to occur (which is why it is eternal). In other words, when you are sitting in your room and feeling lonely, and at that very moment one of your students or those you influence is repeating a lesson they heard from you, or is blessing Hashem just as you taught them, etc., this adds vitality and light to the connection between you. It is impossible for the nefesh elokis within you not to feel this addition, since this matter is of the very essence of your being. After all, the interiority of a person and their true essence is the nefesh elokis within them, and in truth, it is what also gives life to the nefesh habehamis.

I know that not everyone feels what I have described, because it is not visible to the physical eye and the hand cannot touch it. But this does not in the least diminish the truth of the reality of the matter. Therefore, with a little bit of contemplation, the opening is created from the nefesh elokis to the human intellect, and even to the nefesh habehamis, to influence it in the direction mentioned. Since a person is subject to change, there are times that require a special awakening and a special addition. At such times, the advised counsel is to meet with one of the students or those you influence, or at the very least to speak with someone about them, the lessons, etc. For the voice awakens the intention, and speech reveals matters more clearly.

It is a common occurrence, and almost natural among people—in the style of Chazal, "They claimed wheat and he agreed regarding barley"—meaning that people often substitute the true cause for another matter. The cause of your situation is, apparently, that for the time being you have not yet become engaged. This is the place for me to authorize you to convey to each of your brothers, may they live, in my name, that it is a great wonder—and also a cause for distress—that they are not doing everything necessary in this regard. For the blessing of Hashem rests upon you, as it is written, "And Hashem your G-d will bless you in all that you do"—action in the natural way, as required. And the rest is understood.

May it be the will of Hashem that you bring good tidings regarding all of the above, and speedily, and may Hashem grant you success.

## 8865

By the Grace of G-d
11 Nissan, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel everywhere,
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and Blessing!

The Ribono shel Olam has ordained that the Exodus from Egypt should take place in the **Chodesh HaAviv** (the month of spring). And the Torah commands that we must take special care that Pesach always falls in the month of spring: **"Observe the month of spring and perform the Pesach offering to Hashem your G-d, for in the month of spring Hashem your G-d took you out of Egypt at night"** (Devarim 16:1).

In order to ensure that Pesach falls in the Chodesh HaAviv—bearing in mind that our calendar is set according to the moon, which creates an annual difference of about eleven days relative to the sun, and it is the sun that determines the seasons of the year—we have an "intercalated year" (leap year) every two or three years, such as this year, when an entire month, Adar, is added. In this way, the lunar year is "synchronized" with the solar year, and Pesach always falls in the Chodesh HaAviv. Through this, the months of the year and all the Yomim Tovim are regulated and set in their proper time.

***

The fact that the Exodus from Egypt took place in the month of spring is explained by our Sages of blessed memory as a special kindness from the Ribono shel Olam, in that He led the Jews out of Egypt during the best time of the year. However, as with all matters of Torah, there are many instructions, allusions, and reasons here for the collective and for the individual. One of the points I wish to highlight will become clear when one considers the circumstances under which the Exodus from Egypt took place:

For hundreds of years, the Jews had been enslaved by a people that at that time dominated all surrounding nations, not only with the raw power of "chariots and horsemen," but also with its tremendous weight in the fields of science and in everything we call "culture" and "civilization" today.

The culture and civilization of Egypt were supported by the forces of nature and natural phenomena, specifically the Nile River. The land of Egypt is almost entirely free of rain; human ingenuity, however, created an artificial irrigation system that transformed Egypt into a fertile garden surrounded by deserts.

These circumstances brought about a complex idolatrous culture that had two main characteristics: the deification of the forces of nature, and the deification of the forces of the human being who understood how to utilize those forces of nature. From this, it was only a short step to the deification of Pharaoh, who embodied the Egyptian ideal of the "genius" human being.

Such a system, which viewed the world as a combination of various "natural forces"—among which was also the "force" of man—with the added philosophy that **"My power and the might of my hand have acquired this wealth for me,"** led to the lowest spiritual and moral-ethical degradation. This also "justified" the most shameless enslavement and cruelties toward the physically weaker person or nation.

***

The idolatry and superstition of the Egyptians reached their strongest expression at the time of the annual renewal of the forces of nature—in the month of spring, the month of "Mazal Taleh" (Aries), and the lamb was one of the primary symbols of Egyptian idolatry.

***

And then Moshe Rabbeinu comes with the tidings of *"Pakod pakadti"*—that the time has come when the G-d of Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov has decided to liberate the Jews from the hands of Pharaoh and from the exile of Egypt.

It had already been 210 years that the Jews had been subjected to Pharaoh; a portion of the Jews had even been swallowed up by Egyptian "culture." No help could be expected from the surrounding nations; not a single slave had (until then) been able to free himself from Egypt. From a natural standpoint, there was simply no prospect of liberating the Jewish people from Egypt—and yet Moshe Rabbeinu assures them that the time of liberation has arrived.

However, there is one condition: **"Draw out and take for yourselves sheep for your families and slaughter the Pesach offering!"**

**"Draw out" (Mishchu)**—withdraw yourselves from the idolatry of the land; **"and take for yourselves"**—take a sheep (that which the Egyptians deified) and slaughter it as a Pesach offering to Hashem. It is not enough to deny Egyptian idolatry within one's heart, or even at home, hidden and quietly; rather, it must be done specifically in public, without fear, according to all the details associated with the Pesach offering in Egypt.

And then Moshe Rabbeinu assures them in the name of the Ribono shel Olam that not only would they be liberated from Egypt, but that Pharaoh himself would command them to leave Egypt. The Geulah would not take place at a time when the forces of nature are dormant and hidden, but specifically in **Chodesh HaAviv**, in the very middle of the month of spring, when nature reveals its strongest forces.

By this, it is emphasized that there are no separate worlds: a world of nature and natural forces, and a world of "above the world," where sometimes one dominates the other and sometimes vice-versa. There is only one, single G-d, who is the absolute Master over the entire world, and who also unifies the entire world.

This recognition reached its highest expression at Matan Torah, the culmination point of the Exodus from Egypt, which began with: **"I am Hashem your G-d, who took you out of the land of Egypt, from the house of bondage; you shall have no other gods"**—"I am Hashem, your G-d, who took you out of the land of Egypt, from the house of bondage; you shall have no idols before Me."

***

Just as in Egypt of old, so too today there are those who build their lives on deifying the so-called forces of nature, with the addition of the "my power and the might of my hand" of man. Some have found a "way out," that at home they have a place for the Ribono shel Olam as well—but in society, they are "like the people," *niyeh k'goyim*, and on the contrary—even more "goyish" than they are.

Yom Tov Pesach arrives and reminds us once again: *Pakod pakadti*—you have no choice. The Ribono shel Olam remembers you, and it must be—**Mishchu**—to cast off the idolatry of the land, in whatever form it may express itself, and to do this publicly, without fear, and with pride. **"Take for yourselves"**—take yourselves and everything you have, all the possibilities and strengths you possess—to yourselves, to your true, eternal Jewish "self."

And do all this in the Chodesh HaAviv—do not let yourselves be confused by the deceivers who say that since this is a blooming world with man at its center and his "power and the might of his hand"—*eleh elohecha*, this is your god, and to this you are enslaved, and there is no place, G-d forbid, for the Ribono shel Olam—

But on the contrary—*b'chodesh ha'aviv hotziacha Hashem Elokecha mi'mitzrayim*—Hashem, who is your G-d, takes you out of enslavement in the Chodesh HaAviv. The blooming world, with the wonders upon wonders that one sees within it, brings one to see the truth even more clearly—and the formula of our Sages of blessed memory—that Hashem our G-d is the King of the world, *shelo chisar b'olamo klum* (that **He** has ensured that nothing is lacking in it).

***

May the Ribono shel Olam help and grant success so that Pesach—*Zeman Cheiruteinu*—should bring everyone, man and woman, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael to the true liberation from all obstacles and limitations, and may we serve the Ribono shel Olam with a whole heart.

And may the Geulah of the individual bring about the Geulah of Klal Yisrael, the *Geulah HaAmitit VeHaShleima* through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach holiday,

**Menachem Schneerson**

8866

B"H, 11 Nissan, 5765

Brooklyn.

#### ***8866***

Printed in Likutei Sichos, Vol. 21, p. 365.

**Likutei Torah:** In the year 5765, the Rebbe instructed that Likutei Torah be studied according to the weekly parsha. Someone asked that if they are unable to finish everything in one week, should they study the material for the following week during the next week and complete what was missed in their spare time, or should they continue studying in order. See also Letter 916 below.

## 8867

B"H, 12 Nissan, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Shalom Levi, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

I have just received your telegram; many thanks for your wishes and blessings. May the one who blesses be blessed in kind and even more so.

Since there is a presumption that the mail fulfills its mission, you have surely received my previous letter and the copy of my letter, even though you did not confirm receipt. The confirmation is, of course, of no consequence; rather, my hope is that you have reflected on the content of the letter, and my hope is also that you agree with my line of thought, and consequently, that this is also expressed in appropriate actions.

And if you were to say that this is also part of the essence of these days—that on the night the festival of Pesach is sanctified, we begin in all the homes of the children of Israel with the Seder, the intent of which, as emphasized in the Written and Oral Torah and in many places, is "And you shall tell your son," and as our Sages of blessed memory explain, the intent is not necessarily only for the wise son, but also for the other types—further elaboration is surely superfluous.

In anticipation of the festival of Pesach, the time of our freedom, which is approaching for us and for all of Israel for good and for blessing, I send to you and to all those associated with you a blessing for a kosher and happy Pesach, and for true freedom from all matters that cause confusion, from soul to flesh, and to draw from this joy and freedom throughout the entire year.

With respect and blessing.

## 8865

[24 Nissan 5725]

Your article in the Pesach issue of the *Jewish Advocate* regarding "Jewish Atheists" came into my hands "by chance." "By chance," because your article appears on the page opposite a letter of mine on the topic of "dialogue." However, it is needless to say that for us Jews, the concept of chance does not exist at all, for everything is by *Hashgacha Pratis*.

Since a Jew constantly seeks hints, I find in this aforementioned coincidence of our articles an opportunity to utilize the occasion and write you a few lines, following the long interruption in our correspondence, or a few words at a *farbrengen*.

Incidentally, it was conveyed to me that you have been present several times at *farbrengens*, but for some reason, you did not wish to approach closer.

Your article naturally "intrigued" me, and I read it with interest.

You write that initially, you assumed that the outburst of the infamous (or tragi-comic) rabbi against the *Ribono shel Olam* was an expression of protest (against the injustice of the world). I assume that this is merely a figure of speech, for surely you know that someone who was raised in a seminary of a movement whose entire philosophy is the opposite of fighting and rebelling, but is intended only to make life easier and more comfortable—is not capable of such a level.

I am, of course, in agreement with you that the claim of "Shall the Judge of all the earth not do justice!" can be authentic and possess the proper strength—but only when it erupts from the pained heart of a deep *ma'amin*. Therefore, we indeed find that the first one to express this claim was Avraham Avinu, the great *ma'amin* and father of *ma'aminim bnei ma'aminim*.

Our *Chachamim z"l* also tell us that the first one to raise the question of "a *tzaddik* who suffers, and a *rasha* who prospers" was none other than Moshe Rabbeinu, he who declared to the Jews, and to the entire world, the idea of "I am Hashem your G-d" and "You shall have no other gods," where "other gods" includes also human intellect and understanding when one makes them an idol and a final arbiter.

Therefore, I was surprised that you did not continue this train of thought and bring out the conclusion. For, as you know, the answer to Moshe Rabbeinu’s claim—at the time when, according to the narrative of our *Chachamim z"l*, he was shown that they were tearing the flesh of Rabbi Akiva with iron combs, etc., and Moshe Rabbeinu cried out, "Is this Torah and this its reward!"—(the answer) was: "Be silent, for such it arose in My thought!"

Let us remember that Moshe Rabbeinu’s claim was not merely in words, but primarily in thought. Therefore, the answer "be silent" was not an instruction not to speak about it, but also not to allow the thought about it.

And the only explanation was—"such it arose in (the Supernal) thought," which is actually no explanation at all. Nevertheless, it did not weaken the *emunah* of Moshe Rabbeinu or of all other authentic questioners and believers. On the contrary, it only strengthened their *emunah*, as we find explicitly with Iyov; so too with Avraham Avinu, who not only remained firm in his *emunah*, but was also able to withstand all the *nisyonos*; and so too the other "rebels" remained deep *ma'aminim* until the last day of their lives.

I believe that you will agree with me that it was not merely a coincidence that all these authentic questioners remained in their *emunah*; rather, it could not have been otherwise. For if one means the question with truth, and it is understood that such a deep feeling can come only from the conviction that true justice is the justice that stems from an **above**-human source, that is to say, which is higher than both human intellect and human feeling. Therefore, the question touches not only emotion and intellect, but also his *pnimiyus* and his very essence.

But after the first stormy outburst, he must realize that the entire approach of posing the question and wanting to understand with the intellect that which is higher than intellect has no place. Therefore, he must—after a shattering struggle and deep pain—finally come to the conclusion: "Nevertheless, I believe!" On the contrary—even more strongly.

***

The above refers to your article. However, there is another point in it, a point that concerns the entire problem, and it is a wonder that it is overlooked. I mean the following:

After all, the entire matter of the aforementioned "conflict" with *emunah* is not a new thing that has surfaced in our generation. Our people have already had to endure slaughters and forced conversions, *r"l*, in previous generations. The Crusades, for example, were in their scope, "proportionally," and in their cruelty, perhaps no easier than the Hitlerite ones, with the difference that then there was not a ray of hope that the situation would change; the slaughters were conducted in the name of *oto ha'ish* and the trinity, which according to the Jewish interpretation is true *avodah zarah*, which Jews could in no way accept; after the Turks were defeated by the Crusaders, there was no prospect of any "allies." Whereas in Hitler's *y"sh* times, the slaughters took place "simply" out of savagery and the beastly nature of man, and one could hope that perhaps the world would yet be shaken, and most importantly, that the allies would eventually win and put an end to Hitler, *yimach shemo*.

In other words: the Jew, the *ma'amin* until 1940, who was born in the 20th century and knew about Jewish history and the experiences of our people, with all the decrees and forced conversions, *r"l*, from the Crusaders and earlier, until Nevuchadnetzar King of Bavel, etc., could only ask why he and his family were involved in the Hitler plan; but the very concept of *sheteidim omdim aleinu lechaloseinu*—is partly accepted by them—was **no news** to him; consequently, Hitler could not touch his *emunah* in the *Ribono shel Olam*. Only one whose *emunah* was weak even before, and who sought a "justification" for his denial of the *Ribono shel Olam*, found such a justification, *keviyachol*, in the Hitler history.

The Hitler history did bring a *chiddush*, but in a different direction—in the realm of human development, culture, and civilization.

Many believed, especially in the ranks of the so-called *maskilim*, that in the 20th century, having reached such a civilization, with various "high" philosophical systems, with widespread high education, with such a school system and so many universities, with such high ethics and fine manners, that which happened in the "dark ages of the Middle Ages" could not happen. This sentiment was expressed in literature, in the press, and also in verbal conversations of leading personalities and thinkers. With this, they wanted to reject the "outdated" approach of the *Tanach*, that "the kindness of the nations is a sin," and Rashbi’s assertion that "**Halacha** is known: Eisav hates Yaakov." Suddenly, the great crash came, and the entire culture and civilization of the 20th century collapsed. It turned out that there is no contradiction at all that on one hand he is a philosopher, or a poet, with fine manners, and is well-received in high society in a Berlin salon, and the same person then comes to Treblinka, etc., and carries out all the things that were done there. And here it is not about exceptional cases, "monsters," and beasts in human form, but about 100 million people, an entire nation. And meanwhile—quoting the headlines of your articles—"the world was silent." To this, one can add a sub-headline, that a very significant part of the world was satisfied that "the thing" was being done (and/or at least that it was being done by others).

If the Hitler history had to touch the belief anywhere, it had to—and not only touch but also clearly prove—that one cannot rely on the human feeling of justice and righteousness, when even the person has high education and a university diploma, and is also the son of a degreed academic.

To my regret, and to my shame, people are afraid to come out with this obvious conclusion, not to mention the logical consequences to which this conclusion must lead regarding daily life. This unforgivable restraint is unfortunately found also among pious spokesmen, and even among those who have seen with their own eyes what people can do if they are left to their own devices. And this is, as I said at the beginning of the letter, because people seek to make life easier and more comfortable, so that they can sleep better. For it is easier to go along with the world, even though it is the same world that was silent, and in a large part was also satisfied in its heart.

***

And now I allow myself a personal remark, which is connected with our conversation while we met in my room. Your series of articles "And the World Was Silent" has once again awakened in me the thought that I wish to express here, on this occasion:

To remember and not to forget, as the Torah says: "Remember what Amalek did to you"—is self-evidently a positive thing; in the language of our *Chachamim z"l*, this is a *mitzvas asei*. Especially when one sees the growing tendency and the effort to forget and to make others forget.

But after all, this remembering is only one part of the task that lies upon us. The other, and perhaps even more important part, is to work and act **actively** against the so-called "Final Solution" that Hitler, just like Haman, had in mind.

The counteraction must be expressed through deeds in the direction of "so they multiplied and so they spread." To reach this goal, it will not help to make it difficult for oneself in the heart by constantly reminding oneself and not forgetting how important this is. One must increase and spread the encouragement to build up the Jewish people, as a Jewish people, and simply in the area of "and they were fruitful and multiplied and grew exceedingly"—exactly the opposite of the planned "Final Solution."

As in all things, so too in this, it is necessary—in addition to verbal encouragement—to show a living example. Especially someone who has personally survived all these things must certainly show that not only did Hitler *y"sh* not succeed, but to spite him and his helpers, he will specifically raise a large family with sons and daughters and grandchildren.

I allow myself to say with all strength that regardless of how important it is to tell the current generation what happened to us, and how difficult it may be to free oneself from those memories and experiences, nevertheless, according to my understanding, the first task is to fulfill "against your will you live," with the emphasis on **you live**, i.e., the vitality should be visible. In other words: you must make every effort to tear yourself away in that moment from those experiences and enter into a *seder chaim*, a married life, to establish a Jewish home and a Jewish family. This will **certainly** contribute to Hitler's defeat, that he did not succeed in making fewer with a Vizhnitzer Chossid; on the contrary, you will raise children and grandchildren, Vizhnitzer Chossidim until the end of all generations. I do not mean this as a mere witticism, although I am not precise and insist on a Vizhnitzer or a Lubavitcher, or just a Jew who keeps Torah and *mitzvos*. But if it can be in this way, it is certainly good. And since you have gone through harder things in your life, and you are now in America, if you will want to with truth, you will achieve this too. And may the *Hashem Yisbarach* grant you success.

To a longer letter? But if you will get married after Shavuos according to the law of Moshe and Yisrael with *mazal tov*—then my writing and also the effort of your reading will have been worthwhile.

## 8879

B"H, 25 Nissan, 5725
Brooklyn.

In response to your letter of 20 Nissan, in which you write regarding your daughter, may she live, etc.

It is not evident from your letter whether you have utilized, to the fullest extent possible, the influence of others upon her. Surely, such individuals can be found in the school where she studied, and certainly among the military personnel as well. We see at every step that, very often, influence on children that comes from friends—especially if they are of a similar age—succeeds more than the direct influence of parents. Although this is seemingly a simple logic, I felt it my duty to mention this as well.

2) Since all members of a family are connected to one another, not only physically but also spiritually, it is understood and simple that an increase in yiras shamayim by any one of the family members adds to this in the other family members as well, especially an increase by parents regarding their children. The greater the increase by the parents, the greater the result will be.

3) Furthermore, it should be noted that sometimes a situation as mentioned above occurs because, at the time of conception, there was a lack of necessary care in observing the laws and statutes of taharas hamishpachah (niddah, hefsek taharah, immersion in a kosher mikveh, etc.), whether due to a lack of knowledge or other reasons. Since teshuvah is effective to a significant degree even regarding the past, one should endeavor to observe these aforementioned matters, both regarding oneself and regarding others, and in this, too, "he who increases is praiseworthy."

It is appropriate that you have the mezuzos in your home checked to ensure they are all kosher according to the law, as well as your own tefillin—if this has not been done within the last twelve months. Every weekday, before davening and putting on tefillin, set aside a few coins for tzedakah. Your wife, may she live, should observe the good custom of kosher Jewish women: to set aside tzedakah before lighting candles every Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov.

At a time of favor, I will mention them—when you provide their names (along with their mothers' names)—at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for the fulfillment of their heart's desires for the good.

As for your daughter, may she live, traveling to a country where there are few Jews (in quantity and also in quality)—this does not seem appropriate to me at all.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 8871

[27 Nissan 5725]

...It seems you received incorrect information, for when I spoke with Rabbi Menachem Hakohen—may he live—regarding the Sifrei Torah being sent to Eretz Yisrael, in the presence of Mr. Yeshaya, I explicitly emphasized that I do not wish to distinguish between one settlement and another, or one village and another. My only condition was that it be a place where the Sefer Torah will actually be used, and I explicitly stressed that I am not giving it to any specific institution or village, so that there would be no room for anyone to find any fault in my words, or to interpret them in a way that is contrary to my intention. I requested that when they give it to a specific location, it should be emphasized even then that I did not send the Sefer Torah specifically for that place, as that is not my concern. One may only say that the Sefer Torah was sent from the Lubavitch center here, but not that it was decided here in advance to which place or institution it should be sent—which would, by definition, exclude other institutions or places. Based on your first letter, I find it not superfluous to add another point, which is also based on our conversations when you were here: that we were both in complete agreement that there is no place for exploiting matters of Torah and religion for partisan gains that have no connection to religion. And in the same vein regarding the aforementioned matter, certainly one should not exploit a Sefer Torah sent from here, or any Sefer Torah whatsoever, for such matters...

## 8892

8892

B"H, Tiferes sheb'Tiferes, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants of the general farbrengen of friends marking ten years since the founding of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, may they live:

Peace and blessing!

A sicha of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, is well known:

"It is a mistake to think that doing a favor for Klal Yisrael is something that only Rebbes or great figures can do. Every Jew can do a favor through his tefillah and bakkashah."

May Hashem Yisbarach look upon our affliction, hear our cry, accept our prayer, and bring a general salvation to Klal Yisrael, both spiritually and physically.

We are currently witnessing conduct that is above nature—this is something we can clearly see—it is the time when "the weak shall say, 'I am strong.'"

It is now as if one is ascending a mountain, a high mountain. When one comes close, within the four amos of the summit, that is when one must exert himself with all his strength to reach the peak; there is no more than four amos left. At that point, every blade of grass one sees is precious, every twig, every little stone that one can hold onto—with one's hand, foot, or body. At that moment, it is essential for there to be a light to illuminate, and when one is illuminating—the light that one sees while holding on is very precious.

The analogy of ascending a mountain is found in Chassidus: there are two people, one standing high on the mountain and one below. The one below needs to be strong to make the ascent, to know the paths, and to have proper garments so as not to be hindered by them. But when that is not available, one must go with mesiras nefesh. And then, every object one can hold onto is precious, and the light that illuminates is precious.

This is the time when we are near the summit of the mountain. In truth, we see that Moshiach is already close; he is "behind our wall," and one who has a good sense of hearing and a sense of sight hears his voice and sees him. We need only to traverse the little bit that is still lacking. Therefore, one must cherish every good thing to the utmost, and one needs a light to illuminate—which is Torah and the spreading of Torah. To learn oneself and to spread Torah.

Just before the light of day, sleep tries to overcome a person; one must exert himself not to sleep through the time, and then one will also be a vessel to receive the light of day.

This is something every Jew must know, and also, when he encounters another Jew, he must tell him: "Listen, brother, do not sleep through the light of day."

***

May it be the will that with the completion of ten years since the founding of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad—the completeness of the matter—all ten inner kochos should be aroused in each and every one, and in everyone collectively, to perform their function—for the true benefit of oneself and of others—a function in inwardness and completeness (and indeed, the year is "t'mimah" and "shleimah").

This is achieved through avodah with the surrounding kochos—faith (especially when it is in the strength of revelation, as it was at the time of the Exodus), "kavu m'sh," etc.—

For then the inner kochos and their activity are firmly established, enduring, and illuminating.

With a blessing for success in all the above and for good tidings regarding the aforementioned,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8974

8974

B”H, 5 Iyar, 5725
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letters, in which you ask regarding the matter of the *shidduch* and the reasoning concerning touching the beard, etc.

It is understood and simple that a *shidduch* must be founded upon good will and a firm resolution to assist one another in all matters, and certainly in matters of Yiddishkeit, Torah, and *mitzvos*, which are the foundation for the happiness of a Jewish man and woman, in this world and the next.

It is also understood that in matters of goodness and holiness, there are levels, one above the other—as the language of Chazal puts it: a *mitzvah*, a *hiddur mitzvah*, and *mehadrin min hamehadrin*. Even those whose level, for whatever reason, is only in the category of a *mitzvah*, they too know that the concept of *hiddur mitzvah* is, as it sounds, the addition of beauty and splendor to the matter, even if, for whatever reason, they do not personally observe this *hiddur*.

It is understood and simple that the channel and vessel for receiving Hashem’s blessing for everything that Bnei Yisrael require is conduct in daily life according to the Torah and its matters. From this, it is understood that when one is in need of a special blessing, there must be a strengthening and *hiddur* in this conduct.

From all of the above, it is understood that even according to those who hold that not touching the beard is merely a *hiddur mitzvah*, it is *chas v’shalom* to do the aforementioned when one is in need of a special blessing from the Giver of the Torah and the Commander of the *mitzvos*, and certainly when laying the foundation for an eternal edifice—marriage.

It is absolutely simple that according to the *poskim* who hold that not touching the beard is a command of our Torah, and one has conducted himself according to these *poskim* for several years, then *chas v’shalom* and *chas v’shalom* to change this conduct even at a regular time, and certainly at a time such as the one mentioned above.

As stated above, even if one side was raised according to the opinion that this is only a *hiddur mitzvah*, it is their primary duty to strengthen the other side in their good conduct in matters of Yiddishkeit, even in *hiddur*, and certainly if the other side has conducted themselves in this way for several years, and certainly if, according to the other side, this is a command and a *mitzvah* and not merely a *hiddur*.

It is understood that everything said regarding touching the beard has its parallel in many of the Torah’s *mitzvos*, even extending to matters of daily conduct. Therefore, before finalizing the *shidduch*, one must clarify with absolute certainty the position on the aforementioned point: whether one can concede on their own opinion if the other side views this as a matter of *hiddur mitzvah*. In particular, in a way of life, the concession must not be because "there is no choice, so one is forced to do it," which leads to feelings of bitterness, resistance, etc., etc. Rather, it must be that one concedes out of desire, good will, joy, and a good heart specifically. As mentioned, this applies not only to the case of touching the beard, but to all other *mitzvos* of the Torah and the *hiddur* within them, where issues like the one mentioned are liable to arise frequently. The solution must be one of closeness of mind, joy, and a good heart, which is the essential element in all of the above.

From all that has been written, my opinion regarding your question is understood: you must evaluate yourselves with special attention—are you prepared for a concession such as the one described? For as I have written, it is always directed toward one side, with more attention and precision in the fulfillment of *mitzvos* and more *hiddur*. In accordance with the results of this evaluation, you shall decide what is before you.

One more point to note, though this too is understood: although what was written above was in connection to your question regarding the *shidduch*, in truth, it stands in its full force at all times and in all places. For the Torah is eternal, its *mitzvos* are eternal, and every single one of Bnei Yisrael has been commanded that we ascend in holiness and do not descend—or in the phrasing of Chazal, we are commanded to ascend in holiness.

May it be the will of Hashem, who oversees every individual with *hashgacha pratis*, that He guide you in all of the above toward what is good for you—the true good.

With blessings for good tidings in all of the above.

On behalf of the Rebbe,
Secretary

8995

B"H, Erev Shabbos Parshas Kedoshim, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter...

Regarding the subject of this week’s parsha: The first commandment within it, appearing immediately at the very beginning of the sedra, is a commandment that also encompasses all matters of Torah and mitzvos: **"You shall be holy."**

This is prefaced by the fact that the commandment is addressed **"to the entire congregation of the Children of Israel,"** and it is explained by the reason for the commandment: **"For I, Hashem your G-d, am holy."**

Now, the question is well-known: What is the content of the commandment "You shall be holy," and what is the innovation in it, given that this is the essence of the entire Torah and its mitzvos, and the essence of every single one of the Torah’s commandments? The explanation for this is that the commandment is a general one: that we should be separated from things that are permitted—even though we have not been warned against them in the Torah and they have not been forbidden to us, we are warned to be clean, pure, and separated from them.

On the face of it, a person might say—especially when making an honest accounting of his soul and evaluating his situation according to his own measure—"It is enough for you that the Torah has forbidden certain things; if only one could fulfill all the explicit commandments of the Torah—those from the Torah, those from the Sages, down to the slightest detail of the words of the Scribes and the stringencies of the later authorities." Only one who has already reached that level should occupy himself with this higher avodah—to be separated from the permitted.

Therefore, the text prefaces and emphasizes that the address is **"to the entire congregation of the Children of Israel,"** without exception. And the reason for the commandment is **"For I, Hashem your G-d, am holy,"** through which it is understood and simple that the commandment is directed to everyone, since for each and every one it is said, "I am Hashem your G-d"—the reason and cause of the commandment.

Yet the difficulty remains: How can one rise to the avodah of "sanctify yourself in that which is permitted to you" when his strength has faltered in the forbidden (at the very least, the "sin of his heels"—that which a person tramples with his heels)? The answer lies in this very verse, based on another interpretation of it—according to which the possibility and full capacity to fulfill the commandment is understood: that the address was to the entire congregation of the Children of Israel, all together, at which point they are one complete stature. Especially since this parsha was stated in a public gathering (*hakhel*), meaning that they were also **actually** gathered together, and the power of the many is great, and the merit of the many is great, especially that of the entire congregation of the Children of Israel. And there is an additional infusion of strength through the announcement of the reason—"For I, Hashem your G-d, am holy"—to say: If you sanctify yourselves, I account it to you as if you have sanctified Me.

From this, the arousal and enthusiasm are understood when a person contemplates that by fulfilling this commandment, it is accounted to him as if he has sanctified Hashem his G-d. This arouses his inner powers—mighty powers—to overcome every obstacle and hindrance and to fulfill the commandment "You shall be holy" in its fullness and perfection.

And through the fulfillment of "You shall be holy," one arrives at the reward (as is also interpreted in this verse): "For (thereby) I, Hashem, (will be) your G-d"—we will merit to cleave to Him by being holy.

***

May it be the will that each and every one fulfills all that is stated above.

And according to another interpretation of this verse—based on the well-known principle that the imperative form is also a future tense and a promise—the promise will be fulfilled in its entirety: that you will be holy, a holiness so elevated that one "could say" it is "like Me"—like My holiness, I, Hashem (though the text comes to limit this).

And furthermore: "Your G-d"—your strength and your vitality will be drawn from My holiness, "I am holy."

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

***

I mention that the photo is being taken during Chol Hamoed. It is worth clarifying (regarding the future to come) whether one should take a photo during Chol Hamoed, especially now that, as a rule, people intend [to do so].

## 8896

8896

By the Grace of Hashem, Tuesday, Parshas Emor, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Tenth Annual Convention
of N'shei U'Bnos Chabad
May Hashem grant them life

Blessings and Peace!

This year’s convention, which marks a decade of activity, carries more than the usual significance. It should represent a special turning point in your activities, in accordance with the unique meaning and instruction of the number "ten."

The number "ten" concludes the order of **single** digits and begins the order of **tens**. This is a transition to a higher level, not only in **quantity** but also in **quality**. From ten and above, a new order begins, which is not merely greater in number, but incomparably higher in stature.

This is one of the explanations for why the number ten holds special significance in Torah, and consequently in Jewish life. This is expressed by the fact that a *davar sheb'kedushah* and certain prayers (such as *Barchu*, *Kaddish*, and *Kedushah*, etc.) can only take place when there is a *minyan* (ten Jews, as our Sages, of blessed memory, derive from the verse **"And I shall be sanctified among the children of Israel,"** in this week’s *sedra* (22:32). For although every Jew, as an individual, is precious and holy, when ten Jews come together, a **tzibbur** is created, which is already on a much higher level of *kedushah*, and within which the individual is also elevated to a much higher level.

One of the special meanings of "ten" is that it is the number of the **kochot hanefesh**. As explained in holy *sefarim*, especially in the *Tanya* of the Alter Rebbe, the founder of the Chabad approach, a person possesses ten internal powers that are connected to his *nefesh*. These are the three powers of **sechel**: *Chochma*, *Binah*, and *Da'as* (Chabad), and the seven **midos** (inclinations and emotions). In essence, the foundation of the entire Chabad approach is to develop the powers of *sechel* so that they shape the *midos*, especially the fundamental *midos* of **ahavas Hashem** and **yiras Hashem**, which should be expressed in daily life, in all respects.

The Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, and the *Nesi'ei* Chabad of all generations, have emphasized many times the important place that the woman occupies in the realization of the Chabad approach in daily life. The woman, as the **akeres habayis**, the builder of the Jewish home, determines to a very great extent the spirit and conduct of the family, and also has a very great influence, directly and indirectly, on her surroundings.

And the Torah gives her the instruction (and along with it, the power) on how to carry this out — through the proper use of her ten *kochot hanefesh*, as it is said: "Wisdom (*Chochmos*) has built her house, she has hewn out her seven pillars" (Mishlei 9:1) — with *sechel* (which, as mentioned, is divided into three) she builds her home and establishes its seven pillars (corresponding to the various *midos*).

***

May the Ribono shel Olam help that—as you now enter the second decade of activities connected with Torah and *mitzvos*—every group of N'shei U'Bnos Chabad, and every member of these groups, be elevated to a higher level in all the aforementioned respects, and be blessed with the fullest measure of success, both in *gashmius* and in *ruchnius* together.

With blessings for success and good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

8877

B"H, 11 Iyar, 5725

May they be blessed with all good, and in the measure of the Ribono shel Olam—which is measure for measure, and many times over—to derive much true Chassidishe nachas from all their descendants, the sons and daughters together, in accordance with the programs of the Tomchei Temimim yeshivos and the Beis Rivkah institutions.

With blessings for success in all the above and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

With respect and blessing,
