## 8882

B”H, Erev Shabbos Mevarchim Chodesh Sivan, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the annual dinner of Yeshivas Achi Temimim Lubavitch in Newark,
May Hashem keep them alive.

Greetings and Blessings!

The annual dinner is taking place this year during the week of Shavuos, **Zman Matan Toraseinu** — the ultimate goal of **Yetzias Mitzrayim**.

These aforementioned Yomim Tovim, Pesach and Shavuos, signify two historically interconnected events that forged our eternal people.

Their inner and timeless significance lies in the fact that they bring into the personal, daily life of every Jew, in every place and at every time, the experiences and revivals associated with these events.

The point of this is that "Yetzias Mitzrayim"—liberation from slavery, whether from **internal** slavery to one’s own human nature, or liberation from **external** slavery to the surrounding environment—can be achieved only through Torah and mitzvos, which illuminate the daily life-path of the individual and the collective.

This year, there is an additional point, in that we have a **leap year** (ibur-year). The purpose of a leap year is to ensure that the Yomim Tovim fall out at their proper time; first and foremost Pesach, which consequently ensures that Shavuos (the "50th day of Sefirah") will also be at the proper time, and likewise for all other Yomim Tovim.

However, as with all matters in Torah, which possess countless explanations and directives—for the holy Torah is infinite, just as the Giver of the Torah is Ein Sof, blessed be He—so too is the concept of a leap year. One of the directives of a leap year is that a Jew must be the master over his time and regulate his time in accordance with Torah. Even worldly matters, such as sowing and harvesting (Pesach is the time of the barley harvest; Shavuos, of the wheat harvest), and so on, must be connected with "Yetzias Mitzrayim"—not to be enslaved to the world and to nature, but on the contrary, to be the master over them, with the power of Torah and mitzvos that the Ribono shel Olam has given to the Jewish people.

Furthermore: if one has missed something in the past, one can not only make up for it, but even prepare a reserve for the future, as is also indicated by the concept of a leap year (in the additional month of Adar).

May the Ribono shel Olam grant that this year's annual dinner should bring these aforementioned matters to expression in each and every one of the participants and their families, may they live; to strengthen the foundations of Torah and mitzvos within themselves at home and in the surrounding environment, especially by strengthening and expanding the Yeshiva Achi Temimim in your city.

With greetings to all the distinguished guests and participants, may they live, and with blessings for success and good tidings.

#### ***8882***

**Experiences and revivals:** See also above, Vol. 22, Letter 8582, and the references in the note beginning "Chozrim hadvarim."

**Leap year:** See also above, Letter 8865, and the references in the notes there.

8883

B"H, 2 Sivan, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter.

Regarding the significance of this day, when Moshe began to engage with them (the Bnei Yisrael) regarding the acceptance of the Torah, saying to them, "And you shall be to Me a kingdom of priests" —

It can be explained that this refers to the three good qualities (crowns) that were given to this nation at the beginning of the giving of the Torah: **"You shall be to Me"** — that you shall be free for Me and occupied with **Torah**, and not occupied with other matters; **"a kingdom"** — kings wearing crowns; **"priests"** — priests serving.

Especially at the time of the giving of the Torah, every single one of the Bnei Yisrael was free for Hashem and occupied only with Torah, with crowns upon his head, and worthy of eating from the holy offerings.

And the beginning was — Moshe desired and ascended to Elokus, and through an *is'arusa d'lesata* (an arousal from below) came an *is'arusa d'le'eila* (an arousal from above), such that immediately, "Hashem called to him," etc., "And you shall be to Me a kingdom of priests."

May it be the will of Hashem that in these auspicious days, the aspect of Moshe Rabbeinu that exists in every single soul of the House of Yisrael will engage with them—with all the powers of his soul—in the matter of the acceptance of the Torah, and they will not wait for counsel, but will say, from the smallest to the greatest, "All that Hashem has spoken, we will do."

And from this — to the fulfillment of the mitzvah of *hagbalah* (setting boundaries) and the mitzvah of *perishah* (separation), and they shall be prepared for the giving of the Torah.

With blessings — in the language of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, the Rebbe — for the acceptance of the Torah with joy and with inwardness,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8984

8984

B"H, 2 Sivan, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, distinguished, and scholarly, R' Tzvi Hirsch, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated Monday (in addition to your list of *chiddushei Torah*—which arrived earlier). It is well known that it is not my practice to issue *psak din*, etc., especially since many have already discussed this matter. I ask for your forgiveness.

...Regarding the statement of our Sages in *Piftatei d'Oraisah*: According to the opinion of the Rambam (*Sefer HaMitzvos*, Negative Mitzvah 347) that "Do not lie with your neighbor's wife" (Vayikra 18:20) is a prohibition directed only at the man—this is also the view of the *Sefer Mitzvos Gadol* (Negative Mitzvah 97). (And apparently, in *Sefer Yereim*, section 214, it should also read: "Our Creator warned against the adulterer"—and not "adultery," as it appears in the printed editions). In *Sefer HaChinuch*, Mitzvah 35, it states, "And this prohibition is repeated," and in *Minchas Chinuch* there, it notes, "One is warned by this prohibition here, or by the prohibition of 'Do not lie...'"—according to this, the explanation is missing that this applies specifically to the man.

Regarding the words of the Ramban (*Acharei Mos* 18:20): "And it is possible that He said, etc." regarding the reason for the prohibition—it requires further study whether one can derive a halachic ruling from this, given that: 1) He concludes that this reason does not affect the *halacha* (regarding the punishment). 2) He **retracts** his previous statement and writes: "And the correct view in my eyes is that it is because of..." (and he did not write: "Furthermore, one could say," or anything similar). 3) He concludes there: "And our Sages expounded"—referring to our Sages of the *halacha* in the Torah.

#### ***8984***

Published in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 7, p. 320, and *Igros Kodesh*, Vol. 23, p. 245; completed based on a photocopy of the original letter.

**R' Tzvi Hirsch:** Friedman.

## 8885

## 8886

B"H, 3 Sivan, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the older students of the Yeshiva Ketana
of Tomchei Temimim
Lubavitch, Lod
May Hashem protect them and may they live

Peace and Blessing!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter [of the 22nd] of Iyar, in which you write of your good resolution to influence the younger students, to bring them closer to the ways and customs of Chassidus through consistent activities, and to be for them a living example of Tomchei Temimim students.

This, of course, should all be done under the guidance—and certainly with the approval—of the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva administration.

You surely know the law in our holy Torah regarding that which is "wet enough to moisten" (*tofeach al menas lehatfiach*). It must contain more water and moisture than something that is merely damp. In our context here, "water" refers only to Torah, and according to the explanation of our Sages, of blessed memory, "Just as water flows from a high place to a low place..."—which, regarding each and every individual, means that "the shy person does not learn." Even if one is embarrassed to reveal that he does not understand or that he requires further explanation, out of his great love for Torah, he descends from his level, waives his own honor, and asks and seeks clarification. And even when he grows older, our Sages, of blessed memory, have taught us that one learns more from teaching students than from peers, and even more than from a Rav. All of this is alluded to in the general concept of the Giving of the Torah, for the beginning of the Giving of the Torah was through "And Hashem **descended** upon Mount Sinai." The Torah was given to the Bnei Yisrael, whose souls **descended** from a high roof to a deep pit, and it is precisely there that the Torah is received as a "Torah of life," enabling the fulfillment of the mitzvos regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them."

May it be Hashem’s will that you increase in diligence and perseverance in the study of Nigleh and Chassidus, and that this study may be translated into actual deed—in the practical fulfillment of mitzvos and in influencing others—and may all this be with joy and a glad heart, [as is the case] in all matters of the service of Hashem.

With blessings for receiving the Torah with joy and inwardness.

8887

Erev Shabbos, Erev Chag HaShavuos,
Brooklyn, N.Y.

The Time of the Giving of Our Torah – 5725

To the participants in the celebration of the completion of *Iggeres HaKodesh*
by our Rebbe, the author of the *Tanya* – the final authority in the *Nistar*
of Torah – and the *Shulchan Aruch* – the final authority
in the *Nigleh* of Torah –
May Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

I received with pleasure the news regarding the completion of the *Tanya* by our Rebbe, specifically the section of *Iggeres HaKodesh*.

Although it was added to the *Tanya* after the passing of our Rebbe, this addition was made by "the sons of the saintly author, of blessed memory," and the first signatory was the son of the Mitteler Rebbe, his successor.

It is a well-known precision of language: *memaleh* (fills) his place—meaning the entire place is **full** (*maleh*) just as it was at the beginning.

The content of the conclusion of *Iggeres HaKodesh* (Section 32) concerns the merit of *tzedakah* given through a person’s own initiative—which comes about through the arousal of love for Hashem during *Krias Shema*, to cleave to Him and to surrender one’s soul in *Echad* and *b’chol me’odecha* in the literal sense, etc.

In this, the end is embedded in the beginning (*Iggeres HaKodesh*, Section 1), which also speaks of the matter of *kavanah* in *tefillah* from the "depths of the heart," etc., until the "exhaustion of the soul," etc. The difference is that the beginning speaks of the start of the activity of *tefillah*, which relates to spiritual matters—strengthening and fortifying the intellect as it contemplates the greatness of the *Ein Sof*, *Baruch Hu*, and the *midos* of love and fear of Hashem—and after this, it unfolds down to physical matters: *tzedakah* in practice in this physical world.

This aligns with the ruling in the *Shulchan Aruch* regarding the daily order for everyone: that from the *beis knesses* (*tefillah*), one should go to the *beis medrash* (*Torah*), and afterward go to one's business affairs. Furthermore, the engagement in commerce and the like must be in such a way that it becomes a dwelling place for Him, may He be blessed, through the giving of *tzedakah* from one’s earnings. This *tzedakah* elevates everything one has earned, as explained by our Rebbe.

One may also hint at this entire order in the teaching of our Sages on the verse: "They go from strength to strength, appearing before Hashem in Tzion"—a teaching that our Rebbe brought into *halacha* for practical application, stating: "Whoever leaves the *beis knesses* for the *beis medrash* and goes to learn, merits and receives the face of the *Shechinah*."

The path and the vessel for receiving the face of the *Shechinah* is the explicit verse: "I, in *tzedek* (righteousness/charity), shall behold Your face."

As the conclusion of *Iggeres HaKodesh* here states, "Righteousness (*tzedek*) shall go before Him," for it leads and draws down the higher "faces," etc., down to the world of *Asiyah*.

This order is such that they have no rest, without interruption, for day by day, during the time of mercy and the time of favor of *tefillah*, their soul pours out like water before Hashem through the *avodah* of *tefillah*, as mentioned above, from the depths of the heart until the exhaustion of the soul.

This is analogous to a field situated on a mountain (*Behar Hashem Yireh*) which requires constant irrigation.

Therefore, our Sages taught us that throughout the six days—the six thousand years of the world's existence—they irrigate it until the seventh day arrives, the day of Shabbos, which is entirely Shabbos and rest for the Life of the Worlds.

With respect and blessing in the traditional manner, that just as you have completed the aforementioned, so too may you begin other *masechtos* and books, and complete them, to learn and to teach, to observe, to do, and to fulfill.

And with a blessing—in the language of my father-in-law, the Rebbe—for the receiving of the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

May Hashem, blessed be He, bless each and every one of you and grant you success to go from strength to strength in your studies and your handiwork.

As we have just passed the time of the giving of our Torah, it is surely known to you that when the Ribono shel Olam came to give the Torah to His people, Yisrael, He commanded that the women be addressed first, and only afterwards the men. This means that it is in the merit of the women that the men also merited to receive the Torah and the mitzvos, which, of course, increases the responsibility placed upon the women and daughters of Yisrael. However, it is needless to emphasize that along with the responsibility, the strengths and possibilities were also granted to fulfill this role in its entirety. The matter depends solely on one's will, and we have been promised: "He who comes to purify himself is assisted."

With blessings for outstanding success and for good tidings,

## 8890

8890

B"H, Isru Chag Shavuos, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants in the annual luncheon of the N.Y. Committee for the Seminary for Teachers and Vocational Schools for girls in Kfar Chabad in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily,
May Hashem grant them life.

Blessings and peace!

It was with pleasure that I received the news regarding your upcoming luncheon on Sunday, Parshas Beha'aloscha, the coming week.

May Hashem Yisbarach help that the endeavor be crowned with great success in all respects.

According to the well-known teaching of the Alter Rebbe, Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch, that the weekly parsha contains guidance for all the events of the week, it is worth noting and emphasizing the significance of the words **"Beha'aloscha es haneros"** — "When you kindle the lights." As Rashi explains there, the lights of the Menorah in the Beis HaMikdash had to be kindled in such a way that the flame would rise by itself **(shetehei shaleves olah mei'aleiha).**

This is also the task of proper chinuch: that the student, boy or girl, should be able to ascend independently through the flame of **"ner mitzvah v'Torah ohr,"** which their mechanchim and educators kindle in their neshamas.

The realization of this task is made easier by the fact that the neshamah itself—the nefesh elokis that every Jew, man and woman, possesses—is by its inner nature inclined and strives toward Torah and mitzvos. It is only necessary to prepare the "wicks"—to remove the obstacles and rationalizations of the yetzer hara; and then, the flame rises by itself.

The mosdos in Kfar Chabad that you support through your devoted work carry out this task, and you have a great share and a great zechus in this partnership. However, as in all matters of goodness and kedushah, where there is always room to add, it is to be hoped that you will increase your activities on behalf of these holy mosdos, which were founded, and are conducted, in the spirit and path of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

May the Ribono shel Olam help that you should succeed in your work in an ever-increasing measure, and may He also bless you and your families, may they live, with revealed and manifest goodness in all that you need, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for success and for good tidings.

## 8,991

B"H, 8 Sivan, 5725
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 2 Sivan,

It seems I have already answered you regarding your previous letters; in any case, I will repeat it here once more:

According to the instruction of our Torah, the Torah of life, a "kosher woman does the will of her husband"—especially when the conduct of daily life is aligned with the Torah, and particularly if the question concerns employment in the field of educating the sons and daughters of Yisrael, which is the most exalted matter. From this, it is understood and simple that it is worthwhile for you to accept a position in this field (at the very least, a part-time position). When you make the effort to do so, you will certainly find a position and also succeed in it.

Regarding your writing that, in your opinion, you are unable to continue living in Kfar Chabad, I cannot agree with this. For even if, as you write, there are some negative matters (certainly, in every place of residence, there is no absolute perfection in our world), nevertheless, with good will and an appropriate approach, it is possible to overcome them. Based on what I know from letters from the residents of the Kfar, you will certainly find friendship and camaraderie there, and you will be able not only to adapt to life there but also to be satisfied in the full sense of the word. However, as with every matter in a person’s life, one must make an effort in this, and the main thing is to reject the approach expressed in your letter that "under no circumstances will you adapt," especially since your approach is not founded at all on reality.

May it be the will of Hashem Yisbarach, who watches over each and every one with Hashgacha Pratis, that He guide you well, and that together with your husband, may he be well, you will continue to live in Kfar Chabad with true closeness of heart, and with a good heart build an everlasting edifice founded on the foundations of Torah and mitzvos.

As you requested, the letter is being sent without waiting for the turn.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

**A kosher woman:** Tanna D’bei Eliyahu Rabbah, Chapter 9.

## 8992

8992

By the Grace of Hashem, 13 Sivan, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants of the 12th annual luncheon of
Agudas N'shei U’Bnos Chabad in Cleveland, Ohio
May Hashem grant them life

Blessings and greetings!

In response to the news regarding your upcoming annual luncheon on Sunday, Parshas Shelach, may it be Hashem’s will that the event be met with great success in all respects.

It is a well-known teaching of the Alter Rebbe, the Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch, that the weekly Torah portion contains guidance for our daily lives, especially in connection with extraordinary events.

This year’s event takes place during the week of Parshas Shelach, which recounts how Moshe Rabbeinu sent shluchim to scout Eretz Yisrael, and how those shluchim brought back a false report. Our Sages, of blessed memory, tell us that the women were not deterred by the unfavorable report; rather, they continued to desire their journey to Eretz Yisrael, Eretz HaKodesh, in accordance with the will of the Ribono shel Olam. The women were imbued with the feeling that Eretz Yisrael is a land of holiness and special Divine providence, as the Torah states: "A land which Hashem your G-d seeks out; the eyes of Hashem your G-d are always upon it, from the beginning of the year to the end of the year."

As has been emphasized many times, the Torah is eternal, and all its instructions are eternal—meaning they are valid everywhere and at all times.

The attachment of the Jewish woman to "Eretz HaKodesh" is an expression of her dedication to all matters of holiness, Torah, and mitzvos, which manifests itself in an even stronger form than that of the men, from time to time.

From this, there is guidance for our generation as well: that women can accomplish much to strengthen all matters of holiness, Torah, and mitzvos—first and foremost in their own homes, and together with that, in their surroundings in an appropriate manner—and thereby make their homes and their surroundings an "Eretz HaKodesh" for the Divine Shechinah.

This is, after all, one of the tasks of Chabad women everywhere, who possess the additional special merit that their path is illuminated by the light of Chassidus and Chassidic traditions.

And just as, together with Eretz Yisrael, all the Divine blessings of a "land flowing with milk and honey" were given—also in the material sense—provided that one conducts oneself according to the will of the Ribono shel Olam, so too are all Divine blessings always prepared for all those who help strengthen and spread Torah-Yiddishkeit to the fullest extent of their capabilities.

May Hashem Yisbarach grant success to your efforts in an ever-increasing measure, and may He bless you with revealed and manifest goodness in everything you need, both in material and spiritual matters alike.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 8993

8993

B”H, 14 Sivan, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

The Women’s League of Brownsville and East New York
May Hashem grant them life

They continued to desire to maintain their path toward Eretz Yisrael, **Eretz HaKodesh**—"the land where the special Divine providence is from the beginning of the year until the end of the year."

The attachment of the Jewish woman to Eretz HaKodesh is an expression of total dedication to all matters of holiness, Torah, and mitzvos, which at times manifests in an even stronger form than among men.

From this, there is a directive for our generation as well: that women can accomplish much to strengthen all matters of holiness, Torah, and mitzvos—first and foremost in their own homes, and together with that, in their surroundings in an appropriate manner—and in this way, create in their homes and in their surroundings an "Eretz HaKodesh" for the Divine Shechinah.

And just as together with Eretz Yisrael, all the Divine blessings of a "land flowing with milk and honey" were given, even in the material sense, provided that one conducts oneself according to the will of the Ribono shel Olam, so too are all Divine blessings always prepared for everyone who helps to strengthen and spread Torah-Yiddishkeit according to their fullest capabilities.

May Hashem Yisbarach grant success to your work in this direction in an intensified and expanded measure, and may He bless you and your families, may they live, with everything that is needed, in goodness that is seen and revealed, in both gashmius and ruchnius alike.

## 8894

8894

B"H, 15 Sivan, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch
For the celebration of the Siyum,
Montreal
May Hashem grant them life

Peace and Blessing!

In response to the news regarding the upcoming *chagigas hasiyum* on Wednesday, Parshas Shelach, the coming week.

May it be Hashem’s will that every one of the *mesaymim* recognizes in their inner self that this "Siyum" is truly a preparation for the beginning of a higher level in the study of Torah, both *nigleh* and *Chassidus*, with increasing *hasmadah* and *shekidah*, and in the performance of *mitzvos* with *hiddur*, together with *hashpaah* upon their surroundings.

Based on the instruction of the Alter Rebbe, the *Baal HaTanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*, that the weekly *parsha* contains practical guidance for the events of the week—especially an extraordinary event such as a *chag hasiyum*—it is timely to contemplate the verse, **"And your young ones... and I shall bring them, and they shall know the land"** (which is connected to Wednesday of Shelach). The holy Torah, which is eternal and whose instructions are eternal, gives us an instruction here: that children can, and must, strive for higher achievements even than those of their own parents, no matter how high the parents’ level may be. For in all matters of good and holiness, there is always the possibility to ascend higher. And when children also remember that through their achievements they also bring merit to their parents, they exert themselves in an entirely different way.

This aforementioned matter—in the style of our Sages, *yefeh koach haben mikoch ha’av* (the power of the son is greater than the power of the father)—is also reflected in the inner point of this month, the month of *Matan Torah*. As is well known, the Torah was given only after the parents promised, *"Baneinu areivim ba’adeinu"* (our children are our guarantors). It was in the merit of the children that the parents also received the holy Torah, *Toras Chaim*, and its *mitzvos*, regarding which it is said, "and he shall live by them."

May Hashem Yisbarach grant success to every one of the *mesaymim* to fulfill their task and *shlichus* to the fullest extent, as illuminated by the light of the Torah of *Chassidus*—the Torah of our teacher, the Baal Shem Tov, and our Rebbes, the *Nesi’im*, from generation to generation.

With blessings for outstanding success in both material and spiritual matters, and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8996

8996

B"H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Shelach, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings,

I am in receipt of your letter.

Regarding the theme of the day, that of this week’s parsha, its content concerns the matter of the Meraglim (spies). At that time, they were righteous, and for this reason, they were chosen and sent by Moshe, the shepherd of Yisrael. However, after they went up and scouted the land, what happened occurred—as recounted at length in the parsha.

According to the explanation of Rabbeinu HaZakein (in Likutei Torah and elsewhere), it is understood that the contention of the Meraglim was: What need is there for Bnei Yisrael to enter the land, where the primary avodah is the performance of **mitzvos** and the majority of one’s engagement is with the affairs of the land—plowing, sowing, and so on, "that you may gather in your grain, and your wine, and your oil"—and a person plows during the time of plowing, etc., and gathers during the time of gathering—**and what will become of Torah?** But in the desert, everyone’s bread was provided and their water was assured, and they were free solely to study Torah, and they learned from Moshe Rabbeinu, who received the Torah from Sinai and taught it to each and every one.

Seemingly, since they were righteous at that time—which implies that they wanted to fulfill the will of Hashem to scout "the land of Canaan, which I am **giving** to Bnei Yisrael," in order to enter the land **at all costs**—what changed after they went up and scouted, that they retracted and brought back a bad report of the land?

The explanation is based on the words of Chazal that "hearing is not like seeing." When they came to the land and **saw**, as it is written, "And all the people whom we **saw**... and there we **saw** the Nephilim... and this is its fruit," they said (to themselves and to those who sent them), "We cannot go up against the people, for they are stronger than we." They felt it was impossible to hold one’s ground, and certainly impossible to ascend from level to level. On the contrary, "the land eats its inhabitants" (even though their desire was to settle it, to make it a habitable land—their engagement in plowing and sowing is in a manner where "all your deeds are for the sake of Heaven," and even more than that, "in all your ways know Him," and so on—for the fulfillment of practical mitzvos).

There is a lesson from all this for a person’s avodah: one should not let his heart fall when he approaches his avodah in practice and encounters difficulties, concealments, and obstructions that he did not anticipate beforehand, or that he did not realize were so formidable, and that the matter is so strong that it requires conquering and refining. For this has already happened in the past, as mentioned in our parsha—the story of the trial, together with the advice for it, and the firm decision: "Do not rebel against Hashem" (for then, automatically, "do not fear," and "Hashem is with us," etc.).

And even if at times the trial seems extremely great, as do the concealments and obstructions, it is a *kal v'chomer*: If righteous men, whom Moshe Rabbeinu chose from all of Yisrael and who went on his mission with the intent to fulfill it as trusted, righteous messengers, nevertheless:

a) Even after hearing about the land beforehand and making a good resolution, the act of *seeing* caused them to change and feel a fear that, in their opinion, seemed justified.
b) They erred in this, for if "do not rebel against Hashem"—then the fear is nullified, and there is no room for changing the resolution.

How much more so in our generations, the *ikvesa d'meshicha*, one should not lose heart because his natural intellect sees the difficulties and concealments as giants, and that the matter is formidable and stronger than he, etc.

On the contrary, the promise of our eternal Torah is that if "do not rebel against Hashem"—then "do not fear," and "we shall surely go up, and we shall surely prevail, and we shall inherit it."

Surely, everyone’s inner resolution is firm that "we shall not rebel against Hashem," and by awakening this and bringing it to revelation, then—"do not fear," and "we shall surely go up, and we shall inherit it."

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

***

Regarding your writing that the Meraglim had some ulterior motive, etc.—this aligns with what is written in Likutei Torah (37b), "They did not want to lower themselves." See similarly there (41b).

Regarding what was written about the interpretation of "a trap in his mouth"—see Torah Or (20c).

## 8999

B”H, 22 Sivan, 5725
Brooklyn

To the participants of the small meeting in Kfar Chabad,
Regarding the organization of a youth village for “Beis Rivkah,”
May Hashem keep them alive.

Peace and blessing!

Your letter of 22 Sivan has been received. It is not sufficiently clear where the emphasis lies: whether on the “Beis Rivkah” component or on the matter of the “youth village.” The latter is, of course, a much broader plan, but the former has the advantage of being closer to implementation.

It is understood that the matter is necessary, correct, and very good in **both** cases. However, **before** beginning, it must be clarified whether you are in a position to rule out the very same reasons that have led to the most baffling and even alarming situation regarding all building plans in Kfar Chabad. Time and again, an eternity passes before the first **movement** begins, after which there is a halt. Then, various strange and unusual excuses are found for the halt, and another eternity passes until the second movement, and so on. [This is clearly evident regarding the Youth Center, where the **first movement** occurred twelve months after the laying of the cornerstone! The same applies to the construction of houses for so-and-so in such-and-such an area, where, according to the **usual** course of events, a period of two or three years is required! And, of course, each time, various strange and unusual excuses are found, as mentioned above.] This is despite the fact that it is **well-known** that a certain community in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) was built in half a year, and another town (and individual houses) was built in even less time than that. Furthermore, even among Anash themselves, the Shikun Chabad in the Holy City of Jerusalem (may it be rebuilt and established) is being built and developed, etc. There is no need to dwell on this alarming matter. What is the use of creating yet another **plan** if there is no guarantee in advance that it is a practical matter?

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Shalom M. Simpson
Secretary

## 901

B"H, 2 Tammuz, 5725
Brooklyn

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Tammuz, in which you write regarding a wedding in the family, and the bride is requesting that her father shave his beard at least until the wedding, and if not, etc.

Although it is generally not the way to respond to one person regarding matters that concern another—especially since in most cases it is impossible for one person to know the situation in all its details, and certainly not to know what is in the heart of the other—nevertheless, due to my great astonishment, I am responding. My astonishment is twofold:

a) That an adult, for she is already a bride, would base her relationship with her father—and publicly, at that—on the fulfillment of a demand such as the one mentioned. I will emphasize how far things have gone, that she is publicizing this demand, etc.

b) That this involves a Chabad family, who surely know (or at the very least should know) that according to the Nasi’im of Chabad, the matter of growing a beard is a matter of Halacha. Furthermore—and this is also important—it is a unique *segulah* for drawing down Hashem’s blessing in abundance, as is explained at length in the writings of the Admur the Tzemach Tzedek. Surely, every day and in every situation, a person is in need of the blessing of the Creator of man, the Creator of the world and its Guide. This is all the more true when one is in primary need of blessing at the time of laying the cornerstone for a "lasting edifice," such as a wedding and marriage. And precisely in connection with the chuppah and marriage, they come with a demand and a claim, in an ultimatum-like fashion, that he do the opposite of what is stated, *chas v'shalom*!

I must add another point regarding the matter itself, even if we were talking about non-Jews, *lehavdil*: in recent years, the fashion of growing a beard has spread, and from period to period, the number of those who do so increases, and (to borrow the style of your letter) they are viewed as respectable people.

I do not know the extent of your influence on the aforementioned, but our Sages of blessed memory said: "Accept the truth from whoever says it." May it be Hashem's will that you succeed in explaining to her the strangeness of the entire matter and its lack of logic, in addition to the point regarding the Halachic aspect here, especially since her father has been accustomed to growing a beard for some time.

It is understood that what is said above does not apply to grooming the beard with a suitable comb, as the Rav in your neighborhood will explain to you.

Based on what you wrote about your family and background, my hope is that you are active in the motto of Chabad families: spreading traditional Judaism in your surroundings and wherever your reach extends. We have been promised that words that come from the heart enter the heart of the listener and accomplish their effect.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*.

***

901

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 32, p. 249, and completed according to the secretariat’s copy.

**The matter of growing a beard:** See also above, letter 8,974, and the references in the notes there.

**Our Sages of blessed memory said:** See the Rambam’s commentary on the Mishnah, Introduction to *Avos*; the Rema in his introduction to *Mechir Yayin*; and elsewhere.

## 902

[5 Tammuz 5725]

In response to your letter dated 29 Sivan, requesting a blessing and a *pidyon nefesh*:

Since we have been promised, "You have labored and you have found," you should study *nigleh* and *Chassidus* with consistency and diligence, to the point that the Torah describes it as "labor." This study will lead to action—the fulfillment of *mitzvos* with *hiddur*. Then, the promise will be fulfilled: "and you have found." This is the conduit and the vessel for receiving the blessings of Hashem in all that you require.

With blessings for good tidings in the aforementioned matters.

Regarding what you wrote concerning what happened to you with your *tefillin*: You should become proficient in the *halachos* of *tefillin* that are relevant to you (not those for a *sofer* or the like), and from now on, you should also put on *tefillin d'Rabbenu Tam*.

With respect and blessings,

#### ***903***

**Matters are only sweetened at their root:** See Tanya, Chapter 31 (39b).

## 95

B”H, 11 Tammuz, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi Avraham, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter...

We are approaching the auspicious days of the Festival of Redemption, 12 and 13 Tammuz—the redemption of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe—the significance of which you surely know.

May it be Hashem’s will that each and every person be redeemed from all matters that are undesirable, or at the very least, from those that hinder one from the desired activity—in its inner essence, the fulfillment of man’s purpose upon earth: to make the entire world into His sanctuary, a *dirah lo yisbarach*, or in the language of Chazal, "to make Him a dwelling place in the lower realms." One is "sworn and standing" [bound by an oath] to this task. The term "oaths" (*shevuos*) is in the plural, as explained regarding the concept of an oath in general—that through the addition of strength to fulfill the *mitzvah*, the person is granted additional powers. This is why the root of the word for "oath" (*shevuah*) and the word for "satiety/fullness" (*sova*) is one and the same, as explained at length in the *maamar* of the Tzemach Tzedek (whose hundredth *yahrzeit* we mark this year) entitled *Mashbi’in Oto Tehei Tzaddik*.

With respect and blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

#### ***95***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 33, p. 238, and completed based on the secretariat’s copy.

**In the language of Chazal:** *Tanchuma, Naso* 16; *Tanya*, Chapter 36.

**Sworn and standing:** See *Nedarim* 8a.

**As explained regarding the concept of an oath:** See also Letter 8,768 above.

**The *maamar* entitled *Mashbi’in*:** Printed in *Kitzurim VeHe’aros LeSefer HaTanya* (1989 edition), p. 169 and onwards.

## 16

B"H, Days of Redemption, 12-13 Tammuz, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter.

We stand in the days of the redemption of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, from his imprisonment for the dissemination of Judaism, Torah (both the revealed and Chassidus), and mitzvos—dissemination carried out with mesiras nefesh, without regard for any obstacle, hindrance, or opposition.

Our redemption then was, in the words of the Baal HaGeulah, also the redemption of "all who cherish our holy Torah, observers of mitzvos, and also those who are merely called by the name of Israel, for **every person of Israel** (regardless of their personal state regarding the observance and fulfillment of mitzvos) has a heart that is perfect with Hashem and His Torah."

May it be the will [of Hashem] that the memory of the redemption, and the account of the imprisonment and the circumstances that preceded it, will inspire each and every one to great actions (in both quantity and quality) in the dissemination of Judaism in all its details, without regard for the difficulties and limitations from within or without—as instructed by the parsha of the week, "like a lion and like a lioness"—even to the point of mesiras nefesh (surrendering one’s own will) in this avodah.

And as per the promise of Chazal, "One who comes to purify himself (a corollary of which is to purify others as well)—they assist him greatly from Above"—may Hashem, his G-d, be with him, and may Israel (including even those who are "merely called by the name of Israel," as mentioned above) perform valiantly.

Until the verse is fulfilled in its literal sense: "A staff shall arise from Israel (this is Melech HaMashiach) and shall crush all the children of Seth (and his dominion shall be from sea to sea), and Israel shall perform valiantly."

With blessings for the Chag HaGeulah,

**M. Schneerson**

***

Regarding the above: When will the volume of the Talmudic Encyclopedia be published? Many are in need of it, etc., etc.

***

With blessings for the Chag HaGeulah and for good tidings regarding your public Torah classes, and likewise—that you continue to commit to writing (and in increasing measure) the stories and concepts of our Rebbes and the "early Chassidim" of each of them—may you continue to add and add.

***

It is understood that the cancellation of the girls' camp, etc., is distressing—especially since it succeeded last year despite the difficulties and it being a first attempt, and all the more so this year.

And the explanation for the cancellation, even if it is justified, will not increase the "candle of mitzvah and Torah light."

Surely Hashem will grant you double success in the activities yet to come.

***

Regarding your question about studying Likutei Torah: Do as much as you are able, and see Torah Or (98c), the maamar beginning "And so" (in the section on the festivals), that since [one has the desire], it will be completed for him, etc.

## 908

B"H, 23 Tammuz, 5725
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of the First (Old) Beis Medrash in Kfar Chabad, in our Holy Land—may it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu speedily in our days—
May Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 20th of Tammuz, in which you write regarding the addition and expansion, and primarily regarding the addition in quality—by which I mean the Torah study sessions conducted in the beis medrash.

The teaching of our Sages is well-known regarding the verse, "Hashem loves the gates of Zion more than all the dwellings of Jacob"—these are the gates that are distinguished (*metzuyanim*) in Halacha.

May it be the will of Hashem that, in the language of the verse, "All your children shall be students of Hashem," students of Hashem, learners of the Torah of Hashem, and "great shall be the peace" (that they increase peace) in the world (in the sense of *he'elem*—concealment, as explained in Chassidic discourse), and may hearts draw closer yet more and more. May there be an abundance of peace, and consequently, an abundance of blessing as well.

And since the abundance mentioned above nullifies the cause of the Galus, the effect is nullified accordingly, and may there be an abundance of redemption—the true and complete Geulah.

And may these days be transformed into gladness and joy.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all the above.

**M. Schneerson**

## 908

B"H, 23 Tammuz, 5725
Brooklyn.

May these days be transformed into joy and gladness.

**M. Schneerson**

## 909

B"H, 27 Tammuz, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

And just as we have seen many matters for the good that were fulfilled in their entirety, may it be His will that it be so in this matter as well, and that for many more good years, in all details, you will serve in your position, and also, as mentioned, for the benefit of the many—their benefit in both physicality and spirituality together. And it is obvious that, as per the instruction of the teachings of Chassidus, in the aforementioned physicality and spirituality, the motto of the dominance of the form over the matter will be fulfilled.

With appreciation, honor, and a blessing for good tidings, in health and joy.

## 19

B"H, Tuesday, the day on which "it was good" was doubled,
Brooklyn, N.Y.
5 Menachem Av, eve of 6 Menachem Av, 5725

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter.

As we stand in these days, which we are promised will be transformed into joy and gladness with the coming of our Moshiach,

And (in the well-known phrasing) even though he may tarry, nevertheless I will wait for him every day that he may come, as it is written, "If he tarries, wait for him" —

May it be the will that this happens speedily in our days, truly soon.

According to what is brought in many places, it can be said that the very act of waiting for him hastens the coming of Moshiach, for "Hashem will do for those who wait for Him."

For through this, one adds to the "merit" (*zachu*), and consequently, one enlarges and accelerates the result—the "I will hasten it" (*achishenah*).

One can add further to this based on the interpretation of our Sages: "Those who wait for Him" refers to those who press into the words of wisdom, are precise about them, and wait for them in order to know the clarity of the matter and to know their Master.

This means that they strive and toil to clarify the truth of the words of wisdom until they know their Creator—by overcoming the darkness, whether the darkness from within (in the intellect or the emotions of the heart) or from without (the concealment and hiddenness of the world)—to nullify it, and even more, to transform it into an aid, until "the darkness is transformed into light." And "Hashem will do"—that these days will be transformed into joy and gladness (with the coming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu).

And from the twelfth foundation—the coming of Moshiach—to the thirteenth foundation—the resurrection of the dead—

(And today is the day of the passing of the Arizal, who is alive)—

May the prophecy be fulfilled: "These bones shall live," for they are the entire house of Yisrael, through Hashem placing His spirit within them and they shall live.

And may the prophecy be fulfilled: "Your dead shall live, the dwellers of the dust shall awake and sing, and a great congregation shall return here; for thus says Hashem: Sing to Yaakov with joy, and I have transformed their mourning into joy—the word of Hashem."

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 11

B"H, Tuesday, the day on which "it was good" was doubled,
Brooklyn, N.Y.
5 Menachem Av, 5725

To the G-d-fearing, honorable, and distinguished, who engages in the needs of the community, etc., our teacher, R' Shmuel Yehuda, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 27 Tammuz and its enclosure, and I thank you, I thank you.

...You have done a great and useful thing in preparing the map and the illustrations, etc., as is understood. However (and precisely because their function is to be an "illustration" and a complete work), it is a pity that some details (including some that are more than mere details) are missing from it. Time does not permit a thorough review and elaboration at all. I will point out two, and each one of them is a new category and a complete subject:

a) At the beginning of the notes, etc.: The tumah of a chayah—behemoth, etc., which he made into a golel (Rambam, Hilchos Tumas Meis, Chapter 6, Halacha 4 [and see Chullin (129a), the incident with...]), and especially according to the majority of opinions that the tumah of a golel is min HaTorah.

b) The map as a whole: There should be a section for: **Fifth** (for a chatas—Taharos, Chapter 2, Mishnah 5).

And in this, too, we see the great necessity for study, even when copying the words of the great ones exactly as they are, and even those who were most precise in their words (as in the case at hand—the Rambam).

## 912

B"H, 5 Menachem Av, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the dedication of the shul in Kfar Chabad,
May they live,

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby extend my greetings to all those participating in the dedication of the shul, and in particular to those who merited to be the volunteers and those who labored in its construction and completion. May it be the will of Hashem that the "psalm, a song for the dedication of the house" shall not be silenced, and that it will awaken in the hearts of all participants, from near and far, feelings of honor and reverence for all the institutions of the Kfar—feelings of heart and soul whose impression will be evident in actual deed, through the expansion of the institutions and the support of Torah and Yiddishkeit in every way, in a manner of "increasing and continuing."

Although this letter is written during days that have not yet been transformed into days of joy and gladness, it is well known that even the matters of punishment mentioned in the Torah are part of the "Torah of kindness," and in their inner dimension, they are the depth of kindness. This is also true regarding the content of these days. And although because of our sins we were exiled from our land, the ultimate purpose of the destruction and the galus is not, Heaven forbid, because suffering is desirable in and of itself, but rather so that it will bring about the intended rectification through the correction of our deeds and conduct in the observance of Torah and mitzvos in our daily lives; for the descent is for the sake of the ascent, and the consolation is twofold. And if this is true even regarding our conduct in the lands of our dispersion, then all the more so in our Holy Land, the palace of the King.

The very dedication of the shul and the timing of its establishment during the week of Shabbos Nachamu contain much symbolism and connection to the "matter of the day," since our Sages have crowned the shul with the title "mikdash me'at" (a miniature sanctuary). This shul, in particular, is worthy of its name, for it will also serve as a beis medrash for the study of Torah day after day, much like the Beis Hamikdash, which was not only the place sanctified for avodah and korbanos, but also the location of the Lishkas HaGazis, the seat of the Sanhedrin.

And just as in the construction of the Beis Hamikdash, although the wood and stones, etc., were what constituted the magnificent and sanctified building, the essence was the enthusiasm and mesiras nefesh that enveloped the sons and daughters of Yisrael as they volunteered for its construction, and subsequently, the holiness, love, and yirah that characterized the avodah of the Beis Hamikdash—so too, this shul, which was built from lofty sentiments of the heart, will be permeated with holy enthusiasm and an abundance of the light of Torah and mitzvah. And the "voice is the voice of Yaakov"—the voice of song, of tefillah, and the voice of Torah—will fill its entire space, a great voice that does not cease, breaking forth and extending outward.

May it be the will of Hashem that all who participated in the construction and completion of this magnificent shul be blessed with all they require, with blessings from the One who dwells on high, who causes His Shechinah to dwell in every place, and especially in our Holy Land, and particularly in these miniature sanctuaries.

It is my prayer that this project, of such great value and achievement, will be a beginning for further mighty efforts to expand the Kfar and its holy institutions, and to raise the banner of Torah and mitzvos in general. Through this, may we all merit together the complete and true Geulah and the building of the Beis HaBechirah by Mashiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days, truly.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

B”H, 5 Menachem Av, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter of 2 Tammuz (and the one following it), along with the enclosure. Thank you for your attention in informing me of all the details regarding the negotiations between the religious parties in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established.

Regarding the present matter, I am writing once again concerning the establishment of a technical religious front—that is, exclusively for the elections, but not a front thereafter. The front following the elections should be dependent on new deliberations and the state of affairs after the elections. This is in contrast to the current situation, where this [a permanent front] falls under the category of "if you grasp too much, you grasp nothing." Furthermore—and this is the main point—it is highly doubtful whether such a front is desirable at all (if we are speaking of a front from one end of the country to the other).

Enclosed is a copy of my letter at length regarding the aforementioned. It is my hope that you, too, agree with my position on the matter and will do everything in your power regarding this...

May it be the will of Hashem that, in the end, we merit that our Torah—the Torah of truth, which is one Torah—will draw closer the hearts of the "one nation in the land" to Hashem our G-d, the One Hashem, and may they all be of one mind (without the voting that is subject to the opinion of flesh and blood) to do His will with a whole heart.

With respect and the blessing of *Ksivah V'chasimah Tovah*.

## 914

914

B”H, 14 Menachem Av, 5725
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of August 10th, along with the enclosure.

May Hashem Yisbarach grant that from now on you should know of no sorrow or anguish, chas v’shalom, and that you should only be able to report good news, in good health.

Regarding your inquiry about visiting relatives in Eretz Yisrael and staying there until after the Yomim Tovim:

Surely you know that traveling there on a Jewish ship—one that belongs to Jews and is serviced and operated by Jews—is something one must not do under any circumstances. It is among the greatest of sins, and it is a bitter pity for those who do so, not knowing the great troubles they bring upon themselves and upon Klal Yisrael, rachmana litzlan.

If it is a matter of traveling by airplane, which departs and arrives on weekdays, or on a non-Jewish ship, then traveling is a perfectly acceptable matter.

May Hashem Yisbarach grant you success in this journey, and also before and after it, and may you have true nachas—which is Jewish nachas—from your children and grandchildren, sheyichyu.

And may the zechus of the tzedakah (according to the enclosed receipt) stand by you in this.

With blessings for all good tidings, including all that was written above.

## 915

15 Menachem Av, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants in the laying of the cornerstone of the Chabad housing project in Lod, in our Holy Land—may it be built and established speedily by Mashiach Tzidkeinu—
May they live,

Peace and blessing!

I received with pleasure the good news regarding the laying of the cornerstone for the Chabad housing project in Lod, on Wednesday, the 20th of Menachem Av, the coming week. May it be the will of Hashem that this be done at a propitious and successful time.

The great importance of building a home in Eretz Yisrael—the land upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year to the end of the year—is well known. This is especially true regarding the establishment of a housing project that will contain homes worthy of being called a "great house," according to the interpretation of our Sages, of blessed memory: a house where Torah is cultivated, a house where tefillah is cultivated, with shuls and beis medrash buildings—a *mikdash me'at*—where the voice of tefillah and the voice of Torah (both the revealed Torah and the teachings of Chassidus) will be heard. May they radiate their light and their greatness to all the homes in the project, and within every home, may the voice of song and the voice of tefillah be heard.

May it be the will of Hashem that, in accordance with these days that follow the days of destruction—the days of consolation that begin in the month of Menachem Av—our Father in Heaven, the Consoler of Tzion and Builder of Yerushalayim, will console us with a double consolation. May we merit soon the building of the House of Hashem, the Beis HaMikdash, through Mashiach ben Dovid.

"Merit is brought about through those who are meritorious," for there were no days as festive for Yisrael as the fifteenth of Av, etc., and the twentieth day of that month, the time for the wood-offering in our Beis HaMikdash by the descendants of the sons of Yishai, the father of Dovid.

With respect and with the blessing that just as you have begun with the laying of the cornerstone, so too may you soon celebrate its completion—a complete building and a complete housing project, in which wisdom, understanding, and knowledge will increase, until the well-known promise is fulfilled: "For the earth shall be full of the knowledge of Hashem."

**M. Schneerson**

## 916

[Beginning of Elul, 5725]

Regarding the matter of a *zeres* (span) — in my humble opinion, it is worthwhile to cite the source and the like, for anyone who increases the citations for Torah is praiseworthy.

Regarding the vocalization of *samayach tesamach* — it seems clear to me that it is pronounced *samayach* with a *patach* under both letters. I did not note this in the *siman* because I recall that there is a letter from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding this, and I am currently searching for it.

Many thanks, many thanks, for your great efforts regarding the *Chazit Datit* (Religious Front) technicalities, and for not refraining even from going to [the city of] P., etc. In such matters, even in cases of doubt or double-doubt, the action is worthwhile. One may note from *Sanhedrin* (110a), and especially the opinion of the Ramban (in the Eighth Principle of the Rambam’s *Sefer Hamitzvos*), according to which [we learn from] "And Moshe arose and went," etc. (in addition to resolving the doubt—if there was one—as to what is considered opposition).

***

916

A portion was printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 3, p. 281, and it was completed based on a photocopy of the original handwritten letter.

The letter is to Rabbi S.Y. Zevin, and it was written on the margin of his letter dated Wednesday, 27 Menachem Av, 5725. Further letters to him appear above, letter 8731, and in the references noted in the footnotes there.

**Regarding the matter of a *zeres*:** In his letter: "I saw there [in the *Siddur Admur Hazaken im Da"Ch*, 365a-b] what the Rebbe wrote regarding the custom in the Rebbe’s house to raise the *Kos Shel Bracha* a *zeres* from the table. I had seen this long ago in the Rebbe’s *Haggadah Shel Pesach* and I surmised that this was based on the *Zohar* which writes *zeres*. When I worked on the entry for *zeres* to appear in Volume 12 of the *Encyclopedia*, I noted this in the footnotes and added that it requires further study (*tzarich iyun*), for the *Zohar* itself writes in other places *tefach* (a handbreadth), as is the case in the *Gemara* and all the *poskim*. Surely the intention where it writes *zeres* is also for a *tefach*. As is written in the *Targum Yerushalmi* on the *Choshen*, 'a *zeres* in length'—*pashach*, which is a *tefach*. This is also written in *Itur Sofrim* regarding the *Mitpachat Sefarim*. Now, in the *Siddur*, I saw the Rebbe’s holy opinion there. Indeed, the Rebbe wrote that this is based on the *Zohar* which writes *zeres*, but did not bring the aforementioned *Targum Yerushalmi*. Since the aforementioned entry has not yet been printed, I will also add what is written in the *Siddur*, but in any case, I must conclude with *tzarich iyun* (perhaps I should not bring it at all and not write *tzarich iyun*?)."

**Regarding the vocalization:** In his letter: "I saw in the *Siddur* the vocalization of *samayach tesamach* in the *Sheva Brachos* as *samayach*. I checked all the Chabad *Siddurim* and in all of them it is written with two *patachs*. In my poverty, I have said all my life *samayach*, as is the case in all other *Siddurim*, and the main thing is that this is according to grammar. I do not know if this vocalization of the two *patachs* was intentional or perhaps it is from the printer and without supervision."

**That it is pronounced... *patach*:** See also above, Vol. 3, letter 471.

**Regarding the *Chazit Datit*:** See also above, letter 913, and the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 18

[2nd of Elul, 5725]

In response to your request from some time ago to share my opinion regarding the question of establishing a united front of the religious parties for the upcoming Knesset elections: I have not replied until now for several reasons. One of them is that, due to the simplicity of the matter, I hoped that even without my intervention, the issue would reach its proper resolution—at the very least as the final deadline for submitting the lists approached. However, to my great regret, this has not come to pass, and therefore I am now providing a response to your question.

By way of introduction, the subject at hand is the establishment of a **technical** religious front for the Knesset elections. I emphasize the word **technical**, meaning that after the elections, the situation regarding the relations between the parties will return to what it was before the front was established.

My opinion on this is clear and absolute: the establishment of a technical religious front is not only desirable, but also essential for the benefit of the religious situation and for the benefit of the state of true Judaism in Eretz Yisrael—may it be built and established speedily in our days by Moshiach Tzidkeinu. It is so clear that any doubt on the matter is astonishing—from the perspective of the religious situation and its benefit.

Despite the simplicity of the matter, I will propose, briefly at least, the reasons and arguments that mandate the establishment of the technical religious front. They are:

### A. In the realm of profit and loss

**(1) The prospects for gaining additional representatives:**
It is natural that in election campaigning, every party will strive to acquire the largest number of votes possible. Since the resources available to each party are limited (in time, money, number of activists, etc.), it will strive first and foremost to concentrate its resources on those voters whom it has the best and greatest prospects of influencing. In the present case, this means that each of the religious parties (if there is no united front, Heaven forbid) will direct the force of its propaganda and efforts toward the members of the other religious parties. After all, the prospects of winning them over are greater and better than winning votes from the circles of the ignorant who belong to non-religious parties, and all the more so the anti-religious ones.

This has been seen tangibly and clearly from past Knesset elections.

This means that regarding the total number of votes for the religious parties in the Knesset, the propaganda will have no effect, or at the very least, very little effect.

This is not the case if there is a united religious front, in which case the propaganda will be directed outward, and there are good prospects for winning votes from various circles.

**(2) Residual votes:**
It is understood and simple that if there is a united front, the residual votes of each party will not be lost, but will be added to a larger calculation to increase the number of mandates.

**(3) And the main thing is—drawing hearts closer to religious matters:**
The impact of election propaganda is felt for a time even after the elections. If the propaganda is directed toward circles that are not yet religious for whatever reason, then not only is there hope for acquiring new votes as mentioned, but there will also be a gain regarding drawing a certain number of our brethren, the Children of Israel, closer to religious matters.

**(4) Preventing mutual defamation:**
If there is no religious front, Heaven forbid, then the propaganda of the religious parties will be directed primarily against the other religious parties. As is customary in this, and in the manner of election campaigns, they do not settle for emphasizing the virtues of their own party, but emphasize "no less" the shortcomings of the other parties. And as mentioned, as is customary in election propaganda, the truth is not always the lamp at their feet or the bridle on the speakers' mouths; consequently, they exaggerate, inflate, etc. And it is human nature that, in the style of our Sages, of blessed memory, a covenant is made with *lashon hara* that it will be accepted (whereas regarding the virtues of oneself and one's party, they do not accord it full trust, and sometimes not even partial trust). The results are understood, and as mentioned above, not only regarding the election results in terms of the number of mandates, but also regarding the impression afterward—in relation to religion and religious matters.

**(5) Rejecting a religious front—a weapon in the hands of religion's opponents:**
This very fact—that they do not reach an agreement among themselves to establish a religious front for the elections, at a time when several non-religious parties have reached an agreement to go together to the elections—will certainly serve as a weapon in the hands of the parties fighting against the religious parties, especially when they can quote from the propaganda of the religious parties themselves the shortcomings of the religious parties that disqualify one another, etc.

**(6) The change in the situation:**
Since the number of voters for the next Knesset has increased, and consequently the number of votes required to elect a representative has increased—and according to several activists in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established, most of those who have recently been added to the voting public do not belong to the religious parties—the aforementioned change is not to the benefit of the religious parties. Therefore, an additional effort is required in these elections compared to past elections, even if the results of the past elections had been satisfactory, and especially since the results were a disappointment. This reinforces even more the reasons and arguments above regarding the necessity of establishing a technical religious front for the elections.

### B. The arguments against a religious front

Among the arguments I have heard against establishing a religious front are:

**(1) It is not honest or straightforward toward the voters to speak of the virtues of another party during the elections, when until the establishment of the front and after the elections, they do not always speak in its praise and perhaps even fought against it in several areas.**
It is understood that this argument has no basis in reality, since it is explicitly emphasized that this is a *technical* religious front. From this, it is understood that there are fundamental differences between the religious parties, which is why they do not merge into one party, and not even into a front that will continue after the elections.

**(2) Some say that there is a prohibition according to Torah to form a religious front, even a technical one, with a party with which one is not satisfied regarding its attitude toward religious matters.**
This argument, too, is refuted by its own side, in addition to the **precedent of the great** in this—the custom of the great leaders of Israel in Poland, etc., who approved the establishment of a technical front, even with those who are not religious. And in Eretz Yisrael itself, there was already a religious front once, and the second time it was cancelled, it was **not at all** because of reasons of prohibition according to the *Shulchan Aruch*. On the contrary, the cancellation came from the side of those called "the leftists" within the religious parties, as is known and famous.

**(3) Some say that there is a prohibition against establishing a religious front from such-and-such a great leader—**
Now, in general, in such a case, it is simple that one should not take practical action until one sees the text of the prohibition **in all its details**, in order to know if it was said by implication or explicitly, if it was said also regarding a technical front, and if it was said regarding a situation similar to the current one, which is not similar **at all** to the situation that existed in Eretz Yisrael four or eight years ago or more.
Furthermore, one must examine whether the prohibition is not part of a system—that all the religious parties **do not conduct themselves according to it**, and not even according to the principles of this system, and even in matters that do not pose a danger to the religious situation in Eretz Yisrael, but only a reduction in certain activities and regarding certain gains. For if so, it is obvious that if they do not conduct themselves according to the aforementioned system because of limited gains, there is no place to take one detail from the system and make it a reason for conduct that will **harm** the general religious situation in Eretz Yisrael.

**(4) The **actual** conduct of **all** the religious parties throughout the entire time **and also now**—proves that they did not accept the prohibition **at all** (or that it was in a form **that does not apply** to this problem). For example: in several of the largest towns in Eretz Yisrael, they formed a front among themselves (and also with non-religious parties) and handed over **with their own hands** to a member of the other party important departments regarding city affairs, and not just for a few weeks, but for months and years. And the handing over was not just permission to express an opinion and vote, but for actual work in areas that are partially religious, and in the rest—they influence in an indirect way, at least—the state of religion in the city. The justification is that in exchange for this front of several months, which is well-known in Eretz Yisrael and abroad, the party will receive another department, and consequently the religious situation will gain in a certain area of that city. Since this front has existed for several years **and no one raises a voice or objects from any of the parties**—then there is no place at all to say that in their opinion there is any prohibition in a technical front for a few weeks, which has no element of giving and taking in hand, as those elected to the Knesset do nothing but express an opinion and vote. Those who vote for the united list, each one has in the list a candidate from his own party, for whom it is necessary that they vote in order for him to be elected to the Knesset, and he can intend for him (unlike the front in the aforementioned towns, where they voted in a direct and positive manner for a candidate of the other party).

**(5) Another point regarding all the aforementioned arguments:** It is understood and a general rule of logic and Torah law that *bari v'shema, bari adif* (a certainty and a doubt, the certainty is preferred). The gains from establishing a technical religious front are clear, and all the arguments against it are only in the category of doubt. Furthermore: the certainty is for the benefit of the general religious situation, and the doubt is—**perhaps** for the benefit of a party, a faction, etc.

### C. The reasons of those who oppose a religious front

Seemingly, since the situation, as stated above, is quite clear, what is the reason that there are those who cast doubt on the correctness of establishing a religious front? It seems that the reasons are also simple, and the main reason is:
It is natural that the activists of any party are interested in fortifying the status of the party as a party, and in fortifying the status of their faction within the party itself, for which full trust is required, or at the very least, as much trust as possible, from the members of the party and the members of the faction. It is understood that one who conducts propaganda for the establishment of a (religious) front with another faction, and all the more so with another party, undermines his status as a zealot for the platform of his faction and also for the platform of his party. Furthermore, there is a place for the fear that the extremists in the faction or in the party will leave the faction or the party and move to another faction or party, etc. In other words, the establishment of a technical front is desirable and also essential for the benefit of the **general** religious situation, but there is a **fear**, at least a small fear, that it will detract from and harm the situation of a certain faction or the attitude of the members toward the leaders of the faction and the party, etc.

### D. The tactics to sabotage the establishment of a religious front

There are several ways to sabotage the establishment of a technical religious front that I find it my duty to write about in this letter, since there are those who use these methods in order to cancel the establishment of the technical front while **concealing** their hoped-for goal. Among them:

(1) To declare in a loud voice that, on the contrary, the unification of all religious forces is essential, and therefore also the unification of all religious parties; and furthermore, that the merger of all the parties is essential, and one must extend a hand to the right and to the left, provided that all the parties unite together; but that there must be true peace, a complete merger, at least for the duration of the Knesset's existence. Anyone who knows the situation in Eretz Yisrael now has no doubt that the plan to establish a religious front for the entire duration of the Knesset, and needless to say, a merger of the religious parties, is not practical at all, and has no prospects of being realized. The aforementioned declaration can be interpreted in only one way: that this is an attempt to sabotage a technical religious front, in the sense of "if you grasp too much, you grasp nothing."

(2) A second way is to take the path of despair, meaning: what is the use of propaganda to establish a technical religious front, since it will not be realized, because the mood is not prepared for it, and it is a waste of time and energy, etc.

In the style of our Sages, of blessed memory, the measure of good is greater than the measure of retribution. If they could cancel the establishment of a religious front in a few moments after a great effort to establish it over months, it is certainly possible to establish a technical religious front even now, provided that the **few people** who stand at the head of each of the aforementioned parties truly and sincerely want it and do everything that depends on them for its establishment.

The conclusion from all that has been said is that I see no room for doubt regarding the absolute necessity of establishing a technical religious front for the upcoming elections, because the benefit of the religious situation demands it urgently. On the other hand, according to the rule that "a bribe blinds the eyes"—and these words are said even regarding the great and the good—there is room to say that at the top of every party there are hesitations whether it is worth establishing this technical front at the expense of party gains, or the gains of the faction, or the gains of certain individuals. And since this is so, one must assist the parties to overcome their hesitations—by having public opinion and the representatives of various organizations, etc., reveal their clear and firm opinion that the establishment of the aforementioned religious front is essential, and with the addition—

That all those parties or factions or individuals who prevent the establishment of this technical religious front are thereby placing the gains of the party, the faction, etc., above the gains of the general religious situation in Eretz Yisrael, **which concerns thousands and tens of thousands of our brethren, the Children of Israel, in Eretz Yisrael.**

And if this expression of opinion is in an unequivocal form and with the appropriate force, it will certainly have its effect, and a technical religious front will be established.

## 920

B"H, 5th day of the week, 5th of Elul, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Regarding these days—days of *ratzon*, revelation, and the drawing down of abundant mercy, the *Yud-Gimmel Midos HaRachamim*—

In the words of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe: "Therefore, we recite *Selichos* and the *Yud-Gimmel Midos* from *Rosh Chodesh Elul* and onwards (and before that), corresponding to the twelve tribes and the tribe of Levi, which includes them all."

From this, it is understood that the aforementioned drawing down comes to *Bnei Yisrael* as they are divided into tribes, and not as they are still included within the three *Avos*. That is to say, it relates to the individual *avodah* of each person and their specific matters.

And it is explained in other *maamarim*, and is understood, that the arousal to have mercy upon the one who is more distant—and to have mercy even regarding specific details—must come from a higher source: the *Yud-Gimmel Midos HaRachamim*, which do not return empty.

And by way of possibility, one may add to this, based on the words of the Alter Rebbe, "the tribe of Levi, which includes them all"—which is so named in the sense of *yilveh ishi elai* (my husband shall be joined to me)—

That in *avodah*, this means that through the fact that he "includes them all," which causes *yilveh ishi* (the "man," *Hashem*, being joined) *elai* (to me—the drawing down and revelation of the *Yud-Gimmel Midos HaRachamim*: *Hashem, Hashem, Kel, etc.*) in every single person, this will effect *Ani L'Dodi* (an arousal from below), so that everyone will be on the level of the *Bnei Levi*—that their spirit moves them to stand before *Hashem* to serve Him and to worship Him.

As is the final ruling of the great teacher, the Rambam, in his *Yad HaChazakah*: not only the tribe of Levi, but every single person whose spirit moves him—

—and the saying of the Baal Shem Tov is well known, that where a person’s will is, there he is entirely—

—and he understands with his own knowledge to separate himself to stand, etc., he is sanctified as holy of holies, etc.

And through *Ani L'Dodi*, *V'Dodi Li* (an arousal from above) is brought about, as the Rambam says there, that "Hashem will be his portion and his inheritance forever and for all eternity."

And the day of *Chai Elul* is a day of *segulah* for all of the above, for—as per the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe—it is that which gives vitality to the *avodah* of *Ani L'Dodi V'Dodi Li*.

With the blessing of *Kesivah V'Chasimah Tovah*,

**M. Schneerson**

## 21

B"H, 8 Elul, 5725
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter of September 1st, along with the enclosure.

Many thanks for the good news that your trip will be in a manner that Hashem Yisborach permits traveling, and not in a way that involves chillul Shabbos on the largest scale [when one travels on a ship that belongs to Jews, is operated by Jews, and is managed by Jews, during the entire 24 hours of Shabbos, where many labors forbidden on Shabbos are performed—lighting, extinguishing, writing, etc.].

It is a source of the greatest heartache to see such things in general, and even greater is the frustration and heartache when one makes a journey to our—and everyone’s—**holy** land, that it should be done with so much chillul Shabbos by so many people employed on the ship. As mentioned, it is very difficult even to think about this.

May Hashem Yisborach help, also in the merit of changing your travel plans for the better, that the journey should be at a good and auspicious time, and may you be blessed with a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year.

With blessings for good tidings.
