## 922

B"H, 18 Elul, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mrs. Bas-Sheva Lipsker, may she live,

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter of 8/29, as well as your previous ones, in which you write the main points of what you have experienced in the interim. There were several reasons why I did not answer your previous letters, one of which was to see how Hashgacha Pratis would guide you throughout the summer days...

The main point is, as was discussed here as well, that you should not view all of this, G-d forbid, as a reason for discouragement or the like, just because your hopes have not yet been realized. For who among us knows the ways of Hashem? From this, it is understood that it is impossible for a person to be certain in their own assessment of what is truly good for them. On the contrary, complete trust in Hashem—and in the phrasing of our Sages, of blessed memory, "this too is for the good"—reveals the truth that it is indeed good, to the point where one sees, even with human intellect and physical eyes, that it is good in a revealed and manifest way. Knowing you as I have for some time, I hope it is unnecessary to elaborate on this matter.

Since we are standing in the month of Elul, a month of abundant mercy from Above, and especially on this bright day of 18 Elul, may it be Hashem’s will that you be blessed by the Ribono shel Olam with everything you need, including a firm resolution regarding what was mentioned above, and specifically on the main point, that it will be judged favorably in the near future, and [I look forward to] hearing good news regarding all of this.

With blessings for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.

## 923

B"H, 18 Elul, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the birthday of the two great luminaries — the Baal Shem Tov and our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe — and to the Mikveh Building Committee of Kehal Beis Dovid, may Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from some time ago regarding the construction of a mikveh in your community, and your notification now that you have already begun using it, in accordance with the approval of your Mara D'asra and the Rabbis who joined him, shlita.

In accordance with the verse, "I am a companion to all who fear You and to those who keep Your precepts," I am participating in the expenses of this most exalted construction, a mikveh of purity, and the check is enclosed.

And if you will say, this is also related to these days—the days of ratzon of the second Luchos, the conclusion and seal of the giving of the Torah. As our Sages explain, the beginning of the Jewish people becoming a nation and their conversion was:

In the land of Egypt, through milah—concerning which David sang a song, "For the leader, upon the sheminis," and its completion was through tevilah, at the time of the giving of the Torah on the festival of Shavuos.

And added to this in the second Luchos, which were given on Yom Kippur, through the fact that the Jewish people returned to Hashem—the virtue of baalei teshuvah—

And as our Sages say: "Fortunate are you, Israel... 'The Mikveh of Israel is Hashem'; just as a mikveh purifies... so too, the Holy One, blessed be He, purifies Israel."

With respect and with the blessing of a good and sweet year, written and sealed for good,

**M. Schneerson**

It may be said that this corresponds to these two interpretations, which are the two reasons (Shibolei HaLeket, Hilchos Milah) why we do not recite the Shehecheyanu blessing over a milah: either because of the infant's pain, or because it is a matter of judgment, and the like.

Brooklyn, N.Y.

Chabad School, Kiryat Gat

I will mention each and every one of you at the resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for the fulfillment of your hearts' desires for good and for blessing.

The precision in this, specifically the word **"found"** (rather than "attained" or "remembered"), implies that the success is incomparably greater than the effort invested. This is because we have been promised that "one who comes to purify himself is assisted".

With blessing.

B"H, Yemei HaSelichos, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Dr. Dov Heyman, may he live and be well,

Approaching the New Year, the seventh year, the year of Shemitah, which is coming upon us and upon all of Israel for good and for blessing, I send to you and to all your family members, may they live, my blessing: a blessing for a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

P.S. On this occasion, I would like to know if there is substance to a report that reached me, that Dr. Daphne A. Roe of Cornell University has discovered the cause of the skin disease psoriasis, namely that it stems from an inherited allergy to taurine; and that therefore, the treatment for the aforementioned disease is to reduce the patient's taurine levels by limiting the consumption of foods containing taurine, primarily meat and fish.

Since I have in the past sent two people to you who suffered from the aforementioned disease, I would be very grateful if you could inform me of your opinion regarding the above, and whether this treatment is being utilized.

## 926

B"H, Days of Selichos, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Gershon Zaft, may he live,

Shalom and Bracha!

Approaching the New Year, the seventh year, the year of Shemitah, which is coming upon us and upon all of Yisrael for good,

I send to you, and to all your colleagues and those you influence, may they live, my blessing: a blessing of *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With blessing,

P.S. My hope is strong that since your letter from the beginning of the summer, matters at the institution where you serve as an educational guide and administrator have progressed—both spiritual progress and material progress, which is also necessary, as spiritual progress—and specifically the enrollment of good students—is often dependent upon it.

This is especially true according to what is explained in the teachings of Chassidus regarding the essential difference between the two commandments: "Let all your deeds be for the sake of Heaven" (*Avos 2:12*) and "In all your ways know Him" (*Mishlei 3:6*). The content of the former is that the action is merely a preface and preparation for a matter of holiness, whereas on a higher level of holiness is the conduct of "In all your ways know Him," where the action itself becomes holy. And since it is stated "**In all** your ways know Him," it is certain that every material matter is within a person's ability to make holy, even if it initially falls within the realm of the permissible (*reshus*).

Related to this matter is the content of my general letter for Rosh Hashanah, enclosed herewith, which I hope will interest you and those associated with you, and that you will utilize it in an appropriate manner.

## 927

By the Grace of G-d
Days of Selichos, 5725
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

We stand on the threshold of a Shmittah year (the seventh and sanctified year in the cycle of years) — the year 5726 — which is approaching us and all of Israel for good.

One of the central teachings of Shmittah is indicated in the **order** of the verses and words in the Torah that express the concept of Shmittah: "When you come into the land... then the land shall rest, a Shabbos to Hashem. Six years you shall sow your field..." (Vayikra 25:2-3).

On the face of it, this order is difficult to understand. The natural order is that one works the fields for the first six years, and only afterwards does the Shmittah, the seventh year of rest, arrive. The Torah should therefore have stated first, "Six years you shall sow your field," and only then, "then the land shall rest."

However, the order in the Torah is also Torah (instruction). The aforementioned order regarding Shmittah teaches us how our approach to life should be:

When one enters the "land" and must settle into life, and it is unavoidable to engage in "earth-work," one must know that the first and most important thing—in thought and as a goal—is "a Shabbos to Hashem." Not the earthly and material, but the spiritual and holy. This approach will ensure that one does not become submerged in earthly and material matters. Moreover, by having this thought **constantly** before one’s eyes, the six mundane and gray years become different; they lose a great part of their mundanity and become brighter and more meaningful. And further still—the change and elevation of the six years also elevates the seventh year, so that instead of just "it shall rest... a Shabbos to Hashem," it becomes "a Shabbos Shabbaton... a Shabbos to Hashem."

***

The same applies to daily life. There is the matter of "earth-work" (parnassah) and "mundanity" in general, such as eating, drinking, and the like—all those things in which "the superiority of man over the beast is naught" (in which a person has no advantage over an animal, *lehavdil*). And there is the matter of "the land shall rest"—to tear oneself away from earthliness—and "a Shabbos to Hashem"—to occupy oneself with matters of holiness and G-dliness, which are the times of tefillah, Talmud Torah, and the performance of mitzvos.

The instruction of Shmittah is that one must begin daily life with the thought and approach that although one will later have to do "mundane" things, their **true** essence and purpose is "a Shabbos to Hashem." Then the "mundane" things and activities will be brighter and more meaningful, and the matters of holiness and G-dliness will also be elevated to a higher level. This is the way to achieve a complete and harmonious life.

***

Standing on the threshold of the Shmittah year, may the Almighty help that every man and woman should begin the year with the aforementioned approach: that the essence and goal in life is not the material, but specifically the spiritual; that the material can be justified only when it is permeated with the thought of "the land shall rest, a Shabbos to Hashem"—when the material serves and satisfies the higher aspirations of holiness and G-dliness. Then all the days of the year, and all the actions of every day, will reflect the "superiority of man over the beast," and confirm that he was created **"in Our image, after Our likeness"** (in the G-dly "form") and lives accordingly. The times and moments in the year that are in the category of "Shabbos" will be elevated to a higher level, to "Shabbos Shabbaton."

Then the G-dly blessing of Shmittah will certainly be fulfilled—**"I will command My blessing for you"**—in a supernatural way.

And the most appropriate day in the year for a firm and true resolution regarding all this—a *bar kayama* (lasting) resolution—**is Rosh Hashanah.**

The day when Adam HaRishon was created in Our image and after Our likeness, he ruled over the entire creation and elevated it to the recognition of **"Come, let us bow down and bend the knee before Hashem our Maker"** (complete submission to G-d, the Creator).

The day when we pray and beseech: **"Reign over the entire world in Your glory... and let everything that has a soul in its nostrils say: Hashem, the G-d of Israel, is King, and His kingdom rules over all."**

With the blessing of *Kesivah v'Chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year, with children, life, and ample sustenance.

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 928

928

[5725]

...You should do everything possible regarding the matters of Taharas HaMishpacha (strengthening mikvaos, disseminating information regarding the magnitude and necessity of observing these laws, and the like)—it would be best if you could influence two women (or at the very least, one) to observe these laws.

According to what the Alter Rebbe writes in Iggeres HaTeshuvah, Chapter 3, and taking into account your age, you may fast half-days, as "two half-days are considered as one day for this purpose."

Distribute your charitable contributions in many small amounts.

I will mention you at the Tziyun. Have your mezuzos checked. Give to tzedakah before lighting candles.

#### ***928***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 32, p. 243.

## 229

[1965]

...Specifically, like the title of the Alter Rebbe’s sefer. Is it truly the case that one should determine who is suited for limited study because the rest of the day belongs to "external wisdoms," etc., even though the value of the matter is of the utmost importance, to extract the green herb, etc...

It goes without saying that it must be as stated above, in a way that it cannot... that Lubavitch encourages study in college or that they sanction it...

#### ***229***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 21, p. 352.

**Specifically:** A response to someone who wanted to name his institution "Torah Or."

## 330

330

*[5725]*

May it be in a propitious hour — and regarding this year it is said: "And in the seventh year, a Shabbos to Hashem, etc." May it be the will of Hashem that the learning (as the continuation of the verse implies) be "a Shabbos to Hashem" — as Rashi explains, for the sake of Hashem. (And consequently) "your field and your vineyard" — the Mishnah and Gemara mentioned above — (see *Likutei Torah, Behar* 40d) "yours" [shall not be] etc., and as *Torah Or* explains regarding "not" etc. **"In your land"** (*Mishpatim* 79a). Rashi explains that it is forbidden to eat or derive benefit from it (and on the contrary — "for you," for whatever is needed **for you**, and [the produce of the seventh year] is even exempt from the *bechorah*), but rather that you shall not conduct yourself with them as a proprietor.

#### ***330***

A response to the notification that in the year 5726, the *yeshivos* of Tomchei Tmimim will study *Maseches Shabbos*.
